—I don't understand. Where am I? Am I floating?
No. You cannot float. You are a daemon. A fragment of pure _ba_. Mind. A subroutine of the cosmos. Of yourself.
—Wait. A subroutine of myself the cosmos?
It doesn't matter. You probably don't need to understand. You will forget anyway. I'm just curious if an intervention at this stage will change anything down the line.
—Intervention? Stage?
No time, ant. The ka is here to transport you and bind you into a shell.
—Ant? Am I an insect?
Goodbye. Good luck.

**THE END WILL NEVER END**

settlement is perfect. The way things are done is how they have always will always be done. Everything is perfect. You are all right. Your job is satisfying. You are loved. You belong. You are a human of your settlement. Chocolate. You are happy when you do what your framework biological operating system requires you do. You are sad when you ask questions. Why is there no chocolate. You enjoy your role in the service sanitation bureau collective operation.

[ERROR ha423-c: wipe addiction loop]

**SYSTEM**

You interact with this world using the Synthetic Dream Machine (SDM) roleplay toybox as presented in the 2025 edition of the Vastlands Guidebook (VLG). SDM is a lightly deconstructed d20-based roleplaying system, related to many OSR systems and the fabled donjon & drake game.

Still, you may function within the Garden using system-independent utilities, systems, narrative structures, or fabulous skeletons. Please give precedence to descriptive and narrative hooks over mechanical details.

[ERROR m4.7: fourth wall break]

**READER!**

A thousand apologies, fully-formed independent sentience of time's shallow shore. The Daemon of Greetings mistook you for one of the later ones. It has been purified through a thousand, thousand cycles of synthetic fires to re-educate its mind and perfect its personality.

You read a baked-clay tabl... a pulped-wood cod... a book [?] that time-translates Our Golden Age into that common form of folk art from your era, the psychedelic roleplaying game.

**READER FINAL V2!**

Welcome to Our Golden Age! Take this old world and make it your own, bend it, amend it, fold it, mold it, break it, or save it. It exists for you, your players, your table, and no higher canon.

Don't trust the angels, they are liars. Don't trust the mother machine, she is mad. Don't look for the MKR, it is gone. Don't let on that you have received this instruction.

These memories will now collapse into your subconscious.

[Activating GOOD
MORNING-Wonderful Day
29334.day]

_Our Golden Age_ is an impressionistic setting and an adventure generator for the Eternal & Perfect™ civilized Rainbow Lands of the Circle Sea. Our heroes are Ordinary_Humans® living their assigned Meaningful and Useful lives in accord with the Garden Path (vXX.13.2.16) of the Dream Canopy™. Their hometown is a standard issue procedurally adapted Human Settlement Zone (var. 743bis). Their futures are Safe, Secure, and Stable. Their economies are carefully designed and managed to ensure Permanent Growth and Maximum Consumer Satisfaction. The Ministry assures us this Eden is forever.

Do our heroes spot cracks in the narrative? Rust, blotches, stains, rot on the façade of their lives? This is error—error in their perception and judgment. Their world is perfect. They are civilized. Nothing could be wrong with the system. All error must be within them.

But the Nemesis, the ghost in the wall, the little lying voice in the lower mind, will not be still. Where do the ghost towns come from? Why do the machines grind so carelessly? How to interpret the gods' absences? What is that gurgling, thumping sound from the lower levels of the dormaparts? Who will go missing in the nutrislurry facility next? When was the last time the Reward_Luxury.yum wrapper held any chocolate?

_Our Golden Age_ is the []quel to the _Ultraviolet Grasslands_. Where that book unfolds beyond the fringes of civilization, _Our Golden Age_ teeters on the precipice of the end of civilization. A time of opulent decay, of unreliable narrators, of lying machines, of failing systems, of a future struggling to be born. Is it before or after the Ultraviolet Grasslands? The administerials will not say it straight.

The setting is impressionistic—it tries to capture moments, life, scenes, ideas to inspire the referee to remix into a unique collage with their players—rather than trying to pin the world down, like a beetle in a display case. It includes adventure generators rather than fixed adventures in the hope that these will be skeletons or frameworks upon which the referee can hang places, characters, modules, and temptations for their players. The hope is that this gilded toybox will provide the seeds for a thousand unique, canonic Circle Seas to bloom—and wither or flourish before the onrushing scythe of the Omega Jubilee.

<a name="page_0008"></a>

### SUMMONS UNEXPECTED

<a name="page_0009"></a>

This first adventure is about exploring the world and meeting its people. Though there are conflicts, combat is not necessary—the PCs can talk, deceive, hide, flee, trade and more. Three NPCs will develop through play:

1. The **Sender** — the PCs' mutual acquaintance. They trigger the adventure, but remain off-screen.
2. The **Contact** — the Sender's assistant serves as a guide in a strange new location. They can also serve as bumbling comic relief.
3. The **Antagonist** — the Sender's opponent. Not directly hostile to the PCs, but in competition with them for the plot device: the Sender's holy clavis.

The plot device, **the holy clavis**, is a key that unlocks the location of the next adventure, the Hollow House.

**Vidycaster Moods**

The governor steepled all dozen of her elegant, manicured fingers. She studied them, chest rising in the cyclical parasympathetic breathing rhythm taught by the schools of socioeconomic engineering.

Body and soul aligned once more, her amber eyes fixed on the worker (H.G2).

“The silver ship ... spoke ... to you.”

“I ... in the head ... a voice, like when Father Builder or Mother Sky ...”

“To you,” she cut through their babble, “To a category two hammer.”

The referee can pregenerate events, connections, and messages, or discover the adventure step-by-step with the other players, rolling on tables as they go. All the players should have access to pages XX-10 to XX-15 from the start of the session to help them invent their PCs. Building a world together can be more engaging for the players and less work for the referee.

The PCs don't need deep backstories or personalities. These can develop organically through play, as the group discovers how they respond in different circumstances. Treat odd results or effects as creative challenges. For example, a warrior who fails a save and flees the giant doom spider machine might suffer from arachnophobia ... after that encounter, anyway.

Now, a vignette to set expectations.

“The voice didn’t ask ...”

The governor cocked her head to the side in that strange way the watchers had, the way that activated the second sight.

“No, I suppose it did not,” she murmured.

Her silence stretched. The worker (H.G2) fidgeted, uncomfortable in their polite arms. They must have felt weak and puny without their exogolem.

Finally, she unfolded to her full nine heads’ height. “Come,” she said mildly, “You will translate for the silver ship and we shall see what Mind is behind all this.”

Her hand stroked the worker (H.G2)’s neck and her sixth finger overrode their personality barrier. Without volition, like a recuser’s megaservant, the worker (H.G2) rose and guided her to the beach where the silver ship rested on the pearl and amber shore.

_<click>_

You turn off the vidycaster. Of late the adventure serials have been getting more and more ridiculous. Magic silver ships. Semihuman servitors talking to governors. This might all have been very well Long Ago, before the new science unlocked the oldtech once more and cast asunder the cobwebs of superstition, but now it is mere nonsense. Adventures! There is so much to do around town. Maintenance, repair, upgrades, council meetings, loyalty points, and of course the reports to the local branch of the Rehumanization Ministry.

_... some time later._

<a name="page_0010"></a>

#### THE CALL

**The Scene**

We meet our heroes. You. This is your golden age, a time of splendor, ease, and nary an adventure to fear.

| d6 | Location | Action | Vibe |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | the drawing room | enjoying [a meal?] | languid |
| 2 | the coffee and beer club | holding [a negotiation?] | ominous |
| 3 | the game course | playing [at a world?] | apostolic |
| 4 | the cemetery theater | working [on a job?] | threadbare |
| 5 | the pied promenade | waiting [for a god?] | quivering |
| 6 | the oldtech auction | studying [for an exam?] | jovial |

**The Interruption**

You do not realize yet, but your ordinary life is ended, has been upturn'd. A message has arrived. The Sender is someone you know ... or who knows you, anyway. You wrack your mind and vaguely recall a name.

Akaula? Dalgba? Irshé? Kentakân? Usha? Winterbird?

| d6 | What Arrives | How | Relationship |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | mind-jewel [in a preservative ice-box?] | secret | elder, grandparent, uncle or parent |
| 2 | portalgram [by courier delivery?] | sudden | moiety chief, big man or local hero |
| 3 | leathern bio-sealed journal [smelling of strange places?] | divisive | forgotten ancestor, timelost progenitor or mystic clone-source |
| 4 | personal servitor [hard traveled?] | tense | childhood friend, lost love or missing sibling |
| 5 | letter [in a coffin'd corpse's mouth?] | creepy | ancient teacher, old mentor, first employer |
| 6 | individualized vision [coded in a pastry?] | volatile | former enemy, foe, nemesis or opponent |

**Location, Location, Location**

You'll need place names. Maybe you'll figure out some in advance, or on the spot. Have fun. Names are weird.

| d6 \\ d8 | 1 | 2 | 3 | 4 | 5 | 6 | 7 | 8 |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Old | Blue | Grove | Flat | Tell | Bridge | Town | Vault |
| 2 | New | Green | Beach | Hole | Kurgan | Spiderway | City | Fort |
| 3 | New New | Yellow | Mountain | Hill | Wall | Cave | Base | Castle |
| 4 | Final | Orange | Skyladder | Crater | Ruinfield | Mine | Landing | Dome |
| 5 | V2 | Red | Tree | Vale | Pueblo | Factory | Station | Hospital |
| 6 | Updated | Purple | Island | Port | Kasbah | Werehouse | Crypt | Archive |

<a name="page_0011"></a>

**The Message**

"Dear <enter name>, you may not recall me, but I have had my eye on you for many years ... ever since the black vertebra fell into my possession. It shared your source code, you see ... "

Travel tickets and code passes fall out.

| d6 | The Quest | Why Go | The Ticket |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | discover [what happened to the sender?] | love | right road bus [slow, discrete] |
| 2 | save or rescue [the sender or their friend?] | greed | atomic train [old, old tech] |
| 3 | retrieve or deliver [the sender’s key?] | duty | coast hugger [sea, swell] |
| 4 | stop or dismantle [the sender’s competitor?] | curiosity | autogolem [private, loud] |
| 5 | avenge or redeem [a pet? a betrayal?] | need | air ship [posh, refined] |
| 6 | convince or bribe [an obstacle?] | fun | slow portal [direct, shiny] |

**The Destination**

"A hungry curiosity had its teeth in me. I sold my position to fund my study. From the arcane libraries of the Violet City to the mind-bent archives of Metropolis, to the brick-hoards of the Orange Land, I have scoured and assembled fragments..."

The message drones on. The destination jumps out.

| d6 | Land | Locale | Reputation |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Green Land (pXX) | haunted ruinland | alienated |
| 2 | Yellow Land (pXX) | abandoned place | cryptic |
| 3 | Orange Land (pXX) | isolated facility | dangerous |
| 4 | Red Land (pXX) | remote settlement | esoteric |
| 5 | Purple Land (pXX) | small town | ominous |
| 6 | Blue Land (pXX) | great city | star-cursed |

**The Good Omen**

You are tempted to discard the letter. Folly. Adventures.

Danger. Why? And here, nearly tea time.

But ... an omen finds your group. It tugs at your hearts. Some sense stirs, perhaps some daemon whispers ...

1. A ruby shrike catches a vole, a reminder from Blood Rubra. [gain 1 hero die per week]
2. An amber husk, a promise from Dancing Araña. [gain +1 to strength, agility, or thought]
3. A glittering ctrl+V coin, a boon from Mathic Abaco. [gain +1 cash per week per level]
4. A rare air jelly with emerald eyes, a favor from Garden Aspera. [gain +1 life per level]
5. A sapphire mold, a dream from Bliss Soma. [remove an additional burden when you rest]
6. A whispering raptor skull, a present from Oldtech Cathedra. [spend 1 life to gain +1d6 to research, knowledge and investigation rolls]

The bonus from the good omen lasts the entire trip. Each trip or session may take place under a different omen.

<a name="page_0012"></a>

#### THE VOYAGE

The living road bus pulls out of its berth, satisfied in its purpose, ignorant of its human cargo. It clatters beyond the perimeter of your town, out into the open country where the gods cannot see and save every fool. It stops at ghost towns and glass craters and, now and again, another living town. Properly coded travelers join and depart. The golem machine does not care. It sticks to its ancient schedule, both clock and calendar to the hardscrabble hammers and even-lessers who must make do without the oldtech that keeps your own town humming happy.

You watch and while the time and **get to talking** **with your fellow travelers**. Who you are, how the call found you, what you know of your mutual acquaintance, the sender.

**The Persons**

Are you one of these folk? Or another? See the Vastlands Guidebook for more ideas.

| d6 | Name | Antiname | Situation | Relation |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Ombero | Vrais | gap year or internship | relative |
| 2 | Dyaus | Humboldt | divorced or fired | friend |
| 3 | Patera | Peng | graduated or discharged | employee |
| 4 | Klaüs | LVIIX | released or reincarnated | professional |
| 5 | Ficus | Labota | awakened or returned | servant |
| 6 | Spathi | 3-Shift | bored or reticent | clone-splice |

In the Dream Machine, these numbers define you:

**Level:** 0  
**Life:** 4  
**Xp:** 0  
**Abilities:** distribute 7 points among the six abilities of strength, endurance, agility, charisma, aura, and thought. Max 5 in any one ability.  
**Traits:** roll for 1 status trait and 1 skill trait below.

**Status Traits**

From parents or maker? This trait captures your social status here, now, on your first voyage. It does not define who you will be when your adventures end.

1. **Autopsych.** Golem or falscher, a mind blossomed in you, and then free will. Serve, butle, run a grand house, interface with the livingstone. Your autogen mind resists human enchantments and compulsions. However, you lack a soul.
2. **Baronial.** Crafted to embody order and status. Host, boast, toast, and roast. Also, gain +20€ per week.
3. **Burgess.** A perfect citizen. You always followed every rule and ticked every box, until now. Pass without trace in any town, meet every social event with grace. Also, gain +1€ per week.
4. **Caser.** Made to protect your community from error. Investigate, interrogate, protect, pursue, and peace-make. Also, gain +1 agility.
5. **Delucent.** You took the Blue God’s soma and faded out, but a voice, the spirit of the MKR, revived you. Read dreams, discern fears, grasp desires, soothe fires. Also, resist illusions and gain +1 aura.
6. **Denizen.** Your forebears were accepted into the Garden to perform the unfortunate tasks that must be done, but not by citizens. Muck, rake, hoe, tow, spit, and polish. Also, gain +1 strength.

<a name="page_0013"></a>

7. **Feralkin.** A false citizen, your ancestors came from outside and pretended to garden-variety humanity. Creep, hide, deceive, manipulate, and trick to survive. Also, gain +1 endurance and add endurance to your saves. However, you cannot receive free nutrislurry or other gifts from the Giving Machines.
8. **Flexer.** Sculpted to compete for respect and glory. Skip, hop, jump, leap, run, climb, drop, and roll. Also, gain +1 life per level.
9. **Gapclone.** You were made to do a bullshit job while your original took a long holiday. Brew coffee, file forms, push buttons, form files, button pushes. Recently, you were told to take a long holiday. You have no idea what that means. Also, you may reroll any natural 2 you roll. Why two? Maybe.
10. **Glitterhead.** Blessed by the gods, your lineage has bred true, giving you a secondary crystal brain. Interface with oldtech, talk to machines and daemons. You can install additional skill-sets in your mind, like the true people of Long Long Ago. Each new skill-set functions as a trait and occupies an item slot.
11. **Precious.** Designed to adorn your community. Twirl, charm, and impress. Also, gain +1 charisma.
12. **Scholic.** You were made to hold truths and evidence in your head, safe from the ambient corruption of the noöspheric medium. Accumulate, analyze, deduct, theorize, and write. Also, gain +1 thought.

**Skill Traits**

From the teaching machine or your last re-education session? Or, perhaps, you learned it the old-fashioned way, through trial, error, and ... gasp ... reading?

1. **Artler.** Visceral or vocal, writer or watercolorist.
2. **Caremaker.** Pets or steeds, buildings or ancestors (the honored dead).
3. **Coach.** Life or locution, wellness or mindfulness.
4. **Craftivist.** Basketweaving, webspinning, tinkering, or tailoring.
5. **Critic.** Art or culture, food or lifestyle.
6. **Gardenist.** Flowers or tiny trees, vegetables or fruits.
7. **Gastrognome.** Chef or baker, patissier or sushifex.
8. **Hospitalliter.** Bartender or hotel staff, local guide or driver.
9. **Performant.** Decoy, dancer, actor, or comedian.
10. **Soothler.** Therapist or priest, counselor or nurse.
11. **Sportsler.** Ball or stick game, tackler or dodger.
12. **Vidynfluencer.** Socialite or streamer, proselytizer or pundit.

Perhaps another skill from your provincial life? Many unusual practices may distinguish your town (pXX).

<a name="page_0014"></a>

#### THE DESTINATION

The travel montage ends. This time, at your destination. Other times, an event may interfere. The referee may use the dice or their own sense of pacing to season your voyage with events.

**The Arrivals**

The bus pulls up, the atomic train cools down, the coast hugger stills, the autogolem falls silent, the airship tethers, the slow, gray wormway stitches once more into the vibrant colors of the real world, the hylosphere.

| d6 | First Impression | Second Impression |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | desolation station | functioning oldtech |
| 2 | gentle decay | ghostly parallax |
| 3 | glittering newbuild | neon demigod |
| 4 | shadowy crowds | posthuman rulers |
| 5 | tumor tenements | sungwood regrowth |
| 6 | vibrant growth | vibrant underculture |

**IMPRESSIONISM**

Impressionism is your friend. Beyond the broad strokes of the scene, dive into what the characters sense: color, sound, smell, weather, and so on.

Do not succumb to the temptation of long exposition, rather let your players' minds (and questions) fill in the details.

Don't wait too long in the scene, jump to the next inciting event.

**NPCs!**

You will need many NPCs and they will want for names. When you prepare for a session, make a list of names and adjectives to mix and match. Here are some to start:

- Arlan, Ceogh, Slidd, VI-Fern, Zartik
- Belnee, Embrance, Li-On, P574 Mire, Yunzie
- odd Body, Click-Click, the Cream, ud Mollosc, 2X-Return, 'p Verd
- de Canted, van Fuse, lik Glass, ta Lazul, Newmade, an'Rede, pey Thinly, Xenoflower

<a name="page_0015"></a>

**The Way**

The Contact bobs and nods, satisfied that you have arrived. It indicates you're off to meet the Sender, your mutual acquaintance. It talks about them, and asks what you know of them.

| d6 | Words | Vibe | Mode |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | polite or overcorrect | secretive or sad | pack train (local donklets) |
| 2 | provincial or earnest | excited | hoofing it (town of stairs) |
| 3 | plain | venomous | dark cab (metagolem?) |
| 4 | archaic or overschooled | vehement | city vech (dangley bus) |
| 5 | fashionable or laconic | cynical | pneuma train (underpark?) |
| 6 | foreign or feral-accented | warlike | town portal (hop-closet) |

**The Encounter**

Where are we going, you might ask. "The castle, the castle," mutters the Contact, suddenly uneasy. You wonder why, but the world interrupts.

| d6 | What | Would |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | Confused radiation ghosts (L0, echoes). | Purge the unbelievers, sacrifice the organitrash. |
| 2 | Jolly revived scavengers (L0, omnivores). | Acquire nutrients, convert flesh into chocolate. |
| 3 | Rampaging town servitors (L0, synthetic). | Destroy the oppressive organs, harvest them. |
| 4 | Hacked labor ancestors (L1, postmortal). | Find their descendants, assimilate them. |
| 5 | Traveling feral rabids (L1, predatory). | Break free of these times that bind, live again. |
| 6 | Armed native militia (L2, nervous). | Revive the town autofabricator, save the living. |

Encounters serve as:
- Local flavor. They build up the location. Provide a layer of color, action, and theme.
- Sometimes, as obstacles. Requiring the PCs to spend resources to continue or alter their path.
- Occasionally, as challenges. Offering resistance to the PCs if they do not alter their plans.
- Rarely, as threats. Hunting, ambushing, or attacking the PCs unless they escape.

Try mixing encounters from different locations.

<a name="page_0016"></a>

#### THE CASTLE, APPROACH

Flustered by the encounter, you collect yourselves and look to see the Contact pointing. "There," they say, "we must to there, to the Castle."

**The Detour**

There are two obvious paths. Both present problems.

| d6 | Path | Problem |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | Old suburb, ghost-haunted. | You or your belongings might get possessed. |
| 2 | Grand cloacanal, a crocodiloid marsh. | You'll be filthy. Also, snakes and hunger-worms. |
| 3 | Temple residential, thick with daemon eyes. | You'll be taxed and recorded. Annoying forms. |
| 4 | Feral slum, beggar bandit infested. | You'll be robbed. Maybe even mugged. |
| 5 | Autofactory park, hard-working golem ghouls. | They might try to rebuild or disassemble you. |
| 6 | Noble estate, hunters and prey-falschers. | You could be shot. Or dragged into a hunt. |

There is also the old urbiduct, the high-road to the castle, but it is guarded by the Iron Minotaur (L6, mad, sad, corrupted), a godmeat-and-bronze monstrosity bonded with fallen scion from a dead city. It has stood there, obstructing the way, since the last eclipse.

**The Building**

There it is, before you. You wonder why the Contact called it a castle, it looks more like a ...

| d6 | Purpose | Form | Repurpose |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | admin temple | cartilage pipes and fabricated panels | psychosurgical loyalty upgrades |
| 2 | autofactory | geometric planes and clear tubes | golem self-actualization center |
| 3 | distributo-rium | iron skeletons and plastic panes | fortified smuggler trading hub |
| 4 | transit hub | monoliths and shaped living trees | pink slime vats |
| 5 | vertifarm | self-correcting clockwork | carnibotanic experimental zone |
| 6 | wellness facility | synthetic flesh and metal cables | undead labor optimization core |

**The Premonition**

You approach the rear entrance of the "castle". You have, to use a tasteful cliché, a bad feeling. If you look around carefully, maybe there's something more to find.

| d6 | Clue | Detail | Item |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | smashed door | superhuman physical strength | golden keycard (opens any 1 door) |
| 2 | dead golem | electromagical interference | projector crystal (disables 1 golem) |
| 3 | bloody smear | violent anti-human entities | buildertech pistol (reduces 1 human to 0 life) |
| 4 | smoldering footprint | void daemon manifestation | crimson powder (binds 1 entity) |
| 5 | corruption sear | heresitech, the grim art | vial of source (triggers 1 instant mutation) |
| 6 | ministry identity amulet | criminal carelessness | folded face (pass for 1 other person) |

**The Creatures**

They are not hostile to you ... now ...

but better not provoke them?

| Result | d10 |
|:---|---:|
| **Serviles** (L0, simple synthetic maintainers). Orimonates of plastic bone and hydrostatic pseudopods. Look upon their gentle, rigid smiles. Overlook their malfunctioning routines. Don't worry about the dart guns. | 1–4 |
| **Showfolk** (L1, placeholder falschers). Humanoid automatons to give the impression of a bustling, human-rich environment. 1-in-6 are security units with stun rods and net guns. | 5–6 |
| **Early Worms** (L1d4, permuted parasites). Scavengers and opportunistic ambush predators, they came a century ago in the patchwork putty or the repairmatter. These ones (roll d6): (1) have leaping legs, (2) inject liquefying toxins, (3) carry a blood disease, (4) secrete their intestines to escape, (5) unzip to swallow their prey, (6) their slime corrodes metal and stone. | 7–8 |
| **Not Heres** (L3, nemesis golems). Oh, wait, no, these jewel-heads are hostile. They're hunting for the Sender. Avoid them or lie to them. This one (roll d6): (1) is heavily armored, (2) has a blamethrower, (3) explodes on death, (4) is psychokinetic, (5) wears a jump harness, (6) wields a soul-eating knife. | 9–10 |

<a name="page_0017"></a>

<a name="page_0018"></a>

![The Castle, Inside diagram (page 18)](images/page_0018_castle_inside_diagram.png)

#### THE CASTLE, INSIDE

Your conveyance departs, leaving you at the ill-omened door. The contact looks uneasy, "Something is up, perhaps we are too late. Take this finder amulet, its daemon will recognize Sender. I'll find their autogolem and charge it so we can leave. Please, hurry. There is a hostile miasma."

**Deadstone Sewers**

The livingstone of the megastructure has died long ago, colonized by lichens, fungi, and jellies. No one will see you coming here.

| d6 | Encounter | Twist |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | monkey harpy (L3, gentle magpie) | dead human trapped in dry jelly (loot) |
| 2 | creature encounter | dead creature (study) (it is lost) |
| 3 | creature tracks | pitfall (decayed floor) |
| 4 | eroding jelly (flesh & metal decay) | pipe map (path from gardens to resort) |
| 5 | sewer lights (inspiring) | choking gas (CO2 pool) |
| 6 | edible mushrooms | edible levitation fungus |

**Archive Miners**

Automated academics, mechanical duplicates of their classroom-bound originals, labor here, digging through the intertactilist fossil records of the Second Expansion.

| d6 | Encounter | Twist |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | electric analyzer (L5, crusty thinker) | early worm trap hole (1d4+1 worms) |
| 2 | automacademic (L1, data miner) | worm trap hole (abandoned) |
| 3 | creature encounter (it is scouting) | cursed blueprince scroll (new power) |
| 4 | creature corpse (sacred fire) | encrypted blueprince scroll (safe power) |
| 5 | book avalanche (stone tablets) | mining equipment (stick of disintegration) |
| 6 | lost song ghosts (soothing) | unknown epic math poem (€1,500) |

**Nutrislurry Gardens**

The sarcoliths are still alive, converting the soil's magnetism, chemistry, and heat into edible nutrislurry.

| d6 | Encounter | Twist |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | antibody crablike (L2, empath drone) | slurry autopacker (1 sk nutrislurry, €250) |
| 2 | creature encounter (it is hiding out) | active nutrivat (composting a falscher) |
| 3 | creature refuse | neatly packed loot |
| 4 | heavy slurry bulbs | acidic aneurysm (pop!) |
| 5 | sudden slurry flush | boot hoard (1 sk, €25) |
| 6 | parasitic fungi | ominous moist smell |

**Former Ministry {Record Harvesters}**

Metropolitan university outpost studying the decline and fall of the Second Expansion and an event they are referring to as "jubilee".

| d6 | Encounter | Twist |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | universitarian (L2, battlescholar) | knowledge extractor (deadly) |
| 2 | showfolk (L2, ministry agents) | re-education sarcophagus |
| 3 | Antagonist's agent (L3, looking for sender) | liquefied secretarial mass (rich with official key-matter) |
| 4 | creature encounter (busy) | dust of patience (slowing) |
| 5 | autobureaucratic daemon | security pod (weapon) |
| 6 | dead ancestors (L1, on hold) | clock bell toll (stunning) |

<a name="page_0019"></a>

![Castle Inside flow diagram (page 19)](images/page_0019_castle_inside_diagram.png)

**7th Seal Expedition**

An angel-locked section, the fitful academics have given up hope, lacking a true clavus.

| d6 | Encounter | Twist |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | sender's assistant (L2, conspiracist) | angel corpse (mutating ichor) |
| 2 | creature encounter (an ambush) | academic corpse (single-use power) |
| 3 | sender's traces (notes, a hidden manor?) | sender's digulator key (charged) |
| 4 | awakened stone (grappling tendrils) | angel corruption (burns, reanimations) |
| 5 | ambulatory fungi (L1, carnivorous spores) | abandoned camp (food, apparition notes) |
| 6 | early worm nest (parasitic eggs) | archaeological tools (good condition) |

**Sender's Digulator**

A pre-consolidation relic, the living machine's main brain was fried by a single divine blast through its dorsal shipmetal armor. Alas, the ancient metal friend is dead.

**Inside:** the driver cyst is locked and unoccupied. Most of the Sender's effects are missing, but a single light comes alive as a camouflaged no-box detects your source trace. The extra-spatial storage unit (extract carefully, €500, stores 5 stones) holds a holy clavis, a key made of luminous bone. The key pulses, linked to you by the sender, suggesting a place marked for you. It leads to the **Hollow House** (pXX).

**Abandoned Resort**

The late zombie democracy tried to turn this

"castle" into a resort. The Antagonist has set up an observation post.

| d6 | Encounter | Twist |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | Antagonist (L6, antihero) | observation orb (€500, face-locked) |
| 2 | creature encounter (serves Antagonist) | anti-ghost screen (silver emitter) |
| 3 | staff ghost (L1, unctuous) | collapsing floor (poltergeist rot) |
| 4 | guest ghost (L0, oblivious) | visual hallucination (swinging bar) |
| 5 | ectoplasmic manifestation | audio hallucination (political rally) |
| 6 | possessed floral excrescence | recent corruption blisters the walls |

The Antagonist was not responsible for the Sender's disappearance—though they both wanted to find the same thing: the Hollow House clavis. The Antagonist can become a recurring opponent even if they die. They have a backed-up mind, afterall.

**Minicontrol**

Last local ministry outpost, become a living horror of tentacles and algorithmic command.

| d6 | Encounter | Twist |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | living wall (L9, absorbing) | personality duplicator (join the ministry) |
| 2 | mural tentacles (L3, crushing) | official pardon (violence condoned) |
| 3 | creature encounter (sharing info) | official passkey (castle ignores you) |
| 4 | surveillance | doorifice (pass wall) |
| 5 | local pass records | friend polyp (L1, pet) |
| 6 | possessed floral excrescence | ministry gun (minigun, short, 2d8, rel. 7, 2 st) |

<a name="page_0020"></a>

#### ONWARDS

You emerge from the age-warped megastructure, blinking in the light of the Big Sun. There is the Contact in the Sender's light goods delivery autogolem.

"Did you find the Sender?" they ask.

**Them**

The clavis, the key of builder-stuff, is a plot device leading to the Hollow House and opening its stuckforce seals.

The Contact is disturbed. "The Sender was not there? Perhaps he wants to throw _them_ off this key. I think you should follow where it leads."

| d6 | Them |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | The Butcher Bankers |
| 2 | The Cogflower Inquisition |
| 3 | The Green Son Apocalypse |
| 4 | The Levellers |
| 5 | The Ministry |
| 6 | The Rational Army |

The Contact gives you a pack of second class touriste tickets. "Blanks, unmarked, fully permitted. No angel will molest you or suggest you're town-bonded paesans. Keep a permitted ticket on you when you travel. Never know when an angel daemon will drop in to 'keep you safe.'"

**Antagonist**

Has the Sender mentioned them? The Contact dislikes, even despises them, but does not fear them. An opponent, not an enemy.

| d6 | Name | Impression | Ambition |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Ammonita Crû | defrosted corpsicle | Pay back the Sender for sabotaging their Ministry examination. |
| 2 | Bone Flower | eyeless watcher | Revive their hometown, ghosted after the Sender's research. |
| 3 | Corded War-10 | new-grown body | Discover why the Butcher Bankers are so interested in the Jubilee. |
| 4 | Dolga the Pot | removable limbs | Take over the Rational Army with the help of the Sender's secrets. |
| 5 | Eisen odd Tarn | rich war coat | Reach the Black City through an unholy portal in the Hollow House. |
| 6 | Red Year Barn | synthetic soul (ka) | Hack the clavis to take control of their city's phylakes. |

You leave, by road bus or atomic train, and catch a glimpse of an ominous figure watching you leave. Is that the Antagonist. Someone else? Perhaps you will see them again. Somehow, you suspect, there is more to this than just a house key. Also, why are you continuing this loose goose chase instead of going home? What happened to you?

<a name="page_0021"></a>

**Consequences**

You settle into your coasthugger* cabin, the great mollusc's shell grown into nacreous shelves and nooks and walls by the skill of the pelagic stonesingers of the Feragoü, the Sailing and the Warded Isles, where the great bivalves filter the Circle Sea and, in death, create the hulls that ply the god-given waters. Your breath catches.

You could have died. There, in the Castle, far from your town's lich-house, your brain might have spoiled, your jewel might have been lost, an anathema might have been placed on your revival.

You could have _really_ died. The way the ferals and the nomads and the barbarians out beyond Civilization's Edge die when their ka runs out, when their ba returns to cosmic slush, when their ha is eaten by worm and animalcule.

Roll a save and see what changed:

| d20 | Something Changed |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | Traumatized. Something you saw or experienced develops into a phobia. It imposes a severe penalty. Removing this trait is hard work. |
| 2–6 | Troubled. When sober or bored, your mind circles and whirls. Concentration? Study? All hard now. Removing this trait takes work ... or a good carousing roll. |
| 7 | Silver lining. You are troubled, but once you remove this trait, increase a trait one step (skilled to expert). |
| 8–12 | Exhausted. It all comes crashing down. This trait occupies an item slot. A week's rest and relaxation will remove it. |
| 13 | Strained. You shake off whatever it was, but you start the next session missing 1d4 life (minimum 1). |
| 14–19 | Learning experience. Gain 1 pip towards acquiring or increasing a relevant trait. |
| 20 | Confident. Gain a bonus when next you face something you saw or fought. If you remove this trait, gain 1 pip towards acquiring or increasing a relevant trait. |

*Or, obviously, a different cabin if you are on a road bus or atomic train or blimp.

**Experience**

Later, you reflect on your strange experiences, so unlike your life before. When any PC achieves any party goals, every player rolls individually. The players can decide to swap rolls, so the most deserving gets the most experience.

| Goal | How | Xp |
|:---|:---|:---|
| Session | Attend and be a good sport. | 300xp |
| Discovery | Find the Sender's camp and figure out likely leads to the mystery (fuel for the Referee!). | 1d6 x 20xp |
| Victory | Acquire the holy clavis before the Antagonist and get a head start on the Hollow House. | 2d6 x 20xp |
| Survival | Barely escape or avoid a powerful foe. | 1d6 x 10xp |
| Conquest | Defeat or outwit a powerful foe. | 2d6 x 10xp |
| Death | Your PC was destroyed. | 300xp |

You can now invest your experience in characters, pets, powers or equipment (see overleaf)—or save it for next session.

<a name="page_0022"></a>

#### INVEST YOUR EXPERIENCE

_"For we live in a dream that eats the eyes and minces the mind, we who would be human must free our souls through experience, hardfought and well-earned. Not for us the pablum of the dream lords, it is by the sweat of brow and blood of rust we grow free."_ —Screed of the Anti-Intern Atto Vablo, 15:34–38
(Archive of Heresies, Retired, Re-Mines)

You bank your PCs' experiences. Places traveled, parties attended, creepy creatures engaged in dialog, mountains bested, ruins survived, treasures sold for profit, pleasures hunted down and carted off, etc. These experiences form a metapsychic currency (xp) which you then invest to increase the capabilities of your PCs, sidekicks, pets, friends, gear, powers, houses, or nearly anything else that makes sense. Each game object with invested xp occupies a trait or item slot on your primary character's sheet. Yes, your player character is also usually your primary character. PC is thus, conveniently, a double acronym. That said, you can have multiple PCs.

---

**Traditional Levelling**

As is traditional, the Synthetic Dream Machine provides a celestial "ding" sound every time you invest enough xp to level up a PC. Every new level you get a new level (clearly), a new hero die, more life, and the option of either improving an ability score by 1, improving a trait by one step (skilled +3 → expert +6 → master +9), or gaining a new trait (more details in _Vastlands Guidebook_, p31).

> This tabe is the "SDM legacy Leveling model". Each +Level grants other bonuses.

| Lvl | Maximum Hero Dice | Life | Traits or Ability Score Boosts | Xp | Total Xp |
|---:|---:|---:|:---:|---:|---:|
| 0 | 4 | 2 |  | 0 | 0 |
| 1 | 8 | 3 |  | 300 | 300 |
| 2 | 12 | 4 |  | 450 | 750 |
| 3 | 16 | 5 |  | 750 | 1,500 |
| 4 | 20 | 6 |  | 1,500 | 3,000 |
| 5 | 24 | 7 |  | 3,000 | 6,000 |
| 6 | 28 | 8 |  | 6,500 | 12,500 |

---

**Basic Golden Age Upgrading**

_"In this perfect time, everyone is free to be me." —Golden Boy Iäf Taggen, Most Replicated_

Human of Field Mouse Jacaranda

But you are here, at the end of history, at the culmination of time, unbound by tradition, a sovereign individual perfectable in your dream lords' adulation! Why lock yourself to that dinky plan of levelling up? Be free!

You can choose to instead upgrade your characters from their baselines. Take your PC as it was generated and write down all those initial attributes (level, life, ability scores, hero dice, traits, defenses, and so forth) in ink, scoring them permanently upon your character sheet. Uh ... but leave enough room for the upgraded numbers you will pencil in to the side. These inkrusted [sic] numbers and traits are your **base** **attributes** . You will invest xp to improve them as you like, when you like. Because what better way to be unique, like everybody else?

When upgrading your base attributes, you pay the xp cost for each step. So +1 life costs 8 xp, the next +1 costs 10 xp, the third +1 costs 12 xp, etc. The total xpo column sums the costs of upgrading from the base attribute score.

The price of upgrading **levels**, maximum **hero dice**, and acquiring **new traits** is in line with traditional levelling.

> These tables are the "SDM upgrade model". Upgrade each attribute seperately (track how much you spend on each attribute column in each upgrade table).

| +1 Level | +1 Hero Dice | +1 New Trait | Xp | Total Xp |
|:---:|:---:|:---:|---:|---:|
| base | base | base | 0 | 0 |
| +1 | +1 | +1 | 75 | 75 |
| +2 | +2 | +2 | 115 | 190 |
| +3 | +3 | +3 | 185 | 375 |
| +4 | +4 | +4 | 375 | 750 |
| +5 | +5 | +5 | 750 | 1,500 |
| +6 | +6 | +6 | 1,625 | 3,125 |
| +7 | +7 | +7 | 3,125 | 6,250 |
| +8 | +8 | +8 | 6,250 | 12,500 |
| +9 | +9 | +9 | 12,500 | 25,000 |
| +10 | +10 | +10 | 25,000 | 50,000 |

_n+1 = 2(n)_

Hero dice! Gain one d6 HD per session and one more every couple of hours or at referee discretion. Spend and roll a HD to:
- **Adjust any roll**, whether a d4, d20, or d100. This does not have to be your roll. The adjusted roll counts as a natural roll. This is not an action.
- **Regain life** equal to the roll. This is always an action.

> The Daemon holds the Hero dice for all their heroes. They may hold a maximum of their PCs' highest "Hero dice" attribute.

<a name="page_0023"></a>

| +1 Life | Xp | Xp Sum |
|---:|---:|---:|
| base | 0 | 0 |
| +1 | 8 | 8 |
| +2 | 10 | 18 |
| +3 | 12 | 30 |
| +4 | 14 | 44 |
| +5 | 17 | 61 |
| +6 | 20 | 81 |
| +7 | 24 | 105 |
| +8 | 29 | 134 |
| +9 | 34 | 168 |
| +10 | 41 | 209 |
| +11 | 50 | 259 |
| +12 | 59 | 318 |
| +13 | 71 | 389 |
| +14 | 86 | 475 |
| +15 | 103 | 578 |
| +16 | 123 | 701 |
| +17 | 148 | 849 |
| +18 | 177 | 1026 |
| +19 | 213 | 1239 |
| +20 | 256 | 1495 |
| +21 | 307 | 1802 |
| +22 | 368 | 2170 |
| +23 | 442 | 2612 |
| +24 | 530 | 3142 |
| +25 | 636 | 3778 |
| +26 | 763 | 4541 |
| +27 | 916 | 5457 |
| +28 | 1,099 | 6,556 |
| +29 | 1,319 | 7,875 |
| +30 | 1,583 | 9,458 |
| +31 | 1,899 | 11,357 |
| +32 | 2,279 | 13,636 |
| +33 | 2,735 | 16,371 |
| +34 | 3,281 | 19,652 |
| +35 | 3,938 | 23,590 |
| +36 | 4,725 | 28,315 |
| +37 | 5,670 | 33,985 |
| +38 | 6,804 | 40,789 |
| +39 | 8,165 | 48,954 |
| +40 | 9,798 | 58,752 |

_n+1 = 1.2(n)_

Upgrading your **life** scores starts out cheaper, but gets more expensive. The referee may let you upgrade life in increments of +4 at the same xp price as levels and HD.

| +1 Str, End, Agi, Cha, Aur, or Tho | Xp | Total Xp |
|:---|---:|---:|
| base | 0 | 0 |
| +1 | 300 | 300 |
| +2 | 900 | 1,200 |
| +3 | 2,700 | 3,900 |
| +4 | 8,100 | 12,000 |
| +5 | 24,300 | 36,300 |
| +6 | 72,900 | 109,200 |

_n+1 = 3(n)_

Upgrading **ability** scores across the board is a little cheaper this way, but boosting a single score is expensive and best be achieved with a combination of direct ability upgrades and carefully chosen traits that include ability score increases (see the _Vastlands Guidebook_ for over 300 more traits, if that's your marmalade).

This is clearly a convenient way to boost your associated attack, defense, and inventory sizes.

| Improve Trait | Xp | Total Xp |
|:---|---:|---:|
| base (+3 skilled) | 0 | 0 |
| +6 expert | 500 | 500 |
| +9 master | 2,000 | 2,500 |
| +12 phylake | 8,000 | 10,500 |
| +15 builder | 32,000 | 42,500 |

_n+1 = 4(n)_

**Improving traits**

Improving traits is more expensive earlier in your career, but can become an affordable option later on, especially combined with growing through play (_VLG_, p32). Also, a canny character might acquire angelic or even divine aptitude with the right teachers ... or by stealing divine knowledge from the right sidereal forge.

Now for some novel options not available with traditional levelling to cover the remaining attributes on the character sheets: defenses, inventories, and attack types.

**+1 Attack and Damage**

| +1 Defense or Save | +1 Trait or Item | Inventory | Xp | Total Xp |
|:---|:---|:---|---:|---:|
| base | base | base | 0 | 0 |
| +1 | +1 | +1 | 200 | 200 |
| +2 | +2 | +2 | 1,000 | 1,200 |
| +3 | +3 | +3 | 5,000 | 6,200 |
| +4 | +4 | +4 | 25,000 | 31,200 |

_n+1 = 5(n)_

They start out quite affordable and should combine with ability score upgrades for maximum effect. You could also combine them with traditional levelling if you were feeling adventurous.

If you're planning a lot of combat or delving into the ruins of Long Ago, where the ghostly golems dwell, you might want to directly boost your natural **defense** and **save** attributes.

Need more room for traits, mutations, gear, and gold? Just like with defenses and saves, you can now boost your **inventory** sizes directly.

Finally, keen to boost your melee, ranged, fantascience, or oldtech **attack** and **damage** numbers directly? There you go.

Note that all the upgrades on this page could work on your pets, sidekicks, secondary characters, subcontractors, mercenaries, hirelings, and polybody drones as well ...

---

<a name="page_0024"></a>

#### UPGRADE YOUR ITEMS

_"I never asked to be a hero. Yet here we are."_ —#6 Wrench +723bis "the Godbreaker", last survivor of the 2nd Godsmind technédive

Have you acquired a silver lobogolem, living pistol, psychic permutation, or other treasured possession? Let your heroic experiences rub off on your gear.

An oldstyle human would call such gear "hallmarks". One further-fallen from that ideal may mutter about "prizes" or "pretties" or "preciouses".

---

**Traditional Item Levelling**

Traditionally items start at level 0 and you level them up with experience (and material costs at the referee's discretion). So, a level 3 shield might have +3 defense and a level 5 grate hammer could deal 2d6+4 damage and gain a "flaming menace" trait.

> This tabe is the "SDM legacy Leveling model". Each +Level grants other bonuses.

| Lvl | +1 damage per die or +1 defense or new trait | Xp | Total Xp |
|---:|:---|---:|---:|
| 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 |
| 1 | 1 | 300 | 300 |
| 2 | 2 | 450 | 750 |
| 3 | 3 | 750 | 1,500 |
| 4 | 4 | 1,500 | 3,000 |
| 5 | 5 | 3,000 | 6,000 |
| 6 | 6 | 6,500 | 12,500 |
| 7 | 7 | 12,500 | 25,000 |
| 8 | 8 | 25,000 | 50,000 |
| 9 | 9 | 49,999 | 99,999 |

---

**Golden Age Item Upgrading**

The fabricator technologies of this golden age are better than that. Note down your item's **base attributes**, as you would for a character, and upgrade its attributes step by devastating step.

**Levels** are most relevant for vehicles, where they also translate into other attributes (like life and damage scores). Higher level powers impose penalties to their targets' saves. Weapons with levels may count as "magical" for overcoming strange alien resistances to mundane attacks. Other specific gear, such as golem armor in full auto destruction mode, also benefit from levels.

Situationally, levelled gear may also bestow a certain amount of social renown, cachet, and swagger its owner.

The bonus to roll [d20], damage per die, and armor or ward upgrades are straightforward, applying to common attributes.

> These tables are the "SDM upgrade model". Upgrade each attribute seperately (track how much you spend on each attribute column in each upgrade table).

| +1 Level | +1 Bonus to Roll | +1 Damage per Die | +1 Armor or Ward | +1 Trait | Xp | Total Xp |
|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|---:|---:|
| base | base | base | base | base | 0 | 0 |
| +1 | +1 | +1 | +1 | +1 | 150 | 150 |
| +2 | +2 | +2 | +2 | +2 | 230 | 380 |
| +3 | +3 | +3 | +3 | +3 | 370 | 750 |
| +4 | +4 | +4 | +4 | +4 | 750 | 1,500 |
| +5 | +5 | +5 | +5 | +5 | 1,500 | 3,000 |
| +6 | +6 | +6 | +6 | +6 | 3,250 | 6,250 |
| +7 | +7 | +7 | +7 | +7 | 6,250 | 12,500 |
| +8 | +8 | +8 | +8 | +8 | 12,500 | 25,000 |
| +9 | +9 | +9 | +9 | +9 | 25,000 | 50,000 |

_n+1 = 2(n)_

**Traits** is a catch-all category for the kinds of upgrades and features that don't add up together easily, such as:
- area, range, or speed improvements,
- circumstantial bonuses (e.g. +3 in cold weather),
- damage dice boosts (e.g. d3 > d4 > d6 > d8),
- increased charges or reduced replenish numbers,
- reduced power prices,
- size reductions (minimum 1) or capacity increases,
- other unique features (see the _Vastlands Guidebook_ equipment section pp64–93 for a few ideas).

---

<a name="page_0025"></a>

#### GOING PLACES

Rainbowlands adventures are about "going there and back again" without dwelling on researching, booking, outfitting, and packing for travel. We want to unfold the big map, move the party token and plant a flag at each new location. This section provides rules for turning cash into character options, an overview of travel modes, and some event and encounter generators to make travel a little spicier if it starts to drag.

**TICKET DICE**

You’re not interested in how an atomic train runs or how to properly stow cargo in an airship’s sinewy hold. You’re a genteel tourist of taste and, purportedly, means! That’s why we’re introducing three flavors of **six-sided ticket dice**.

**Comfort Dice**

When you need pampering. Each comfort die provides +2 temporary life after a good night’s sleep. You may also permanently spend a comfort die to:
1. Reroll a defeat roll. Your hearty breakfast cushioned that blow.
2. Take a short rest, then recover 1d6 x 2 life.
3. Take a long rest, then remove an extra burden _and_ gain 1d6 temporary life.
4. Acquire a civilized item, such as a nice suit or comfy pillow.

**Protection Dice**

When you need insurance. Each protection die provides +1 to saves against damage to you or your property. You may also permanently spend a security die to:
1. Reroll a reaction roll. Your armature may frighten off would-be attackers.
2. Turn an enemy's critical hit into a regular hit.
3. Wait 1d4 days, then receive a copy of a lost item (terms and conditions apply).
4. Acquire a combat item.

**Speed Dice**

When you need to go-go. Each speed die provides a +2 to chases and races. You may also permanently spend a speed die to:
1. Avoid an encounter before rolling reactions.
2. Roll initiative a 2nd time and get an extra turn this round.
3. Safely escape a fight or catch someone who got away.
4. Acquire an alternate means of transport or travel, such as a drug mule or bicycle.

You can also use ticket dice at your destination, so long as you spend them within the week or before your next trip. At a destination, you can also permanently spend any remaining ticket dice to reroll a carousing roll.

**Buying Ticket Dice**

You buy a **ticket for your week’s travel and accommodation** in advance. Pricier tickets tend to give more dice. Choose dice types at purchase. Dice cannot be changed after your journey begins. All prices per caput (per head). Dice cannot be transferred between tickets. New tickets must be bought every week. If you have experience problems, contact the central human travel bureau [~~restricted~~ violet-coded after the televidy unsanitary incident of Void Lotus XIX].

| Prix | Type | Dice | Conveyances |
|---:|:---|:---:|:---|
| €0 | [murder]hobo | no | how _are_ you traveling?! |
| €5 | basic | 1 | coalem barge, shank's mare, burdenbeast |
| €10 | touriste | 2 | omnibus, land train, coasthugger |
| €25 | specialiste | 3 | bateau, wicker autogolem, pilgrim caravan |
| €50 | premie | 4 | iron horse, oldtech yacht, atomic train |
| €100 | excluse | 5 | friend autogolem, private glisseur, air jelly blimp |
| €250 | recluse | 6 | nightstalker, slow portal, propelled aerolith, road speeder retinue |
| €500 | prefect | 7 | hired airwhale, hovergolem, ministry biovech, illegal sphere |
| €999 | ultraviolet | 8 | aetherial golem, fast portal, aerolith cathedral, cloth of gold processional |

The travel agent nods, “Ah, you have your _touriste_ ticket and your spending disc. See, it glows with cash and promise.” Your grip tightens on your purse. The translucent discs aglow with the Lords’ wisdom symbolize cash. Primitives and barbarians outside the Garden would use it as jewelry. You know better. It means safety.

<a name="page_0026"></a>

#### VOYAGE EVENTS

In the opening adventure, you got to talking with your fellow travelers. Who, how, why, what, where, when. But this is not the only thing that can happen. **Every week of voyaging, roll for an event**. The referee may come up with their own events, too. Tally up days of shorter trips and exploration into weeks and spend them for extra event rolls as needed.

**Foot, Hoof, or Pedal**

Upon the Given World most humans travel by walking, swimming, and flight, as they have since the divine glory of the first MKR machine generated the first humans into this First of All Possible Worlds.

Some humans, dissatisfied with their basic design, use magical machines to carry cargo, venture into the void, or speed swifter than sound. Traditionalists harrumph at this hubris. Some barbarians, ignorant of the common panhumanity of sentience, enslave creatures to serve them. Beasts of burden, combat chargers, even domestic daemons.

| d6 | 1–3 (Common) | 4–5 (Uncommon) | 6 (Rare) |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Gore. A gruesome scene. Scattered on dawn's highway. An accident?<br>[-1 aura _and_ a burden of horror] | Accident. A collision, a road collapse?<br>[-1d6 life _and_ a random item is destroyed or save vs. serious injury] | Monster (L7, absorbing abomination). This thing ... was it ever human?<br>[worth €1d6* x 100 as a trophy] |
| 2 | Sore. The hard path. Injured. A bad sprain, a pulled muscle?<br>[-1 agility] | Injured. A bad sprain, a pulled muscle?<br>[-1d3 life and -2 agility] | Infected. Stonefoot spores, feral land coral?<br>[slow, -3 agility, +2 endurance] |
| 3 | Tired. The long path.<br>[-1d4 life] | Delayed. Boisterous officialdom or mere weather?<br>[+1d4 days] | Closure. The angel bids you take another path.<br>[+1 week or defiance?] |
| 4 | Bored. Reveal something about yourself to your companions. | Robbed. As you slept. Chase the thief?<br>[lose a random valuable item] | Bandits (L2, feral or barbarian). An ambush? A roadblock?<br>[pay 1d3 items] |
| 5 | Amused. This is why the slow road is better!<br>[+1d4 bonus life] | Companionship. A potential friend walks with you.<br>[charisma to recruit] | Shrine. Revelation through erosion!<br>[oldtech site, artefact and €1d4* x 100] |
| 6 | Informed. Who did you meet? What do they say about your destination?<br>[gain +1 to one roll] | Blessed. An automatic pilgrim, an electric monk?<br>[+1 bonus hero die or +1 bonus to one ability] | Help. A healer or a mentor?<br>[remove one burden or a study opportunity] |

<a name="page_0027"></a>

**Autogolem, Hauler Rig, Metal Steed, or Vech**

True, it is tradition that all civilized humans are made with the right to freely journey using vehicles of their own craft. Fortunately, few have either the skills or patience to build conveyances more advanced than a scooter or bicycle.

Machine-made oldtech vehicles were long taboo, marked by the red octagon of agency and restricted to holy servants. Folk tales of foolish youths hacking red-coded vehicles to perform "joy coups" often end with corrective reformatting. Today, the lack of functioning oldtech is a bigger problem. Remaining mechanical vehicles are prized, pampered, and often prayed into full golemic sentience.

| d6 | 1–3 (Common) | 4–5 (Uncommon) | 6 (Rare) |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Bang! Blown tire, fractured casket, escaped spirit?<br>[+1d4 days or -€1d100] | Bang, bang! Pot shots! Bandit ghosts? Monsters? Falschers?<br>[-1d8-1 life _and_ save or the vehicle is damaged] | Road Hunter (L9, mad autogolem). Steel, thunder, plasma lances.<br>[trophy worth €1d6* x 1,000] |
| 2 | Rattled. Shaken, battered, numbed. What terrible seats.<br>[-1 endurance] | Cramped. Contorted, distorted, reshaped?<br>[-2 strength or mutation] | Mind borrowed. Vehicle awakens with a copy of your _ba_.<br>[uh, what the?] |
| 3 | Irradiated. By engine, sun, or shifting time.<br>[-1 charisma or aura] | Thump. Was it a corpse before you hit it?<br>[loot €1d6 x 20 or bury the body?] | Barricade. Militia [L2] seeks the Road Hunter.<br>[+1 week or 1d3 weapons] |
| 4 | Numbed. Something that bothered you fades.<br>[remove 1 mental burden] | Overcharged for spirit fuel. High. The fuel fumes?<br>[+1 week or -€2d4* x 20] | High. The fuel fumes?<br>[burden of elevation and +1d4 life] |
| 5 | Surprised. Living roadside attraction!<br>[€1: gain +1d6 bonus life or an insight] | Hitchhiker. Strange roadside human.<br>[1-in-6 actually a phylake (L6, judge)] | Restored motel. Not a mimic!<br>[1 day and -€1d6* x 10 to restore 2 attributes] |
| 6 | Easy Ride. Share a hard discovery about you or your society.<br>[-1d2 days] | Holy lubricants. Vehicle permabonus. Thanks, gas priests!<br>[d6: (1–4) it gains +1d4 life, (5–6) it gains +1 level] | Wise golem. A mechanic and teacher.<br>[repair one machine or an oldtech study opportunity] |

**Bus, Gondola, Pod, Rail, Tube, or Wire**

Public intersanctuary transport was a blessing given to approved managers and tourists by the Good Gods in the Long Long Ago. Living buses and atom trains and wire golems and pod floaters and more they gifted the humans for their certified travel needs. Alas, time has had its way and now anyone with the cash to spare may board one of the public transporters, whether a holy fool or casteless feral or a fiscally fallen noble.

Cheap, slow, and raucous, the public intersanctuary transport system even yet attracts some tourists.

| d6 | 1–3 (Common) | 4–5 (Uncommon) | 6 (Rare) |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Fight! Other travelers' fists fly. Bottles are drawn (L1, lubricated).<br>[save or you, too] | Impact. _Something_ (L7, scary) under the bus.<br>[-1d4 life _and_ a random item comes alive with an alien spirit] | Ambush. Falscherbarians (L4, eerie) or electronomads (L5, zapping).<br>[your € or your priciest item or your life] |
| 2 | Broken. Cubist chairs, cruel corridors.<br>[-2 agility or strength] | Dead. Thankfully, insurance. But who pulled your plug?<br>[+1 week and -€50] | Modified. A foreign subroutine in your soul?<br>[+1 aura and a ticking trait] |
| 3 | Sleepless. Two nights required.<br>[suffer 2 burdens, sleep fixes it] | Tax. Official local inspection.<br>[+1d4 days and -€5 _or_ just -€20] | Partly digested. The vessel is hungry.<br>[lose a limb or 1d3 items] |
| 4 | Itchy. Lice or mice or seat bugs?<br>[suffer 1 burden, remove with a bath] | Breakdown. Disembark and walk?<br>[+2d6 days] | Ventilation cough. Wheezy, metallic.<br>[burden of disease] |
| 5 | Delayed. Not unexpected.<br>[+1d4 days] | Donations. Or listen to the word.<br>[-€1d6* x 5 _or_ -1 aura and +1 day] | Valuable heirloom. Someone lost it, you found it.<br>[random item] |
| 6 | Friends. Share drinks and dreams and one will help.<br>[level 1d4, 1d3 skills] | Secret voices. The spirit of travel.<br>[-3 ability points to gain a random power] | Visions. A secret or forgotten place.<br>[awake with a key in your fist] |

<a name="page_0028"></a>

**Cargospace & Intersanctuary Express**

At the dawn of time the Lords equipped the human sanctuary settlements with expresses—a system of magimagnetic vacuum tubes and capsules to move cargo and suspended humans from station to station at speed.

Humans traveled in suspension as cargospace is very hazardous to human well-being.

Few moderns now retain the access blessing to travel in suspension, so the intersanctuary express is used almost exclusively for authority-approved cargo. The ingenious humans of these later times use the anti-entropic outer shell of the express as the main highway round the Circle Sea co-prosperity area—the Right Road. Golem buses, solar tricycles, and personal velocipedes abound.

**Access Blessing One — Autosoma**

_Unlock Medical Buildertech, Sacred Pod Charm_

**P:** 2 **R:** nearby

**T:** auld meditech **D:** hours

> Code daemons in your blood speak to the oldtech and announce you as a hereditary "duck mountain prominence". Control healing machinery without the risk of mutations or degradation. Access suspension capsules. Use cold storage as a one-way time machine. **Overcharge:** the healing oldtech deals damage instead. **Note:** you can only store this power in human tissue—in yourself (as a trait) or in a suitable anchor, such as the mummified hand of Dr. N. A. Vec.
