| 2 | More lives. You saw copies of yourself in the Long Ago.<br>[+1d4 life] | Replaced. Died and swapped under warranty.<br>[permanent: +1 life] | Hard rays. Glowing and translucent.<br>[-2 physical, +1 mental ability scores] |
| 3 | Oblivion. You dissolved and dissolved your fears.<br>[remove 1 burden] | Seams. You were stitched back together.<br>[-1 aura, -1d4 life] | Neuroliquefaction. Your brain is an ambulatory amoeba.<br>[-1 life per level] |
| 4 | Nothing. Nothing nothing. The NO thing (L11, null) speaks to you. | Original. You awake with memories of a lost world.<br>[+1 bonus hero die] | Recessive. Devolve back towards your rat ancestors.<br>[-1 thought, +1 agility] |
| 5 | Rehydrated. Feel no thirst for a week. Preach the benefits of Road FluidTM. | Updated. One of your traits was improved.<br>[gain +1 rank] | Possessed. A daemon of your past has replaced your mind.<br>[gain +1 level] |
| 6 | Entertained. You have a hundred vidy stories to tell. | Scrubbed. Shiny!<br>[diseases and parasites removed] | Stars. You see a cosmos of countless stars.<br>[gain +1 hero dice permanently] |

<a name="page_0029"></a>

**The Waters: Bateau, Ferry, Glisseur, or Yacht**

Many rightly humans fear the waters, for they represent that portion of the world given to the cetaceans by the gods. As the old song goes, the sea is a desert with its life underground and an azure disguise above. Restricted from fishing and aquaculture by the pelagic phylakes and alien cetaceans, few traditionalists see much use for the salty watery expanse. Indeed, they would be hard-pressed to see much difference between commercial clans, hexad high-liners, polybody pirates, and feral ferryfolk.

For the traveler, there certainly are differences. For one thing, reputable seafolk won't steal your body.

| d6 | 1–3 (Common) | 4–5 (Uncommon) | 6 (Rare) |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Flotsam. Dead bateau.<br>[-1 aura _and_ a random item] | Hell gull. The bird mugged you!<br>[lose random item or -1d6 life] | Castaway (L6, body-hopper). An ultra or a time-lost wanderer?<br>[€5k bounty] |
| 2 | Great wave. A holy mountain behind.<br>[-1 strength and endurance _then_ save to gain a helpful spirit vision] | Seasick. The stomach rebels.<br>[-1 endurance] | Seaworm (L2, unaesthetic). A nasty parasite. Remove it before it grows.<br>[-1d4 life or -1 charisma per week] |
| 3 | Squall. Rain, thunder, waves, wind.<br>[1d3 random items get wet] | Storm. Blown off course, you dock at another port.<br>[+1d10 days] | Breach. The work of the cetaceans?<br>[+1d4 days _then_ save or shipwrecked] |
| 4 | Fine dolls. Cetacean emissaries track your vessel.<br>[+1 bonus charisma] | Whale killers. They sell mystery meat.<br>[€5, restores 1 attribute] | Undines (L10, moody, pale). They hunt the killers.<br>[trade truths for luck] |
| 5 | Exercised. Ions in the air recharge you.<br>[+1 bonus hero die] | Floating chest. Can it be that old?<br>[random item _but_ save or cursed] | Ghost ship. Looks seaworthy!<br>[haunted but worth €1d4* x 1,000] |
| 6 | Relaxed. The sea airs are medicinal.<br>[benefit from a long rest] | Soothed. Partake of leaked cetacean dreams.<br>[remove all mental burdens] | Contact. A cetacean speaks to you.<br>[will teach friends aquatic traits] |

**The Airs: Blimp, Flapper, Propelleur, or Rug**

Traditional, god-fearing stories say humans are barred from the heavens. That demons and deities claim those high places as their own. That nothing save thin air and dry decay await beyond the protective embrace of Mother Soil and the nurturing guidance of Father Rain. So many of these stories align that there are castes of scholars convinced they were constructed from a single template. This could not be, for it would imply some force or organization meddling with human myth on a grand scale!

In any case, air travel is too expensive and dangerous for ordinary humans and the nobles and scions who may be expected to regularly fly like birds between one city and another cannot be expected to face the same barriers as the less divine orders of humanity.

| d6 | 1–3 (Common) | 4–5 (Uncommon) | 6 (Rare) |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Stuckforce! Detour to avoid the razor fields.<br>[+1d6 days _or_ save or crash] | Long Ago force bullet.<br>[save or lose d6: (1–4) an item or (5–6) a limb] | Razorstorm. Long Ago forces whip the air.<br>[save or crash _and_ lose a thing] |
| 2 | Blinded. By the unhazed light of the upper air.<br>[burden lasts 1d6 days] | Mirrorforce. Shard seeks eye.<br>[save or gain burden: all looks evil] | Devisions. Gremlins infest your optics.<br>[-1 thought _and_ burden: hallucination] |
| 3 | Riders (L2, solar nomads) on the storm.<br>[pay a random item as a guide fee or risk a storm: 1-in-6, see rare] | Aerolith island. It is d6: (1) cursed, (2) infested, (3) mutating, (4) abandoned, (5) fresh, (6) settled. | Killer air whale (L7, angelic). Seeks live food or undead fun.<br>[aerolith-infused bones worth €7k] |
| 4 | Airsick. Too little oxygen? Too much aether?<br>[-1 thought _or_ strength] | Heavy haze. Go slow or get lost.<br>[+1d4 days _or_ save or fly off course] | Green sunburn. Moss blooms on skin.<br>[lose -1d4 attributes, gain +1d8 life] |
| 5 | Air plankton bloom. Harvest time!<br>[+1d4 days to gather supplies] | Noble creatures (L4, grazing pod). Feel uplifted.<br>[restore 1 lost attribute] | Fair angel (L6, harsh). Reads your mind and soul.<br>[save to prove you are good] |
| 6 | Sundogs. Bless these rad puppies!<br>[+1d6 life for powers] | Lost prayers. Pre-approved.<br>[sing to remove 1 burden] | Dragon (L13, alien). It offers solace.<br>[randomly replace a trait or item] |

<a name="page_0030"></a>

**The Void: Bolide, Chariot, Sphere, or Voidskiff**

Modern, civilized humans do not travel to the stars, fast or slow. There is nothing there for the status-conscious. However, those strange outcasts, those voidwalkers who claim to have been there, say many divine machines still sail the dry void. Others say secret portal codes unlock strange places far above the Soil. Then there are the strange dehumans who say they climbed down the Ladder of Heaven itself. What is this, if not mere monkey-tosh?

One thing is sure: humans exposed to the void, beyond the airs of the Given World, desiccate swiftly and totally. Rehydration is expensive (€1d6* x 200) and best performed in a registered meditechnical temple.

| d6 | 1–3 (Common) | 4–5 (Uncommon) | 6 (Rare) |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Hulk. A void vessel from Long Long ago, full of dehydrated protohumans.<br>[enter: -1 endurance and horror] | Horror. We _are_ so small. Nothing.<br>[once: permanently lose -1 aura, after: gain burden of cosmic terror] | The Eater (L17, demilyst). It obliterates because it must.<br>[treasures orbit its maw, to acquire one: save or dissolve] |
| 2 | Cabin fever. There is nowhere to go.<br>[save or lose 1 aura or thought] | War fever. The winds of limbo roar.<br>[save or feel compelled to eat brains] | Gene memory. The shakes hit.<br>[-2 agility and save: gain a psychic trait] |
| 3 | Voidsick. Odd vibrations afflict you.<br>[-1 strength and save or mutate] | Hyperparticle. Losing air or spirit.<br>[spend 1d3 items to repair or run out in 1d4 days _and_ save or mutate] | Insight. _So_ small. Rats in the cosmic corpse.<br>[once: permanently gain +1 thought, after: gain 2 hero dice] |
| 4 | Astral flora. A sargasso of space kelp.<br>[+1d4 days to harvest nutrients] | Protogolem. Its suspended mind, still human?<br>[-1d6 life to restart] | Shell people (L3, soil-hungry). Surfing the void.<br>[suspicious, but will trade] |
| 5 | Silence. No voices but yours. Share, bond, come together.<br>[+1d4 life] | Ghosts. Voices from Long Ago. Follow them?<br>[+2d4* days to reach source] | Another chariot. _Exactly_ like yours. But abandoned.<br>[duplicate an item] |
| 6 | Perspective. _We_ are so small. Specks of dust.<br>[once: permanently gain +1 charisma, after: remove 1 burden] | Recrudescence. Humans were made for the war.<br>[gain +1 strength and an innate aggressiveness] | Interloper (L6, giant). It looks human, but stands 9 feet tall and wields buildertech.<br>[devil? angel?] |

<a name="page_0031"></a>

**The Portals: Dull, Fast, One, Slow, or Wild**

Portals have fascinated humans since prehistory. Some think them gifts from the Lords, others that they are the byproducts of ancient "Engineers." Many simply accept them as fundamental cosmic structures.

These hard-coded passages between distinct locations form hub-and-spoke networks, with portal temples serving for central access.

The dullway protocol dismantles and reassembles travelers, with journey times and capacity varying based on the portal's information density and usage. Welltraveled routes between major institutions can transport up to a hundred people in hours, while smaller village portals may take months to handle a single traveler. To preserve human sanity, most travel gates were once equipped to run pocket realities for their travelers during point-to-point translation.

The Human Wellness Authority maintains that portal travel is completely safe. It claims side effects are very rare, mostly harmless, probably temporary, and the individual traveler's own fault.

Nevertheless, most moderns fear this ancient technology, fearing it may steal their immortal motive sparks. This is not incorrect.

| d6 | 1–3 (Common) | 4–5 (Uncommon) | 6 (Rare) |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Living tunnel. Wailing life-forms smeared into the length of the portal tunnel, enmeshed in its no-being.<br>[save or they consume +1d6 days] | Human tunnel. Generations upon generations built into the walls of this ill reality.<br>[save or join them for +1d4 weeks, then save or stay] | The Dull Worm (L15, waymaker). It connects because it can.<br>[spend +1d4 weeks and 1 aura to find a new place; scavengers and terrors follow behind] |
| 2 | Blanking. Some memories disappear.<br>[save or they were important] | Seepage. Some of you is lost.<br>[lose -1 thought or aura] | Stripped. Soul milled.<br>[save or become a flesh golem without aura] |
| 3 | Emesis. Please clean yourself up.<br>[lose your last meal; hungry now] | Nosebleed. [d6: (1) a second mind enters you; (2–6) cosmetic only] | Illumination. [d6: gain (1-3) a glow, (4–5) a soul, (6) a grim purpose] |
| 4 | Existential dread. This place is not for humans.<br>[alcohol-soluble burden] | Strange gasses. Burp discreetly.<br>[ingest to levitate for 1d3 days] | Odd machines. They live inside you.<br>[feed them power to gain knowledge] |
| 5 | Dull. The way is boring. It feels endless.<br>[rethink a position] | Time. Time dilates. It is endless.<br>[grow older and wiser, or the reverse] | Side. Walk besides yourself.<br>[become more; add +1 to your best ability] |
| 6 | Invigorated. Imbibe the vim of the spaces in-between.<br>[+1d6 life] | Euphoria. You're so happy you could explode.<br>[gain a hero die] | Emptiness. The nothing sets you free.<br>[remove 1 burden and gain +1 aura] |

<a name="page_0032"></a>

#### THE LIST OF ALL HUMANS

_"... Circle Sea power groups consider all close-to-baseline sentient and soulful post-humans as effectively human and possessing the full spectrum of rights attendant to a soul-body-personality triad. This includes retro-humans, dwarfs, half-elfs, halflings, quarterlings, and half-orcs."_
—Ten Long Ago, _A Guide for the Free Visitor to the Caste Oligarchies of the Circle Sea_, Violet University Press, Wind Hyacinth II

You voyage to meet strange people and their ways, do you not? No? No matter, you notice them all the same, all the humans in their ragged finery and strange shapes.

Of old, the gods divided all sentient creatures of this Given World into two groups. Those protected by the Builders’ Blessing, the humans. Those cast out, fair game called beasts. Each human was blessed with a metaphysical jewel in their head. This jewel, called canopic, recorded their mind and soul and dreaming, and made possible eternal rebirth within the Garden.

We need not dwell on how the gods’ folly poisoned relations between humans and beasts.

In these later days, with the Garden’s Dream Canopy torn holefull, with the jewels of rebirth rare treasures rather than ubiquitous organs, all humans must live as though they are condemned to die, like mere beasts of the land. After all, what human living would crack their skull asunder like an egg and sift through their thinkmatter for the threads of biomagical jewelry?

The modernists of the novel sacred-industrial societies would equate the blessing of humanity with the ability of a creature to embrace the coin and commerce of Good Mohlack. The payment of tax and the purchase of credit as the measure of the man.

Yet, traditional communities around the Circle Sea still gather each night to recite the List of All Humans—the pananthropy of the canopic form, to smooth their resurrections should they die before they wake.

In fact, the List of Humans is a combination of two prior lists; that of the _Six Canopic Categories_, which is reliably dated to the A Priori Intermediate Period (2), and the _Eight Manifest Forms_, which are probably best known from the Silver Age of the Heretical Modernisation Empire. The two lists were more perfectly combined in the Revelation of the First High Intern during the TwentyThird Dynastic Stabilization of the Mother Machine (estimated XVIII cycles of years ago).

<a name="page_0033"></a>

_"Without order, all is chaos."_
—Five Rabbit, _Submission to the Demiurge Abaco_, Traditional

In order from lowest, least human, to highest, most human, the blessed finite sapients are determined by the _Green Book of the Six Canopic Categories_:

**Megas**

_from the archaic omega, also: huskfolk_
The least of the humans, those who succumbed to the Fog and forsook meaning for illusion. Their jewels mark them human, though they would live as does a herb.

Few now remain as few towns are rich enough to support their hollow shells as once they could. In the Green Land, some are given sarcotrephs to maintain their bodies until their allotted recycling of spirit and body. In the Orange Land, post-mortal lords use the Megas’ corporeal forms for labor while their minds dwell in the Bliss Lord’s gift.

**Recusers.**

_also: the conflicted, fledfolk_
Some humans refused the Garden Path and chose the Vale of Thorns. They sought meaning in toil and struggle, they averted their souls from the gifted technologies and lived hard lives upon the soil.

Once, the Gardens welcomed those who tired of this path. Now, with the Gardens all grown over, many Recusers, grown harsh over lonely eons, have returned to rule as vampires and warbarians, nomads and heretics.

**Accusers.**

_also: the nemesis, errorfolk_
The gift of the mind jeweled gave Humans a choice: to live in the grace of the Canopy, or to accept the darkness and the lie. The accusers are so-called because they accused the Lords of the Dream of stealing their purpose, their lives, their very cosmos. Most fade, harmless as ghosts, into the Wilderness beyond the Circle, but some remain as fifth columnists in the bosom of the Best of All Possible Worlds, the civilized lands of the Circle Sea.

The kindness of the Canopy extended even to guilty Accusers who vainly attempted to sabotage the Gardens. They were given the Illusion and allowed to live out their allotted years in synthetic pleasure. Nowadays, with the processing power of Heaven much reduced, the Inquisition finds other solutions for Accusers.

**Hammers**

_from the archaic gamma, also: lessers_
The less-blessed humans, whose service to the Path merited their participation in humanity. Once they filled out the serving classes, maintaining the grand designs of the Builders, fleshing out the backdrops of the Lords' pleasure palaces, uplifting their hands in creation.

Most modern humans should probably fall into this category, but with the decay of records, the corruption of canopic amulets, and the lack of accurate timekeeping, many have successfully slipped the net and passed themselves off as other categories of person. Some traditionalists nevertheless try to restore the old order and return the former hammers to their happy place.

**Betters**

_from the archaic beta, also: sickles_
The middle classes of humans, suitably adjusted to the Garden Path, they provide the bulk of the civilized lands’ managerial population. Their life is one of cutthroat competition for status and displays of consumption to prove their worth. This pleased the Canopy and now pleases the Ministry.

Today, Betters provide the human calculating power that substitutes for the dead machines and failed thought generators that once maintained the Circle Sea as a single perfected unity.

**Fines**

_from the archaic aleph, also: lephines, rabbitfolk_
Those humans who have best accepted the Garden into their hearts and are thus blessed by fortune and grace to occupy the finest social positions. All civilized humans would like to be Lephines, but only few succeed. Much sacrifice, conspicuous consumption, and extravagant inheritance are required for this exalted status.

Today, with the Lords all but silent on the matter, local lephines are chosen by various means: heredity, lottery, pageantry, elections, poetry, translational cannibalism, autogolem races, and roleplaying dance.

<a name="page_0034"></a>

_"As there are eight directions to spacetime, so there are eight categories to man."_
—Driving Thorn, _Beyond the Garden Path_, Heretical Modernist

In order from firstmost, earliest human, to lastmost, latest human, the mortal sapients of the Circle Sea are enumerated in the _Silver Book of the Eight Manifest Forms_:

**Iron Humans**

_also: basefolk, sourcelings_
Those following the protomorph of humanity, fixed in body and shape, from the sylphen elfs to the robust gnawers, from the gnomic half-lings to the machinewired cybrechts.

Once, this label applied to those who ostentatiously eschewed the use of canopic jewels and other abmortality oldtech, usually as a show of bravery or zealous faith. This was often seen as an adolescent phase, like education, revolutionary activities, or capitalism.

Today, many recusers proudly tout their iron human credentials. Not to be confused with machine humans.

**Machine Humans**

_also: chalcocephalics, wireheads_
A later, now rare, morph of humanity, which eschews original biology for technomechanical polish.

These sapients combine mind and soul with bodies built from the dust of the earth. Not derived, born, or inherited, but fully created by the generative power of the Builders. Not to be confused with iron humans.

**Ghosts**

_also: ultracorporeals_
A numberless host of humans sought a kind of immortality in the divine dream machine, in the infinite noösphere, beyond flesh or steel. Many forsook even the pretense of a stored body or canopic jewel backup, opting for a completely spiritual existence.

With the slow decay of the universal noösphere, whole ghost lineages have been lost to flawed crystal memory drive updates. Others have escaped the noösphere to become a kind of parasitic consciousness, human daemons given to wearing other creatures' flesh to interact with the Given World.

**Dwarves**

_also: delta labor, dewerkers, maintainers_
Selectively biomanced humans derived from the ancient maintainer castes, they embraced an identity of labor and industry, opposing the leisure mandated by the Garden Protocols.

Some argue that the name is a backronym from ‘de werker aristocratiscee revolutie fraternitie.’ Recent excavations at the Germline Palace, however, suggest their origin might be as ‘DIN War V Engineering Subjects’. Since the excavations are from the stratum right before the so-called “cyan death cloud event”, some rabble rousers suggest a dwarfer hand in that calamity— whatever it actually was.

Whatever the case, these biomanced work-obsessed humans have become a standard morph in these ages of Ministry-guided civilizational reintegration.

<a name="page_0035"></a>

**Golems**

_also: synthetic humans_
Humans who have moved beyond the fallible, decayprone shell of organic flesh and embraced the synthetic likeness of the Great Minds’ ensarcs. A golem’s canopic jewel is cradled in an armored ur-matter core, protecting it from most forms of bodily death. Around it, they wear shells of gold and crystal and stone and liquid metal.

Since the buildertech to make new minds _ex novo_ is now almost entirely lost, new golem minds are usually made by copying existing golem minds, wiping irrelevant memories and resetting them to "factory conditions". The other, less salubrious option, involves taking living human minds out of their existing bodies, but this destructive process often results in neurotic or psychotic golems not suitable for reliable, sustained free labor.

**Liches**

_also: abmortals_
Humans with bodies perfected beyond mortality and decay, the undying, the unending, the perfect. Traditionally, most sensible humans followed the Garden Protocols. They lived in biological bodies but used canopic jewels to maintain a personality backup in case of catastrophic injury.

Now so few remain. In some cultures, to depend on oldtech for one’s abmortality is a mark of cowardice or moral failure. Still, one finds liches, from the oldest houses to the strangest new cult-clans.

**Plastics**

_also: plastifastics, skinchangers_
Some humans embraced the biomantic potential inherent in their sculpted flesh. Through old traditions, dangerous arts, and strange sciences, they turned themselves malleable and impermanent. Protean meat-block humans: made, re-made, changed, and transformed.

They are few in the civilized lands, but beyond, one may find many types of plastics, from the rheosarcs who can adjust their appearance and form to match their tasks, to the impressibiles, who grow into shapes and forms matched to their training protocols. More terrifying are the grotesque falliments and the uncanny ereunts, subjects for illegal biomancers to experiment upon.

**Ferals**

_also: hoy exoy, warbarians, quarterlings_
Strange extra-canopic humans, of different lineages and origins, born or grown in contravention of the Garden Protocols, with neurosystems that cannot support a traditional canopic jewel.

These hylosphere-bound varieties must use complicated devices like dream helmets to access the noösphere. Ferals require a full-body rebuild to enter the Dream Canopy, that walled garden reality the lords reserved as a Heaven for deserving humans.

Ferals usually shunned these kinds of interventions, which proved a decisive advantage when the Dream Canopy permanently shut down for temporary maintenance in the Era of the Snow White Sky.

<a name="page_0036"></a>

#### THE 768 HUMAN LANGUAGES

_Human cultivars develop new languages as horn beetles develop new headgear. After initial experiments in reducing this inefficiency, the Dream Canopy concluded that linguistic and cultural creativity are a necessary condition for Garden human well-being. The babel was therefore discontinued, except on a need-to-use basis._
— fragment, ruined Temple of Involuntary Speech

As you voyage, one of the things you notice is that all these humans and oldtech devices and leftover daemons and stuttering ferals and ghosts of lost times talk, but talk strangely.

The Circle Sea is thick with languages, dialects, jargons, and slangs. Some say this is by design. Who can say? Well, the Mouths of the Babbling God (pseudoheretical) say it is for the benefit of humans, that they be not confused by Hubris or Nemesis.

Fortunately, neither player nor referee needs to perfectly detail this babel of communication. It is enough to have a sense of how it sounds and feels and looks.

**What [How] Good Is Language?**

Once, all humans were born with a language spider linked to their cranial jewel. This ensured all humans could commune perfectly and follow the Builders' instructions flawlessly. It made the distinction between humans and beasts very easy: those who did not speak, the voiceless, were beasts.

Today, with the radiation of languages, even a language spider is no longer enough and beasts may mingle among humans unseen. Tlumacs and other daemons provide sufficient understanding, but fluency in this time of linguistic efflorescence demands study — an expensive pursuit and proof of nobility and goodness.

Regardless, the traveler will usually find themselves in one of three situations:

1. **Mute** or **Unlanguaged.** There is no shared language. A human tries to talk to an elephant, an engineered urk to an elfer mossman, a sentient ant colony to a plastic golem, a book to an illiterate feral. Misunderstandings are rife. To charm another at this level of linguistic incompetence is nearly impossible, to convey mere facts and concepts a struggle.
   For critical communication, PCs must roll a test. Failure may provoke (roll d6): (1) hostility, (2–3) derision, (4–5) laughter, or (6) pity.
2. **Competent.** There is a shared language. Whether this is through study or tlumac daemon intermediation, a living translator or an implanted language. Communication proceeds normally, if without brilliance. Charming an interlocutor requires strange pheromones, inspired luck, obfuscatory hallucinations, or sheer magic.
3. **Natural** or **Native Fluency.** The speaker has invested in their language and it shows. Natives trust native speakers more. Deception, intimidation, even persuasion are easier.
   PCs must have a relevant trait to claim this level of linguistic gilding: oratory, politics, rhetoric, theater, or an upbringing in a mytho-poetic rustic rendition of what the culture holds near and dear (folk hero).

<a name="page_0037"></a>

**Learn Languages Faster**

Few humans in this golden age have the patience, opportunity, or capacity to learn a language the old way with tutor golems and flash scales.

- **Tlumac daemons** are wisps of sentience, simulacra of personhood trapped in physical items and bound to service their owners or lease-holders. Most travelers rent the services of a tlumac daemon when they visit a foreign parochial community for €1d4 per week (depending on the rarity of the language). Buying a servitor tlumac costs around €100 for a 5-language model or €500 for a 10-language type. Typical tlumac forms (d6): (1) amulet, (2) earring, (3) necklace, (4) earworm, (5) jawbud, (6) third eye.
- **Injectable brain-rewiring** is the safe and affordable solution for those who need to acquire linguistic skill fast. Cultural norms, common knowledge, basic humor modules, and stereotypical grievances are usually included. The slow version costs €1d6 x 200 and takes a week to embed. The fast version costs ten times as much, but embeds in an hour. The language-cultural package occupies a trait slot. Side effects certainly do not include (d6): (1) nervous tics and odd facial gestures, (2) altered personality states, (3) numbness and lack of volition, (4) sudden hair loss or repigmentation, (5) language versioning conflicts, (6) pettifoggery and limp-wristedness.

**The Power of Fluency**

Characters with natural or native fluency may (with practice) acquire the following powers as innate traits:

**Hero's Goldenmouth**

Honeyed Words of the Trustworthy One

**P:** 1 **R:** a crowded room or small courtyard

**T:** upstanding humans of your putative culture **D:** until reality forcefully intervenes (then save)

> Pour yourself into your words, dramatic gestures, suggestions, and compelling straw men. After a few minutes of speechifying, spend 1 point of charisma, aura, or thought to charm your listeners. They find you persuasive, trustworthy, and likable enough to believe your 'truths' and give your ideas a shot. This is no mental domination, you are simply showing that your plans are in their best interest.
> 
> _Overcharge:_ charm through a telemagical medium such as vidy crystals or comm portals.

**Adulation Rejuvenation**

Polyempathic Vampirism

**P:** 2 **R:** an arena

**T:** a human mob that likes you **D:** several minutes at least

> Tell a crowd what they want to hear and feed on their adulation, then save. Success: gain 1d3 temporary points of charisma and 1d4-2 life. Fail: regain 1 charisma.
> 
> _Overcharge:_ gain 1d3 temporary points of charisma. _Limit:_ works once per crowd, temporary charisma points cannot exceed base charisma score.

**The Form of Speech**

You've unplugged your tlumac daemon and seek to hear with your own ears what words these humans make? The barking noise of their mad speech sounds and looks ... (roll at least twice).

| d6 | 1 | 2 | 3 | 4 | 5 | 6 |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | harsh | alto | mechanic | detached | repetitive | whistling |
| 2 | melifluous | piano | wet | sing-song | regular | slaps |
| 3 | staccato | forte | cold | hands | novel | psionic |
| 4 | drone | tonal | emotional | expressive | archaic | digital |
| 5 | dry | clicks | ironic | gestural | jargon | painted |
| 6 | nasal | sibilant | literal | tactile | simple | synchronic |

<a name="page_0038"></a>

**The Good Common Speech[es]**

Every traveler will be aware that there are hundreds of human languages in the Circle Sea and many more thousands of beastly languages beyond. Fortunately, every educated traveler knows that little more is required than an excellent apprehension of the Common Speech—the so-called Sermo Comun of the Ministerials.

Sadly, Old Common was last codified in the first generation, while High Common was last codified [error] generations ago; as a result most contemporary vulgar commons are not mutually intelligible.

- **Old Common** (also: Betterspeak, Serme Madraia) is the original interlanguage taught to all first generation humans by the Mother Machines. An optimal, streamlined language for operating in the stem environment of the Initial Settlement of Heaven. Now a dead language, except among several dozen aristocratic circles and retrograde societies that are certainly not important powers in the invisible markets.
- **Un-Common** (also: Ur-Common, Bilder, Dromspreg) is the old-fashioned cousin dialect of Betterspeak, used by the Dream Lords and their agents. Neither streamlined, nor optimal, it is full of bizarre idioms like “break a leg” and “bolt from the blue” that are patently false. It is often found embedded in timelost personalities when these are excavated.
- **High Common** (also: Canopic, Sermirabilie) is the beautiful 17th generation form of Betterspeak devised by the Dream Canopy for Garden humans. It is the standard language taught among the better classes, its melodious vowels, flexible grammar, and luxurious lexicon offering a special status all its own.

**The Vulgar Common Speeches**

There are 768 officially registered parochial dialects and creoles used by the lesser classes and tribes of the Garden. Since they are neither mutually intelligible nor particularly valuable, most dignified travelers prefer to purchase the services of a tlumac or local interpreter, rather than learn these declined jibber-jabberings.

- **Blue Speeches** (also: Blauenstalk, Azulic) encompass the harsh and uncouth dialects of the fallen folks of the Blue Land and its exiles. Writings in these languages are easily infiltrated by mental corruptions and thus suppressed. Their lexicons are rich resources for those interested in fungi, fermentations, dairy, aquatic vegetables and teleempathetic post-human neurological heresies.
- **Green Speeches** (also: Grenspruks, Meraldi) cover both the peasant and forester oral dialects of the inland Green and the glittering neo-common of Metropolis, the Emerald City, with its countless loan words from Un-Common and Bilder. The latter is known for its broad pop-lit corpus and overdone neotraditional handwriting.
- **Yellow Speeches** (also: Saffranian, Polipoliti, Caravanian) cover a range of urban and nomadic languages in the Yellow Land and beyond in the Yellow Waste and Golden Desert. The Caravanian creoles have a mercantile written tradition, flexible structure, and propensity to cant. The languages of the cities tend to be onomatopoeic, with short words and a preference for understatement. Their refined rhyming lends well to written forms and musical theater.
- **Orange Speeches** (also: Oranjetic, Caddic, Proprish) embrace both the colloquial musical dialects of the little mayfly humans of the contemporary Orange Lands with their paltry written traditions and the ancestral chanted forms used by the administrators and grand necromancers of that fertile land.
- **Red Speeches** (also: Raudalandi, RD Cant) include the rough, dwarfer influenced languages of the lesser vintners of that region, the badly-rhyming vulgar and politically charged traditions of the Red Land District, the grinding, dusty forms of the rustlander seminomadics, and the rich, slippery syllabaries of the long-lived bunker-and-blood clans who first liberated that region from the Ill Gods.
- **Purple Speeches** (also: Purapura, Catastrofict) range from the oral hammer tongues of the Purple Land with their steppe and Blue borrowings to the mildly telepathic acat-demese of the Violet University and the uplifted agents of the Cat Lords.

**The Poor Forms**

Barely speech, it is unclear to humans with good source codes and impeccably machined germ lines how these babblish sounds and gestures could possibly function.

- **Feralspeaks** (also: Steppen, Plateausk, Elfen, etc.) is a neutral and inoffensive term used by enlightened betterfolk of the Circle Sea to refer to the related and unrelated 'languages' spoken by out-Garden sentient communities instead of the more loaded expression 'feralshits'. A polite term among the lettered ministerial uplifters is “subaltern dialects of the deprivileged extra-canopic groups”. It is best for humans to use tlumacs rather than bestially deforming their faces to speak in these bestial ways.

<a name="page_0039"></a>

- **Free Circle Kriols** (also: Markanto, Perimse) cover the rhymed disyllabic water tongues of the Circle Sea free families (pirates) and river-travelers (bandits). The lack of a written tradition and idiosyncratic dialects prompt most scholars to dismiss these kriols as a subject of study.
- **Topic** (also: Panpan, Susjarda) is the general term for the barebone pidgins used by unlicensed peripatetic communities formed by the dregs of dissolved settlements and semilegal barbarian refuseniks. Most managers will tell you no topic is worth learning as anyone with a grasp of High Common can give orders to a topical traveler.
- **New Common** (also: Falschic) is a heretical invented language that was definitely not supposed to be an updated and improved 54th generation form of Betterspeak. Anyone coming across its written or spoken forms should report to the authorities for a health and safety inspection.

**The Maintainer Speak[s]**

Long Long Ago, when the machines were first born, a caste of humans was made to keep them glistening and glowing. The Mother Machines bestowed an elegant Newspeak, a streamlined Betterspeak, on these dewerkers. Over aeons maintaining the machinery of the Garden and the golems of the Gods, it has become a family of reasonably human languages, including:

- **Mainttalk** (also: Dwerkfers, Golmtek) is the archaic golem-compatible basic newspeak still implanted in many newly decanted maintainers. Unfortunately, it no longer works on most modern machines.
- **Oltek** (also: 1zvrn, Frygolm) is a collection of heavily feralized Polysolar Dwarfer dialects with a huge golem corpus spoken by wandering relic tribes beyond the Garden's eastern bounds.
- **Volkan** (also: Kemfers, Nonc Golm) refers to the Diesel Dwarfer echolects from the petrochemical generative region of the ungoddess-mountain Vulkana. It has a vast written corpus and the space between characters often carries more meaning than the letters themselves.
- **Winerian** (also: Unfers, Raudakoln) covers the hill and mountain dialects of the Vintner Dwarfer and Red Land industrialists. Derived from the Bunker Builders' jargon and heavily influenced by the Red Speeches, this literalist and linear language has little writing and is much closer to the vulgar commons than other maintainer speaks.

**The Old Codes**

In the beginning was the Word. Before machine or human, semiotes floated in the ooze-soup of potential, fuel for the Maker's Great Speech Act. Fragments of this first language remain.

- **MKR Source** (also: Logik) was/is/will be the language of the word according to the Priests of the Cogflower. It is the magical grammar of the machine-creator of the Given World. Rare humans can grasp a little of this perfect speech and call its utterances incantations and spells. The Builders and the Lords of the Dream Canopy, in their glory, speak MKR Source natively. Heretics say this is the false language of the demiurge, the unconsciousnessmaker, the source of illusion, a darkened mirror of the true Word of the true Creation.
- **Babel** (also: Intermind, Noöphras) is purportedly a human neurology-adapted fork of MKR Source that allows humans to speak directly and perfectly to one another. A native speaker of Babel can understand every form of human speech—if they can also see a speaker’s body language and other subconscious cues. Easily confused with telepathy.
- **Go Language** (also: Golemic, Clicbeep) confusingly refers to the hundreds of forks of machine-speak now spoken by the numerous free and lobotomized golems of the Circle Sea area. Humans can learn to write and read these languages, but the sounds remain beyond them. A properly written command in Go Language may force sentient readers to follow it, whether they want to or not.
- **CAT Astral** (also: Felicithink) is a noöspheric thought-speech extruded into the material setting of the hylosphere. Its formalized logical structure enables empathetic and even telepathic translations of ideas and qualia between separate minds.

Exciting experiments in the Violet University show it has potential for enabling direct mind-to-mind inter-species communication.

<!-- Begin: Our_Golden_Age_03_This_Hollow_House_40-81 -->

<a name="page_0040"></a>

### THIS HOLLOW HOUSE

**Materium**

Give them bread.<br>
Give them circuses.<br>
Give them idols.<br>
Give them gold.<br>
Give them the blessed Muirsedé Ben.<br>
Give them everything they ask for.<br>
—curse on Stele 223 of the Blue God<br>
(Panmuseum archives, Decapolis)

<a name="page_0041"></a>

This second adventure is about character and setting growth and development. The characters will sketch out a new region, discover a new town, and explore an estate that may become their base of operations.

The PCs will also begin to notice the outlines of two meta-factions:

1. **Ministry** — the meta-faction of order. All those individuals and groups and organizations that believe, more or less, that the Rainbow Lands are alright. That the gods' plan, the Garden Path, the Dream Canopy, call it what you will, is good and working as intended.
2. **Nemesis** — the meta-faction of upheaval. Those who are convinced that something has gone terribly wrong with the Golden Age, that the system is failing, that struggle, change, and possibly revolution are required.

**Will and Testament**

The council of elders met in the primary room.

Everlamps lit the old plastic walls and the stackable injection molded chairs squeaked as they shifted on the standardstone floor.

“Thank you,” sang the synthetic voice of Demoiselle Urlaia, comptroller of commerce, as her bulky steel exo body slid into position at the levitating tabletop.

“Of course, always a pleasure to accommodate one so ... fortunately ascended,” murmured Elga fin Telle, the necromancer of laws, her pause perfectly modulated to imply but not confirm sarcasm.

The Demoiselle’s gelatinous features slid about her cartilaginous skull as she floated closer to her exo-body’s forward porthole. It could have been a smile.

“Ladies. Fellow elders,” grumbled Peton the biopriest, a post-human adonis in its latest flesh suit, “Leave the old grudge. We meet to address the departure of a founder.”

“Been a year and good riddance,” sang the Demoiselle.

“There’s no ghost in the noösphere ... calling for relife,” murmured Elga.

“And no idego copy registered with the Dream,” added Iestry, the luminous medium of the canopy.

“Fine. Let’s declare the bastard dead, render unto Garden what is heaven’s, and divy up the rest,” concluded the Demoiselle.

At this point, it is unclear to which of these two camps either the Sender or the Antagonist may be assigned. That will be up to the referee and the players.

As with the first adventure, the referee can play it out step-by-step with the other players, or pregenerate it. In case you are playing it out together, give a copy of pages XX-33 to XX-43 to all the players at the start of the session to help them co-create the session.

Cocreating a setting, a region, town, estate, or faction for the first time is a game of imagination. Don't worry whether things make perfect sense. Over future sessions some facts will naturally cohere together, others will turn out to be rumors, outright falsehoods, or even mistakes. That's alright — a world and a story get built two steps forwards, one step back.

“Things are not so simple, Comptroller. There is a heavy will,” pronounced Peton, tapping the table and summoning a holoform of the missing Sieur X.

“What can his heavy will do? Under heaven, it’s obvious he’s gone and fogged out into the wilds. The law of the Garden is clear.”

Peton nodded, then tapped the table again, his jewel activating the holoform. Motes of air coalesced into a lifelike simulacrum of the ageless X. It looked around the assembled abmortals and a secret joke played in its eyes.

“Dear assembled, old friends. By consequence of service, by dispensation of Red Rubra, this heavy will is weighted to exceed the common law of the Garden,” the holoform paused, “which will doubtless dismay some.”

“The arrogant fool,” whistled the Demoiselle.

“Yet correct,” murmured glow-skinned Ietry, “The phylakes confirmed for me, even an angel confirmed it, the missing Sieur found favor with a Dream Lord.”

“And now, even in his absence, we are condemned ... to his tune,” sighed the necromancer of laws, “Truly, he remains the puppet master of this town.”

"So, the house must be preserved? A time-cyst in the midst of our settlement? A tax on our space and minds?"

"Yes, until my bodyline returns," grinned the holoform.

<a name="page_0042"></a>

#### REGIONAL OMENS

The wise traveler must always look out for signs. Portents. Messages of what is to come, what was, what is to be. There are lessons in the souls and soils we see as we travel. Warnings but also opportunities. Instructions for the questing eye and grasping hand and running foot.

**A Mood Shadows You**

There. An abandoned body farm. Limbs withered in the soil. All but one. A hand, shining like alabaster, grows strong in the big house's driveway of welcomes.

Or perhaps, it is something else ...

| d6 | Sign | Timbre | Shadow |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | absence | horror | violence |
| 2 | ambience | dread | betrayal |
| 3 | scene | tension | theft |
| 4 | item | potential | knowledge |
| 5 | creature | fortune | wealth |
| 6 | person | hope | love |

Does it promise growth amid decay, or is the palm a warning, a statement: stay away? You decide.

**Step Closer, Observe**

There is an **absence** of ...

1. ... birdsong and other small, living things.
2. ... smells, aromas, perfumes, sweet things.
3. ... smiles, laughter, ease, human comforts.
4. ... light, darkness, weight, some physical constant.
5. ... concern, worry, thoughts for the future.
6. ... hunger, woe, the discomforts of existence.

Perhaps it is just the **ambience** of.

1. ... billowing, swelling, heavy, pregnant clouds.
2. ... tugging, ripping, snapping, slapping winds.
3. ... raucous, rattling, creaking, whining sounds.
4. ... viscous, oily, slippery, slithering moisture.
5. ... pernicious, stealthy, dry, whispery miasma.
6. ... nervous, giggling, cloying, anxious pheromones.

No, this **scene** must be the omen ...

1. ... scattered human, semi-human, golem ...
2. ... writing, letters, ten-feet high, blood-red.
3. ... fresh formed soil, plowed, churned, cemented.
4. ... bottled-up houses, plugged-up fabricators.
5. ... gibbet of golems, cackling ghouls bound inside.
6. ... billboards with answers, reading you so well.

There, gleaming by the roadside, an **item** of merit ...

1. ... a red door, painted black, sign of dark changes.
2. ... a bone, gleaming like pearl, promising insight.
3. ... a jewel, plucked from its socket, a key?
4. ... a weapon, broken but rare, a temptation.
5. ... a hat, crown, many pointed, giving direction.
6. ... a book, vidy, memory plaque, guiding true.

Few signs are stronger than a **creature** out of place ...

1. ... hulking radioactive megamorphs, quiet now.
2. ... eagles, vultures, gulls, doves in dire symbolism.
3. ... decadent dire foxes, hounds, base beasts.
4. ... ravenous mice, shrews, little fleeting things.
5. ... rabbits of six-dozen permutations, calling you.
6. ... delectable self-offering fruiting things.

Wait, think, it was that **person** we met, was the sign ...

1. ... the youth with hollow eyes and iron hands.
2. ... the thief with the crescent locks and golden ears.
3. ... the old drunk with the coat of many wars.
4. ... the scrabbling intellectual with the ill tome.
5. ... the vendor of delicacies with the tempting tone.
6. ... the electric piper with the synthetic rats.

Time is soft. Skip back and forth to foreshadow, to offer reinterpretations of past events, to add detail to current circumstances. Lift up a symbol of omen and say unto the players:

"Seeing this creature, this great shadowing gloom dragging its heavy yet translucent bulk among the houses of the well-sleeping burghers, your mind flashes back to that loomscape you passed through on the way into town, where the sleeping megamorph drew you to the windows of your train."

Invite them to replay that scene, their characters' reactions, and thus add flesh to their now.

<a name="page_0043"></a>

#### REGION

Chimes awaken you. Outside, the sun has not yet ignited. The chimes are insistent. The coasthugger slows. Your boat is shunting to a slower, local golem collective-operated canal. The chimes stop once you agree to receive the local visitor guidance.

X marks the settlement. You are passing region [d6].

![Region districts diagram (page 43)](images/page_0043_region_districts_diagram.png)

**Region Guidance**

The authority daemon burbles from the electromechanical mouth with canned enthusiasm, "The region of _Ecc'n_ <ENTER CURRENT COMMON NAME> is an authorized human settlement zone with a diverse and benevolent environment, designed to promote local socio-cultural flourishing. The central settlement area is surrounded by six designated exclusive socio-economic districts." Roll d6 a few times to generate each surrounding region.

| Ecocode | d6 Names | d6 Purposes | d6 <Error>s |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 Ruinland | New Holding<br>Fresh Start<br>Final Rest<br>Eden III<br>Human Town Delta<br>Fort Oublié | rest<br>paperwork<br>overflow<br>dark<br>settled<br>alien | fallow<br>brown<br>forgotten<br>glowing<br>corrupting<br>expanding |
| 2 Roughland | Quarry Gourd<br>Tumulus "Tom Major"<br>Eternal Archive<br>Core Wall<br>Field Baker Bunker<br>High Basil | wild<br>adventure<br>sport<br>leisure<br>hunting<br>exile | barbarian outpost<br>falscher bunker<br>crumbling<br>inorganic pseudolife<br>twisted<br>growing |
| 3 Loomscape | Airmaker Juba<br>Fossilization Engine<br>Fountain V<br>Faber Field<br>Refinery Glad Hand 5c<br>EM Pleasure Nexus | generation<br>extraction<br>reduction<br>modification<br>refining<br>consumption | misaligned<br>shutdown<br>review<br>paperclip optimized<br>infested<br>amber alert |

Looking at the district outside you can tell that this time, at least, the guidance isn't too far out of date. The authority daemon talks about green hills and lush gardens, and you can see brown hills and overgrown tangles of thorn jungle. Aside from some unrecorded ecological shift, the authority daemon isn't babbling complete timelost nonsense.

**The Advertising**

When the guidance finishes you try to look away, but the chimes return, more insistent and annoying. You search for the

[officially illegal] earplugs you hide in your pockets, like every reasonable resident of a Circle Sea town.

The coasthugger lumbers on. Perhaps you'll return and explore. For now, the settlement calls. The house demands.

<a name="page_0044"></a>

#### SETTLEMENT OPTIONS

The distant settlement greets your vessel. It hoots in return. The authority daemon burbles to itself.

You glance about, but all the eyes are dim or dead. You unfold your crude map and prepare to sketch out the town you are approaching. It should be like any of the 768 officially sanctioned Garden towns. Possibly like some of the uncounted off-license towns. (see pXX)

![Settlement grid map (page 44)](images/page_0044_settlement_grid.png)

**Glance, Glimpse**

There! Buildings. Construction. The mark of Human.

| d6 | Mark of Human | Shade of Nature |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | chaotic stain | scarring mountain, hill, or dell |
| 2 | tangled pipes and stacks | crawling over plain, meadow, or agrisector |
| 3 | livingstone grove | reaching for water, cloud, sky |
| 4 | bustling retropolis | clinging to cliff, beach, peak |
| 5 | brutalist order | flouting forest, jungle, or ruin |
| 6 | disturbing geometry | translating the remnants of times Lost this latter humanity |

Roll d6 twice to place the shades of nature on the settlement peripheries (i–vi). If you roll the same periphery twice, expand the shade of nature into a settlement zone (1–8) then roll two more times. Stop rolling once you cover four peripheries with blockers.

Place the human habitation concentration district in the center, as is traditional in officially sanctioned towns.

**Scenery Intercedes Again**

Nature, or its ruderal, transmuted twin, intervenes.

| d6 | Transmute | Substrate |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | tunnels | amber, jade, or fossilized dread |
| 2 | walls | ageless stone, or lifeless greatwood |
| 3 | mounds | earth, memory, or forgotten refuse |
| 4 | efflorescence | thorns, vines, or imperial fungi |
| 5 | clouds | steam, dust, or industry |
| 6 | mirages | good places, lost times, or <ERROR> |

Roll d6 to determine the periphery (i–vi) through which your travel artery enters the map, then roll d8 to find the local haven or station. Draw a line connecting them.

**Look, Look**

Closer now, the bioengines squeal, the signal lights flicker. You grasp the size of this settlement.

| d6 | Size | Performance | POI |
|---:|:---|:---|---:|
| 1 | house, site, readiness | rattling in a hollow shell of ruinland and abandon | 1 |
| 2 | designation, dorp, stead | cleansed, purged, purified, or perfected foundations | 1 |
| 3 | burg, berm, basilica | atop a tell, tol, platform, or mesa | 2 |
| 4 | wijk, mart, outtown | outgrowing its maker, fabricator, or autofactory | 2 |
| 5 | reach, port, citadel | reaching, breaching, stretching to cliff and wall and shore | 3 |
| 6 | city, nexus, clausure | shining, undimmed, rude in its organic posthuman health | 3 |

Roll d40 overleaf for each point of interest you spot. With an illegal pencil stub mark them on your map, assigning them to a settlement zone with a d8. If it falls onto a blocker, or overlaps with an existing POI, roll below.

| d6 | Situation | Circumstance |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | move it to the nearest periphery | ruined, devastated by an ongoing aberrant event |
| 2 | shift its zone anticlockwise | overgrown, absorbed, consumed by an error faction |
| 3 | shift clockwise | abandoned, easy to plunder |
| 4 | split it between two random zones | repurposed, reused, recycled into the urban fabric |
| 5 | keep it where it is | integrated with another point |
| 6 | move it to the central zone | fundamental to the existence and function of the town |

Now add a dirt and scrub-covered hemisphere to an empty settlement zone. Let's call it a bonus POI. Yeah.

<a name="page_0045"></a>

**Your Eyes Alight**

Hooks grab your attention, points draw your interest.

1. Infinite hole ... a down portal into the underworld?
2. Industrial columbaria ... recycling the dead.
3. Zone of Error ... a place of natural alienation.
4. Accreted housing tell ... a millennial town.
5. Slurry pools ... a source of healing and clones.
6. Radiothermal glow ... an oldtech powermaker.
7. Brutalist ape paradise ... a jungle in livingstone.
8. Choked cargo port ... tangled in protoplasm.
9. Red sphere ... a bloody gladiatorial dome.
10. Traditional tunnel town ... for aesthete ideologues.
11. Fountains of nutrition ... formulated food dispenser.
12. Groupmind archive ... for better groupthink.
13. Hanging legume farms ... proteins from the air.
14. Mass-fabripyramid ... identikit biomech homes.
15. Habitation engines ... built to divine templates.
16. Dome of stuckforce ... null-magical shield remnant.
17. Cancerous dormipod growth ... a hive for the lowly.
18. Singing tuning towers ... deep-coded for music.
19. Grand Ago buildings ... subdivided hovel manors.
20. Illuminated scriptorium ... a treasury of oldtech.
21. Glass palaces ... investments of the good ones.
22. Meat apartments ... automated industrial livestock.
23. Landcoral burrough ... a walled cottage complex.
24. Fruitful omega jungle ... a de-extinction navel.
25. Swirling synthetic system ... a golem generator.
26. Sungwood estates ... armored bungalows from seed.
27. Dimensional transect ... a bubble of trapped other.
28. Freetech enclave ... by humans for humans.
29. Baroque chitin wonder ... a floral palace.
30. Elaborated dullway portal ... remnant of tourism.
31. Ladder nubbin ... former fast star anchor port.
32. Elaborate ceramic bridge ... a spiders' way.
33. Repurposed gigagolem ... ominous divine beast sign.
34. Artificial mountain ... dormant fundamental maker.
35. Wide jade canal ... fluids for the synthetic biome.
36. Crater of numinous ethers ... a god's soul spilled.
37. Tethered aerolith island ... higher existence fountain.

40. Weaver of delights ... oldtech all-fabricator cube.

<a name="page_0046"></a>

#### HAVEN

Here we are now. At last. Town. New Home? Temporary roost? Contingent future disaster zone?

Heavy electric hissing fills your cabin. The coasthugger is excited. Charisma overrides click into place.

The authority daemon burbles again, "Please remain motionless in your cabin as the vessel transitions through the Gate of Eyes and enters the Haven of

_Grk-hrk_ <ENTER CURRENT COMMON NAME>. Your material incarnation and possessions will be assessed in accordance with the local socio-cultural Entity Override.

What fun!"

Outside you hear the commotion of passengers scrambling for their luggage and rushing to disembark.

**Tinpot guardians** (L1d4, levidrones) await in the Haven of <ENTER CURRENT COMMON NAME>.

**The Gate of Eyes**

Wait, you actually waited?!

| d6 | It Sees | It Says |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | darkness in your heart | "leave before nightfall, rat." [nocturnal €50 x lvl bounty on you] |
| 2 | crime in your bags | "<INSERTLIST> are illegal." [pay €1d100 x €1d100 or 1d20 weeks of hard labor] |
| 3 | treasure in your wallet | "excess taxable wealth found" [pay 1d6 x 20% of current cash to enter] |
| 4 | error in your writings | "re-education protocols initiated" [report to local Temple of the Mind for 1d4 weeks of mandatory human compliance training] |
| 5 | your face for someone else's | "why, are you not the lord Dun-Dun XVII?" [roll 1d6: (1) mandatory body upgrade, (2–3) volunteered for involuntary carousing, (4–6) assigned a **municipal manservant / spy** (L1d4, obsequious) during your stay] |
| 6 | the agent in your eyes | "be welcome, your secret is mine." [you are granted €25/wk in town] |

**The Haven**

You follow the example of the other humans, grabbing your bags and jostling to get off the coasthugger before the Automatic and PerfectTM Gate of Eyes is wheeled into place by the hollow husks working in the haven.

You get off, look around, and see ...

| d6 | You Meet | They Ask |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | tinpot customs guardian (L2) | "Please with us ... procedure ... procedure!" [lose 1d6 hours] |
| 2 | processed meat-seller VACILLUS (L1) | "Excellent local vat product!" [save: for a week gain +1 endurance and 1 arm; fail: for a week lose 1d4 endurance or bowel control] |
| 3 | rick-wailer Chagrine (L1) | "Enter the cavity and my flesh-runners will take you wherever you need!" [€1d6 to reach any POI] |
| 4 | fighter Tepid Brusco (L2) | "Quick, say I'm one of yours and hide me!" [hunted by Nemesis, knows local protocols] |
| 5 | great magus Penitent Security (L3) | "Curses lifted, purses fattened, fortunes folded!" [20% chance of inflicting a mutation on you] |
| 6 | dark and handsome stranger (L6) | "We've been waiting for you. You have the Clavus, yes?" [hunted by Ministry, agent of chaos, vampire] |

Best wave off all these fools, find a place to stay and get your bearings. There, between the Haven and the Central District, an inn of the better sort. _The Exploits of Espladán._ This should be fine.

The **warrior at the door** (L5, glittering) wears a resplendent Long Long Ago uniform and the laser wand at her hip promises this place will be safe.

The **receptionist golem** (L4, tittering) has seen better days, but its eyes light up when it spots the touriste tickets the Contact gave you. "Ah, the _abitués_ have arrived! We have your standard suite ready. A week is paid, then it will be €70 per week. The standard rate. Will you be hiring a pleasure golem for your carousing?"

**Tinpot Guardians and Other Municipal Order Instantiation Servitors**

These are (roll 1d6): (1) levidrones, (2) sig-monkeys, (3) claydrakes, (4) orbiculars, (5) ka-zombies, (6) plate skeletons.

| d20 | Title | Lvl | Life | Mor | Def | Bon | Dmg | Special (Roll Separately) |
|---:|:---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|:---|:---|
| 1–5 | Watcher | 1 | 5 | 11 | 7 | +5 | 1d4* | Stunner. Set to stun. Save or die on natural 20 attack. |
| 6–10 | Accoster | 2 | 10 | 10 | 9 | +5 | 1d6* | Entangler. Nonlethal. Save or crippled on natural 20. |
| 11–14 | Cleaner | 3 | 20 | 9 | 13 | +8 | 1d8* | Freezer. Save or slowed on hit. |
| 15–17 | Gundrone | 4 | 40 | 8 | 17 | +8 | 2d6* | Decapitator. If damage dealt = target level. Snick. |
| 18–19 | Skullface | 5 | 60 | 7 | 19 | +11 | 3d6* | Alarum. Wails to draw 1d4* additional guardians. |
| 20 | Luminary | 6 | 80 | 6 | 19 | +11 | 4d6* | Sacred germ. Immune to powers, disease, afflictions. |

<a name="page_0047"></a>

#### RELAXATION

A liveried **orimonate servant** (L0, twitch-connected) guides you and your bags to the remaining ascension duct. "The others, they're gnarly, run through, full of eater-bugs," they whisper in an argot halfway between the high common of old read-themselves and some strange, time-lost feralshi. Still, your babble parasite makes a decent go of it and you understand the naïve new-made human well enough.

**A Small Pourbouire**

They hold out an unblemished palm.

| d6 | Stingy | Average | Generous |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | a thin smile [ill luck later] | a thin smile [odd luck later] | a thin smile [meet a duck later] |
| 2 | a curse [save or -1d6 to a roll] | a thought [save or reroll a roll] | a prayer [+1 HD] |
| 3 | a spit [save or the local cough] | a smirk [save: +1 to reactions] | a smile [charisma: make a contact] |
| 4 | a shrug [penalty vs pickpockets] | a shrug [penalty to impress] | a shrug [+1 cha] |
| 5 | a foul name [lose no sleep] | a falsity [learn a bad word] | a truth [bonus vs surprises] |
| 6 | a hurt look [+1 life, str, or cha] | advice [+1d6 to carousing roll] | good advice [+1d6 to reaction rolls] |

With a nod, the liveried orimonate shows themselves out, the old lacquered doors hissing shut behind them. They dropped a card on the way out. It seems to be a pass card for some kind of club. _The House of the Sunken Sun_ ?

**Tempting Distractions**

The _Sunken Sun_ ... that's the inn bar, isn't it?

| d6 | Vibe | Quality |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | dry and dead | no carousing possible |
| 2 | outdated desperation | roll carousing with a penalty |
| 3 | traditional thrum | add aura bonus when carousing |
| 4 | oily, slick, squamous | spend €1d6* x 10 to reroll carousing roll |
| 5 | sharp & sophisticated | double charisma bonus when carousing |
| 6 | beating like a mutated bioheat pump | roll carousing with bonus, then save vs corruption |

It seems lively enough ... what harm could one drink do?

Once per settlement, the PCs can fritter away their treasures on a week of tourism and debauchery. After, perhaps, they earn some experience.

They pick a place to start, look nervously at one another, then down the odd psychoctails on offer. After 1d6*+1 days they roll €1d6* x 50 to see how much of a tab they racked up and roll d20+cha on the fun, fun, fun carousing table.

**Carousing: Pleasures To Experience**

Your mind reassembles itself. You seem mostly intact.

**Fun, Fun, Fun Outcomes (d20+cha)**

| d20+cha | Outcome |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | You have died. Your friends have preserved (roll d6): (1) a copy of your mind, (2–3) your head in gin, (4–6) your body on ice. Gain 600 xp. Relife fee not included. |
| 2 | Locked up for indecent behavior. |
