<a name="page_0048"></a>

#### EXECUTION

After your days exploring the town ... or perhaps after a week of compliance training ... or perhaps after your relife procedure ... or perhaps simply after a god night's sleep. That's the god night. The one night every month that's extended to ensure every month is of a suitable length and that the calendar remains perfect.

Your head is pounding like your mind is being assaulted by a hack-hammer. You look around. It's the ancient contraption by your bed you had thought a curio.

**The Babblebox Rings**

You are nervous around the ancestral device. Usually they are swamped by mad ancestor ghosts trapped in the wires, arguing over strange issues. But this is an inn of the better sort. This babblebox seems to work.

You lift the receiver and interact with the oldtech device. Daemons assail you, but the wards are still strong. Roll with a great advantage this time; but with other archaic devices, you may not be so lucky.

**Taught By Books (d20 + thought)**

| d20 + thought | Result |
|---:|:---|
| 1–3 | corrupted or save vs daemonic possession. |
| 4–6 | save or corruption (roll d6): (1) severe, (2–3) minor, (4) temporary time slip—store a free action for later. |
| 7 | time slip—store a free action for later. |
| 8–12 | suffer to proceed [pay 1 life to access device]. |
| 13 | the device steals 1 ability point then offers access. |
| 14–19 | divine the super-user code that unlocks the infernal device. |
| 20+ | gain advantage when using this specific device in future or you recover a hero die. |

**Guided By Ghosts (d20 + aura)**

| d20 + aura | Result |
|---:|:---|
| 1–3 | possessed by a timelost spirit or save vs corruption. |
| 4–6 | voices fill your head. They are (roll d6): (1) malevolent, (2–3) toxic, (4–6) annoying. |
| 7 | helpful guidance—store a free hero die (HD) for later. |
| 8–12 | pray to proceed [sacrifice €1 to access device]. |
| 13 | listen to the ghosts in the machine and give them the soothing lies they seek. |

You bat away at the ancient voices, the corrupted ghosts in the device's shell, the foul daemons of pre-time drawn from the noösphere by its sacred mechanisms.

| d6 | They Claim To Be | They Are |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | eaters, destroyers, errors | malevolent lies |
| 2 | consumed, afflicted, broken | agents of chaos |
| 3 | lost, trapped, bound | hungry for you |
| 4 | ancestors, apes, players | who you wish |
| 5 | maintainers, servants, protocols | who they say |
| 6 | friends, helpers, angels | better than you |

**Come, A Meeting**

Click. Click. Hiss. Then a voice, modulated and suave. It speaks your dialect like a native, putting you at ease.

"Chaams, good you made it! All your organs in place, ha-ha? Contact Sender said friends, protean geists, but here, you, larval-fresh humans! I am your Executor! All safe, butcher-cut proof, come to the _Smog Louche_ and I'll explain it all. Ask for Half-and-Half, but they'll know you.

The Eyes shared your pictures, hark hark!"

An invitation to the _Smog Louche_ ? Surely you'll go?

**Ask About the Smog Louche**

| d6 | Response |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | "That place has been shut for years!" |
| 2 | "Broken after a raid. Ministry agents. Scum villeins." |
| 3 | "I heard they reopened under new ownership." |
| 4 | "It's a front. Terrorist antihumans." |
| 5 | "Beware, it's riddled with inquisitors." |
| 6 | "If you're going, make sure to take protection." |

**Your Executor Mako Papertoy**

There's a tug at your sleeve, a pat on your arm. You feel comforted by the **pleasure golem** (L4, established) in its lounge cut suit.

"Chaams, you feared, yes! I see it. Thought tricky-trick, snippy-snip and off with your vittles! No, no. This a _civil_ raised place. See, mamba card!"

It is indeed a snakeskin leather card with the word Executor embossed beside the polychrome official glyph of the Authority, six gods spinning in perfect order about the Maker. On the other side, the velveteen smart paper reads Mako Papertoy Level 13 Legitimate Legal along with a truetint holotype of the golem before you.

"I will perform this execution, you see," the pleasure golem flexes, giving hint to the synthetic musculature under its soft outer shell, "and you are the recipients. Oh, I know you have the clavus. But I also know you have the name. And the transmitter in your bloodstream."

**Watching Court**

| d6 | Watching Court | They Are |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | cat-eared quarterlings | rogue inquisitors |
| 2 | archetype humans | barbarian interlopers |
| 3 | union golems | random clumsy tourists |
| 4 | leather ghostautomats | Mako's protection friends |
| 5 | robed cult specialists | local order manufacturers |
| 6 | four-armed agents | turned nemesis agents |

<a name="page_0049"></a>

**The Certification Amulet**

Mako Papertoy L13LL produces a certification amulet, a glinting tablet of bronze and glass and flickerlight.

"The Sphere of Dirt. A sealed estate. Yours."

...

"You look dubious, but it's legit. Sealed with your bodyline, soul and mind too. Butcher Bank certified!"

**The Estate Is Made Out To**

| d6 | Recipient |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | smudged and unclear. *[In a court case, the player who secretly bids the most cash will win. Players can borrow cash from loan sharks to boost their bids.]* |
| 2 | the party as a collaborative hive or co-op |
| 3 | half to the youngest *[age]*, a third to the strongest *[strength]*, a sixth to the lowliest *[pedigree]* |
| 4 | the wisest in the party *[highest charisma]* |
| 5 | the smartest in the party *[highest thought]* |
| 6 | the noblest in the party *[pedigree reference]* |

"It's ready to use. Just take it to the Sphere of Dirt and it'll unlock for you. I suggest you go quickly and quietly. The Sphere's been a ... feature ... in town for a while.

Folks learning there's going to be an unlocking, well ... that'll be a curiosity. A novelty! A mob."

**The Sphere of Dirt**

Sphere of Dirt. Well, the locals have their own names for it. Soulchill Hill, Bleeder's Edge. You approach the archaeostructure. A few locals approach you. Curious.

**These Locals**

| d6 | Locals |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | glitchy vome-infected farmers (L1, secret machines) |
| 2 | hungry vagabond scrabblers (L1, non-citizens) |
| 3 | pernicious ruin-scratchers (L2, scavengers) |
| 4 | suspicious terrace gardener squatters (L1, floral) |
| 5 | post-mortal yellowland escapees (L1, pungent) |
| 6 | bloodbound servants of the clavus (L1, traditional) |

They probably won't do anything. After all, they don't possess any kind of official permit to occupy this estate.

You do. You have the certification amulet. There's the gatehouse bearing the symbol of the clavus, at the foot of the hill. Go on, unlock it. This will be fine.

An agent (L2, somber) approaches on a rusting horse. It shouts, "Wait! Do not get involved! They're using you!"

Who is? And, anyway, look at the size of this estate. Even if you just sell off the land, it will net tens of thousands.

<a name="page_0050"></a>

#### ONWARDS, AGAIN

"This is all a bit much," you think, "I just wanted a few simple adventures."

Butler nods, "Don't worry, Sieur's Chosen, I'll gladly run the estate for you. Ensure nothing goes wrong in your absence. Maybe you'd like a small holiday at Babylon Beach to recover? Drink some riviera reactors and ogle the flamingos. I hear their wings are beautiful in the light of the local flickersun."

"Can we drive there?"

"I'm sure they'll let you take your autogolem through the visitors' gate, why not?"

"We'll go right away!"

"Then have some needle tea and to-day's document of novelties, while the servitors pack your bags."

**A Surprise In Your Bags**

| d8 | Item | Item | Item |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | ash biscuits | psychic salts | philter of hate |
| 2 | bone coins | smelling pepper | prophylactics |
| 3 | black vertebrae | doghead soap | storm feathers |
| 4 | undead cat | psionic fungi | timelost hat |
| 5 | mimic repellent | living parchment | vibrant € card |
| 6 | golem bait | electric owl | heretic gold |
| 7 | silkerchief | clockwork sheep | divine toenail |
| 8 | postholy water | android blood | the anticlavis |

"Use me," reads the cryptic label.

**Document of Novelties**

It would be a dead world if things did not happen in the background, yes-no?

| d12 | Place | Faction | Goal | Action | Outcome |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Blue Land | Butcher Bankers | claim lands | daemonic infiltration | pyrrhic victory |
| 2 | Purple Land | Cogflower Inquisition | dominate markets | public agitation | unintended alliance |
| 3 | Red Land | Green Son Apocalypse | spread beliefs | pseudolegal raid | internal schism |
| 4 | Orange Land | Populist Levellers | develop neoldtech | psychic propaganda | collateral awakening |
| 5 | Yellow Land | Ministry of the Dream | gain legitimacy | covert sabotage | oldtech backfire |
| 6 | Green Land | Perfect Rational Army | monopolize resources | recruitment drive | martyrdom cascade |
| 7 | urban region | Dewerker Hexads | control population | fortification project | demographic chaos |
| 8 | suburban region | Vampire Knights | recover lost secrets | research initiative | psychic contamination |
| 9 | rural region | Sailing Island Pirates | restore environment | ruthless purge | knowledge corruption |
| 10 | ruderal territory | Timelost Ancestors | settle old score | sacred ritual | economic crash |
| 11 | wasteland | Barbarian Liberation Front | transcend limitations | economic warfare | ecological disaster |
| 12 | wildland | Nemesis of the Garden | preserve status quo | necrolegal overture | crude success |

<a name="page_0051"></a>

**Consequences, Again**

The autogolem ... Wait, you do have an autogolem, yes? If you don't yet, perhaps you should spend some time exploring your estate? There are said to be unknown places beneath many of these old time-vaulted mansions. Surely the Departed Sieur has left some very loyal living device for your percurration?

Right, apologies, distracted. You sit back in the living seat (slightly reanimated) at the back of your cartingolem and the slightly mildewy servitor slips you some jay needle tea and the day's document of novelties.

You marvel at the contrast a small fortune makes to one's outlook on life. As you sip the tea, the ultra jay courses through your system, granting you +1 charisma and immunity to gater sickness. Just €250 a dose, you recall.

Roll a save and see how you are now:

**d20 Something Changed**

| d20 | Something Changed |
|---:|:---|
| 1–2 | Puffed Up. All your luck is the result of your own hard work. Fools call you arrogant and conceited. Permanently lose 1 aura. Anytime you critically fail a social check, your target despises you and will hurt you if they can do so at little cost to themselves. |
| 3–6 | Spendthrift. You hate haggling and are only too happy to overpay by at least 100% to show off your success. When you overpay a significant purchase by 500%, gain +1 charisma (max +5). You can remove this trait once you are broke. |
| 7 | Humbled. Your fortune comes with responsibility. Every time you tithe 10% of your income, remove one mental burden _or_ temporarily gain +1 defense. |
| 8–12 | Carefree. No longer will you have to worry about every little purchase. A weight lifts off your soul. Gain resistance to anxieties, worries, fears, and other malicious enchantments. |
| 13 | Hubris. This proves you are destined for better things. Gain +1 to all defenses, saves, and d20 rolls. However, foes strike a critical blow against you on 19–20 from now on. You can remove this trait after suffering its negative consequences three times. |
| 14–19 | Learning about yourself. Gain 1 pip towards acquiring or increasing a relevant trait. Probably a bourgeois social background trait or something. |
| 20 | Secrets in Your Source Code. Something in your blood whispers to you of destinies and secrets. Gain +1 endurance. When faced with an oldtech or fantascience artifact, you can sacrifice this trait to gain 1d4 pips towards acquiring and/or increasing a relevant trait for using that artifact. |

**Experience, Again**

These few weeks here, in this new town ... this has been different. These experiences seem almost dreamlike now ... perhaps this is what it means to live in the good graces of the Dream Lords, blessed by this golden age?

| Goal | How | Xp |
|:---|:---|---:|
| 2nd Session | Attend a second time. | 350xp |
| Theater | Play along with the omen, ham it up, make others laugh or groan. | 1d6 x 25xp |
| Invent | Each contribution to the shared setting; fleshing out the region, the settlement, and other details. | 2d6 x 10xp |
| Carouse | Go and waste your cash partying. Double if you suffer a silly mishap. | 100xp |
| Confabulate | Escape a tricky situation using an elaborate false narrative. | 100xp |
| Explore | In detail an area, building, zone, or district. Double if you discover and extract something special. | 1d6 x 25xp |
| Survival | Escape or avoid a mighty foe. | 35xp |
| Plumb | Enter the bubble of old surface and explore at least one area or zone. Double if you extract a precious heresitech artifact. | 2d6 x 25xp |
| Conquest | Defeat or outwit a mighty foe. | 70xp |
| Death | Your PC was destroyed. | 300xp |
| Die | Or otherwise lose a PC in a hilarious, memorable way. | 500xp |

Excellent! More experience to invest in characters, pets, powers and equipment. Truly, you are growing as a player. Soon, you will be a powerful puppet master, a daemon willing your PCs onwards to terribly hilarious dooms and tribulations! Mwahah ... um ... ahem.

<a name="page_0052"></a>

#### ESTATE FLOWERING

Hush. Shake off the agent. Warnings? From some ruster tramp in an agent's old-fashioned coat tails? Here, step to the cyclopean gatehouse.

**The Gatehouse of the Clavus**

A one-eyed ancient, mummified beneath their silver weave robes and electromagical bandages, detaches from the scabrous livingstone encrustation. Their temporal pod crumbles, releasing them into the now.

"I am Butler. You bear the certificate, the bodyline and the clavus," it intones in old common, the betterspeak,

"Release the seal and you may have my guidance along with the estate of the Departed Sieur."

**Bonus Specialty**

| d6 | Bonus Specialty | Lvl | Fee/wk |
|---:|:---|---:|:---|
| 1 | timelost languages & scrolls | 3 | pound of flesh |
| 2 | master of curses & afflictions | 3 | tub of blood |
| 3 | intuitive biomancer | 3 | intact skull |
| 4 | experimental chirurgeon | 4 | blue jewel |
| 5 | daemon summoner | 4 | golden egg |
| 6 | mummified legal knave | 5 | €25 |

"Is Butler my title? Why no, it's my name."

**Break The Seal**

"You may want to hurry. I sense someone approaching. I can legally protect you. I think." chants Butler.

The seal is an oldtech device. It looks like a variant of a gate seal, but adapted. Someone might wishfully say improved. It looks a little dangerous (see babblebox).

1. Click. The clavus unfolds like a clockwork flower. 1d6 rounds pass.
2. The gatehouse sloughs off its rocky layers, revealing a timelocked shell. Waves of cold explode from it. You are safe inside, but any crowding locals? Fresh corpsicles. 1d4 rounds.
3. The Antagonist arrives. They keep their distance. Nervous? Excited? Hard to tell. 1d3 rounds.
4. The hill ripples. Wavers. Then falls into itself, like a young man's face disintegrating into a skull when struck by *Aspera's Chronic Affliction*. 1d2 rounds.
5. Rippling explosions flinging dirt and dust, rock and tree, as nihilation barriers obliterate the falling hill. The PC with the lowest charisma saves or is impaled by a bolt of mistledoom wood.
6. The dust clears, revealing a field of debris and one house standing, sparkling under its nihilation aura.

"Hmm ... it has been longer than intended," muses Butler as it surveys the ruined estate.

**The Rubble is Alive**

The debris field writhes, settles, burps, shifts ... the things within are put out by their new situation.

| Roll d10 | Encounter |
|---:|:---|
| 1–2 | **Glutinagas** — (L3, jelly authentics). Malleable gelatinous worms of great size, prodigious appetite, and utterly failed control routines. Leave them alone to digest the rubble. Maybe they will go away. |
| 3–5 | **Scuttlemonks** — (L1, automatic cultists). Three crabs in a trenchcoat with a prayer wheel and a feather duster. Mostly crushed. Seem to have operated the estate? |
| 6–7 | **Protean Postlagomorphs** — (L2, bioadjustable). Swiftbreeding rodents intended as raw material for biomantic work. They haven't gone feral, just grown very big. |
| 8–9 | **Heresitech Plants** — (L3, infestants). These vegetables shouldn't be here, with their (roll d6): (1) wriggling traps, (2) spying eyes, (3) memetic leaves, (4) hypnotic flowers, (5) judo tendrils, (6) cybernoxious taproots. |
| 10 | **Sleepers in Orange** — (L5, magisterial). Not quite angels, more like angels-in-potential. Statues of marbled stone, prone to coming alive when signal and blood combine. But what signal? Do you dare cart these heavy things off? |

<a name="page_0053"></a>

#### A SIMPLE ESTATE OF MIND

The house and its estate are the PCs home base, but also a shared character for the players.

Butler looks about with its one eye, "Yes, the neighborhood has gone downhill, but then hasn't everywhere ... hmm ... well, perhaps we shouldn't say that out loud, should we? After all, official chocaine rations have gone up seventy-three times since they were first introduced ... hmm ... Long Ago. If someone could do basic mathemagic, you'd be eating three times your body weight in chocaine per day."

The eye twinkles when Butler notices your alarm, "Don't worry. This is a gentry class house. See those walls? Bunker Era construction! Hey, House, how many ghosts in your shell?"

Bioluminescent signals pulse in the walls and Betterspeak code dimples protrude for added emphasis.

Butler nods, "That's right. Just the one daemon. Old House. You still mad about being locked up in that time sphere by the Departed Sieur? Don't be ... you didn't miss much. Just night after night, flood after flood, and the ... well ... didn't miss much. Seems the humans are about to be interesting again."

Butler stops and grabs you with a surprisingly strong mummified hand, "You will be interesting, won't you? I think the times call for it, yes."

[![Estate map (page 53)](images/page_0053_estate_map.png)](images/hires/page_0053_estate_map.png)

<a name="page_0054"></a>

**The Estate Berubbled**

"Yes, the whole sphere of the dome belongs to the house. Though, ah, much of it seems buried now. And the rabbitherders may be upset at all the rabbits killed when you used the clavus to collapse the seal..." says Butler.

**Gatehouse.**

Not actually part of the estate. It is owned and managed by the Butler Watcher LLC BDD.

**Geigerfac.**

A sleeping autofac that used to make geigers ... or was it gigers? Anyway, some kinds of gizmos. With a brain replacement, some ancient lubricants, and a bit of sprucing up, this could be a tidy earner. Please ignore the biohorror (L9, human-derived) stalking its halls.

**Hollow House.**

A manor in the echobrutalist style. It belongs to you. You can rename it.

**Folly Ziggurat.**

Ornamental, not meant as a real ziggurat. Claimed by the scuttlemonks as a real ziggurat. Could be turned into a real ziggurat with some faith and paint.

**Obscure Structures.**

Possibly intended for some kind of bioindustrial activity. One still promotes NEW chocaine. Another suggests the new shade of the season will be taupemarine, a hue that famously bankrupted the Ivy Saint Bistecca procedural fashion conglomerate emirate, which led to the downfall of the Circle Sea Union Mk 2.

**Pit of Descent.**

Level-locked by daemons blood-coded by the Departed Sieur. The bloodbound servants of the clavus claim it leads down to heaven and want to rent it.

**PyramytombTM.**

A time-traveling tomb bought from a Long Long Ago catalog. It's empty and waiting for you.

**Servaparts.**

High-density hive for storing unneeded servants. Perhaps some are still stored here, but the broken **lotus dreamgiver** (L7, font of pablum) fills the whole area with comforting delusions.

_(more locations described overleaf)_

So far we've been handwaving time and travel at destinations. That's generally fine, but sometimes we'll need to keep track of time more carefully. Perhaps the PCs need to reach a specific NPC before curfew, or they only have three hours to search a ruin. Here are some suggested time frames for moving about, from local to regional:

- ⚙ **Within the house** (or in another building). Moving from room to adjacent room takes one round. Let's say a minute. Actually doing anything useful in a room takes roughly five (5) minutes.
- ⚙ **On the estate**. Moving from building to adjacent building takes five (5) minutes. Doing something meaningful in a building takes roughly fifteen (15) minutes. We're abstracting the rooms away here.
- ⚙ **Within the zone**. Moving from location to adjacent location takes fifteen (15) minutes. Performing a useful action at a location takes an hour (60 minutes). We're abstracting finding the right building and room.
- ⚙ **Within the settlement**. Moving from zone to adjacent zone (or periphery) takes thirty (30) minutes. An action within a zone takes two hours. We're abstracting moving around, finding the location, then the building, etc.
- ⚙ **Within the region**. Moving from district to adjacent district (or settlement) takes two (2) hours. Taking action there consumes four (4) hours. That makes it a whole watch (6 hours) to go to another district and do a thing.

<a name="page_0055"></a>

**The Good Neighbors**

Mobs of puzzled scuttlemonks and upset locals keep one another at bay at _your_ garden gate. A fluffle of postlagomorphs is grazing and defecating on the lawn.

**Cold Turtle Pond.**

Home of the **millennium turtle** (L7, 1-way time-traveler). Lovely landscaping. Mind the lotus.

**Eremite's.**

On moonless nights, the **flickering avatar** (L2, electric) of the godless eremite manifests to read scripts.

**Feeder Canal.**

Full of **feeders** (L3, amphibious). They feed.

**Heresitech Grove.**

The baobabs offer to tell you what you want to hear in exchange for life and worship.

**Lesser Inn.**

Used to accept motor vehicles, but in these fallen times only takes bicycles, velocipedes, and mules.

**Locals, The.**

Former Extramural Vagabond Settlement 7. Now legalized. True name restricted to residents only. Please don't say the **farmers** (L2, augmented) are vomes.

**Lost Neighbor.**

Missing since a star-summoning event. Portals do not work here anymore. Nor other magicks. Do not dig up the buried **golems** (L3, doomed).

**Memory Farm.**

Can't afford immortality? Give yourself to the **Extrangling Fig** (L10, mind-eating tree) and talk to your descendants even after death!

**Mutagenic Well.**

Clearly marked as dangerous. Severely corrupting. Don't fall in. The lid will be repaired soon.

**Orchardite.**

Cherry cabbages, gilded peaches, glowing berries, a **mechanical gardener** (L4, rusting) and its **loving maintainer** (L2, technohuman).

**Slumprabbit Pipe.**

Due for repair. Leaks **protean postlagomorphs** (L1, lamarckian). Harmless, yeah?

**Viridian Pavilion.**

Property of the **Lady of Waters** (L6, liquid human). Occupied by **liberated post-mortals** (L1, mummified). Is the lady actually the water in the canal?

...

Just then, before you've even visited a single neighbor, you spot the executor Mako Papertoy approach on a chair carried by two headless lobogolems. It grins, as if expecting something.

"Houssler chaams! My, my, done good! You have my mamba card, yes? Rememberings, yes? The tax priest is coming, holy holy to the Invisible Hand, good Abaco. You're ready, yes? Inheritance tax? A small retainer. €10 per week, and I'll assure the tax priest won't bescam!"

Butler rolls its one eye, "The tax priests are still about?"

"Oh, my, yes! But kind, soft now. No rack blood sup!"

<a name="page_0056"></a>

**Bubble of Old Surface**

Error. You are not supposed to be here. This surface is no longer rated for human settlement.

**Arcolocontrol.**

An overshoot upwelling of HeavenTM, it seeks to take control of the Cube of HTM and siphon its human minds downstream to HeavenTM. Do not question its designs. Why is it leaking? Why is its dome cracked? Why are its **messengers** (L6, death angels) mummified, with twitching wires coursing through their papery flesh?

**Biomatter Oversight.**

All the control consoles are broken.

**Buried Ruins of Lago Lago.**

Ignore these cyclopean walls, these promethean technofossils. An archaeologist would only grow discouraged to know that the Old Surface was not the Oldest Surface. Do not release the demon **Pilot Samoroga** (L9, nemesis hero). The demon is not related to the gods. Do not trust its lies.

**Cavern Turtles** (L8).
Big as boats, six-flippered, spitting.

**Cliffs of Living Stone.**

Oh, look, the landcoral has escaped its programming and is eating the subsurface to make more of itself. This will surely never be a problem.

**Clingmeat Trees** (L5).
They cling. To meat. With thorns.

**Cube of HTM, The.**

A livingstone residential-commercial complex now haunted by its doomed ghosts?

**Dream Weaver** (L9).
Totally not an illusionist dragon.

**Feral Servant Hive Levels.**

The brain-locked **servant humans** (L0, feeble) have survived in the dark by becoming a **metahuman organism** (L13, super-posthuman). Please don't let them out.

**Fossil Rabbit God** (L17).
Nothing short of an apocalypse will wake it. In the meantime ... divine biofuel?

**Glutinaga Levels.**

Ah, so that's where the **jelly worms** (L3) are generated from the pipeworks. Perhaps a different protocol could generate other jelly creatures?

**Great Tap Root.**

It flows with the fuel of life, with deep biomatter. It whispers, "heaven is down, always down."

**House of Changes.**

Here dreaming lies the **Lady of Waters** (L16, original human). Why is she 10 feet tall?

**Lake of Blind Turtles.**

It's really full of all kinds of armored beasts. Bobbers. Chargers. Lurkers. Hurlers. Stringers. One's boat cannot but go thump-thump as it moves.

**Levitant Substations.**

Aerolith? Down here? Valuable! Oh, also, controls the pipeworks.

**Lostgarden Levels.**

The corpse of the **phylake Antipater** (L12, angelic) clutching a flaming sword is worshipped by the uplifted rabbits (L1, postnuclear) who have made an idyllic garden lit by the godlight of Antipater. They sacrifice humans to keep the holy corpse aglow.

**Memetic Escape.**

**Strange ideas** (L2, daemons) flutter like butterflies, escaping the garden that generated them. They teach new things. Terrible things. Things not meant for humans. Burn them and deliver their charred corpses to the administration for rewards (€500 per corpse).

**Pearleater Levels.**

Ragged splendor and baroque chambers. **Waxy humans** (L4, mannequins) eat the pearls of the holy **tentacled oysters** (L7, chronotoxic) to survive until the path down to heaven opens up.

**Rabbit Pipeworks.**

A slurry of protean rabbits. Some are fossilizing and turning into oil.

**Sleeper Subapts.**

Stored **archaic humans** (L3, very tall) stalked by **psychic safeworms** (L5, many-legged).

**Scaverdwarf Levels.**

These blind **subterranean humans** (L3, scavengers) are assembling a time-ark that will let them sleep until HeavenTM climbs up to save them.

**Scuttler Burrows.**

These **crab people** (L2, horrovores) are not monks. They feed on horror. And flesh.

**Spy Pikes** (L2).
These fish do not seem to belong, what with all the metal and silicon in their brains.

**Sunken Teahouse.**

Strangely colourless and textureless. Decayed signs announce the arrival of the late **Dee Elsie** (L?, error). The patrons are **crystalline simulacra** (L0, repetitive) who call soggy wood shavings tea.

**Timelost Boat.**

Light as balsa, hard as adamant, powered by a golem engine. Worshipped by the cavern turtles.

**Well-Lit Levels.**

**Shadow humans** (L4, vampiric) still selling the shiny baubles and dire fashions of Long Ago.

**Wrigglemind, The** (L13, funny guy).
Oh, here's the fungal core-mind that keeps this bubble habitable?

**Wriggling Isle.**

**Glittering mycelium** (L3, sticky) threads the isle, inventing eternal dreams for the Lady.

<a name="page_0057"></a>

#### RUNNING ESTATES

If cash is the petty coin that hammers and other proles spend to keep themselves in bread, the estate (Σ) is the wealth that gives and keeps giving. The land and bonds, stocks and cryptids, digital daemon tokens and other arcane promises. Illiquid assets.

Estates come in different sizes, and all healthy humans want big wealthy estates. So teaches the Cogflower.

![Estate properties grid (page 57)](images/page_0057_estate_properties_grid.png)

- ⚙ **Humble Estate**. Worth €5,000. Generates a revenue of €5 per week (€5/wk). Enough to scrape by.
- ⚙ **Small Estate**. €10,000. €10/wk. Enough for a whole family of pauperlings.
- ⚙ **Middling Estate**. €50,000. €50/wk. Enough to live comfortably in a middle class neighborhold.
- ⚙ **Fine Estate**. €500,000. €500/wk. Upper class life.
- ⚙ **Grand Estate**. €10M. €10k/wk. The minimum to call oneself a proper baron.

You will find estates are excellent money sinks. After all, the key to more extravagant adventures is a bigger estate! And, clearly, an estate can never be big enough. As the old folk faith song goes, "make number go up to the moon." Academics disagree which moon the song refers to, as there are at least 17 easily visible moons.

**Properties In Their Variety**

One could keep estates abstract. Numbers kept in arcane ledgers by strange daemons and deciphered by the noöspheric ghost essences of the sulphurous priests of Mathic Abaco in their clock-tok zero-one temples.

One could. But that would be awfully trusting. No, far better and safer to trust in soil, for land alone gives birth to that net product which can be called the wealth of humans. Thus spake master Turs Quay Nay Shtra.

There are thus four categories of estate:

- ⚙ **House**. Your castle. Where you live, grow, learn, pray, entertain, shelter, bunker, recover, and revive (if you have a chamber of living waters).
- ⚙ **Property Present**. Lands abutting and controlled by your house, where you can extract maximum revenue from the souls chosen to serve you.
- ⚙ **Property Absent**. Far away lands, administered for you by conniving, untrustworthy agents.
- ⚙ **Property Abstract**. The aforementioned numbers in arcane ledgers. Barely comprehensible. But very low maintenance. Please do not look behind the curtain.

Your starting estate, by the wisdom of the Sender and the generosity of the Departed Sieur, includes a house (see Domus Nova, pXX) and properties present.

Ah, a harsher referee might have started you out with a smaller estate, but we have what we have. Turn the page and attend to properties present, absent, and abstract.

<a name="page_0058"></a>

**Properties Abstract**

By the glory of the Dream, wealth may be abstracted from the crude matter of this world and held entirely in the mind of the Lords. "Fiat divitiae!" cry the daemons.

- ⚙ Invest €1,000 in the butcher bank or another entity to gain revenues of 1 cash per week (+€1/wk) in perpetuity.

Your abstract investments are completely safe. Honest. The referee is totally not making a secret annual roll.

| d00 | Public Event | Secret Horror |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | rational disincorporation | Colleague, your assets have been volunteered to promote the cause of the new popular rational republic. Be joyous! |
| 2 | zombie bank run | Turns out they hadn't covered your deposits ... uh ... it's a race to your nearest branch office to get your cash out. |
| 3 | unnatural proliferation | Your assets have been quarantined until the ERROR is contained. Care to venture into the vaults and help root it out? |
| 4 | natural disaster | Flip a coin. Heads, your assets are fine. Tails ... |
| 5 | ministry shakedown | Perform a quest or the Ministry has a claim to 50% of your property. |
| 6 | phylake intervention | Your invested cash is safe and totally really there. |
| 7 | ancestor sacrifice | Roll d6: (1) actually, your investment fell by 20%, (2) it fell by 10%, (3) stayed the same, but no cash withdrawals for a year, (4) unchanged, but revenues are down 20% for a year, (5) all unchanged, (6) revenue up by 10% for a year. |
| 8 | ornate occult ritual | see 7 |
| 9 | public murder | see 7 |
| 10 | licentious scandal | see 7 |
| 11–95 | Growth has once again exceeded expectations! | — |
| 96–99 | Growth has actually exceeded expectations. | Investment and revenue grow by +10%. Hurrah. |
| 00 | Toil extracted from outgarden subhumans benefits shareholders, including you! | Investment and revenue are doubled. That's +100%! Yay! Also, you receive a free servitor. |

**Properties Present and Absent**

Lands! Here or there. If they are here, you can run them yourself! If they are absent, you had best hire an agent. Upkeep will be required when things go wonky (p59 XX). But other than that, it'll all be fine, yes?

Your starting properties present are an estate of eight plots, covered in rubble. They have a value of €40,000 but bring in no revenue. Clearing each plot costs €1d10 x 1,000 and takes 1d8 weeks. Rented to a tenant, each plot then brings in revenues of €2d6+3 per week.

You could upgrade those basic plots with additional revenue-generating facilities.

| d8 | Property | Value | Revenue |
|---:|:---|---:|---:|
| 1 | sump potato farm & farmbob | €5k | €5/wk |
| 2 | lagomorph hatchery collective | €10k | €10/wk |
| 3 | houseseed nursery | €20k | €20/wk |
| 4 | luminous valov orchard | €40k | €40/wk |
| 5 | blacklight lotus ponds | €100k | €100/wk |
| 6 | beastmass proliferation center | €200k | €200/wk |
| 7 | certified blood vineyard | €500k | €500/wk |
| 8 | biomatter-to-energy conversion and re-education facility | €1M | €1k/wk |

Rolling once a year should be enough, right?

**Running the Estate**

| d20 | Result |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | Disaster! Pay the bank 50% of the estate's value. |
| 2–5 | Failure. No revenue from the estate next year. |
| 6–10 | Partial success. Earn half revenue from the estate next year. Or, uh, take the tenants' seed crop ... |
| 11–15 | A good, standardized, normative year. Earn normal revenues from the estate next year. |
| 16–19 | Look at you, managing that estate so well! Earn +25% revenues next year. |
| 20 | Blood from a stone! +100% revenues next year. |
| 21–25 | Beautifully done. Add 25% to the value of the estate and earn +50% revenues next year. |
| 26+ | As above, but you've also turned a tenant, sharecropper, or uplifted member of the local fauna into a skilled and loyal follower. If you like, they'll serve you as an agent on the estate for free (ignore the small and reasonable sum they pocket from the profits). |

Referee! Obviously don't pull the wool over the PCs' eyes. After all, there must be some kind of rules in place to prevent powerful actors like the referee from abusing ordinary heroes with pump and dump schemes, scam cash schemes, and other cryptic ponzi rituals, right?

Selling properties is just about as fiddly as selling houses. Generally, you can expect to take a small loss on the value (after all, it's a golden age, so all the prices are always dropping, except the ones you need to pay!) unless you're lucky (charismatic) and skilled. See the Selling Your House section for a table (p52-XX).

<a name="page_0059"></a>

#### DOMUS NOVA

The Antagonist approaches. With a gesture, their doghead goons hang back. Hand up, chironomic gesture for peace and words. There are witnesses. If the Antagonist were to break their honor now, there would be expensive repercussions.

"This is your house now, eh? Well, the clavus has done your part, eh? I'll buy it off you right now. Fifty thousand cash. Set yourself up comfy, free to enjoy the leisure of this town. Lander gentry, eh?"

The Antagonist looks around. Nervous? Angry? Excited? Worried? Flustered? Surprised? The emotions flicker, like they are trying them on. But ... there's no one there.

Their attention snaps back to you, "I'll be back soon. I hope you'll be ready to sell. Won't get a better deal and then they'll be all over you."

Whether you take up the Antagonist on their offer, roll d20 in each column as required for your new casita, dormicile, house machine or what is it.

| d20 | This Your House | Color | Pretty Feature | Rooms (Usable/Total) | Refurbish (€/room) | Rental Revenue (€/room/week) |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---:|---:|---:|
| 1 | stackpod cargo cluster | beige | biomass eater | 0/10 | €10,000 | €1 |
| 2 | servant hive dormicile | black | carniflora | 1/3 | €9,000 | €2 |
| 3 | DemeterTM human dwelling hut | brown | ceramic scales | 2/3 | €8,000 | €2 |

<a name="page_0060"></a>

#### HOUSES

Domesticity is the mark of civilization. Are you civilized enough to own a house? If you own no real estate, are you even real?

**Bones of the House**

This section (dissection?) lays its rooms bare for your occupation, refurbishing, specialization, and upgrading. The room is the core segment of the house-as-character, its inventory, if you will. Each room has two main attributes: its **revenue** (if rented out) or its **expense** (if maintained).

Note that "room" is an abstraction. It might represent a single room, or it could be a suite of chambers, a warren of burrows, or a mass of livingstone bubbles in a bowl-house.

![House room grid (page 60)](images/page_0060_house_room_grid.png)

**Usable and Unusable Rooms**

Some of your new house's rooms may be unusable, gone to dust over the nameless aeons (several years) in the house's protective bubble field.

"No! That is a lie! There has been no decline whatsoever. Any troubles are mere temporary disasters. The living mosaic will be reactivated shortly," crackles a voice from the speakmouths integrated into the walls.

**Usable** rooms are (roll d6):

| d6 | Condition |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | haunted |
| 2 | musty |
| 3 | dusty |
| 4 | fussy |
| 5 | overstuffed |
| 6 | quite nice |

You can rent these rooms out or upgrade them.

**Unusable** rooms are (d6):

| d6 | Condition |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | cracked open |
| 2 | fire-damaged |
| 3 | water-logged |
| 4 | rotted |
| 5 | gone feral |
| 6 | corrupted by error |

These rooms must be refurbished before you can rent them out or upgrade them into your quarters or a special room. The refurbish cost is set by the local autonomous repair servitor guild union and takes into account available materials and skills.

Refurbishing a room to make it usable takes 1d6 weeks. Upgrading a usable room into quarters or a special room takes another 1d6 weeks.

**Expanding Your House**

Total rooms are all the rooms the original shell of the house was designed for. To build additional rooms, the autoarchitect recommends a new (d10):

| d10 | Section |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | cellar |
| 2 | wing |
| 3 | courtyard |
| 4 | floor |
| 5 | annex |
| 6 | section |
| 7 | conservatory |
| 8 | solarium |
| 9 | outbuilding |
| 10 | tower |

This extension will take 4d6 weeks to build and add 1d6 rooms at 1d6 times the price of refurbishment per room.

**Renting**

Renting out a usable room is a great and safe way to earn money! Your tenants are sure to be great and reliable people! You can invest €500 to reroll how much rental revenue a room can earn for you. An increase may require evicting tenants who won't pay up (1-in-3).

Perhaps your tenant NPC is a ...

| d6 | Trade | Bent | Quirk |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | student | surly | sarcophagus |
| 2 | soldier | cheerful | void parasite |
| 3 | clerk | secretive | blood debt |
| 4 | performer | proud | regal heir |
| 5 | merchant | nervous | heinous crime |
| 6 | artisan | eager | vile treasure |

**Selling Your House**

It takes 1d30 weeks to close your sale. Make a charisma roll with relevant deception and marketing skills.

| d20 | Sale Price |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | House confiscated under asset forfeiture laws. |
| 2–6 | Bad market, bad sale. Earn 1d6 x 10% of value. |
| 7 | Sale fails. Earn +25% if you succeed next time. |
| 8–12 | Reasonable sale. Earn 2d6 x 10% of value. |
| 13 | Sell for 150% of value. Buyer feels cheated. |
| 14–19 | Good sale. Earn 3d6 x 10% of value. |
| 20+ | Proper property flipper. Earn 200% of value. |

<a name="page_0061"></a>

**Your Quarters**

How you live defines how others see you and directly impacts your adventuring effectiveness, how long you live, how likely you are to get sick and even whether you die. Quarters are a proxy for your lifestyle. You can turn any usable room into quarters by paying the requisite price. When you improve or reduce the quality of your quarters, the lifestyle benefits take 10 weeks to manifest.

Your new house has 1d4 rooms (but no more than its usable total) set up as quarters. The quarters are (roll d6): (1–2) humiliating, (3–5) frugal, (6) comfortable.

If you **share quarters** with your friends, like in a household, commune, polybody hive or labor-unit hot bunking system, you only occupy one room of the house and reduce your expenses by 30% (rounded down) per body. Of course, this does mean living together. And you know how loudly redlanders snore. High-altitude adaptation and all.

| Quality | Lifestyle Effects | Price | Expense |
|:---|:---|---:|---:|
| Quarterless | You sleep in a ruin, hole, or ditch. You scavenge for supplies, tap nutrislurry ducts for food, and wash yourself in rainwater. At the start of every adventure save to see if you are sick. Oh, and subtract 1d4 life per level (no minimum, careful). | €0 | €1/wk |
| Humiliating | You cannot have nice things. If you want toilet paper, you cannot go out for a coffee. If you want shoes, you can't get a haircut. If you want vegetables, you won't have a coat. The tradeoffs are constant, and grueling. When you go on an adventure, start by subtracting 1d4 life per level (minimum 1 life per level). | €100 | €5/wk |
| Frugal | If you don't go on holidays and avoid any unnecessary expenses, you can just about make ends meet. To adventure, come as you are. | €500 | €10/wk |
| Comfortable | You can participate as a full member of society, go to the opera, enjoy promenades, have a bit of cat's whisker in the evening, buy books, and afford some basic health insurance. When you go on an adventure, start with 1 bonus life per level. If injured, you can get one limb or organ replaced every 10 weeks. | €3,000 | €30/wk |
| Luxurious | You are welcome everywhere. Doors open when you flash your vantablack status card. You rarely have to pay for anything, since your credit is so good everywhere. On adventures, start with 1 bonus life per level and 1 immunity die per level (works like a hero die, but only for resisting daemons, diseases, and other ill effects). If killed, you are revived in your rack-ready clone in 10 weeks at no extra fee. | €25,000 | €150/wk |
| Paradisiac | You get the best of everything because, obviously, you are the best. Daemons and servitors cater to your every whim, tone your body and mind while you sleep. Start adventures with 2 bonus life per level, +1 to all physical abilities, and 9 immunity dice for resisting afflictions. If killed, seriously injured, or annoyed, you can transfer your conscience into a backup you in 1d4 days at no extra fee. | €333k | €999/wk |

<a name="page_0062"></a>

**Twenty Special Rooms**

Now, quarters are all fine and dandy, but perhaps you'd like something more interesting than a posturban fortified conapt for yourself and your henchlings?

Besides the particular **benefit** a special room offers, it also has an installation **price** (in addition to any cost for refurbishing a decrepit or useless room) as well as a maintenance **expense**. Special rooms may be _betterbuilt_ for 10x the usual price, offering increased benefits.

A character must spend a week's relaxation action (pXX) using a room to gain its special benefit. The benefit occupies a trait or inventory slot on the character's sheet (yes, the vehicle and item benefits, too). Replacing the benefit with another trait, item, or burden wipes it off the sheet. Regaining it requires another week's relaxation action.
