<a name="page_0064"></a>

#### CASH ASSETS

_Property makes a proper person._ —traditional saying, Yellow Lands

What is property? It is a relationship between subjects and objects, between people and things. The thread that connects care and labor with the world physical. The law that divides scarce resources. The narrative that makes the world useful.

It is how you prove that you exist. It is the shackle that binds you to this Given World. It is the resource that fuels your ambitions.

Every proper rainbowlander knows what cash (€) is. The twice-barred "c". Liquid assets.

- ⚙ €1 = An unskilled human's day wage.

Cash is an abstraction for the different kinds of bills, coins, cards, cheques, and credits that the humans of the Circle Sea Civilizational Megaregion use in their daily truck and barter.

**Spending Cash**

Cash is your most versatile social resource. Credit crystallized. You spend it to buy gear for your adventures. You use it for fines and bribes, food and tickets, hotels and guides. Anything, really.

In play, you can get by without tracking coins and credit when something costs much less than a day's wages.

**Investing Cash**

Crucially, you need cash to become a better person, because the more you are worth, the better you are.

This is obviously true. Everyone says it, even the Mother Machine.

The secret to having a lot of cash is to be very wealthy. The way to become wealthy is to invest your cash in your properties, where it will be fruitful and multiply and come back to you by the mysterious workings of the Invisible Hand. Praise Mohlack (but discreetly)!

**Mortgage**

You can mortgage your properties to get quick cash.

- ⚙ Reduce your revenue by €1/wk and get €500.

It will probably cost €1,000 to pay off a €500 mortgage. Hope you invested that cash well. Like in a profitable trade adventure.

<a name="page_0065"></a>

**Revenue**

Revenue (R) is your cash flow before expenses. It's the amount of money you imagine you could have if you were a creature of pure light, who didn't need air or water or food or shelter or a social life.

The simplest source of revenue is your estate, but it can also come from other sources like titles, tributes, tithes, contracts, and other nifty rent-extraction schemes.

Tales say that once, when the Dream Canopy was untattered, every human received a cash each day to consume as they liked. Some say this was a lovely time.

Nowadays, when dragons no longer fuel furnaces, some grovellings and many of the plebeian sort must trade their given time on this Given World for cash. The unskilled and shiftless earn €7 per week, but master servants of earn up to €60 per week or more (p57).

**Expenses**

Expenses (E) is the cash that leaves your accounts every week, like grains of emerald sand pouring through your fingers as you try to hold it together while the jade dragon's visions assail your sanity.

As with revenue, your estate is the source of most ongoing expenses. Your quarters and lifestyle, specialized rooms, rented machinery and more. However, you can incur almost infinite expenses, such as wages for followers, fees for experts, gifts to worthy causes, and other generous status-enhancing efforts.

Fairy stories say how once, when the sky was full of more stars than one could count, humans had no expenses or obligation other than to sing, dance, and make poetry in the Garden of Delights—not to please some distant Lords but to entertain themselves. Other stories say these were not humans but those creatures now called Viles.

**Income**

Income (i) is revenue less expenses. This is how much cash you actually gain per week. Your disposable income.

Revenue (R) - Expenses (E) = income (i)

Go on. Go wild. Spend it on something nice, like a longsword or a classic cinematic vidy or maybe that fancy hat you've wanted for a while.

Income increases your cash pile. If you need a large amount of cash to go on an adventure, you can simply spend some time accumulating cash, let the world-clock wind along, seasons come and go, events happen, and then finally go on your adventure.

Of course, time will crumble your collections, visit illness and indignity upon you, and kill everyone you've ever loved. But, hey, trading time for money is still worth it, right? Right? Or you can just **get a loan**. The terms you get depend on your status in the community.

- ⚙ **Nobody.** Get €100 and increase expenses by €10/wk until you repay the full €200. Wait, what?
- ⚙ **Disreputable.** Get €200 and increase expenses by €5/wk until you repay the full €300.
- ⚙ **Ordinary.** Get €300 and increase expenses by €3/wk until you repay the full €400.
- ⚙ **Reputable.** Get €500 and increase expenses by €2/wk until you repay the full €600.
- ⚙ **Wealthy.** Get €1,000 and increase expenses by €2/wk until you repay the full €1,100.

_Attention: actual loan rates determined by local butcher banker branch. Please avoid loans from hexads, self-organized co-operative syndicates or secret societies._

This page is sponsored by the Cogflower Chamber of Commerce, your ally in eternal growth and progress.

Are you a high-net-value sentience, individual, or distributed consciousness? The CCC has the experts to ensure your eternal moral-economic worth.

- ⚙ Necrolegal services to keep your good fortune regardless of your current mortality status.
- ⚙ Sacral accounting & advocacy systems to save you from meddling tax and customs apparatchiks.
- ⚙ Act-of-god grade insurance to perpetuate your physical existence in perpetuity.

If you are a candidate for CCC services, submit proof of worth at your temple of communications today!

<a name="page_0066"></a>

#### REST? FOR THE WICKED?

You take a deep breath and start pondering what kind of time-lost vintages the Desiccated er... Departed Sieur may have left in the drawing room drinks cabinet. Something to celebrate perhaps.

Then ... then there will be plans to make. Places to explore. Rooms to renovate. Friends to invite over. Enemies to sabotage with your new-found wealth.

Perhaps you will even find an uplink scroll of _Summon Seaside_ and the lords and unlords, the gods good and gracious, will see fit to drown some neighborlands and raise the value of your real estate.

**Weeks At Home**

When not adventuring, the usual baseline human PC effectively does three things each week: **sleep plus two other activities**. With the proper high-line drugs, a human PC could probably replace sleep with another productive activity, like painfully sculpting their mortal shell to conform to the desires of faceless noösphere daemons for a chance at fame and fortune.

Conveniently, the tasks a PC faces would never overwhelm their ability to deal with them, right? Wrong.

It is the human lot that weeks are mayfly-brief, eye-blinks that tease with possibility when Moon Day rolls around and torment with dread and regret when Solar Day swivels back into view. But that is for later.

So, what do adventurer landlords fill their weeks with?

**BED REST**

Broken from their adventures, they hide abed, tended by twitchy golem doctors and beset by haunting mothering voices in the walls. Bed rest precludes _all_ other activities (except sleep).

A resting character normally fully restores one missing or damaged attribute each week. They may regain all their missing life, or fully restore one damaged ability score, or remove one burden or similar affliction.

A character **resting in their bed at home** restores **two** missing or damaged attributes each week. The sense of peace and prosperity that comes with owning a home promotes faster healing and recovery.

Special rooms or home improvements may provide additional benefits.

<a name="page_0067"></a>

#### RELAXATION

Pleasurable activity that builds up mental and physical resilience, and removes some burdens or afflictions.

[Self]-improvement may combine with relaxation. After a week of relaxation roll d20 + endurance or aura.

| d20 | It's All Fun And Games Until ... |
|---:|:---|
| 1–5 | Acquire expensive new "hobby". It occupies a trait and costs €10 x level to indulge for a week. After such a week (d6): (1) lose d6 x level life, (2) lose your clothes, (3) lose 1d4 burdens, (4) make a new friend, (5) gain 1d4 temporary HD, (6) restore all your mental abilities and remove 1 burden. |
| 6–10 | Refreshed. Restore all your endurance or aura, _and_ gain +1 temporary life. |
| 11–13 | Invigorated! Restore all your endurance or aura, _and_ gain +1 temporary end or aur. |
| 14–16 | Smooth. Remove a mental burden or affliction, _and_ gain +1 temporary end and aur. |
| 17–19 | Wired to eleven. Remove a mental burden or affliction, _also_ gain +1 temporary agi and thought. |
| 20 | Reset. Remove a mental burden or affliction, _and_ gain +2 temporary bonus to an ability. |
| 21–23 | Uplifted. Remove a mental burden or affliction, and gain a resilience die (d4). Note the resilience die as a trait or item. At any point, you can roll the resilience die and remove that many burdens or afflictions. You can only have one resilience die at a time. |
| 24–26 | Fortune-marked. Remove a burden or affliction, and gain a second chance die (d6). Note the die as a trait or item. When you are reduced to 0 life or would be killed, you roll the second chance die and end up with that much life. |
| 27+ | Personal or spiritual insight. Restore all your endurance and aura, _also_ permanently gain +1 end or aur. |

Special rooms or home improvements may provide additional benefits.

#### UPKEEP

Estates require work. Food must be cooked. Rooms refurbished. Servitors supervised. Tenants terrorized. Butcher bankers paid in flesh and flattery. Most incidents (pXX) or nuisances (pXX) can be handled by proper upkeep. Roll d20 + any relevant skills you might possess.

**... Taking Care of Stuff**

| d20 | Result |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | Not only did you not take care of it. Things are now somehow ten times worse. |
| 2–5 | Failure. €15 to hire a trades-servitor and fix your mess. Try again next week with a penalty or hire a master of labors to fix things for €1d6 x 50. |
| 6–10 | Partial success. One more week of fiddling and puttering around should do it. Roll again next week. |
| 11–15 | Fixed. Doesn't look too bad. Not going to win any prizes, but it does the job. |
| 16–19 | Good job. Whatever it was, it's handled. This problem won't be back. The chrome mold will surely not eat any more chickens now. |
| 20 | Not only is it a good job, you've learned something! Gain 1 step towards learning or improving a trait. |
| 21–25 | Beautifully handled. You've increased the value of your property by 1d6%. |
| 26+ | Not only have you increased the value of your property (see above), you've turned the butcher banker or the terror taxmonk into a valuable and well-disposed contact for future adventures. |

If you are wealthy enough, you might hire an agent or representative to deal with upkeep for you.

- ♟ _No Body (€0/week)._ You really need a body to handle upkeep. Roll d12 to see what happens. No bonus.
- ♟ _Local Schmuck (€10/week)._ Local is a personal name. Honest. Makes a d20 roll for you. No bonus.
- ♟ _Perspective Naftofosfat (€20/week)._ A handy aide who will roll with a +3 skill bonus.
- ♟ _General Utility Jonesie (€40/week)._ An expert right hand orimonate who rolls with a +6 bonus.
- ♟ _Butler Primula Manastir (€80/week)._ A true majordomo who can handle most eventualities better than you ever could yourself (+9 bonus).

<a name="page_0068"></a>

#### IMPROVEMENT

Whether yourself through study, your pet through training, or your estate through cash, becoming better takes action. Action and time. Action, time and luck.

First, write down the trait you wish to acquire or improve.

Second, figure out how many successes you require.

- ⚙ To gain a **simple, common trait**: 3 successes. Perhaps a typical skill, such as riding a bicycle, or a common estate upgrade, such as vidy screen walls.
- ⚙ Gain a **complex** or **uncommon trait**: 3d2 successes. Running an estate, from bookkeeping to human resources exploitation, or installing an oldtech privacy field to keep daemons and phylakes out of your house.
- ⚙ Gain a **background** or **rare trait**: 3d3 successes. Learning to live and move like a local barbarian, or training your pet to access the human-level kaaugmentation routines in its source code.
- ⚙ To **improve a trait one step**: 3d2 successes. This might progress your or your pet's trait from skilled to expert (if relevant), or increase the effectiveness of a trait of your estate or vehicle or item.
- ⚙ To **improve a trait a second time**: 5d2 successes. Progress a trait from expert to master, or boost another trait to its ultimate limit.

Mark the required successes on your character sheet to fill out after successful improvement attempts.

To attempt an improvement, you require resources. These may be sources of knowledge, such as mentors, memory bones, or vidy crystals. They could be liquid truths, injectable reflexes, or biomechanical implants. They could even be songs for sungwood house, or stone manipulation protocols to grow a new livingstone fence.

A resource secured, dedicate a week to improvement and make a thought roll (d20 + tho).

| d20 | Progress At Any Price |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | No. This will not happen. You hate this. You will never gain or improve this trait. |
| 2–4 | Fail to make any progress. _Also_, the new concepts shake your core. Suffer a burden, injure your pet, or damage your property. |
| 5–10 | Fail to make any progress. But, you're making an effort! Feel proud! Gain +1 temporary life. |
| 11 | Fail to make any progress _unless_ you sacrifice something personal and meaningful. |
| 12–17 | Success! One success! One is infinitely more than zero. Be happy! |
| 18–19 | Success! _If_ you sacrifice something personal and meaningful, make that two successes! |
| 20 | Two successes and +1 temporary life from pride. |
| 21–24 | Two successes and you can tailor the trait to better fit your character and needs. Perhaps it benefits from a different ability score or has a different flavor. |
| 25+ | Two successes ... three, _if_ you sacrifice something very personal and meaningful. _Also_, adjust and improve the trait to your character and taste. If you like, you can even name it after yourself—especially useful if you're trying to internalize a new power and fancy calling it something like _Astral Diogenes' Forcefield Barrel of Force_. |

At home, **you can make two attempts at improvement each week**—unlike in the field, where you would only be able to make one such attempt per week. Heck, with high-line drugs, you could make three attempts!

If you fail to make any progress, you can try again a second time with the same resource. If you fail a second time, this resource will never work for you.

**Improvement Resources**

Roll d10 and d8 if the resource is safe, d10 and d10 if it might be cursed. This resource is found (d6): (1) a quest away, (2) far away, (3) guarded, (4) next town, (5) in town, (6) near here. A sufficient amount costs €(1d10 x 1d10 x (1d8-1)) or €100.

| d10 | (1–2) Mentors | (3–4) Knowledge | (5–6) Tools | (7–8) Materials | (9–10) Error |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | purged oligarch | antentropic tablet | electric microscope | memory ooze | reality-freezing |
| 2 | aged scavenger | stone book | bonded golem helper | ur-obsidian | soul-rippling |
| 3 | tireless academic | vidy crystal | flesh sculptor | golem clay | radiologically active |
| 4 | maintainer priest | injectable poem | focal autopurifier | livingstone | highly addictive |
| 5 | heretic inquisitor | blood song | antimemetic suit | beast egg mass | toxic to humans |
| 6 | barbarian savant | memory bone | biomech implants | stuckforce | memory altering |
| 7 | falscher sapient | biomechanical brain | liquid reflexes | ghost bone | personality lathe |
| 8 | uplifted animal | cogflower archive | stonelife rod | carving stone | holon duplicator |
| 9 | post-human wisp | pulpwood manual | soul-brain interface | butter metal | time draining |
| 10 | electric cetacean | infectious dream | florawakeTM trowel+ | aerolith | hue bleeder |

<a name="page_0069"></a>

#### LABOR

Is your estate too small to grant you a respectable weekly ration of bread, water, air, and fire? Then you may have to suffer the indignity of work to secure a sad pittance of revenue that will keep you clothed and appointed in accordance with the humble expectations of good society. Yes, it is embarrassing to admit, but even a hero of leisure such as yourself may stoop to trading your precious finite time on this Given World for liquid assets.

- ⚙ **Unskilled Labor**. Earn €7 per week (+€7/wk). If you have no skills, or your skills are not in demand, you can always work as a golem polisher, street sitter, manual substitute, or some other job too unprofitable to automate. Roll 1d6 for work rewards.
- ⚙ **Skilled Labor**. Earn +€15/wk. If you are skilled with a professional trait like tinker, tailor, soldier, or spy. Roll 1d8 for work rewards.
- ⚙ **Expert Labor**. Earn +€30/wk. Specialization in a trait has its perks. Roll 1d10 for work rewards.
- ⚙ **Master Labor**. Earn +€60/wk. The pinnacle of the wage labor pyramid. You'd better identify with the authority, now! Look how much it's paying you! Roll 1d12 for work rewards.

Any trait that could be considered a profession may render you eligible for skilled laborer status. See your local wage slave allocation division for more details.

After a week's worth of work, roll for your rewards.

**Work Rewards**

| Roll | Result |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | What a terrible week (d6): (1) you are severely injured—but at least you earn half pay, (2) you are fired and blacklisted in the town for affray and disarray, (3) you are robbed of your wages while having a drink with your comrades, (4) your fashionable clothes are terminally damaged in an unfortunate incident with a blood tuber and two mechanical octopi, (5) you are conscripted for a voluntary baronial corvée, (6) you are selected for an honorary unpaid role in a popular community spirit-building activity involving a ferret and a flag. |
| 2 | You earn your pay by blood and sweat. You lose 1 life per level _and_ next week, the only action you can perform besides labor is relaxation. |
| 3 | You earn your pay, but the toil has drained you. Next week, the only action you can perform besides labor is relaxation. |
| 4–5 | You earn your pay after a satisfying week of labor. You are invited to (d6): (1) meet some black market workers who might have a little "sidegig" for you, (2) an illegal but entertaining night of radical liberation speeches and theater, (3) a wreath of hard drinking and poetry with your coworkers, (4) an office party organized by your employer, (5) a local union cult membership ritual, (6) a neotraditional community sporting conflict event. |
| 6–7 | You earn your pay and more. Your kind employer recognizes your efforts and grants you a 10% raise going forward. Redouble your loyalty, worker! |
| 8–9 | Your skilled work is rewarded with a pat on the back and a firm handshake from the boss. A surge of canine gratitude surges through you, granting you a temporary +1 life per level. Work does give meaning! |
| 10–11 | Your expert work is recognized with a small plaque naming you employee of the week. It grants access to the porcelain slurry pipe in the canteen and a temporary +1 to charisma and endurance. |
| 12–17 | You are promoted to a managerial role! It comes with a timepiece of authority, a badge of honor, a cravat of distinction, and an NPC toady ... er ... direct report named **Toddwards** (L0, eager). From now on you roll 2d6 for work rewards. You are also given a 20% raise going forward and, if you succeed at a hard charisma roll, you can combine your labor action with a relaxation or improvement action. |
| 18+ | You used a hero die, didn't you? Look at you! Thinking outside the box! You are promoted to the position of a vice president. It comes with a corner office that provides a +1d6 bonus to all relaxation rolls. Additionally, you are assigned an assistant manager named **Mangely** (L2, maniacal laugh). Any week you don't feel like actually working while in the office, Mangely will roll 1d10 for your work rewards instead. You can spend that time on relaxation, upkeep, or improvement. |

Ah, well, you'll be away a while, yes? Good thing nothing could go awry in your absence! The referee rolls for interruptions on the INTR tables (pXX). Your agent will handle it just fine. You have an agent, yes? For that upkeep table two pages ago?

<a name="page_0070"></a>

#### TOWNSABOUTS

_The hundred thousand generations since the builders programmed and decreed the many ways that humans would live have resulted in this, the Garden, the perfect human lifeway. Who could doubt this eden of humanity?_ —Pathon's _Apology for the Gods_, 4:14.

"Though this tome purports to convey the variety of six lands and four regions and more, it cannot encompass all that lies under the eggshell sky."

Thus opened the _Ensiklopedia Perimaritima_ of the great world-wanderer Satišpe, apologizing for the author's inability to detail all the towns and cities of the known world. Indeed, by the time the seventh and final volume was censored, edited, politically corrected, proofread, and published, over 100 settlements described in the first volume had disappeared.

Now, this tome in your hands certainly provides a more comprehensive, concise, and nice account than that inevitable scholarly failure. After all, it is written by a ...

Oh? What? Those fools would _wandel_ off script? They'd like to visit a town unlisted, engage with a culture unrecorded? Do they _want_ to break their immersion? Peer behind the potemtech facades and draw aside the green drapes of the wizardmaster?

**Improvising Places**

It is time to bluster and invent your way out of this situation. For their own good, of course. After all, to improvise is the way of the referee.

Wheel out your oracle, the random die. Start up the imagination engine. Even toss the question back at the players. Let them engage in co-creation. Ask questions, hard and strange questions, to build a vivid place:

- ⚙ What is the one and only thing that defines this lazyplace? What is its stereotype? Of course it is incomplete, incorrect, and always misleading. But somehow also quite true.
- ⚙ What is a trait of this commune? Exaggerate it! What is a thing they oppose? Assign that to their neighbors.
- ⚙ What do these people say about themselves? What secretly defines them? Even they do not know themselves!
- ⚙ How do they describe a minority that dwells among them? What do they ascribe to the nearby others? How are both these ideas wrong? What is a hidden fact about those groups? Again—they may not understand this.
- ⚙ What do they say they want? What do they really need? How are these things different?
- ⚙ What do they not want to see? Remember: there are none so blind as those who will not see.

**Places in their Categorical Abstraction**

_All happy towns are alike; each unhappy town is unhappy in its own way._ —Qara Hana, _Observations on Utopia_.

For any settlement, small or large, a single rumor will suffice at a distance. For all places are fractal, the closer you look, more unfolds, and more, and more—until you uncover the local ant civilization working on a humanosaur-defeating nanoplague.

But up close it is worth remembering that human habitation zones feel different depending on the size of the human population. As the electric saint Nepo Lu said in its _Antilects_: "quantity has a quality all its own."

<a name="page_0071"></a>

1. The **metropoleis**, the great cities, from Red End to Violet City, are hives of activity. The great engines of the lands; clockwork bureaucracies, the flowering of social machinery, every human a cog in a greater destiny. Humans come seeking meaning and betterment, but those seeking a contented mind do not stay. Each such city is described with its own page and map and tables in its own Land. But these are sketches, leaving many gaps to fill. Indeed, each neighborhood and quarter might well be a polis or a commune in its own right.
2. The **pluripoleis**, the many towns. After 374 social experiments dissecting human individuals and communities across 2,430 parameters, the holy science of human social organization is settled. A self-governing autonomous polis or town of several kilohumans and a like number of non-human sentients and resident non-citizen humans creates an optimal long-term collective vehicle for the transmission of culture with minimal human wastage over the observed period. A perfectly utilitarian arrangement. Or so claim some traditionalist sects. Drift, error, and phylakes have driven these towns to differentiate and each can handle many contradictory traits and rumors.
3. Smaller are the **communes**. These weiks or villages are sub-authorized human settlements existing outside the strictly beneficial authority structures and prone to going feral. Humans should be wary of the temptations of village life, as they may lead to an unacceptable decline in their level of civilization. Villages may be smaller and stranger than towns, their traits fewer but very exaggerated.
4. Smaller yet, or abandoned, or further off in the vast where Garden civilization has ended, or never gone, are the **lazyplaces**. These consist of a name and a rumor, a whisper of humanity shading into radiation ghosts and singing dusts. They are not lazy merely because the author has been lazy in barely describing them, but because time there moves more slowly with fewer observers to push the lazy slavegod Time along.

**Places in their Posthistorical Variation**

_Call no city happy until it is no more._ —Samotar Endbringer, _Consolations of Metahistory_.

Why is there such diversity among humans? Why does each settlement cling so to its local folkways? Why are there so many languages? Why does each community have its own strange taboos and quaint customs?

In a world seeded with big divine objects and incomprehensible aberracts, a human mind easily jumps to fantastical conclusions. The truth is prosaic: time, technology, and cultural evolution. Still, can one be sure?

Many scholars of the postnöospheric totality admit a gnawing doubt that divine meddling lies behind what the poet Humerus calls the "variation engine". The end is the world we see, but their arguments vary:

1. According to Zuffa d'Alzavo of Safranj, each settlement's **amusement daemons** algorithmically tailor generated content to local tastes, leading to rapid and unpredictable cultural divergence.
2. The omniglot Semmero Yeziq of Oranje puts the blame in the mouths of the **babel daemons**. Most humans can afford an amulet with a trapped babel offering real-time full-spectrum translation, so there is little pressure to learn other languages and cultures. Each community thus forms its own cant.
3. The dewerker druid Beri Staganoy emphasizes the **physical law of knowledge corruption**. All information stored in the noösphere mutates and accumulates errors. The need for hard records makes maintaining a coherent truth culture impossible.
4. The rustlander fiveborn wisechief Slackmaw Bentley Vinecomb states that it is a byproduct of the unhealthy **lack of war**. The grand phylakes make empires and centralized polities nearly impossible, so local political solutions proliferate and mutate.
5. Figaro Figaro Simplecult of the Purple University holds that the persistence of **local oldtech** is responsible. Many communities have some ancient magical infrastructure providing basic necessities, reducing the need for external trade.
6. The wrecker scholar Rauda Kornpsalms points to the **difficulty of travel**. Portals and other public transport are slower than necessary and unreliable, the bureaucracy and human security daemons unpredictable, the personal transportation licenses baroque. It is more comfortable to stay put—and many people do precisely that. Rauda claims this is by design and proof of the hostility of the gods, but this is a nemesis heresy and good reason to discount such an ill-mannered scholar. It is said that Rauda even sought to corrupt the youth by inciting them to question authority and tradition! Fortunately, the Young Guardeners informed the inquisition and Rauda's antieducational circle in the Grove of Cacodemos was dispersed with mercy and justice. Many scarves of honor were handed out that week.

<a name="page_0072"></a>

#### THE 300 TOWN TRAITS

_Polyculture makes Heaven better than monoculture. Diverse cultures make another mass die-off less likely. After the six erroneous utopian experiments, we must encourage a diversity of cultural expression among the different human communities, tribes, and classes._ —Orange Araña's Letters, 373-56, contested translation

The Rainbow Lands and the Circle Sea are the greatest, greenest, most wonderful and pleasant of lands. The most civilized, the best cultured, the most beautiful and safe. Yet, they are not at all the largest part of the world.

Far from it. But they boast such diversity!

The traveler, that blessed good person, possessed of permit and means, will find more variety wandering from one settlement to another, even if they are but half a day's autogolem ride apart, than they would in a week's iron horse journey on the Thin Air or deep in the grasslands beyond the Violet.

**1. Architecture**

What do these human settlements look like?

1. Collective hives for groupthink and groupmind. Prefabricated, regurgitated, post-modulated.
2. Crude slapped-together huts and functional containers, for the true world is the noösphere.
3. Baroque and organic, grown not built. Landcoral, livingstone, or sungwood.
4. Accreted, adapted styles have created a tell town. Layers upon bones upon layers of life and death.
5. Traditional subterranean tunnel town. Bunker palaces, nuclearlithic sub-urbs, plastic parklands.
6. Brutalist paradise of posthuman biomech ruins. Raw materials, glistening veins, gasping pipeworks.

**2. Art**

The aesthetics these humans make and love.

7. Vigorous festivals of dance and mind-bathing.
8. Synthetic generative visual arts.
9. Elaborate ceramic decoration.
10. Deep-coded musical traditions.
11. Illuminated sculptural schools.
12. Bloody gladiatorial trials in old public buildings.

Ethnographers observe the quaint ways of different settlements with great interest, collecting them as birdwatchers do different beasts of the air, from the air jelly to the sky whale.

The rulers of each polis argue that in its form their polis represents the perfect tradeoff between individual freedom and communal competence.

The ethnographer, or the traveler familiar with a city or two, may well doubt this argument. Perhaps this cultural efflorescence exists precisely to defeat the ennui which could so easily overcome a better person in this golden age at the end of time.

To generate a random trait, roll a die 300-sided; or a die 50-sided for the category, then a die 6-sided. Many of these traits are odd. The referee is invited to use discretion, humor, and jaundice in their application.

**3. Birth, Advanced**

How they make new humans.

13. Natural neonates born eight at a time from the Village Womb®.
14. Well-behaved matrix-baked mesonates, between the apparent ages of 3 and 5, delivered to approved parent humans by storklings.
15. Full-grown orimonates from living matrices.
16. Synthetic humans of an appropriate age category stitched together in vitro by mother machines.
17. Uplifted through biomechanical intervention from pre-selected domesticated animal or ling lineages.
18. Recycled from captured ferals.

**4. Birth, Traditional**

How they reproduce new humans.

19. Single mothers select optimized fetuses and carry them to term as part of their civil service.
20. Mothering sisterhoods maintain the reproductive mysteries of Red Rubra and the older gods.
21. Synthetic midwives assist nuclear family units.
22. Carried to term by parents in marsupial pouches.
23. Birther is a respected lower class profession.
24. Grandmothers and medicals perform the ancient rituals at the local temple of the Petal Host.

<a name="page_0073"></a>

**5. Care, The Weak**

How the helpless and infirm are cared for.

25. Care is available to anyone who can pay for it. The poor are encouraged to perform feats of gratitude to earn handouts.
26. Unfortunates are encouraged to visit the recycling facilities. Their families receive consumer goods.
27. Free re-body facilities are available in exchange for a three-year community service contract.
28. All citizens must volunteer their time at the local care complex. Unvoluntaries are re-educated.
29. The carer clan alone may offer help and succor.
30. Golems and synthetics run pleasure hospices, with full end-of-life synthetic heaven for their patients.

**6. Care, The Young**

How babes and children are provided for.

31. Creches with basic indoctrination protocols ensure happy well-adjusted children.
32. Extended families provide free labor.
33. Vidys and magical tablets substitute for carers.
34. Ancestors, ghosts, and holograms help biological parents. Often they replace them.
35. Pavlovian training implants let the young care for themselves with mechanical care devices.
36. Each child is assigned a personal daemon who cares for them and grows with them.

**7. Class**

How their property relations divide them.

37. The concept of class is taboo. Even the cruelest of differences are strictly ignored.
38. Rigid caste structure to preserve guild domains.
39. Meritocratic privilege unlocks the benefits of greed.
40. Regular jubilees to cancel debts and obligations.
41. Idealistic egalitarianism supported by strict sacred doctrines of the Invisible Hand and Fair Market.
42. Mandatory equality through cloning, empathic indoctrination, and psychosurgical intervention to remove individual differences.

**8. Courtesy**

What is good manners for these humans?

43. A 13-fold handshake shows friendship and respect.
44. To show the face is to offer your soul for theft.
45. Only a scoundrel would be unwilling to duel.
46. One only talks directly to objects, not people.
47. You cannot have a meaningful relationship if strict records of napkins and kerchiefs are not kept.
48. Swearing shows honesty. Polite people trick you.

**9. Crime**

What is a crime? How is it perceived?

49. To breach etiquette is to summon the manacle man.
50. Borrowing another's words or ideas is theft.
51. Citizens have relationships with every object in their domain. Touching or moving an object in a relationship with a citizen is a vile act.
52. Property is theft. Sharing is mandatory. Owners are criminals, subject to branding and burning.
53. To treat an outlander like an inlander is treachery.
54. Refusing to pay a bribe is grounds for re-education.

**10. Death**

How they deal with death.

55. Final mulching into the local herbal matrix.
56. Destructive recycling into new humans.
57. Elite abmortality with anti-senescence magicines.
58. General abmortality through biomechanical intervention. A society of bionic humans.
59. Post-mortality via canopic jewel.
60. Noöspheric postmortality. Premium postmortalities available for an additional fee.

**11. Demographics**

How many here reside.

61. None. It's all ghosts, the echoes of a lost past.
62. Barely any. It's mostly falšers, soulless biological machine replicas of humans.
63. Few. It's mostly synthetic or undead servitors.
64. Smattering of abmortals cling on as new humans build a new culture.
65. Plenty. A vibrant culture, full of hope, ideas, and delusions of novelty.
66. An overcrowded behavioral sink breeding strange beliefs and warrior death cults.

<a name="page_0074"></a>

**12. Dwellings**

What kind of nests do these humans live in?

67. Dormipods for the lowly, glass palaces for the good.
68. Mass-produced identikit biomechanical homes.
69. Freetech wood, brick, and plaster homes. Made by humans for humans.
70. Repurposed grand buildings from long-ago subdivided in hovels, homes, and manors.
71. Landcoral cottages and sungwood bungalows grown from seed and killed on occupant death.
72. Habitation engines fabricated according to the divine templates. Quite safe. Low corruption risk.

**13. Emotion**

How do these humans feel?

73. Emotions are irrational. That's why they replace their meat brains with full-metal at age 5.
74. Negative emotions are bad. Smile all the time.
75. Expressing happiness invites bad luck.
76. Loud emotions after the age of 11 are punished.
77. Their language uses emotion markers to avoid confusion. A statement that does not carry a clear emotional label is impossible.
78. Creatures of pure emotion and intuition, reason must always come second. To repress is to sin.

**14. Faith**

How these humans believe.

79. Cannot believe. Their edited brains are fully rational.
80. To question the faith of the elders is mandatory.
81. A charmingly naïve faith in the scientific gods.
82. Faith is personal and individual. To share beliefs once is a terrible faux pas. Twice: an ostracism.
83. Unbelievable beliefs must be loudly and publicly affirmed to signal group loyalty.
84. The engines of faith implant perfect orthodoxy.

**15. Fashion**

What is in vogue with these humans.

85. Severe monochromatic uniforms.
86. Deeply understated class-based dress system.
87. Ostentatiously useless ornaments and decorations indicate taste and status.
88. Universal undifferentiated bathrobe styles.
89. Ritual naturalism used to discretely flaunt biomechanical modifications in a public setting.
90. Bioideological lineage-based sartorial combat wielding the concepts of the five pneumas.

**16. Food, Ordinary**

What these humans eat of an ordinary day.

91. Formulated pellets from a dispenser. With chondrin for joint support, additives for glossy hair, and a mild sedative flavor.
92. Slime from a tap. Available in seventeen different colors and flavors.
93. Eternal stew, dispensed thrice daily from the village autocanteen as the good book requires.
94. Sugar-dusted cereal flakes mixed with one of five sweet beverages for maximum calory uptake.
95. Healthy mix of vegetables and pulses from local polyculture gardens.
96. Wide and varied buffet, a feast for all the senses, different each day.

**17. Food, Special**

What is eaten on special days.

97. Chocolate. Actual chocolate.
98. Warm slurry. Heated food is as good as chocolate.
99. Recycled ancestors to commune with the infinite chain of humanity.
100. Meat from the local sacrificial beasts.
101. Foods decorated with inert metals like gold, platinum, and uranium.
102. Synthesized foods of extravagant shapes and textures, from authentiporridge to zetafries.

**18. Freedom**

How they handle their liberty under the Maker.

103. Flat denial and retreat into rigid communal dogma.
104. Fatalistic resignation and refusal to make choices.
105. Simplistic assertion of individual freedoms without social or cosmic responsibilities.
106. Delusions of grandiosity, assertion of self-creation.
107. Loose melange of pragmatic pro-social and creative individual needs.
108. Courageous acceptance of the burden of freedom as the duty of bearing witness to the Given World.

<a name="page_0075"></a>

**19. Friendship**

How humans relate to others.

109. Laissez-faire. Anything goes. Poop happens.
110. Genetic relatives prioritized.
111. Chemical bonding for intra-group cohesion.
112. Rituals of stress and trauma to create permanent connections between consociates.
113. Machine friends assigned at birth.
114. A life alone is a life well-lived, for every human is an island and an island attached is a peninsula.

**20. Gender**

How they sort their sociobiological roles.

115. Strictly disgendered. Masks to hide faces, robes to disguise forms.
116. Loosely binary, with some ambiguity.
117. Traditional trinary division into ladies, leits, and lords as specified by the Original Congress of Cities.
118. Six- or seven-colored. Great battles rage between the culture-first sixers and hierarchy-plus seveners.
119. Closely tied to biomechanical source and structure.
120. The concept is incomprehensible to this culture.

**21. Killing**

How these humans kill.

121. By killing, a beast becomes a person. A human must kill to acquire a soul and an identity.
122. Life is struggle. To kill an enemy is to become an adult. To be an adult is to be a warrior.
123. Human life is sacred. A killer ceases to be human.
124. A tragedy, a weakness. Those who kill must be purified in the mill of souls.
125. All life is sacred. Killing is an abomination unless the victim is willing. Only willing meat may be eaten.
126. Taboo. All who kill are unclean. To eat that which once lived is to be sullied. The most pure replace their organic digestion systems with electromagical batteries so they no longer need to consume life.

**22. Kinship**

How individuals become relatives.

127. Completely determined by biology: mother, mother's brother, sister's child, and so on.
128. Biology and a smattering of nudge, nudge, wink, wink. Mother, husband, postman, child, and so on.
129. Sortition. Assigned for life by the stochastic kinship engine at birth.
130. Resortion. Remixed regularly by the lotto council.
131. Found. Left to individuals to figure out. May take years, if at all. Anomic ghosts populate the shadows.
132. Psycho-optimized using deep preference analysis and dream-reading engines.

**23. Knowledge**

How human curiosity is satisfied.

133. The pursuit of knowledge for the sake of knowledge. Natural scientists proliferate. Discovery jubilees occur often and scientists perform mystery rites to preserve their lore.
134. Memorization of randomly generated sacred texts.
135. Construction of memory stone complexes.
136. Duplication of key humans in the noösphere.
137. Hive mind protocols.
138. Curiosity decay due to excess hedonism.

**24. Law**

How do they decide what is right and what is not?

139. The ordination obelisk rewrites law codes daily.
140. Oral traditions of honor, debt, and blood-feud.
141. The semi-divine progenitor laid down perfect laws Long Long Ago, when the angels still roosted near.
142. Codified rules refined by undead lawyers.
143. Common law derived from accreted democratic anarchist council decisions.
144. No law. Each citizen is wired into the communicodex through a psycho-empathetic link. Each new ruling is decided by popular subconscious referendum.

<a name="page_0076"></a>

**25. Leaders, Power Of**

Relationships between the big and the small person.

145. The leaders are infallible. To question them is grounds for personality formatting.
146. Fed on blood and pneuma, the leaders are harder, better, faster, and stronger than the rest.
147. They are the best of us. So they tell us.
148. They are the best of us. It is proven by their ritual standardized administration exam scores.
149. Random people put into positions of excruciating difficulty, forged and refined through trial and error.
150. Fools, chosen as figureheads. The leaders are sacrificed to the gods when things go wrong.

**26. Literature**

What are the stories and books of these people?

151. Jumbled communal histories, myths, operating manuals, legends, and prayers. All spiral-bound.
152. Violent poetry and gentle oral horror tales.
153. Surprisingly deep cat-girl and bunny-boy folk fics.
154. Baroque, recursive novels used as bricks.
155. Parables of self-improvement, guru hagiographies.
156. A unique canon, sifted from the decamillennial labors of ten thousand electric simians.

**27. Magic**

What do they make of fantascience and other powers?

157. All magic is corruption. Burn every which witch!
158. Everyone needs to take out supernatural insurance.
159. Delusional magic denial.
160. Espouse a deep post-humanism and appreciate the scientological underpinnings of fantascience.
161. Deny human agency. Ascribe all occult knowledge to the gods and builders.
162. Power-hungry desire to master the dark arts. Shame no such thing as "dark arts" exists.

**28. Meaning**

How these humans deal with the presence of oldtech and buildertech far surpassing their powers and abilities.

163. Drugs and shutdown to avoid their unimportance.
164. Cult of strenuous physical activity. Tiredness defeats despair. Break on through, kick a hole in the sky.
165. Self-delusion and myths of local importance.
166. Denial of the existence of the builders and the gods.
167. Local trials require them to strive to survive.
168. Unaware of the existence of oldtech and buildertech thanks to specific local conditions. Please do not disturb these neoprimitives.

**29. Medicine**

How are damaged humans repaired?

169. They are not. They are replaced with replicas.
170. Don't all humans regenerate? Just wait for the missing limb to grow back.
171. Each house has a vivi-coffinTM to rebuild its citizen.
172. Prayers to the autodoctor at the mechaclinic often work. If they don't, sacrifices will surely help.
173. Herbs, chants, and telewitchdoctor appointments.
174. Daemons are summoned to possess a local worthy, filling them with medical knowledge as required.

**30. Memory**

How these humans deal with memory.

175. Memories are surgically removed.
176. Altered to maximize well-being.
177. Synthetic memories to remove all frustration.
178. Stored in souvenirs for regular analysis.
179. Shared in group storytelling rituals.
180. Recorded with personality forks for later interrogation, optimization, and improvement.

**31. Money**

What is their universal fungible commodity?

181. Mutual obligations, remembered by the infallible mechanical debtmaster.
182. Great immovable coins of stone.
183. The shells of levi-cowries, harvested with light nets.
184. Beasts. Inhuman living things. The more inhumans one owns, the wealthier one is.
185. Memories, crystallized in the perfect vidymax format.
186. Relics. Polished bits of the town's ancestors.

**32. Politics**

How humans decide what matters here.

187. Mechanical laws governed by the authority engine. To citizens, the laws of politics are like the laws of physics: immutable and eternal.
188. Unspoken norms and taboos structure politics.
189. Factional power struggles and public blood sports.
190. Traditional conservative hierarchical methods proven resilient over millennia. Also, shock collars.
191. Electoral snout-couting rituals ensure a peaceful rotation of career overseers.
192. Sortition and lottery with algorithmic ancestors as a depository of institutional wisdom.

<a name="page_0077"></a>

**33. Population**

What kind of humans are these?

193. Perfect baseliners, devoted anti-modificationists.
194. Pragmatic biomechanical long-term optimizers.
195. Mad expansionists, devoted to constant viral growth, even at the cost of their own souls.
196. Modified specialists diversifying into a new form.
197. Tailored human castes, creating a homeostatic hierarchical clockwork society.
198. Polymorphic changelings, modifying their own body templates till some many are unrecognizable.

**34. Property**

How do these humans maintain the idea of ownership?

199. Communal property enforced through surveillance. Money controlled by hereditarily pure chosen caste.
200. Collective property continuously redistributed by stochastic ownership daemon routines.
201. Private property regulated by tradition and taste.
202. Citizenship requires individual property ownership.
203. Property held by one sole sovereign citizen or a traditional benevolent oligarchy, while other residents gratefully live on universal basic subsistence and absolutely never rebel. Honest.
204. Property is mandatory. If you are without property, you are property.

**35. Punishment**

Who is punished? How? Why?

205. Punishment is random. Anyone might breach a law, so it doesn't matter who is punished.
206. Harsh, spectacular, theatrical, deterrent.
207. Re-education or hard labor. Learn faster.
208. Bodily suspension while the mind is run through an accelerated purgatory simulation.
209. Body becomes a town slave to work off its sentence, while the mind is suspended.
210. Implanted mind shackles punish bad thoughts.

**36. Rebirth**

How re-humans are dealt with.

211. Personality copies inscribed into newborns.
212. Life experiences chopped up and remixed to offer a quickstart to newborns.
213. Souls released back into the greater cosmic sphere.
214. Personalities are trapped in memory matrices for later access. Once a citizen, always a citizen.
215. Condemned souls sold or milled for energy.
216. Souls transfer between shells to maintain the continuity of the local divine spark, while personalities may fade back into the noösphere.

**37. Recreation**

How do these humans consume their leisure time?

217. Approved mass-food-consumption competitions.
218. A pre-cosmic ball game, invented by the gods.
219. Skipping lozenges on a pond.
220. Biomechanical horror combat.
221. Vigorous extended rhythmic physical exertion with loud thumping music.
222. Body-hopping and races through forested ruins.

**38. Resource, Air**

A polis without air becomes a necropolis.

223. Void. Local humans carry portable air tanks.
224. Private. Even if abundant, breathing rights cost €5 per week. Those who will not pay will serve.
225. Synthetic. Piped into homes, full of happy smells.
226. Natural. Abundant and ignored.
227. Polluted. Glorious facilities fill it with dust and ash.
228. Thick. Glitters with local symbioflora or spores.

**39. Resource, Food**

Where their food comes from.

229. It doesn't. Humans use tinned food. Or each other.
230. Collective. All food is property of the monopoly collective LLC and eating costs €5 per week.
231. NutriSlurryTM. Piped from the automatic food factory into homes, full of jolly molly.
232. Natural. Hunted and gathered in the surrounding parklands and ruinlands.
233. Traditional. Grown locally by the sweat of brows and pong of processed night soil.
234. Cornucopia. Produced in abundance by grickles and the local bio-engineered food plants.

<a name="page_0078"></a>

**40. Resource, Electricity**

Humans were made to harness lightning.

235. None. What is this, Electric City?
236. Private. All energy belongs to the Mother Electric. Power costs €5 per week.
237. Rationed. Wires bring enough power for constant entertainment.
238. Natural. Solar fields, wind mills, and frond-like rectennas harvest ambient ka energy and convert it into power for human games.
239. Reliable. A standard radiothermal egg produces standard power, sufficient for a normal human as stated in Human Needs Manual 94-gertrude.
240. Omnipresent. A great sub-reality field envelops the polis, providing near limitless power to any device or human equipped with a zero-access plug.

**41. Resource, Water**

Water is the gift of sky to earth.

241. Barren. Carried in portable bottles. Corpses are drained. Clean water is a ritual offering.
242. Private. Drinking rights cost €5 per week.
243. SuperClearTM, better than water. Piped into homes, full of good vibrations. It's got what clams crave!
244. Natural. Cold and pure.
245. Filthy. Either the local sewage system failed or was never built. Boil or barf.
246. Living. Refreshingly full of semi-sentient colony plankton. Drink and dream, friend.

**42. Responsibility**

How they handle their duties to cosmos, society, and self.

247. Submission to the id and the basic bodily drives.
248. Rational, utilitarian calculation with the help of implanted ethical subroutine jewels.
249. A treadmill of guilts and desires keeps the society on an even keel, like a whizzing gyroscope.
250. Pervasive socio-empathic field ensures compliance.
251. The spiritually and socially elect guide, lecture, and hector. And control the redistribution matrices.
252. Evolved traditions of asceticism, friendship, honor, reciprocity, and ultraviolence ensure fairness.

**43. Ritual**

What rituals have they developed to tame the vast?

253. Ritual arrhythmia. Live without rhythm so you don't summon the void worm.
254. Oldtech knowledge coded as ritual, but the great machine is dead ... for now.
255. Regular purification with fragrant machine oils.
256. Mandatory sacrifices insure against divine wrath.
257. Beautiful festivals hide dark soul-burning horrors that keep the community fertile.
258. Simple void navy protocols as symbols of status.

**44. Socialization**

How humans learn to be humans in their settlement.

259. Born preloaded with an algorithmically generated variation of a standard social protocol.
260. Trial-and-error based on their preset general information acquisition protocols.
261. Taught by approved parent humans in accordance with tradition.
262. Trial of survival in peer-group packs.
263. Instruction through rote mechanical learning rituals.
264. Trained as members of class-defined cooperatives.

**45. Status**

What say they is best in life?

265. Aesthetic perfection and visual supremacy.
266. Physical and mental health for ever. Abmortality. Lichdom. Eternal humanity.
267. Retreat from the wheel of suffering, a life of contemplation and restraint.
268. Rational refinement and cruel wit.
269. Gold. If this be a golden age, gold is where it's at.
270. To see one's enemies crushed, et cetera. But in a civil way.

<a name="page_0079"></a>

**46. Technology**

How do they approach oldtech and modern tech?

271. Man was not made for technology. Only women may use these sorceries.
272. Technologies corrupt. All who use them must purify themselves if they wish to rejoin the community.
273. What a human can make, a human can use.
274. Oldtech is dangerous. Beware the greedy who dabble in it.
275. Technology is power. All men have a will to power.
276. Technology is the hidden god. To use it is to worship the true maker of this world.

**47. Trade**

What is it to truck and barter?

277. Only the weak buy. The strong take.
278. Trade outside the group is impure. Autarky is purity.
279. Only a special caste is allowed to trade.
280. One group may only buy, another only sell. Among one other, they must ritually gift.
281. Every child must buy and sell to become an adult.
282. To trade and trick is the highest virtue.

**48. Travel**

How do they view travel? How do they do it?

283. Travel is against the garden protocols. Travelers are taboo. Leave home and die to the community.
284. Reluctant due to well-founded fears of dangerous oldtech. Feet, bicycles, and beasts are best.
285. To travel for business is acceptable. Frivolous travel is a sin. The tourist endangers their soul.
286. The rich and good travel to protect the community, the poor should stay put for their own good.
287. To travel is to be human. Extra points for traveling in luxury and sharing vidys to show happy you were.
288. Everyone must be a nomad at some point and the perfect house is a mobile home.

**49. Undeath**

How these humans deal with undeath.

289. The final tax. Everyone gets to become a plantation zombie and contribute to the commune.
290. Undying computers. The best and the brightest, filed and stored for consultation.
291. Protected by unquiet ancestors. The dead guard the living with ancient blades and cosmic ray guns.
292. Buried under the floorboards, the ghosts of the ancestors ward the homes of their children.
293. Taboo. One must not speak of them, lest they return.
294. Abhorrent. All undead are destroyed on sight.

**50. Work**

What do humans do that they must do?

295. Fully-automated luxury. No work required. High futility expected.
296. Manual labor opportunities provided to occupy all members of society.
297. Social status games dominate, service tasks proliferate, manufacturing suffers, agriculture is dead—or reserved for the reanimated dead.
298. Free-market mixed economy simulation uses starvation risk as a motivation for labor participation.
299. Cargo cult of work prioritizes productivity as a spiritual practice.
300. Meditative and religious art dominates human efforts. Some automation required to prevent population collapse.

<a name="page_0080"></a>

#### COLORS

_"The color codes protect us from Error."_ —Long Ago catechism, Blue Skull meta-codex 74:147

Long Ago, when people dwelled in ignorance and fear, their world was divided into objective color categories. Today, civilized peoples still use colors subjectively.

- ⚙ Green. Good things, which humans can use at will anywhere in the Given World.
- ⚙ Yellow. Sacred things, which require divine power and can only be used by the gods and their agents. Forbidden to mere common humans.
- ⚙ Red. Dangerous things, which humans may only use on the fringes of the civilized lands or under supervision. Forbidden to unlicensed humans.
- ⚙ Blue. Unholy things, such as errors, forbidden to all everywhere. Usually dangerous and useless.
- ⚙ Violet. Divine tools, such as buildertech, which work anywhere. Forbidden to all. Coveted by many.

Orange was not a traditional color code and there is some debate among traditionalists whether the Orange Lands should properly be divided between the Yellow and the Red. Some radicals have suggested using Orange to categorize dangerous sacred things, but this has been struck down by the Council of Ancestors and Descendants, which argues that it would stigmatize abmortal custodians of civilization.

**The Monochrome**

_Have you or someone you know come into contact with white or black matter? If you suspect corruption, please report immediately for purification and reset. The Dream knows all, and innocent humans will suffer no loss of canopic status for accidental contact with white or black matter._ —the "pure" signal, repeating, 750?–27ya

The last purification station was lost around the same time recorded history resumed. Today it is thus impossible to fully expunge the corruption from interactions with taboo monochrome categorized matter.

Even the wizards, wont to call the monochrome taboo mere superstition, still spin the cleansing color wheel when they fear they have been near the colorless.

**Yet, what even is monochrome?**

1. That is of the noösphere, for its colors are false.
2. Glass, water, air. To wash is to invite discoloration!
3. Grime, filth, the gray of the wastes. Ash is death!
4. Zealotry and division. The truth is middle brown.
5. Black stands for oil and coal, white for spirit and uranium. It is a moral-environmental injunction. It is what we must not burn.
6. There is no white or black alone, these are principles in balance, in rotation, in interpenetration, in coexistence.
7. Midday and midnight are the times to hide.
8. The underlying source code of reality is white glyphs upon black void. That is forbidden to humans.
9. It is the colors spun together, admixed too swiftly!
10. The little-knowers of long ago used white and black as proxies for the colors beyond colors, for the places out of space. This is but a warning against voidwalkers who tamper with the extra-cosmic!

<a name="page_0081"></a>

**Pray Read Further**

For this map is not the territory.

—World Emperor One One, Time of Soil and Sowing, Before Long Long Ago

# I: THE RAINBOW LANDS

[![The Rainbow Lands Map (page 81)](images/page_0081_rainbow_lands_map.png)](images/hires/page_0081_rainbow_lands_map.png)

<!-- Begin: Our_Golden_Age_04_Blue_Land_82-105 -->

<a name="page_0082"></a>

### BLUE LAND

<a name="page_0083"></a>

_"Dead gods, soarstones, living rains, and endless liberty."_ —Belico Chaparral, reintegration prophet

It seems the Blue Land was where the Dream came alive, a place of creativity and innovation, where the [illegible] adapted the best of Heaven to the merest of the Humans.

Sadly the old histories were corrupted by the Incident (War?) and current theories on what this meant are in disagreement. Was it a holy pleasure preserve? A radical edenoforming zone? A labor designation for lobogods?

Some modern authorities, such as the High Realist of the Svat of Hexad Foreign Affairs, suggest that Blue is just a geographical expression, a borderland between the oldtech might of the Green and the mystical fantascience of the Purple.

As it is, the Sacred Reintegration Protocols (SRP) divide the traditional lower Blue among the externally administered UCC, CUC, SEZ, and various subsidiary polities—viz. Azula, Indigo West, Mur and UVS. The upper Blue is maintained as the Designation, an independent monitored territory for surviving Bluelanders.

Though popular imagination still holds this to be a fallen land, roving with chimerical horrors suitable only for disaster tourism, the SRP has made it one of the most dynamic region of the Rainbowlands, with scavenging conglomerates and renewtech startups transforming human possibilities in ways unthinkable for generations. If you want to get a head, this is the place to be!

**Climate**

The great Halt Blank (Alto Blanco in the local patois) to the north caps the realm in ice and air so thin unassisted human lungs must shrivel. The deep-carving rivers ensure winter's chill is ever but a hike away.

The low-lying valleys are drenched year-long, swathed in fogs and cloudbursts from the ageless rainmakers humidifying the world as the Builders intended. Occasionally, aerolith towers or fossils of the Blue God crumble, unleashing landslides, floods, and miasmas.

**Population**

reintegration territories: ~1.5 million, designation territories: ~0.2–1.2 million

**Groups**

new bluelanders 28%, old bluelanders 23%, dis-integrated laborers 17%, greenlanders 13%, free purplelanders 9%, purplelanders 6%, others 4%.

**Languages**

Canopic (official), Blaunestalk (suppressed), RD Cant (unofficial), Neo-Azulic (trade interlanguage), Perimse (river traders), Free Pura (unclear).

**Capital**

Official: pending reconstruction. Practical: Special Economic Zone has been designated a New Model City and will feature amenities unheard of, such as hot and cold running plumbing, free indoor sunlight lamps, and edible mycelial wall panelling. It is currently 6.2% finished and funding is being secured!

**Government**

Polycondominium concession zones. Radically overlapping competing administrations use market signals and the Invisible Hand ideology to maximize uplift returns. The Designation is probably an autarkic subsistence-level zone of human disaster settlement.

**Ideologies**

Cogflower: regrowth (supported), Cathedral: innovator (free), Blue God: cave horror (suppressed), Free Industrialism: honorary (imported).

**Economy**

"But then the [illegible] went False and embraced the Error and the War followed. Devastation," mutters the Econotabulator, mad in its oversight bunker. Thus, the modern Blue Land economy is left to its own devices.

**Resources**

bacterial cultures, bio-autogenerators, dairy, lamarckian modulators, godsflesh, aerolith structures, living bone.

**Means of Production**

Until reintegration is complete, private enterprise is encouraged. Bluelander ownership is discouraged for obvious security reasons.

**Material Conditions**

Official: each registered laborer is entitled to a personalized living dormisac and 10 cash per week. Effective: black market research suggests reliable laborers uncorrupted by the various error plagues command 28 to 35 cash per week.

_Source: Seventh Eye Hexad [collective work], RLD Friends of Industry Bulletin, Soil Sunflower IX_

<a name="page_0084"></a>

[![Blue Land map (page 84)](images/page_0084_blue_land_map.png)](images/hires/page_0084_blue_land_map.png)

**Ambient, Valley**

Each deep valley is like a land all its own, kept apart from its neighbors by high mountains, the underways blocked by the sprouting corpses of the [redacted] false god. Yet, the rainmakers and airmakers ensure the climates are surprisingly similar, seemingly better suited to squamous, crawling, slick-skinned things than to humans. Please don't forget your anti-fungal ointments.

| d6 | Winter | Spring | Summer | Autumn |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1–3 | dripping fog, slick stones, tongues of shadow | clinging mists, glittering greenery, chill shadows | pungent, gnawing, sticky, trickly, oozing fog | dry days, crisp nights, polychrome vegetation |
| 4–5 | wet snow, nuzzling mud, sprouting icicles | scattered suns, cool winds blow away ghosts | clear skies and glittering archaeomagical debris | blue days, bright mushrooms, light nights |
| 6 | toxic snow, orange bright, blue glaze molds | crumbling aerolith gravel, curtains of rain, butterflies | turbid mud flows, brown waters, torn herbiage | miasmatic films cling to tree and tower, glowing |

<a name="page_0085"></a>

**Ambient, Highland**

The Highlands soar above the soil, rich in aerolith, riddled by dead god-matter.

| d6 | Winter | Spring | Summer | Autumn |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1–3 | collapsed air, daytime stars, indigo skies | rarefied, winds, clear plankton blooms | scorching ultraviolet days, sunscreen essential | thin air, supplementary oxygen advised |
| 4–5 | churning, sucking, rushing aerolith, sudden gusts | clear sky thunderstorms, drifting ice clouds | soup-thick cloud, booming air plankton, dead voices | flying snow, sun dogs, sparkling delights |
| 6 | blue skies, frost fogs, ice geysers, rising berg-bris | geld mists, rainbursts, gasping dead god-matter | howling ice storm, sudden silence, snowbow | whiteout, thick-drifting snows, decaying god-dust |

**Events**

In these ill-favored lands, keep one hand on your wallet and the other on your safekeeper.

| d6 | 1–3 Expected | 4–5 Surprising | 6 Error |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Heavy rain, terrible visibility, and water shadows (L1, most) prowling about. It'll pass in a few days. | Waterlogged, dead soil and rock collapse. Road washed out, aerolith struts suspended in mid air. | Strange eruption leaves a devastated terrain of wriggling holes, dying statues and/or flesh. Terratoonic! |
| 2 | Clerical errors compound and you must be held for a few days. It's not a quarantine. €10 to €40 will clear that matter up. | Nat, unsightly, and possibly psychedelic fungal infection. 3 weeks with the little "red runner" pills should fix that. | A twitching mycelial mass erupts in tentacles and livingstone bubbles. A godburst (L11, erratic). Leave this to the cleaners (L4, efficient). |
| 3 | Botherpickers (L2, sporebrained) scavenging fools after nightfall. | Wizard cultists (L3, ragged) attack nearby facilities. Prices spike fivefold. | Noble neo-fauna (L2d6) reclaim the environment for the ecosphere. |
| 4 | Stochastic peacemaker (L4, just) roadblock charges €5 per creature and vehicle. Are they just bandits? | Broken peacemaker golem (L6, strong), its brain stolen. Supplies worth €75 remain. Nobody will know. | Once-humans (L2, anthropophages) gone to biological seed. Beware their heat lances and plasma lances. |
| 5 | Traditional locals (L1, friendly) offering themselves for a better life outside this hell lovely place. | Toxic drifts ... or hallucinations? The sky sparkles with electric snow. It'll pass on its own in 1d6 days. | God fog contaminates the area. Strange visions and emptiness assail you. Nose filter recommended. |
| 6 | Local waters poisoned. Perhaps by the oldsettler cultists (L2, shade-shifting)? They'll give you 2 regular runes, 2 blood runes, 3 strange visions, (4) cheese brain, (5) lockmind, (6) enlightenment and a permanent +1 to aura. | Strange detour to a settlement from Long Ago. They have no truck with Dead Gods or peacemakers. That means things might be ghost helmets in their ancestral pod shrine. Spark? Spend €1d6 x 100 to learn a random power of void and deep time. | Stalwart inquisition civilians (L5, authorized) out: (1) farming taxes, (2) carrying trophies, (3) harrying wizard cultists, (4) burning out an infestation, (5) building a personality rebuilder, (6) helping an exiled landholder reclaim their property. |

**Travel**

The sky-thrusting mountains, rainmakers, gully-rivers, and fungal tunnels of the Blue Land are a menace to the casual traveler. Roads are in poor repair, holes are decayed, and security is precarious at best.

| Type | Status | Price |
|:---|:---|---:|
| Portal | A narrow week-walk thread links the Ruins Azure to Red End and Safranj. | official [€200] |
| Right Road | A week from the Ruins Azure to Metropolis (Emerald City) or the Violet City by armored bus. Soylent pink and hydration fluid are included. | [€30] |
| Coasthugger | A week to the Violet City or Metropolis by registered peacemaker vessel (bank). Local law usually by the same route (berth), but they're infested with cultures and take two weeks. | bunk / berth [€15 or €5] |
| Air Lane | The skies are thick with archaeomagical debris and closed to private travelers. Peacemakers flag people in need of cash offer interior flapper services. Flights to neighboring lands cost double. | [€200] |
| Local (River) | Heavily armored diesel golem barges chug the Indigo River and its tributaries. | rough [€5–30] |
| Local (Off-channel) | Local porters are unreliable, as likely to be anthropophages as not. Automules are a better buy. Peacemaker defense golems (L4, bonded) make expensive porters, but worth it. | strange [€15–100] |

<a name="page_0086"></a>

#### AZURE COMMERCIAL REINTEGRATION PARKS

_"Everything and everyone is for sale! It's an amazing opportunity!"_ —Patchick Bel-Bel Ressorum-3, reintegration consultant, former peacemaker

The Blue Land is no peacemaker shopping destination like Safranj, but it has a quaint, rural charm. Visitors should not display large quantities of cash in the streets, as they may be set upon by packs of feral post-humans who imagine that money would improve their class. Of course, it would not, but this is of little solace to the mugged tourist.

Due to poor trade links, Blue Land goods purchased abroad sell for 2d6 times their usual price. The same poor logistics mean that foreign products cost twice as much as in other lands.

**The licensed reintegrator:**

1. snake head grafted onto an animatronic dummy with a vocoder speaker;
2. electric lucky cat with eyes that bore into you;
3. jolly cat friend with dead eyes and a critic smile;
4. shifty wagebound with ill-lifting skin;
5. jittery lime nomad with metallic arachnid pets;
6. three robed figures with identical ceramic masks.

**This Commercial Reintegration Park**

| d6 | Reintegration Park | Reintegrator Mien | Specialty | Product Quirk |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Resources & Resources | grasp, grippy, handsy | bacterial biomachines | overheats when excited |
| 2 | Free People Options | polished, bony, silvery | animated dairy products | spreads like mold ... uh ... it's mold? |
| 3 | Dairy Free Tech | mild, moist, moldy | lamarckian editors | adapts to better do its job |
| 4 | Dead God Materials | dry, delighted, dark | detritolith extracts | technology decays near it |
| 5 | Hydras and Hitches | fleshy, roiling, gassy | living fossils | randomly animates dead insects |
| 6 | Aerolith Extractions | mechanical, technical | aerolith microstructures | prone to levitating |

**Weapons Against the Blue God**

| 2 | Blue Leather Armor | Squamous fabrics feed oxygen through skin. Dive +30 minutes. Armor +2, swimming, 1 st. | €50 |
| 3 | Cloak of Scales | Swim like a manta ray. Take half damage from coherent light and fire attacks. 1 st. | €100 |
| 4 | Kawada Shield | Hard torc of translucent god-stuff no-there-ness. Armor +1, ward +1, 5 sp. | €250 |
| 5 | Godflake Reliquary | A cell of the Once Living God's skin in an amulet. Ward +2, 1 sp. | €400 |
| 6 | Peacemaker | Even outdated golem armor will overawe the Fair Bluelanders. 2 life, +2 strength. | €2k |
|  | Archaic | Armor +7, heavy, powered & environmental, cumbersome, 3 st. |  |

**Blue Land Mobility**
