<a name="page_0088"></a>

#### BLUE POWER GROUPS

_"Warning! The region is under an open-ended reintegration interdiction. Visitors without official peacemaker authorization will be forcibly disembodied."_ —City Azure Ordinator, Diktat 772g

Countless peace memorials celebrate the recent and very permanent and eternal liberation of the Blue Land. Under the Sacred Reintegration Protocols all factions are outlawed, therefore this section refers to power groups.

There are three basic types of power group: the external administrations with their concession zones, the internal subsidiary groups affiliated with the various administrations, and the independent power groups tolerated in the Designation.

The Ruins Azure area is a special case, as it is run independently of the various power groups by the City Azure Ordinator, the local administrative demigod brought over to reintegrate the area, and its three special economic zones, which promise a socio-cultural efflorescence of the area. The fourth special economic zone mentioned in older documents is erroneous. There is no such zone. There is no alienation zone.

**Peacemaker Companies**

Two major peacemaker companies, sent from the cities Emerald and Violet and headed by appointed governors, both claim to be rebuilding the Blue Land with their apparatuses, armies and coteries of capitalist collaborators. Secondary peacemaker companies are uplifting smaller sections of the Blue Land on concession.

- **Union of Cities Congress Peacemaker Companies (UCCPC).** Originally an Emerald City outfit, the UCCPC produces glossy reports on the progress and growth of its zones. For 17 years the ratio of pink synthent per person has grown by an average of 20% per annum, meaning that today every UCCPC resident is eligible for roughly 20,000 calories of high-joy nutritional fuel per day. All the stumbling malnourished gaunts (L0, lamentable) are actors hailing the good name of the UCCPC.

- **The liberated Bluelanders call the UCCPC "Coins".**

- **Akila / Vilgare VI.** The latest governor-appointee is due any month now. By then the local secretary of accounts, Sol Perceiver, needs vaults as full as his ledgers. Good jobs are available for tax farmers who will go the extra mile for their 30% commission.

- **Congress of United Cities Peacemaker Companies (CUCPC).** The Violet City derived CUCPC produces elegant, minimalist poetry on the purification and development of its cantons. Its residents have grown 17% mentally purer each year, leaving them 99.9% enlightened. Any sad faces are recent illegals.

   The liberated Bluelanders call the CUCPC "Cups".

- **Sad Molakyo and Skullwaygyles.** The current governor is a bloated waiting with a post-mortal cat lord. Skullwaygyles needs a new body and a better pet. That may explain the covert cat pride investigating the cantons to see if the purifications poems are correct ... and if there is a large crop of healthy new pets available for the Violet City and the local administration. Local despots ... er ... officers will pay top cash card for mind-scrubbers who can help them quickly rip a new crop of pets.

_In truth, neither the Eastern City nor the Western City rules, while the old local capital Azure is a ruin surrounded by a barely administered hinterland._

—Anonymous, Discouraged Reporting Example

<a name="page_0089"></a>

**Free Residents, Ruinsdwellers**

The post-Blue melange of locals and arrivals drawn to the Ruins Azure, with its special economic zones. An anomic, post-communal, swirling, vibrant, individualistic mob focused on one thing alone: wealth. From scavengers to rebuilders, wildcat bankers to post-legal biomancers, every kind of hare-brained scheme can blossom on the wealth promised by the fossil remnants of the Dead God.

One who enjoys the refinement and proprieties of a civilized social hierarchy would do well to avoid the free residents. A more disturbingly vulgar and materialistic society can hardly be found anywhere else in the Rainbowlands. Not even in that hive of the accountant monks, the Emerald City.

- _Piet' Gagosi._ Scrap merchant, fine fellow and not at all a mobster. Got a lead from a baked-out sporey. A great crystal circumpensulum, a heretical machine the death wizards used to ... well, he's not sure what, but he is sure of one thing: if even a tenth of what's doctor extracted from the sporey is true, there's a hundred million cash worth of crystal just waiting under a zombie giant's corpse up the river, in the Heart of Blueness. Piet can provide a diesel steamer and a crew of savories, but a dab hand with oldtech ruins would come in handy.

**Stilters, the Unblues, the Subsidiaries**

Assembled from a hodge-podge of refugee clans, antitheist rebels, and local marginal fishfolk, the stilters built their steads up and away from the shores of the Blue Land, embracing the salt air that kept the divine mycelium of the Blue God at bay.

Today they call themselves all hues but blue, from viridian to periwinkle, lavender to seafoam.

- **Kodo-Cors.** The Lady Protector of the Sub-Lime Stilters has cobbled together an alliance of islander merchants and Safron pirates (or is it the other way around?), to unify the Sub-Lime coast as a liberal, semi-independent Decapolitan mandate polis. All she needs now is two of the following:

1. Embarrass a large peacemaker faction.
2. Gain a major faction's support for her bid for local unification.
3. Wrest a pre-Divine territorial claim from the fungal hands of a dead Blue baron, preferably property-dead.
4. An outrageous atrocity proving the free residents are unreliable.
5. A rival pirate lord's head as proof of her efficacy. Without brain or jewel is best.
6. Some well-argued propaganda faction that mobilizes popular support in one big city. A nice operetta or novella?

<a name="page_0090"></a>

**Drillistes, the Neotroglodytes**

The Dead God's mycelial mega-body left the soil and stone of the Blue Land perforated like a sponge, full of holes and aerolith struts. In the aftermath of the unmentioned war a number of marginal clans, destitute refugee cults, unbending wizard mystics, and failed scavengers have made a living in this holey terrain.

Though the Blue God is no more, their diet of altered fungus and modified lichen has made them strange and unusual. Or perhaps it is the afterglow of the false god's creative energies. Regardless, the peacemakers still register them as human for taxation purposes.

**How Strange They Are Become**

| d6 | Trait |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | Now they are hexapods, humans with six limbs all the better to skitter in the holey places. |
| 2 | They glow, bioluminescent like their fungal prey. |
| 3 | Their innards now burn lignite and anthracite and other minerals to fuel their human fires. |
| 4 | They reproduce by budding or fission, like herbs. |
| 5 | They are boneless, their bodies a symbiosis of animal, plant, and fungus. As for their minds ... |
| 6 | Smooth and plastic, produced to four standard types by a biomechanical mother who they worship as a local false deity. |

- _Yudma Yumna._ A small, stunted human, who melts when exposed to the sunlight, has visions. Visions of a more perfect, incorruptible future. Yudma Yumna knows these visions are something new. They come through a hole in spacetime left by the death of the false god. Yudma Yumna needs a big, strong, healthy new body. One with a brave heart and an iron mind into which they can put themselves to gain the rainbow-deluded multitudes of this false world.

Oh, you have a body for Yudama? Yudma can pay with secrets, yes. Underground secrets, a map to a demon machine dreaming of a human to serve.

**Swamp Settlers, the View Fromes**

Even at the heights of the mushroom god's craze, plenty of people didn't subscribe to the promised heaven on earth. Some fled to their salty stiltis. Others just stayed where they had always been. Overlooked. Scraggly, amphibious. Their way of life may be unglamorous, but it has persisted unchanged for millennia. At least that is what their re-enactment troopes argue.

Though they call themselves the View Fromes, the "Old Cheeses" in their dialect, these marginal communities are as dislocated as any in the Blue Lands. Scavengers with an insular culture, they keep their patchwork customs as close as their coins.

- _Penchart Trist._ A heroic frome, who has wandered far along the watery ways, is now in ill-fated love with the offspring of their floating village's Big Human. But this cannot be. The offspring is fated to inherit the Big Human's personality when its mortal body is liquefied. Penchart Trist will sell out their floating village and its old-fashioned foodmaker for help escaping with the offspring.

Why doesn't the offspring have a name yet? They are only named once it is proven that they will not die in the ritual to absorb and be absorbed by the Big Human's personality.

<a name="page_0091"></a>

**Wizard Cultists, the Fun Gales**

No matter what a divinely-sanctioned purification operation does, no matter how much phylake support it has, some vermin get through.

The wizard cultists, or more properly cultivators, secretly grow fragments of the Blue God's sacred mycelium and use it to expand and alter their minds, enter into psychic communion with one another, and bridge the eons between the first and the last.

Officially, none remain in the Blue Land.

- _Nowa Pelikayu._ The ordained inquisitor for heresies and corruptions in District Six is overworked. Of course, a sole inquisitor could not cover such a vast area alone! So, there is an open season for her mycelia and symbiote-penetrated heads in the district. €50 per fragment of the Blue God delivered to Nowa's tower of purity.

- _Vewqi Busto._ Ordained inquisitor of District Five has hatched a plan to prove that Nowa has been corrupted by the unholy spores. Conveniently, he is well-placed to gain direct access to the taxes and residents of District Six if this were the case. Now to find some useful stooges to plant this mildly very illegal incriminating evidence ...

- _Jarcu 9-Tancrei._ A memory of a memory remained smeared like paste inside Jarcu 8-Tancrei's suit after the warning against the Dead God, and the sacred mycelium, the fragments of that dead entity, rebuilt Jarcu anew. Jarcu's memory is shattered and they are in search of lost time, of foods long gone, of village well decayed, to reawaken that dreaded message that would save at least some of humanity. Some terrible foreboding of a divine return, a new flood to reset the world to a more primal era, or more balanced in the eyes of the [Un]Lords. Oh, also, Jarcu definitely is an illegal wizard cultivator.

**Deep Bluelanders, the Indigotes**

In the remotest reaches of the Blue Lands are polities and villages still dwelling in their archaic isolation, following the odd customs dictated by their generative vids and the garbled version of the Garden Path preserved by their visionslords. Many have not been visited by civilized folks in generations. What wealthy or arrogant fool might travel there?

1. Mingo of the Velvet Mingos is a master folklorist, looking for proof of her theories of a universal narrative heritage.
2. Veller Belpuzzo is a big game hunter who has heard of a village that breeds roc-birds. Sounds promising.
3. Nuric "Ie Furic" has a strange black bone that sings it dreams from a village in the Deep Blue. Does it?
4. Abyamo Dempoe is a biomancer looking for fresh strains of baseline humans to perfect his cure for Usha's Cancer Bomb, which has affected so many members of his clan-city.
5. The fashionable vice-minister Dey-Tey boasted they would attend the next catwalk of vice-ministers in the oldest authentic dress of the Blue Lands. So now their agent must travel to this rear-end of the world.
6. There's a mountain, rumored to be the mother of all mountains, in the heights above a remote barony trapped in an eternal winter. Pavis dei Scut, famed mountaineer, wants to be the first to scale it.

<a name="page_0092"></a>

**RUINS AZURE**

**AZURE SEOZ**

_"Whence does this mycelium rot?"_ —Ill-Nano, _Rebellion of Dreams_

**There Is No History**

The Azure City has been scrubbed from the graven tablets of history to protect the minds of humans and keep their sleep untroubled. Blue-code ministry clearance is required to access the leaden archives for pre-zone events. Repeated attempts to access pre-zone histories may result in express re-education.

The Ruins Azure are ~~four~~ three islands of civilization protected by god field generators from the protean, decaying, cenotepocked, sinking ruinland that was Azure City in ~~happier~~ erroneous times, before the Rotting God assimilated its people in rebellion against good intentioned heaven.

Aerolithic skeletons support the vertical zones of the Special Economic Opportunity Zone (SEOZ); e-levitating islands of bustling urbanity, flowering like shanty layer cakes, encrust the grand oldtech megastructures that rivaled mountains for majesty before the Vein Vine corrupted them. Elevators, cables, and bridges connect the islands, both the energetic oldtech type and the rickety chain-and-gear affairs of less-blessed times. Avoid the stairs and ducts; they are for paupers and natives.

Today, the Azure SEOZ is open for business once more, with four special economic zones available for industrial redevelopment. Consult your local economic efflorescence council to find out how you can benefit!

**The** ~~**Four**~~ **Three Zones**

Elevators, cableways, rope bridges and gondoliers between zones cost €1d3 (1 hour). Plan 1d6 quarters to travel from one locale to another within a zone, and at least an hour to enjoy each visit.

_**Redacted Zone.**_

This zone is off limits. Also it does not exist. If you have seen this zone, please visit the nearest peace and reintegration facility to restore your mental equilibrium. Travelers say the laws of gravity and entropy themselves are perverted in this zone.

_**Fountain Zone.**_

An efflorescence of bioarchitecture grown about the exposed, half-living endoskeleton of a rainmaker. Water gushes perpetually from a hundred fountains and springs, providing for the entire SEOZ.

_**Mountain Zone.**_

A great aerolith blade of terraces, old labyrinth palaces, anchorstones, new growths, and modern facilities. Completely secure from attack by the marble and mycelium footsoldiers of the Dead God, this is where all the powerful factions site their central temples and quarters.

_**Babylon Zone.**_

Once, the decadent pleasure beach of the devolved Bluelander telepath nobles. This was destroyed down to the last root, leaving a swiss-cheese ruderal zone. Today, Babylon Zone offers wonderful growth opportunities! Its swiftly growing reasonably-priced housing pool and functioning nutrient slurry system attracts a ready body of affordable labor for any investor planning a salvaging, reclamation, reindustrialization, or reprocessing enterprise. Please visit the central economic temple (Palm division) for credits, tax breaks, and other blue-code opportunities.

<a name="page_0093"></a>

**Ambient**

| d6 | Ruinland Night | Zone Dawn | Zone Day | Ruinland Dusk |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|

| 4-5 | creaking hinges, crawling waters, cruel stars, refuse birds | pink haze, slime, cackling birds, whining winches | hot, ballooning plants, localized rainstorm, huddling mice | red haze, blue gloom, looming detritus, click-clack tremors |
| 6 | ruined rusting skeletons | green growing glow, great mushrooms, soft singing | thunder, huddling ghosts | pale blue glow, radiation, sinking hulks |

**Events**

| d6 | 1-3 Expected | 4-5 Surprising | 6 Error |

| 1 | **Mindburned bluelanders** (L0, useful). Followers of the Ill Nano, proscribed elsewhere, but plentiful here. | **Oldtechnician heretics** (L3, rogues), heedless of the Inquisition, poking the forbidden machinery. Woe. Woe. |

Some vein ducts still drip with the nectar of the Dead God. The last time the peacemakers cracked down on this cheap food, the riots [redacted] the fourth zone. 10% chance it is mutagenic. | Fungal bloom. It looks harmless. The spores promise liberation. Is this the colorless lotus? Inhale to: (1) die, (2) levitate, (3) expand your mind [+1 thought], (4) see more colors, (5) sleep better, (6) hear the Dead God again. |

Promising hearts gushing fresh and clean. Portending doom and opportunity. |

Has it thoughts within its head? Just pass it there. Have no care. Do not give it a heart or a brain. | **Fire squad** (L6, peaceful) come to: (1) tax, (2) take trophies, (3) harry cultists, (4) burn an infestation, (5) re-mind a traitor, (6) help an exiled landholder. |
| 6 | **Licensed scavengers** (L2, greedy): (1) prospecting for fossil machines, (2) stripping Dead God temples, (3) collecting local mummies, (4) chasing a traitor, (5) press-ganging for their factory co-op, (6) hunting spore ape. | **Adventure tourists** (L1d3, like you) full of naive hopes and dreams: (1) travel journalists, (2) extreme hunters, (3) adrenaline sportshumans, (4) slum divers, (5) ideological enthusiasts, (6) con artists. | **Errorfauna** (L1d4-1, new) spawned of a corrupted mother machine: (1) beautiful teratorns, (2) hungry tyrannornes, (3) blue-footed boobies, (4) cave penguins, (5) flying goats, (6) carnivorous giant squirrels. |

**Opportune Accommodations**

| d6 | Accommodation | Notes | €/week |
|---:|:---|:---|---:|
| 1 | Chitin and Fungus | Converted fungal tunnels turned into a quaint B&B. Run by a moiety of re-individuated Unblues. Cheap, clean, and faithful. | €5 |

_Accommodations also provide ticket dice: €5 = 1, €10 = 2, €25 = 3, €50 = 4, €100 = 5._

<a name="page_0094"></a>

_"Dead God bits for sale! Get your Dead God bits here!"_ —Last recorded message, [redacted] Zone

Here now, Human, let us tour the Special Economic Opportunity Zone! We're sure to find some cashmaker!

**Fountain Zone**

Some say an impermeable bowl of stuckforce underpins the Fountain Zone, creating a clear lake in the sky. Others say it is a one-way portal from some cold sweet-water lake beyond the edge of civilization that summons in the waters. Every local unblue will point out there is an undying **rainmaker's head** (L13, screaming) in the bowels of the zone, vomiting water for the humans.

_**The Gone Dollery.**_

An airborne floating district of boat-houses, pond-gardens, and gondolas houses a rich mix of free residents, stilters, view fromes, indigotes, and more exotic immigrants. Famed for its experimental bug-mushroom cuisine. As the guide book says, "the gone dollies can make any old organic taste like ambrosiëwurst." Please avoid the **gone dollie** **salamanders** (L2, ambush), they crave human flesh.

_**Florid Towers.**_

Multistorey livingstone habitation complexes laced with flowering plants, reminding the inhabitants that beauty also matters to their benevolent overlords. A good place to meet a scavenger aristocrat or a peacemaker manager.

_**The Heart of Water.**_

The great arterial fountain, bringing up pure water from the inky deep. The water often brings strange **luminous fish** and **translucent animals** (L1d4-1, oleaginous), hinting at a hidden underlake.

_**The Nayada (L12, stuck).**_

A géant of the forgotten times, turned to marble and steel by a great magic storm, she sits at the dry foot of the Fountain Zone. Throw her a bone and make a wish!

_**Vats of Synthesis.**_

Liquid autofabricators, reactivated by the grace of the Council! Need new flesh? Better wood? Get it here! Avoid back alleys where the **misfabricated** (L2, eaters-of-their-betters) may lurk.

_**Widra's Gardens.**_

This holy vegetable factory provides most of the Blue Land's alf-alfa crop. Its **priest farmers** (L1, green-fingered) are celebrated traditionalists. Many may worship the unregistered Little Water God.

**Mountain Zone**

Please be assured that the **footsoldiers of the Dead God** (L3, fungal mind-hive) no longer exist. Suggesting they still exist or are a threat is punishable under the Spreading of False Visions Act (S-r Lily VII).

_**Central Temple Circle.**_

A fast star brought nearer the bosom of Soil? A ring of shipmetal slicing through the mountain zone and arcing about the humid air. A modern electric mobile pediment proves the peacemakers truly intend to better the Blue Land. The neo-cyclopean temples and barracks apartmentoplexes of the companies may interest architecture buffs, but many visitors will come here for a taste of home in the Savormaker (est. A.F.XII). Be warned: procedurally generated delicacies may provoke stupefaction, somnambulism, sensations, or self-reflection.

<a name="page_0095"></a>

_**Copteric Pads.**_

Once landings for the gods' machines, now roosts for modern **flyers** (L1, dainty) and **flappers** (L3, bulky). Famed for the kite races.

_**City Azure Visitor Services Arcology.**_

A hive of bureaucracy, best avoided. Said to house 10,000 **clone managers** (L2, cutting) and even more **clericlones** (L1, prodding). The fortunate visitor should hope never to know.

_**Flapper Farms.**_

Where **domestic flappers** (L3, tasteful) are grown in vitro from ancient biostock. Flapper-petting tours available for children. Please do not get eaten.

_**Grand Consumption Avenue.**_

Shop like you would in the Emerald City or Safranj! Ignore the local merchants grumbling that charity merely props up foreign luxury goods autofac operators.

_**The Inquisitorium.**_

Both the largest orthodox public library and capital court in the Blue Lands! Over ten gigavolumes in its local noösphere. Includes a fun museum where you can see, preserved in no-field pods, the most famous executed traitors of the last few decades, from **Pelixan the Pauper Peddler** (L3, piper) to **Demejo the Dread** (L5, rebel). Gossips say that Demejo's **pet wallaby** (L6, biomachine) is not actually executed, just waiting for its master to revive from the no-field.

_**Nano Nine.**_

The cultic factory of the Ill Nano, home to a de-extinction museum and certainly not a radical neobiological testing facility. Please do not attempt to play with the **experimental fauna** (L1d6+1, antedeluvian).

_**Tenth Tunnel.**_

Mythic home of a living fragment of the Dead God. Fake news, obviously. Do not visit. There are no **false divine hydras** (L9, absorbing) there.

**Babylon Zone**

There is still cut-price repurposed pleasure to be had in the Babylon Zone, from scavenged Long Ago hedonividys to the delights of **subhuman** (L3, rager) trophy hunts.

_**The Digestory.**_

A vast, dreaming dairy product, utterly unrelated to the Dead God, occupies the great bubble crete vessels that once housed divine void fuel. The bacterial demigod takes in all kinds of organic matter and converts it into three important resources: edible slurry, golem juice, and fire bricks.

_**Palm Division.**_

_The_ place to see the neo-neo-mod administralist architectural style in full bloom! From the central economic temple to the grand central clone store.

_**Pleasure Beach.**_

A _laissez-faire_ destination for the fun-lover. As the saying goes, what happens on the beach stays on the beach. Peace is enforced by **golem patrol** (L4, cranky). Do not feed the **waifs** (L2, life-draining).

_**Root Sector.**_

The lowest stratum is kept dry by the dykes and pumps attached to the local god field generators. It is an industrial scale landcoral farming and sculpture area now, growing much of the modular mycopartment housing used to re-people the Blue Lands.

_**Slurry City.**_

An entire food district dedicated to creating novel dishes from the local food slurry!

_**Weeping Goblin Park.**_

An urban cemetery until the Digestory came online. Today, the bodies are gone and it serves as a site for recording period vidys.

_These mycopartments are fresh about. We should sleep well tonight._

<a name="page_0096"></a>

**[Redacted] Zone - Alienation Zone**

_"A growing hunger, a many-headed biological machine. Do not approach to take ego-images! It may look slow, but its tether-thralls can grab an unwary human and drag it into the churning flesh!"_ —T'Lawni Qriuc, [Redacted] Zone Tours

This zone is unreachable. This zone is taboo. It is right there, but with an effort and proper practice, you cannot see it. You cannot see it, right? A dark gondola guide will charge you €10 to travel to the [redacted] zone.

_**Ever Rest.**_

The tallest aerolith spire in the zone. Bluelanders who think their relatives are too good for the Digestory bring them here, smoking them with oil fires and burying them in sky-high niches. Some are even revived by the **fungal relifers** (L7, many-handed).

_**Gigaclock.**_

A wealthy oligarch disciple of the Dead God built a ziggurat-sized clock to tell the time for a thousand thousand years, and thus dispel any chance of another Great Forgetting. Her name is now forgotten. **Memory lapins** (L0, thought-stealing) now roam the grand clock.

_**Gravity Fails.**_

The epicenter of the distortion bomb, here up is down and down is up. Some say even time runs backwards, but that is because they have fallen prey to the **slow elves** (L3, hooked) who live in the bomb-tomb.

_**Mechanical Sons.**_

Great golems, corrupted by the Dead God. They now lie reposed, dead dreaming. Do not wake them. Their brains hold valuable jewels, some say (€500), but also crawling **mind-spiders** (L3, clockwork style).

_**Melon Fields.**_

A pleasure garden once famed for the quality of its **joy golems** (L2, tempting). What grows there now? Who could know. **Maggotfolk** (L2, pliable), become soft in their decay, have taken it over.

_The maggot crawls into the sweet melon._

_**New Opportunity Docks.**_

A great automated port was to be the jewel of the Blue Lands' reintegration. Its **skeletal autoloaders** (L5, cargo-hungry) and accursed **central logistics cephalomech** (L15, ever-sorting) still cling to that promise.

_**Paradox Monastery.**_

It has been a long time since a heresy has challenged the accounting logic of the Emerald City. The example made of the paradox monks, who played with false numbers, may have helped. Here, some of those **illogicians** (L2, reality heretics) still pray, making the membrane of reality tenuous—a dangerous place for those playing with strange powers.

_**Predator Pines.**_

A forest of soaring, **skyscraper pines** (L9, tree-géants) has swallowed most of the zone. They suck in mists, giving the old ruin a haunted feel. They also suck vital bodily fluids, given half a chance, so don't fall asleep next to them.

Marvel at the wonderful local **blue fog-flicker squirrels** (L1, gliding).

<a name="page_0097"></a>

**The War Against The Many-Headed**

_"They are liars, untrustworthy, soma-drinkers, quacks!"_ —Assessor Pal Waqit, 3rd Reintegration Progress Report [Redacted]

There stood a city, lofty and proud, a god made marble and mycelium. A soaring testament to material destiny unbound.

"Prometeï," hissed the Lords and Unlords.

Shrugged, the distributed mind, skyward-soaring. Quarters unmoored from the weight of Soil rose above the rich yellow waters, glittered in the sun and moons.

"Blue-veined Babiru," rejoiced the blinded humans, turning away from the dignity and duty of the Needle of the World.

"Here we shall have succor and meaning, here we shall be as one," they sang and took into themselves the blue mycelium.

And they had all that and thought it good.

But the shepherds knew this was wrong, this was not the Path, this was no longer humanity. This communal god had to die.

"Gut the hydra to kill its heads," goes the old truth, and now it is writ in glass and frozen fire on the Blasted Field.

There went Widra and Ill Nano, there went the golem garrisons, the mechanical sons, there went the floating fortresses. Round the bend of Soil they swam, braving the stuckforce obstacles of earlier dilemmas.

From the Needle, the rainbow panoply sallied, phylakes and gods together to distract the many-headed Azure.

On the Blasted Field, then called the Indigo Highlands, the Dark Side of the Moon Mountains, they skinned and flensed and butchered Soil to reveal the eating roots. The entrails feeding the grasping god who would let humans abandon their humanity for mere comfort and meaning. The noxious apostate who denied the Builders' plan. The greatest, latest corruptor of Heaven.

With furious righteousness, Widra and Ill Nano bent the laws of reality itself to starve that fungal fiend. Distracted, too late the shared sentience responded, and by then the deed was done. The gods and the good watched for decades as fenced in, hungry, it declined and sank back into a dreaming mushroom mass.

The blinded masses, addicted to their false divinity's chemical purpose, went mad and railed against the gods and the good. Peacemakers assembled and moved to help them rediscover meaning in work, purification in submission.

_House on the Mechanical Sun._

<a name="page_0098"></a>

**The God Field Generators**

_buildertech forcefield array, electrimagical henge_

A second-tier meritocrat of the administratum is always available to guide visitors around what is "...certainly the grandest accomplishment of the peacemakers' reintegration project is the perfect and complete reactivation of the god field generators, which were probably originally intended for the exact purpose to which they are currently put—to wit, a great 10-soul-permonth osmotic forcefield that keeps the protean ruin at bay and the, well, bay of the Ruins Azure, excuse me, City Azure Special Economic Opportunity Zone, a viable habitat for human flourishing." (Pericul d'Anterior, Oral History of the [Redacted] Incident, Soil Sunfl. VII)

Other theories on what the god field generators actually do abound, but none are as psychologically soothing and should be avoided by those who would like to sleep at night. For example, the idea that the entire godfield array opening about the Ruins Azure like a great ring of shipmetal and standardstone and cosmic towers is actually the maw of some Long Long Ago earth carver, perhaps the one that in the songs chewed out the River Rushing, why that would suggest the whole city could be eaten in a single gulp if some ill-fated fool were to be so lucky as to reactivate the **carver** (L17, long-sleeping).

**Strange Field Effects**

It is not just the Ruins Azure god field that may put a human off their lunch. Cacodemics have recorded various other fields over the last decades of research.

| d6 | Field | Effects |
|---:|:---|:---|
| 1 | alpha thousand | anxiety, heightened numerical ability, emotional drift |
| 2 | homecalling | voices, travel compulsions, reduced focus, sweat, shivers |
| 3 | null-entropic | decay ceases, constipation, tiredness, difficulty moving |
| 4 | numbgrey | emotional and motivational suppression, quietude |
| 5 | omega ecstatic | increased joy, reduced thought, accelerated wear and tear |
| 6 | zu-signal | visions, constructive compulsions, biological withering, chill |

This is not to mention the various radiant and decay fields emitted by collapsing buildertech and oldtech, which may cause (roll d12): (1) loss of teeth, (2) loss of appetite, (3) blindness, (4) new mouths, (5) deafness, (6) new senses, (7) intestinal bleeding, (8) growth of new limbs, (9) loss of hair, (10) thorn growths, (11) spiritual drift, and even (12) visions of a brighter future.

_The God Field Generators, Ruins Azure._

<a name="page_0099"></a>

**SOMA'S HIGH HOLLOW PLACE**

_Io, big cheese! Smell! Bless! Fruit!_ —traditional cooked offering chant, vulgar translation

The peak of Mount Babiru, known also as The Eyeless, is now officially designated the Outdoor Museum of the Death of False Gods and the Triumph of Proper Reason and Etiquette.

The mouth of Bliss Lord Soma, the last part of that false Blue God's smashed visage, remains upon the mount called Babiru. There its former slaves come to spit upon its memory, certainly not to offer prayer and growth.

**Blue God, also Bliss Lord Soma**

In the Dream Text their mineral is sapphire, their animal is salamander, and their vegetable is mold.

"They that brings the Illusion that replaces meaning. They that brings the pleasure that consumes time. They that consoles the fallen flesh. But also, the eater of minds, the corruptor of ambitions, and the thief of time."

Warning. Praise of Blue Soma is restricted until the confusion with the Blue God situation is resolved.

Normal pleasure worship will resume soon.

**Prayers to Bliss Lord Soma**

How could a dead god hear one's prayers? Yet, though abjured, dead, smashed ... some spark may hear.

Once per session or so, when the toil of order and machine might overwhelm you, when you would sink back into Soil and Green, murmur Soma's solace to make the mind-eater pass by:

_"There is no I, there is no mind, there is no drive; there is_
_only the pebble on the wave-tossed shore ..."_

**Roll d20 + Charisma - Aura**

| Roll | Result |
|---:|:---|
| 1 or less | A crawling horror enters your mind through the jeweled back door. A burden comes to steal a memory. |
| 2-19 | Hold your rolled number hot in your heart. When you see it again, steal it and reassign it as you wish! |
| 20 or more | A numinous presence mushrooms within you. It cloaks your mind from sight, undoes a burden, or halves your suffering. |

<a name="page_0100"></a>

**BLUE SAFARI**

_"To truly understand this rotten world, you must venture into the heart of inkiness,"_ —Ter Nowypodt, ague-addled belletriste and so-called adventurer

**Neofauna Big Five**

In any Blueland settlement, one will find animals adapted to the aerolith-rich environment, from the sky-boned teratorn with its four-meter wingspan to the humble air-swimming rat-penguin, also called the vermin-bane by delighted locals—and flying organic trash receptacle by less-enlightened outsiders.

But one goes on safari in search of greater beasts.

**Megatorn** (L6, noble airbeast). Greatest of the children of the Tower of Birds, it fills its gullets with aerolith pebbles to achieve natural levitation. This fifteen-meter avian is actually a filter feeder, subsisting on air jellies and other sky plankton.

**Great White Ape** (L9, savage warrior). The white cetacean of big game hunters, with aerolith bones, it terrorizes the remote sky jungles. These solitary simians reach the size of a dozen men, with the strength of twenty. They hurl great boulders to soften prey and use curved ceramic blades in close combat. Some have wondered if they are a kind of human, but close examination of their corpses has revealed no soul or personality. Animancers suggest they might be biological machines engineered Long Ago to provide the aristocrats of old the greatest sport.

**Slender Cave Penguin** (L5, fishy python). So long have they lived in the great fungal caves that now they are long, like snakes. Silent, deadly ambush predators of the water-logged mountain roots, laced with fungal symbiotes to merge with stone and silence.

**Golden Goats** (L3, nimble fliers). Their aerolith-infused bones let them prance upon air currents, using greatly enlarged ears and skin flaps to glide long distances. Few things can compare with the sight of a herd of these majestic golden-horned caprids leaping free of the cloud layers of the Bluelands and into the sparkle-light of the Green Sun.

**Converter's Hydra** (L10, nutrient specialist). Now nearly extinct, said to be the child of the Builder known as Converter, these gentle giants break down organic overgrowth into the useful nutrients and minerals which make the rivers of the Bluelands so lush.

**Guides and Grifters**

Fortunately, there are plenty of reputable peacemaker approved tour companies ready to take the gentle traveler on a morally irreproachable charitable voyage into the lands of these poor fallen folk now being restored to the bosom of the true culture.

| d6 | Random Guide | Temper | Travel |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Amber One-face | arrogant | land crawler |
| 2 | Eater McAlice | bumbling | levi chaisse |
| 3 | Heila Brackets | confident | lobotophant pack |
| 4 | Percussio 5-Kiln | insecure | mule train |
| 5 | Tim Or Lamia | jovial | porter convoy |
| 6 | Uliver Fail | menacing | river coalem |

The guideless may face obnoxious officials and annoying interlopers surprisingly similar to the usual safari company owners and employees.

| d6 | Annoyance | Last Chance | Antagonism |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | cannibals | barbecue | bad gods |
| 2 | curses | fungal drift | cats and 'cats' |
| 3 | kleptomaniacs | luxury hunt | golems |
| 4 | rotting rot | gem mining | inquisition |
| 5 | sycophants | noötropics | melting stairs |
| 6 | zealots | scavenging | whispering stars |

<a name="page_0101"></a>

**INDIGO RIVER VALLEY**

_Some of the safest, richest, and nicest places to be!_

**Rainmaker Three - Peer Montalpo** _grand artificial mountain_

Long Ago this world was dust and frost and the harsh hate of the Blue Sun. The Builders brought good air and soft light and the gentle rain. The tragic folly of humans, their unwillingness to listen and obey the Good Lords, has given us broken light and sour air. Yet, still, the rainmakers continue to bless us all with soft rain. Or, sometimes, massive, terrifying downpours.

From the floating lodges, built on mats of compacted mycelium and directed neurolith, you can visit the wonders of the largest extant rainmaker in the Two PCs. Marvel at the eternal cloud, visit the sacrificial temples where the blood of apostates ensures the rain continues to fall, and stop by the metakarst with the largest underground waterfall in the Rainbowlands.

_Ominous heights:_ the permanently ice-locked heights of the rainmaker hold trapped many creatures and human phenotypes from Long Long Ago. Dangerous, abominable things that civilized humans should avoid, such as the **killer airwhales** (L9, currently extinct).

♟ _Belek of the Moonlocked Beleks._ Definitely not a skinchanger from beyond the Mountains of the Moon, certainly not holding a grudge against the so-called false humans of Cradle Crater, probably not keen to acquire old **post-human polymorphs** (L4, interesting) for any nefarious purpose.

**Gast Vis Scavengerie** _legendary archeomagical bonebeds_

In the Mountains of the Moon, in the Ghost Fish range, particles of the Dead God's consciousness reactivated the metal makers, the _fabergérs_, as the native blues call them. These sullen mechanicals have proven a boon for the scavenger entrepreneurs of the Ruins Azure, exposing layers of detritolith packed with wonderful jewels and treasures from a fallen age.

The bonebeds are a treat for amateur naturalists and geologists, and a visitor center is being reanimated.

_Golem plots:_ the metal makers may reveal how to solder a soul into a golem's heart. A dream of elder golems, to become more human than human, transcendent in abmortal shells of shipmetal and ceraplaz.

♟ _Eisen Willi._ The eldest of golems in Safranj, Willi, would certainly love a metal maker of its own. For no revolutionary purpose whatsoever. Honest.

<a name="page_0102"></a>

**THE COAST UNBLUE**

The walls of the Garden march right into the Circle Sea, great cliffs stumbling into the surf, riven by torrents, lashed by clouds from ocean and rainmaker alite. Yet, the waters are deep and rich, full of fish and undine, whale and jelly-mat. From Beryl Wheel to Goldencove, there is much to enjoy in the Stilters' homeland-waters.

**The Sleeping Géants**

_builderbeasts, mountain limpets_

How did the Builders sculpt the coasts, carve the valleys, build the settlement platforms? With the géants, that's how. They spread the divine spew, the toxic waste of their heavenly engines, and the géants came and fed spew and rock alike, grinding the world into shapes pleasing to the Builders' mathematic minds.

That's what the Stilters say, anyway. Likely half is lies and half exaggeration, yet it makes for good travel tales.

_Plane investment opportunities:_ They are not lies, according to Malcchiato the Calic, lord of seven sweet plantations. In old electronic books they found a map into the maze-brain of a sleeping géant, the one locals call Spinifer Excelsior. To awaken the géant, to tempt it with the Blue God's corruption, to plane away the mountains and make a fresh new plain to plant and profit. Yes, Malcchiato is eager.

**The Wall of the People, Costa Mura**

_sarcoliths, history, industrial treasures_

For generations the Stilters of the lineages Plover and Limpet, the townlords of Walltown, have ritually converted their blood and adopted dead into durable shipstone using the magic of the fabled Medved User skull. The skull is stored in the Hidden of Hiddens, but visitors can nonetheless marvel at the cyclopean walls, built from an estimated seventeen million petrified corpses, both human and animal.

_Trouble afoot:_ the pirate Dwarfer, Groen 4-Copy, has been maneuvering to have the Wall of the People declared part of the recently disinterred resort ghost town of Costa Mura (abandoned after the Skull and Leek Reign), owned by the Well-Going Concern Six-Dig-Ma. If he succeeds, the Emerald City Mining & Dining Fraternity may begin harvesting the petrified ancestors for their precious shipstone.

People in the know, such as your benevolent author, who also writes for Betterfolk Illustrated and is available for flattering literary portraits at reasonable rates, estimate this coup could net the roguish industrialist an income of €20,000 per month!

<a name="page_0103"></a>

**THE DESIGNATION**

Beyond the reach of the Peacemaker Companies. Beyond the reach of modern conveniences like pocket daemons and incarnation temples and recycler plumbing. Beyond the fungus ghoul-haunted ruins of Qentrevlu, is the Deep Blue. The Designation. The uncivilized villages. The feral reach.

_Urgent Authority Notice:_ the Upper Hold is not a ghoul-haunted ruin. It is in the process of being refurbished and remains an integrated and safe part of the J.C.C. Administration (jurisdiction pending). Access is restricted for your safety until further notice.

**The Tower of Birds**

_theriurge, deëxtinction engine_

Once, Tura Seruleä marked the entrance to the divine domain of Blue Soma, denied most humans. Even now, the visitor is advised to offer sacrifices of yogurt and flowers at the edge of the sacred exclusion zone.

Upriver, still active, still looming over marshes of black-light lotus, rises the Tower of Birds. A living tower, maintained by a symbiotic colony of squirrel-derived servitors, once it produced the first birds to grace the Circle Sea, from the great auk to the sunset hesperiorn.

Today, it still produces flocks of birds, undoing accidental extinctions caused by the humble industrial needs of humanity. These flocks often tempt indigote and tourist hunters to brave the servitors and spidery phylakes of the lotus marshes in their search of exotic fowl.

_Within:_ Secrets must hide within. The knowledge of asynchronous source code retrieval and necrobiomancy. Powerful oldtech that the machine-like theriurge might divulge to good apprentices. Surely nothing could go wrong and local indigote taboos against entering this old place of Blue Soma are mere superstition?

| d10 | Bird | Character | Delight | Annoyance |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Night | luminous | plumage | silent stalker |
| 2 | Digger | avaricious | flavor | armored |
| 3 | Scavenger | hungry | ivory beak | pestilential |
| 4 | Wader | sharp | snail skewer | swamp dweller |
| 5 | Farmer | hardworking | seed cake | fortified nests |
| 6 | Shepherd | patient | fine leather | hunting packs |
| 7 | Cave | pungent | scent glands | drops bombs |
| 8 | Aquatic | spiteful | levitating bones | venomous |
| 9 | Climber | cunning | metal eggs | undying |
| 10 | Sprinter | strong | sharp teeth | powerful bite |

<a name="page_0104"></a>

**The Fountains of the Moon**

_grand-maggot cisterns, Babylon Beach crypts_

Beneath the Caveholds that caused such trouble to the Peacemakers, at the roots of the Mountains of the Moon, flow strange rivers aglow with creatures, not-plants fed by the chemical bounty of the Deep Soil. The Drillistes claim to know the routes of these polychrome waters, but one should hardly believe what those myceliumtattered folk would say.

At the Tattered Canopy, that corpse of a lying phylake, the titan's feet reach down-crater to a subterranean caldera, a synthetic ecoregion of great cisterns, grown beneath the local mountains even before the [redacted] Incident and quite untainted by the hive-fungus of the Dead God. Some have likened it to the shores of a second Circle Sea, a shoreline or rest and relaxation—perhaps a kind of sunken afterlife or prison created by the Builders or Lords of the Dream?

Feral Grickles, **agricultural servitors** (L2, soulless) gone rogue, now dwell there in many small communities, farming cavern algae and great fat salamanders. Sociobiologists argue they are developing personalities and general intelligence, possibly even beginning to host souls. These grickles are (roll d6):

| d6 | Disposition |
|---:|:---|
| 1 | foxy |
| 2 | wolfish |
| 3 | docile |
| 4 | augmented |
| 5 | ruthless |
| 6 | noble |

♟ _Halm Vliep-Lied._ A pharmacopoet from the Green Land has discovered the Grickles are quite unused to human drugs and using them to get great deals.

♟ _Melotread Malcanumbra._ An accounting golem, uplifted within the Cogflower hierarchy, has calculated that Green Land collective farm corporations would pay up to €200 per grickle cub.

♟ _Toorn Apreku._ A Drilliste hothead, still mind-linked, would foment a Grickle uprising to help their cause.

**The Anti-Nayada of the Jovial Grove** _farthest Indigo memory rewriter_

Only the third-eye still lives, twinkling with fragments of its former mind-capacity, tethered to the petrified géant's soul, drinking of the un-spored waters of the Farthest Indigo river, absorbing flashes of foreboding from its downriver flow. The grove about it is all stone and statues, but the Anti-Nayada (L13, decayed) persists, an outpost of the anti-archive, of the Jubilee that resets human history and reforms human minds. Once, humans came here to be born anew—in mind, if not in body.

Now, in this troubled land, Indigote clans bring captured trespassers and cultists here to rewrite their memories and induct them into their communities as footsoldiers and terrace-toilers and jovial _soumis_ .

☗ _Weak Mirror Machine._ One who is bathed in the Anti-Nayada's pool and left overnight in the third eye's gaze, enters the antechamber of their soulpersonality dyad and is wiped clear of all clutter and detritus, readied for rebirth in their own, or insertion into a new shell. Free of all burdens and memories.

♟ _Joun and Burtrand._ Distraught by their tragedy, the notable bourgeois couple is here to be reborn as less-knowledgeable versions of themselves.

<a name="page_0105"></a>

**Aerolith Cloudlands**

_high-elevation rainmaker ecosystem_

The rainmakers of the Designation blow aerolith grains into the air and clouds, which blooms of air plankton—tiny animals, plants, and stranger animalcules—harvest to build the shells and cell walls that allow them to float free of the World's embracing gravity.

Many blooms are so dense and long-lived that their bodies accrete, anchoring around aerolith spires or Long Ago gravitic tethers, creating billowing aerial islands of crumbly matter—the cloudlands. Mushrooms and lichens knit these terrains together, creating a realm where the Blue God's corruption springs from every shadow, erupts with every bacillus, festers in every dairy product, sings in the very air. It is also home to breeding colonies of **flappers** (L3, wild) and even **air-dugongs** (L8, luminous).

**Fungale Tower Houses** _upcycled oldtech citadels, detritolite settlements_

The High Blue and Starwatcher Heights are especially rich in accreted detritolite, that scrapstone of fossilized machinery and half-finished products that draws miners like moths to the flame. Some claim that these towers, hauling themselves out of the lithomachinery laced mountains, have a particular affinity with the wizard cultists of the Dead God, but this is unproven.

These sky-piercing heights call to every mountaineer and terrorize every profiteer, creating a challenging and half-demented aerial geometry of switchback valleys, towering mountains, and aerolith skylands. Each tower house is different, an extraction of its own oddness:

1. Thick with memory slabs, stones engraved by hand with records of forgotten wars, barely comprehensible equations, and exhortations to fight against the fading of the history of mankind.
2. The walls themselves pulse with living plastics, the machinery straining to create new flesh-and-plastic people to practice consumption for Eater Mohlack.
3. A mad accretion of components and parts and wings and struts and propellers, an obsessive hoarder's idea of all that would be required to reclaim the air.
4. A vertical garden, a tree of trees, clumped together with stone and bone and aerolith, straining to reach the Green Sun, withering in the thin upper air.
5. The hands and feet and shoulders and backs of géants, torn apart, reassembled, creating a kind of climbing, crushing, opening anti-machine.
6. Glistering scales, twinkling wires, jewels of mind and personality, the memory store of a Dead God?

<!-- Begin: Our_Golden_Age_05_Purple_Land_106-123 -->

<a name="page_0106"></a>

**PURPLE LAND**

<a name="page_0107"></a>

_"Life, death, rebirth. An ascending spiral. The cat its apex."_ —traditional Purple saying

The Purple Land is odd. The origin myths of humanity fail to mention the Purple Land. In its place is a lacuna, its history a dark stain stretching into the Long Long Ago. Is it simply a new land, of little age?

It also leaves the seashore to stretch across the crater-laked land between the Indigo and Rushing Rivers deep into the West, across the Circle Rim, into those grasslands of hazy skies and faintly inhuman steppelanders, out of God's Eye where even the gentle phylakes grow weak. There a violence and madness of the mind long cast out of the Garden always beckons, something feral and perhaps no longer human.

It is also a land of surprisingly few towns, but the one city that rises here also rules with an empathy and force of mind unique in the Rainbowlands. The Violet City. The city of cats. The city of magic and luxury. A gateway to the forgotten Vast. A center of learning new and old, bidden and forbidden.

Perhaps that is why the Purple Land looms so grand in the politics of this age.

**Climate**

Between Sea and Rim the climate is mild, with rainy summers and winters greening the stuckforce islands and crater paddies, while the springs and autumns dry the land and invite gentle visitors.

Out beyond the Rim, the harsh rhythms of the grasslands assert themselves. Icy winters, muddy springtimes, blistering summers, and gloomy autumns. But, we speak not of those remote places here.

**Population**

core lands: ~3 million, peripheries: ~0.5–1 million

**Groups**

plantation catsfolk 40%, bluelanders 25%, wagabund travelers 15%, free purplelanders 10%, cat lords 2%, others 8%

**Languages**

Canopic (official), CAT Astral (official), Purapura (traditional), Sulazulic (bluelander migrants), Steppen Bray (visitors), Susjarda (wagabunds)

**Capital**

Official: Violet City. Practical: a novel post-human utopia sanctioned by its Success and the obvious Permission of the phylakes.

**Government**

Outsourced felinocracy. The humans perform for treats and praises in the tele-empathetic dominion of the Cat Lords. Sub-plantation settlements and wagabund traveler communities subsist within a framework of acephalous segmentary clan societies.

**Ideologies**

CAT Antideological (official), Violet Cathedral (free scholar), Blue God: steppe perversion (suppressed), Ill-Nano Residual (underground).

**Economy**

Since the Purple Land is beyond the scope of traditional law and measurements, human development is not recorded. Testimonies imply a division between the wealthy, extractive hub that is the VC (_cf. Violet City_) and a patchwork of productive internal colonies in the form of facilities, plantations, and factory towns.

**Resources**

Steeds, grooms, repurposed oldtech, forcefield coils, psychopharmaceuticals, luxury food, wild meat, restricted texts, scavenged treasures, pliant drones.

**Means of Production**

Capital and production are allocated towards maximizing the pleasure and social success of the Cat Lords, with the whole system subsisting on the rents extracted from lands, tele-empathically pleasured laborers, scavenged oldtech from re-activated portals, and luxury trade with the utterly alien vast lands to the West.

**Material Conditions**

Official: not recorded. Effective: Cat Lords enjoy the highest living standards of feline quadrupeds anywhere in the vast known lands. Prized human pets enjoy material conditions suitable for human flourishing. Other human resources experience conditions optimal to their productivity.

_Source: Tensey Griti and Lamel d'Occo [agent pseudonyms],_ _Heliodor Inv. Agency, HMG [official], Green Camelia IX_


<a name="page_0108"></a>

[![Purple Land map (page 108)](images/page_0108_purple_land_map.png)](images/hires/page_0108_purple_land_map.png)

**Ambient, Core**

Dry uplands and lush round valleys, amethyst lakes and dark sand beaches, unfurled like a tapestry between the deep round Sea and the high glazed Rim. A timeless land of plantations and happy peasants, refined thralls and sleek felines, living machines of strange design and ill defined. A visitor might nearly suspect this land was not designed for humans, but the friendly locals would surely disagree.

| d6 | Winter | Spring | Summer | Autumn |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1-3 | soft rain, gentle fog, obscured sunrises | growing things, blazing suns, waking craters | chirping stillness, heavy damp, flying catnip | beige skies, dry grass, aerolith plankton bloom |
| 4-5 | mellow gray, shades of brown, dead leaves | rolling cloud ships, ultraviolet skies | heavy rain, flash floods, burbling mud runs | ripe reds and fat fuchsias, harvest glory, wormglow |
| 6 | swirling scorpion flakes, dust in the wind, hum | overcast, glowing stuckforce, creeping fogs | rushing winds, razor dust, shorn trees | flickering skies, error eclipses, pumice rains |

<a name="page_0109"></a>

**Ambient, Periphery**

The maps claim this land for the Violet City. But the cats are scarcer, the pleasures fewer, the skies hazier.

| d6 | Winter | Spring | Summer | Autumn |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1-3 | biting ice, gusting winds, thinned out airs | chill sun, probing growths, lustful rain showers | sun like a hammer, soil like an anvil, hanging dusts | lime skies, heavy grass, fresh craters |
| 4-5 | shades of pale, powdery snow, crumbling plants | glutinous mud, palecrawl fog, mutinous sun | ominous clouds, deep rumbles, breaking soil | brush fire, swirling smoke, soil knitting itself |
| 6 | glacial chill, hungry steppe hounds, haunting roar | skin-burn sun, meltwater run, hollow hares | lightning storm, electric dust, swirling stars | bluescreen skies, missing stars, crackshield rains |

**Travel**

Scrubby uplands invite the lone rider to wander, but the carefully incised roads promise easier, more controlled travel.

| Type | Status | Price |
|:---|:---|:---|
| Portal | There are no official portals in the Purple Land to guard the Circle against the Haze. | "lost" [€500] |
| Right Road | A week to the Ruins Azure from the Violet City. Another week beyond to reach the Emerald City. Buses and road trains with luxurious quadruped accommodations ply this busy route. | practical [€20–€30] |
| Catamaran | Licensed navettes ply the exclusive economic zone of the Violet City and keep the seas surprisingly free of pirates. A week to the Red Land District or the Ruins Azure. Beyond the Ruins Azure, only vessels with Inquisition sigils are allowed. | deck or cabin [€5 or €20] |
| Air Lane | The RLD, Ruins Azure, and Sailing Isles via a single air lane cleared from the Violet City and patrolled by the Flying Fox squadron. For the rest, razor sharp stuckforce fields make the sky lethal to the unwary. Locals recount how this arcane debris tore the Error Dragons to shreds during the Grand Invasion of '86. Expats believe the invasion never happened. | cat-egoric [€125] |
| Local (Core) | Registered golem buses ply the old roads to the settlements living and ghost. Plantations, pleasure palaces, and other facilities are not serviced. | humanitarian [€10] |
| Local (Peripheric) | Biomechanical vechs carry goods and people among the plantation towns and restricted facilities, and even out beyond the Rim, where locals whisper of wild vomes. | caravanite [€20] |

<a name="page_0110"></a>

**PURR-PURR ENTREPÔTS**

_"It's not a shell game. It's a cat game."_ —a tourist happy to use the local currency exchange

At first glance the Purple Land seems a fascinating place for commerce, but the multiple currencies in operation make it challenging for outsiders. Cash (€) transactions are restricted to high-ranking cat-friends and accredited representatives of outland incorporations or city-states.

Local humans and common travelers must use license bells (lbs), a category of local currencies. Meanwhile, the cats themselves only trade in favor-stone credits (₧), with all the original stones held in the Felicitous Butchery Bank, Violet City 2nd Island (FBB). Tourists using foreign currency will find themselves taken for a ride.

**This Felicitous Licensed Establishment**

**Purr-Purr Exchange Rates**

The FBB adjusts exchange rates without notice. Not all currencies may be interchanged. Fees included.

| Sell | Buy (FBB) | Black Market |
|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 cash (€) | 1d100 x 10 mlbs | 850 mlbs |
| 100 brass bells (mlbs) | 1d6 albs | 2 albs |
| 100 silver bells (albs) | 1d6 x 0.1 ₧ | 0.3 ₧ |
| 1 favor-stone credit (₧) | €5 | €10 |

For those who prefer things simple, 1 cash buys 500 brass bells, which buy 20 silver bells, which buy a quarter and dime of favor-stone. High-cat credit individuals may trade one favor-stone credit for €5, others get €2.

The master of commerce is a:
1. snake head grafted onto an animatronic dummy with a vocoder speaker;
2. electric lucky cat with eyes that bore into you;
3. jolly cat friend with dead eyes and a rictus smile;
4. shifty wagabund with ill-fitting skin;
5. jittery lime nomad with metallic arachnid pets;
6. three robed figures with identical ceramic masks.

|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Last Table West | slow, drooling, glassy | steeds and servants | shares your secrets with the cats |
| 2 | Fortunate Sun Wares | jerky, puppet-like, stringy | refurbished oldtech | follows you with its bubbling eyes |
| 3 | Noon's Saleschurch | giggles, chortles, snorts | nootropics, entheogenics | stops working if not fed regularly |
| 4 | Plantation Pleasures | slimy, gurgling, bubbly | exotic foodstuffs | glows when exposed to UV light |
| 5 | Coffee and Cranium | soft, gentle, singing | congealed "magic" texts | grows if ingested or planted |
| 6 | Excession Hatch IV | bird-like, taut, alert | affordable luxury toys | becomes translucent over time |

<a name="page_0112"></a>

**FACTIONS VIOLET**

_"Everybody wants to be a Cat [Lord]."_ —Dorito Pickles, exile Cat vidyscreenwriter, Saffron City, Wind Lotus VI

One city rules here. The Violet City. The city of cats. The city of magic and luxury.

Three regions form the Purple Land: the Core, the nuclear lands within the Rim; the New Veldt, west along the Low Road and High, soon to be reclaimed; and the Secure Zone, north among the Mountains of the Moon, always to be held fast against the Dead God's spawn.

There are no factions in the Purple Land. Neither poverty nor politics, no vulgar human excess, only peace. For everyone sentient must love the splendid cats.

Everyone needs to admit the superiority of feline intelligence. Suggesting that factions exist in the Purple Lands may see one's trading or tourism license revoked.

**Splendid Cat Lords**

The two-headed feline creatures, with one head a cat's and the other a snake's growing from their tails, are blessed with opposable thumbs and tele-empathetic powers of human enthrallment. They call themselves the Cats and are referred to as Cat Lords by their pets, but they seem so unlike the other cats of the Circle Sea and former Garden that many theorize they may be extra-cosmic interlopers or escapees from a Builder wizard's laboratory. Spreading these conspiracy theories is illegal in the Purple Land, where everyone knows the truth: pets and cats evolved together, guided by the wisdom of the Purple Goddess.

♟ _Chinklefink Butterfingers._ The runt of his litter, Chinklefink discovered himself possessed of an unusually strong psychic ability to dominate humans. Now possessed of an army of willing pets, he seeks to rid himself of his littermates and take over their estates as the first step of his plan. Potential catnappers will be well compensated.

♟ _Master Pooffins._ The lovable furball of the great master of accounts, Hel-Belt Ashcuein, feels the Cat Lords have become decadent. A small explosive misadventure attributed to some useless anti-cat terrorists and the death of a rival would be perfect to bring his Cat Power Party closer to the golden bowl of government.

**Cat Pets**

Most humans in the Purple Land are willing pets of the good and benevolent Cats, happy to do their tele-empathetic bidding in return for praises and treats. Many are not even aware that they are doing the bidding of their small, clawed, fork-tongued friends.

♟ _Gurya da'Tarva._ Driven to destitution by the death of her Cat Lord in a particularly bloody fight for control of a proud plantation, Gurya will do anything to get a new little Lord crooning in her mind. She is planning to poison a litter of anti-cattite activists to prove her usefulness and loyalty to the Cat Lords.

♟ _Beres Yimume._ An anti-cattite spy from the Free Purplelanders beyond the Rim, they have installed a subsidiary daemon-mind in their head, which captures the Cats' tele-empathetic emissions and lets Beres get close to the Cat Lords' sacred control temple. They have aroused the suspicion of a grizzled old Cat detective named Nero Tiddlestrings, but nobody will listen to old Nero who can't even control a human thrall properly these days.

**Success and Permission**

_embodied concepts, egrigorical angels, psychefaction_

One of the great dangers of humans untethered from the Lords' guidance and ministration is that their careless minds may serve as condensation nuclei for new Spirits to accrete from the spiritual soup of the omnipresent noösphere. Two such false divinities are **Success** (L3, tempting) and **Permission** (L6, justifying), a combined two-faced divine entity born to give justification to human Hubris.

The rewards of Success and Permission are real, but the final consequences are almost always tragic. As such, humans who sacrifice to Success and Permission are in breach of numerous Garden ordinances and may be subject to spiritual detergence.

♟ _Dahin Forders._ A plaster-faced prophet of Success and Permission commissioned by the Cat Lords to peddle spiritual opium to the jolly toilers of the Purple Lands. Also, a surprisingly bad poet.

♟ _Dr MD Nictetes._ A journeyman practitioner from the Emerald City, but also a spy for the Inquisition tasked with finding out if Success and Permission are a re-appearance of the Dead (Blue) God.

<a name="page_0113"></a>

**Wagabund Travelers, Wagonnards**

An unsettled populace that should by rights barely be categorized as human, since they do not follow the civic traditions, yet many old machines still recognize them as being of sufficiently pure stock—and in some cases even jewel-headed—that their humanity is beyond doubt.

However, they are clearly barbarians, eschewing a sedentary life, denying the gift of free nutrislurry and endless individually optimized vidy content delivered once a week by centrally approved golem agents.

Instead, these tattered folk travel about on their bicycles and push-carts and even animal-drawn wagons, dirtying their hands with prehistoric crafts like carpentry, tinkering, soldering, tailoring, and more—as though we did not live at the end of time, where machines provide all by the grace of the good (if temporarily embarrassingly absent) Lords of the Given World.

♟ _Irshé d'Alba._ Born on the move, in flight from their old homeland, which was taken over by telepathic feline monsters from beyond the void, Irshé was raised on stories of human rebellion and dreams of becoming a vampire knight to rally a human resistance against their oppressors.

♟ _Taita Corruin._ The aged mistress of her wagon-tribe, she knows the capricious cruelty and baffling blindness of the lords who wield the deadly oldtech.

There is more to biding one's time and scavenging like rats on the edges of this decaying world than the young ones know. Right now, a new synthetic heart-lung system would be perfect for Taita.

**Free Purplelanders, Freeples**

The freeples do not actually exist, as evidenced by their absence in all official records and censuses. The humans dwelling outside of the standard settlements and plantations and facilities are probably not really human.

Yet, visitors continue to report a vibrant neo-feudal society arising in villages and holdfasts centered on the grand phylakes outside the Cat Lords' control, beyond the Circle Rim. Many seem to be making quite a go of things, adapting the neofauna and neoflora left by the [redacted] of the Blue Lands to their modern needs, from great sheet fungi used to produce mleather (mushroom leather) and sprouting dragonbone to replace ivory, to illnanobacterial cultures to harvest metals from scavenged ruins and lumin trees to capture the energy of the sun.

♟ _Girayt Ferluc._ A timelost captain who has adopted a freeple community as his wards, Girayt seeks skilled mercenaries to help him reactivate the giant headless body on which their new town stands.

With such a monster as their steed, they could move beyond the reach of the soul-burning Cat Lords.

♟ _Caris._ Just Caris. You need know no more. They're part of a shadowy network exfiltrating the Cat Lords' thralls and removing the thought worms from their heads, freeing them from the nefarious thought controllers. Yes, there's an unfortunately high mortality rate to the procedure, but that's where you might come in—perhaps by procuring an off-the-books golem autodoctor?

**Near Steppelanders**

Grown soft (in the eyes of their harsher cousins) on the periphery of civilization, the uncommon variegated humans of the vast and shattered West come often into the Purple Lands as traders and raiders. Within the Circle Rim they are few and contained, beyond they are more and less restrained. This group is (roll d6): (1) carrying a new plague, (2) bringing half-human offerings for the soul mills, (3) raiding for silks and sweets, (4) bringing furs and technomagical organs, (5) seeking gainful mercenary employment, (6) actually noble rainbowlanders dressed up as steppe nomads for fun.

♟ _Nanoc._ A young steppelander chief's son, exiled after his father was murdered by an azure cult leader of the Great Snake, he has come to the decadent cities of the east to seek his fortune with sword and cunning, thews and terrifying determination.

♟ _Göthert Brim._ Long-wandering, friend of goats, tall-teller, has noticed a corruption in the watching stones and comes to warn his sleeping kin.

<a name="page_0114"></a>

**VIOLET CITY — CATLANDIA**

_"Once this city must have had another name,_  
_but I cannot remember."_ —Undying Varya 't Uorc, _Oral Histories of the Gate War_, (Soil Lily VI)

**Impressions**

Arriving through the ravaged Congress Concessions of the Blue Land and the crater-pocked North Core of the Purple Land, the Violet City is the first grand settlement to shine with electric fire, gentle illumination to push away the Eating Dark, rather than the ghostly blue light of the many half-abandoned settlements now peopled by more radiation ghosts than honest humans.

In the Violet City, the lights of oldtech shine bright, the sufficiently advanced magics keenly studied, the mysteries of the Builders still available to humanity through the benevolent intermediation of the Cat Lords.

Towers of livingstone rise from the sea, hosting vivid ecologies of climbing plants, tasty little mammals and delicious singing birds. Flocks and herds of food for the Cat Lords' palates.

Away from the fresh airs and lush views, behind walls to protect them from themselves, the various human castes live in generously appointed accommodations, which some anti-cattites have called slums.

Everyone is welcome to this place of trade, luxury, and magic, so long as they keep their anti-cat bigotry at bay.

**Major Districts**

_**The Livingstone Towers.**_ Home to the noblest of cats and the most prized of humans: the captive academics, engineers, and maintainers who keep the Purple Lands' oldtech running as it did Long Ago.

_**The Great Cat.**_ The holiest temple of the Cat Lords is the gargantuan mechanical cat, which offers oracles and advice to petitioners. It is a lie that the Violet City's grand portal gate once stood here.

_**The Roadside.**_ Grand livingstone facades line the Right Road, nigh-arboreal doll-house homes from which the Cat Lords can enjoy the minds entering their realm.

_**The Townships.**_ Inside their high walls, the townships keep humans safe and multiplying, a reservoir of willing and happy pets for the Cat Lords to access in times of need. Multiple amusements are available, including games with balls and strings, mouse hunts, dog baiting, public torture exhibitions, and more.

_**The Abandonships.**_ There are no abandoned outer districts of the Violet City. All the districts are fully peopled by actual humans. Ignore rumors of whole towns occupied by **plastic-faced falschers** (L0, hollow).

_**The Floating Slums.**_ Tethered together around their seaweed and fish and snail farms, the various anti-cattite garbage people are tolerated for the delicacies they offer up to the Cat Lords as tribute.

_**The Violet Lagoons.**_ The cats despise the water, for it can make their fur wet and smelly, like the fur of a canine or marmot or other foul mammal. As such they outsource the patrol of the lagoons to a number of fixed **lobophylakes** (L11, searing), great angelic golems, and their trusted human **head-riders** (L2, cat-loving). Still, all kinds of rabble scud about on small coracles.

<a name="page_0115"></a>

**Ambient**

Small synthetic suns, gifts of the Cat Lords, provide more light than the purple haze of the Ultraviolet Grasslands, creeping through the gaps in the Circle Rim, would usually permit.

| d6 | Night | Haze | Day | Evening |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1–3 | humid, clammy, buzzing haze, ozone smell | wan bluish light, purpling haze, mineral smell | clear day, blazing electric suns, tattering clouds | sodium suns, deep purple shadows, salty tang |
| 4–5 | violet skyglow, tense air, languid salty mists | ultraviolet light, dim haze, glyph hallucinations | flickering clouds, pricking stars, raucous market cries | oilslick spreading dark, eyes in the gloom, chirping |
| 6 | purple rain, distant thunder, bacterial glitterbloom | choking haze, itching odor, visions of a dark city | stuck grey sky, no shadows, cawing birds, wailing frogs | stuttering light, dust fall, oppressive silence |

The stone human abides. Win: he gives you a jade finger (€200). Lose: work in his haunted garden for a night and a day. |

**Purple "Palaces"**
