<a name="page_0172"></a>

**COUNCIL & 404 PROVINCES**

_The following unreconquered_ ~~_rebel_~~ _evil provinces (404 gowoz) may cause some temporary travel inconvenience._ —outdated and outlawed travel guidance to the unserviced regions of the Orange Lands

A brave academic or a foolhardy tourist may get their hands on a highly illegal political _map_ of the Orange Lands, rather than the travel _itineraries_ approved by the Council for Tourism and Leisure Travel [sic]. Said academic or tourist may notice an oddity, namely that many of the provinces are prefaced by the age-old mystic number 404, the number of the Unknown and Lost.

These provinces are taboo within the Council provinces of the Orange Lands, their very mention punishable with immediate labor duty among the Citizens Dead.

Therefore, we shall not mention them.

**Council Provinces**

Instead, we shall mention the pleasurable provinces under the benevolent, eternal and perfect stewardship of the Council of Ancestors and Descendants, where, if you are lucky, you will even see a Council Agent!

_**IV Provinces.**_ The heart, the IV drip, of the Orange Lands are the provinces of the Irrigation Valley, home of the traveling lake-city of Plough-Oranje. Their verdant waters and floating gardens, both tended by countless (actually roughly 20 million) Citizens Dead, are the cornucopia of the Rainbowlands. Truly, all manner of delights are available here, and an ivory servant is always at hand to ensure one's comfort and delight. These provinces are Basis, Fielding, ~~Gate,~~ Sluices, Turning, and Verge.

_**Highland Provinces.**_ The frontier, where the Irrigation Valley will expand once the buildertech is reactivated, includes the provinces of Bloom, Bridging, Eastway, and Verge. These lands are emptier, the laboring citizens dead fewer, and thus one comes across more Duckies in unauthorized manufacturing or agricultural activities.

_**Amber Territories.**_ Falsely claimed by the disgusting anti-humanist Red Land Vintners, their Vinterns and Vampires, the territories Central, Electric, Further, and South are completely under the control of the Cads and their shock-mummies. Suggestions that enterprising Redlander bloodwine cultivators have infested the Eternal Grove in the Bulbtree Savanna are absolutely false and there is no way the Council will ever be dislodged from beneath the gaze of the glorious and well-controlled Betrayer.

**Meetings With Council Agents**

When you meet a Council Agent, present your Hedonic Recordbook for review, to confirm your ongoing right to the infinite pleasures afforded to every Citizen of the most pleasant of republics.

| d6 | Their Ride | Their Manifestation | Their Will | But, Quietly Also |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | A gleaming carriage of brass and livingwood. | The flesh copy of a Council meta-judge. | Drink from their nutriteat to abolish your doubts. | Eyes grow in blossoms of plumeria and talipot. |
| 2 | A barge of synthetic ivory and chelonian flippers. | Holo-dramatic visions of a Council historian. | Look, prod, spy, and root for corruption and heresy. | Snails with electric blue shells swim and crawl. |
| 3 | An autogolem truck of apricot and plum hues. | Liquid essence of a Council homeotherapist. | Sample the waters, study the interlopers. | Living tattoos, symbiotic messenger colonies. |
| 4 | A booth of rubber and steel and glass. | Gently embracing steel-and-glass Council medicus. | Suck air, drink sunlight, rest old bones in radiation. | Amber rain from silver clouds, whispering mists. |
| 5 | A levitating pyramid of tawny brick & lapis scutes. | Electric ghosts of a Council administrator polymorph. | Instruct the trees and grasses of the land. | Glowing shadows woven as a cloak to hide from men. |
| 6 | A giant, ten-foot tall, man of iron, with a glass visor. | A Council guardian's noble, mummified visage. | Measure needs and means, revise hedonic tables. | Scribe monkeys with ivory and ebony tabulators. |


<a name="page_0173"></a>

**The Near Upbroad**

Only well-equipped warrior merchant caravans brave the soaring heights of the Thin Plateau and the Broken Terraces, where strange autofactories and archaic subcommunities struggle in that fabulous way sub humans, unblessed by abmortality, must. The journey to the fabled oriental cities is thus often a lonely one—and short on oxygen.

**Free Orange Provinces**

_"These time-stuck liches and their four-armed cad servants had their time, once we revive the Araña, they shall learn the true purpose of Nature-born humanity!"_ —salvaged logs from the fall of Old Haven, subversive literature, double-double redacted

_"All along the Hollow Coast, pyres burned, a glorious illumination, a hecatomb of our stolen Ancestors, returned to the pre-divine cycle, ash to fertilize the Green to be recycled by the Given World!"_ —mad ravings of the captured Pirate Priest-Poet Twinbarrel Uolcsird

_**Sailing Islands, 404Islanding.**_ Free for over two cycles, a haven of freebooting, thick with dwarves and cetaceans, liberator of the Warded and Wardless Islands, scourge of the corpse-lovers on the Hollow Coast, beacon of human liberty against the dead hand of the post-mortal order.

_**Hollow Coast, 404Haven and 404Uck.**_ Little left to see but empty deadstone towns and swirling dust, the post-mortals savage all attempts at settlement here. The port-fortress of Hafnorsk (Duck Haven) stands here as a sanctuary for the Citizens Living fleeing the tyranny of their Hedonic Bureau's corpse tax.

_**Sudopol, Pseudopolis, "South" HS17.**_ Claimed as Outernorth by the post-mortals, it always was and will remain a font of independence against the anti-Human lich-lords of the Orange Lands. Citizens and friends of this settlement claim to have access to a fundamental truth or revelation about the human condition thanks to the whispered secrets of the Fourflesh Teratolith uncovered in [redacted]. The Council threatens all evangelists of this "heresy" with purification in the solar farms.

_**Fire Provinces, 404Unlost, 404Gate, Bloom.**_ The lich-lords blame the crafty, gold-eating Gelvolanders (Yellowlanders) of Safranj for the theft of the ash-soil farming region. The local residents fear the Council wants to mulch them back into their Citizens Dead collective if they ever "recivilize" the region.

_**Heartland, 404Pump.**_ The Council confirms this province never existed and no settlements were ever established here. No free residents ever escaped. Sales of lifelike human weepstone sculptures from the region are restricted due to their toxic radiance.

_**Roadvalley, Further Territory.**_ The Council claims the foreign residents of this province were not instrumental in the Redlander theft of this territory and as such will be permitted to join the Citizens Dead after they return to the fold. The Roadvalefolk refuse any discussion of such ideas, elect their own Vintner Lords-for-a-Year to rule them, while sabotaging roadmakers sent from the Central Territory to knit them once more to the body Orange.


<a name="page_0174"></a>

**THE MUTE PLACES**

_..._ —Protests of the Citizens Dead, a symphony in 3 acts

In a Land where the post-mortal labor force outnumbers the living citizenry by twenty-to-one, there are many places where birdsong reigns while the silent laborers perform their toil day-moon to day-sun without cease.

Save for the occasional clatter of a necromancermanager's voiture and the bark of their willsniffer hound (for the development of free-will in a reanimated shell has an odor all its own, a hint of citrus and ozone, like a purple haze descending from a slow star), these places work like quiet clocks, tracked by silent eye-plants and other biomechanical watchers, extracting produce to fill the groaning road trains and wheezing cargo cruisers that feed the Yellow, Orange, and even Purple Lands.

**Silent Approach**

Draw closer to the mute place. Feel your aura pale.

1. No small creatures. First no midges. Then no flies. Then mice, even birds disappear.
2. The day-stars fade, the fast-stars slow, the sky grows gray like dead god-screen.
3. Cold leaches from ground and sky. Frost flowers blossom in shadow and crack.
4. Eyes water, depth drains away, all grows flat. Voices, reasons, dreams.
5. Coiling ironthorns, warning vines sprouted from the soil itself by the power of the Builders. "Away!" they seem to say.
6. The ground becomes glass. Sand, rocks, buildings, rails, roads give way to scratched translucence.

**Here, Now, Somber Monument**

It surrounds you, clusters in, drawn by your words, your vitality, your malleable nature. Feel your aura shrink.

1. Houses and halls insubstantial as ghosts, flickering echoes of past lives, trapped behind the veil of Error.
2. Ominous tumuli cloaked in heather and hellflower. The wights of a lying age bound in torture tombs. They cannot be released, they are but lessons against the hubris of man.
3. Bricks. Boulders. Shells of sandstone. Bars of rustless metal. Contorted parts. Destruction preserved in amber time. More lessons.
4. Silent plazas. Pretty porticos. Memorable mosaics. Abandoned autogolems. Living dust to scour every surface, polish and preserve for masters never to be seen again.
5. Gardens of rutile roses. Parks of olivine oaks. Towers of carnelian corpses. A decayed visitor center. Posters commemorating a petrifying plague.
6. Sigil-warded, sign-posted, sarcophagus-entombed. A great square mountain. Within, they don't say but one suspects, an autofaber. A rogue creation machine. A false god.

**They Call This Place Home**

Life, says the poet, finds a way. Feel your aura flicker and snicker.

1. Ghosts, **living ghosts** (L0, plasmic). Naked ka-ba sentiences, unbound from the gift of flesh, they suck vitality from the bonds of this place.
2. A **radiation of rabbits** (L1, tool-using), grown bold and rat-like, with grasping hands and snarling eyes.
3. **Ground vultures** (L3, huge), therapod in proportion. Immune to the dark aura, they wait for visitors to drop into inevitable catatonia.
4. **Dog-sized ants** (L0, modular), pack dividuals, smart as a man if assembled.
5. **Falschers** (L1, punctual), golems of manflesh perfect in every way, save without spirit or mind. They perform their routines, reproduce, and self-repair in the crystal cabinets prepared for them by long-dead masters.
6. **Recusers** (L1d6, translated) who abandoned the path of humanity long, long ago. Shaggy and protean, they seek a means of further uplift in this place.


<a name="page_0175"></a>

**Sweet Honey Traps**

_false settlements, bed and banshee houses_


It's not just the Orange Land that is dotted with ghost orchards and hollow plantations and robot cottages, but they are most common there.

The weary traveler follows a sign, spots hearthsmoke, and expects a bed and bath, rest and repose. Lights welcoming wink, tended trees and furrowed fields invite. Closer, figures go about their duties, smells tempt the palate, the circle of life seems unbroken.

Yet something rings hollow. No spirit stirs. No mind inquires. Men and beasts alike are false, machines of flesh, programmed to simulate social life. Survivors of masters gone to futility, dead to ennui, died out while the gods looked away.

Still, the biomachines continue. Ceaseless as the suns.

1. Tasked with marketing a perfect house of the future, they upkeep the half-ruined place, try to sell it.
2. The masters left on a journey a century ago and the falscher butlers have been keeping it livable since.
3. The abmortal minister who retired to a little cottage, but felt lonely in the empty village of her youth and brought synthetic shells to simulate a vanished era.
4. A plague killed all the humans here, but the quotas kept coming at the Adminimind900®, so it animated these plastic people to keep up.
5. The withered people are still there, become Megas, hooked to nöosphere drips in their cellars, their day jobs taken over by falscher clones of themselves.
6. They are not falscher ghost humans, but ferals without mind jewels, who settled here illegally.

**Windling Valleys**

_ghost traps, voice harvesters_


But where did the voices go, the minds chased out of all these mute places? Most faded, many translated into the noösphere, and some—some made other stranger attempts at immortality. One group that still sings their timelocked songs to this day are the windlings, minds trapped ghost-like in the carving of highland rocks and sculpting of stuckforce membranes to channel air and light, giving them voice when the catabatic winds blow.

They mostly have little to say to interest a modern human, complaining about the price of groceries or grousing about their incomprehensible politics of amusement, but their wind-voices, though annoying, are often used to guide travelers in the underpeopled Highland Provinces and Amber Territories.

**Homebody Bulbtrees (p182)**

_vegetable bodyvaults, engines of patience_


Not limited to the Bulbtree Savanna, the pachydermic trunks of these trees were engineered by Long Ago vegetable lich masters to serve as warm storage for human bodies resting through time, whether omegas grown dull and sessile through overexposure to noöspheric viruses, citizens barely-living stored for later reanimation, or volunteers seeking to sleep-travel into the future, when the Amber Zone would be ready for full-scale human settlement.

♟ _Gau Mirvoz._ A would-be lich keen to make their name as an excellent purveyor of laborers, Gau is surely not alone in seeking to harvest a few dozen sleepers from some isolated bulbtrees.


<a name="page_0176"></a>

**THE SHALLOW SEA AND THE SAILING ISLANDS**

_"The Sea is a desert, all life within it false. Those who eat_

_fruit of the Sea lose their minds to the Lightless Unlords. Turn aside from the Sea, that it would not eat your soul."_ —Councilorleit Veyelhuit 5-Perimeter, _Towards a Renewed Orchard_ (Flux Dandelion IV)

Some say. Some. Ah, that lazy, sneaky word. Some may hide so many. Some may hide hypocrites and heretics, rebels and ruiners, corruptors, devastators, all those who turn their eyes and hearts away from good Path and wise Council! And there may be so many now that to say Some should hardly suffice, but we shall not say Many, for that would be to breach the Act of the Disavowal of the Unreconstituted Provinces, and such a breach would see us undone, become as unconscious as an undine.

But surely, surely, the Council and the City must note that though our popular speech of the Citizens Living and the dream tongue of the Citizens Dead may have a thousand song-names for the orchards and the streams and the delights provided by Hesam [Hedonic Satisfaction Ministry –Ed], it has no songs (Hesam). But it has no song-names for the mute places, the places fallen away from the Garden Path, the places sunk to corruption and slow decay, and least for those most-sunk, those reclaimed when the Sea consumed the Perisea.

How without song-names are ministers and magisters to deal with such despondent places, which may exist, I do not claim they do, without a word for them? How can one resolve the challenge of a hush-where, a mute place that no longer speaks, that cannot be spoken of?

The voices of the gods, the whispers of the noösphere, may be stilled in the hush-wheres, but to the old-minded the stones still have dirges to share. If we listen and conduct these words, are we in breach of ADUP?

Why does Oranjetic have no longer a word for Sea?


<a name="page_0177"></a>

**Shallow Sea and the Lost Perisea**

_"Geohistorical heresy holds that the Sea once was smaller."_ —Anti-Council Tract on the Sea Pirates

Long Long Ago, prior to the Rainbow of Lands, prior to the Garden of Panhumanity, prior to priority, the Builders excavated a great bowl in the world, whose name is now taboo but was then Cradle Crater and before that _Volyi Kraatr_. This they filled with waters and air, creating the Settlement Area Designated (SAD), while the rest of the world was made habitable.

This Shallow Sea was the Perisea, the Great Plain of First

Garden, the Eden of Reeds, benevolently given to the humans by the lords of the cetaceans, the Undines, for their fruiting. But the humans performed a Forgotten Deed and the Perisea was drowned by the Circle Sea.

No, it was to protect humans from the Builders' worldsculpting magics, the terrifying buildertech, that the Circle Sea drowned this original land, creating the water-desert as a sacred domain for the cetaceans and the Undines who now lock away these unusable powers.

Then was written the Sufficient Water® Myth to help humans to fear the Sea: "Once, the Lords of the Dream Canopy created Sufficient Water® for the Garden. However, the first humans rebelled and sailed to wrest the Eye from the Lords. The Lords, in their mercy, created Rising Water® and flooded the first settlements and made strong the currents and great the distances, throwing the first humans against the thin air that they might gasp and flounder to amuse the Lords."

Good Citizens and Humans should have no word for Sea.

All who dwell in the Sea must be Inhuman. So says the Council. So says the Minister. So says Mother Machine.

**The Truerooted Islands**

Few islands are truerooted in the Soil beneath the Sea.

There is of course the Eye of God, reserved for Lords and Phylakes and the Purest of Humans certified by the Authority, but that is not the domain of any land. Here, in the Shallow Sea, only Heroes Haven has that massed connection, and thus the Citizens' Dead militia walked across the seabed to its roots, ascended its shores, and ate its foul terrorist anti-citizen rebels, and reaffirmed its eternal and unchanging status as a Council Province. It is currently unmentionable in Orange Land documents.

**The Tensefoot Islands**

Tethered by ropes of living chitin, chains of sungwood, and tendons of shipmetal, the tensefoot islands are moored to great crawly anchors. They may move about, but only slowly, at the bidding of the Undines. Those who would dwell on these half-Built islands should supplicate the Undines and other aquatic daemons to protect them from the vagaries of nature and the depredations of land-born peacemakers. Antansible Beach is the largest such island-town in the Sailing Islands, but others may hide on the East Ridge.

**The Megachelonian Isles**

Last are the so-called truesailing islands, human-compatible biospheres borne on the biocrete backs of the great many-handed, slow-moving, filter-feeding organisms completely unrelated to turtles. Though they have preferred territories, to properly map them is something of an impossibility. It is rumored that the Undines shepherd them, forming a watery constellation that amplifies their song-signal into the Void.

The most liberal is the Free Drift, the Oh Megachelone hosts a terrifying temple to the Oh Mega.


<a name="page_0178"></a>

**WHISTLER'S WATCHTOWER AND PENNYBURST CRATERVALE**

If the Orange Land is the beautiful, delicious, enlightened fruit of civilization, its edge, where the South road to the delights of the East once led, is bitter and strange. A thorny land to guard the sweetness of life, say the Recollectors.

Yet even to such strange places the traveler, the adventure-seer, will endeavor.

**Whistler's Watchtower**

_ghost arcology, automatic vertical village_


A living tower, an arcology from Long Long Ago, _betoniste casalbéres_ rising into the thinnest air, sucking light and moisture and vital force, it remains a vibrant golem town, full of radiation ghosts, on the edge of the Orange Lands. Designated an autonomous cultural area, it is run under its own laws and does not contribute citizens dead to the confederation. It is the major fabricator of oldtech autosurgeons in the Rainbowlands and a protected area.

**The Angel Villages**

_cera-fungal cliff villages, oldtech fabricators_


Most of the arcology's wide-sprawling heartwood is dead, a gnarled labyrinth of support struts, desiccated ducts and petrified passageways. Clustered on cerafungal brackets on the southern extensions of the tower, the villages offer a glimpse into the simple lives of Long Ago humans. The villagers live simple, hard-working lives, tending their hanging gardens, killing parasites, and protecting their arcology.

The villagers are called angels because they are all androgyne and sexless. They do not reproduce; new villagers are brought once a year by the sister servitors.

**The Sister Servitors**

_buildertech abbey, institutional mother machine_


In the arcology's northern buds, the sister servitors tend to the Watchtower's germline, watching over the stock of angels and protecting them in accordance with the Great Plan.

They are not able to fully articulate the plan, as it is embedded in their intuitive subroutines. As they put it, "they know when they're following the plan when they're following the plan."

The sister servitors maintain great birthing banks of wombs and gonads sustained in biomechanical nutrient baths. With these, they produce great numbers of new humans. At birth, they divide them into three groups:

- The breeding population. Those with the best germ lines are sent to the anthropozoo, at the heart of the arcology, where they are kept in a realistic human environment to preserve their way of life.
- The settler population. The largest group. Bundled into sustainer cradles and shipped to the High Plateau Settlement Facility by armored hovergolems.
- The angel populations. Surgically desexed with their organs used to replenish the birthing banks. The angels are then sent to the angel villages, to restock the arcology caretakers' numbers.

The servitors have received no critique of their work from the High Plateau Settlement Organization for over two thousand years. They are sure they are doing a good job.


<a name="page_0179"></a>

The Pennyburst Cratervale was not accidentally created during the Pennyburst incident. Regardless, it proved a lucky accident, creating a settlement zone ~~isolated~~ protected by the harsh environment of the Thin Plateau, where the air is barely there. The faithful say the Maker bade the Builders leave it untouched for the far aeons when the mountains will be rebuilt. Portable rebreathers and enviro suits are required to reach the Cratervale.

**T.P.S. Organization**

_organization monument, autosouvenir fabricator_


Defunct independent settlement organization, shut down 18 centuries ago, after the Great Airsucker Scam, when 97% of the Legume Farmer Nation® died within a week of delivery to their new agricultural zones in the third quadrant of the planned Peach Land human habitation area.

It seems the organization vastly overstated the atmospheric density of the High Plateau and manipulated gas generation records for over three generations while siphoning off most of the proceeds.

In the ensuing trials, the organization's rulers were charged with gross negligence and fined a whole year's income. The middle-managers who circumvented the HM Initiative's guidelines on habitability enhancement were publicly executed to encourage whistleblowing and compliance.

A tastefully-sized processed slag palace field now marks the 712,523.5 Legume Farmer Nation® lives lost in the scam. All 320 thousand recorded names are listed, as well as retinal scans of the remaining dead. An automated gift shop remains nearby, ready to sell souvenirs to visitors at this tragic memorial to human courage and endeavor.

**T.P.S. Facility**

_zone of alienation_


Danger! Severe vome infestation! Do not enter this zone.

The domed crater is filled with biomechanical activity. Its antennae continue to transmit ancient all-clear signals.

Long-distance observation suggests a corrupted facility subroutine is now cancerously overproducing itself.

There is no sign of the babies regularly shipped to the facility by the sister servitors.

_**Within:**_ the facility mind is now an idiot god, running a bizarre society of enslaved biomodified human drones in an endless ritual quest to dig down to the highest heaven. The drones dig through bedrock using the most primitive of tools, subsisting on soylent slurries made from their own recycled companions.

<!-- Begin: Our_Golden_Age_08_Yellow_Land_180-203 -->

<a name="page_0180"></a>

### YELLOW LAND

_"The Given World will run itself away,_ _unless you take it for yourself."_ —traditional Diesel Dwarf admonition


<a name="page_0181"></a>

The Yellow Land was the human frontier, the zone of sowing, harvesting, processing, making and expansion. As the rains follow the sky plough, so the garden was to follow the Builders' glass houses.

It did not. The canopy tattered, the noösphere frayed, the orders were unfollowed.

The géants, bereft, still lift mountains, carve valleys, deposit raw materials. The factory towns still churn jobs for their townsfolk.

But this is no garden. This is now a churning mass of fiercely independent city states extracting, processing, reprocessing, producing, trading, and fighting one another and all comers to within a stuckforce fieldsbreadth of what is permitted by the phylakes, and beyond when opportunity presents itself.

**Climate**

The mountains called Chaos bestow waters and black soil here, but drought and sand there.

Microlocal climates are varied and unpredictable, not least due to the undying climate fabricators.

**Population**

towner: ~6.5 million, stepper: ~0.3–1.1 million

**Groups**

- Yellow autochthones 26%
- adopted citizens 24%
- yellow generated 20%
- half-born semi-citizens 13%
- barbarian stepper 5–10%
- itinerant residents 4–9%
- others 3–9%

**Languages**

Saffranian (esteemed), Canopic (deprecated), Oranjetic (provincial), Free City Kriol (peri-trader), Volkan (industri-dwarfer), Topic (peripatetics)

**Capital**

Official: Saffron Public Thing. Practical: Safranj, loomstone house primary of the Heliodor Mercantile Guild.

**Government**

Competitive polyarchy. Experimental local autonomy maximization. Tribal anarcho-segmentary groups.

**Ideologies**

Yellow God: trader (official), Invisible Hand: explorer (popular), Chemical Mother: generative (sustained).

**Economy**

By sane statistics, the richest land and the measure of market freedom. Symbiotic fabricator-human townships harvest, produce and compete, creating wealth that is only poorly understood by the Ministry.

Trade with the half-known lands beyond the Golden Desert, the Lands of the Two Suns, those of Many Mirrors, the Living God, the Rational Army and more provides a further boost.

**Resources**

Proteins, hydrocarbons, rare earths, radio thermics, saffron, burdenbeasts, phylake-approved mercenaries.

**Means of Production**

The polities control and dispose of goods and capital through semi-sentient symbiotic agglomerations.

The Heliodor Mercantile Guild adjudicates disputes.

**Material Conditions**

Mandatory roles offer safety, sustenance, and amusements. Designated roles offer baseline survival. Non-citizens may adopt roles undesired by citizens.

_Source: Taurisc Betel-Nut CC, HMG Trade School [branch 2],_

_Sun-Setting Hyacinth II_


<a name="page_0182"></a>

[![Yellow Land map (page 182)](images/page_0182_yellow_land_map.png)](images/hires/page_0182_yellow_land_map.png)

**INTERRUPTION**

_Error Stamp: Unauthorized Journal Entry, Unnamed_

Fools or liars? I don't know. I don't know. Maybe both? We're goin ~~g~~ to reclaim our herita ~~ge~~. We're going to brea ~~k~~ free of the old restrictions. We're going to be rich. We're ~~go~~ ing to going to goin ~~g~~ to.

Stop. My brain keeps stuttering. Stop.

Listen to me, we should have paid attention when we found all the corpses. This is a place of no ho ~~n~~ or. Sure, it's on a lovely tethered aerolith just above Fociverry (Fireglass, HS01Y South-Ed.). Purified by the Green Sun ~~l~~ ike the Metropolitans say. But it's a lie. A trap?

We were suckers. Kers. Kers. Kers. Ack.

I left my heart on yellow grass hill. I left my heart where the party people swill. I left it there with a lass who didn't care. Her bon ~~e~~ was stone, her soul was glass, her voice cut me like a scalpel. Pell. Pell. Pell.

No, look, you have to believe me. I can see your face. I see you've found this contract. Don't go! Like they deboned my Moranna. They'll take your bones and wire them a pu ~~pp~~ et, draw you jiggle jiggle jiggle.

Damnit. The contract virus. In my brain. Click. Click.

RESET

**This Liberated Trader**

_"They don't make 'em like ole' Vidyscreen_ _Venera anymore. Look at this raw_ _throughput! The dynamic error control._ _The delicate embossing. The cryptorchid_ _watermarks. She chungs out ten faux-_ _dream vidyscreens a day and we, her_ _veneralboys, we're the only retailers. You_ _want a vidyscreen like they had in the old_ _days, dontcha? Special price, just for you_ _my high frontier friend, €349. Less than a_ _yearslave!"_ —Veneralboy Ta Vera,

Traducive Electromagics

Sym., HS2-1 "Dream"

Anyone can be a merchant in the

Yellow Land. Everyone is a merchant in the Yellow Land. What are you if not a merchant when you buy your life cheap from your Maker and sell it dear to your owner of common capital and maker of beloved goods? If you are not a merchant, are you even a citizen?

Admittedly, most Yellow Land merchants are so far down the mercantile guild hierarchy that in another land they might be called workers-at-gigs or labor-beggars, yet—if they are citizens, they are guild members and thus own a coveted merchant evidence dragon spirit neck-lock chit.

<a name="page_0186"></a>

**JAUNDICED FACTIONS**

_"Get two Yellow Landers and you've got three factions."_ —Popular Orange Land slur.

Unlike in the other lands, no one great center lays claim to the entire region. Yes, the Saffron City bestrides the intersection of Right Road and the Yellow River, but the shifting geography of the Decapolitan Chaos and the locally controlled autofabricators make for a patchwork of bloody-minded independent city states, ranging from fervent open-traders to reclusive bunker-cities grown strange with countless years.

Pop polititheologians claim to discern two dominant value groups: the pro-unity integralists and the prolocal-patriotism autarkics. They dismiss the patently less important groupings such as the bypoliticals and the barbarophiles. The fact that the individual towns' factions barely cooperate—or even comprehend—their co-ideologues in other towns does somewhat undermind these theories. Still, they keep the polititheological entertainers busy and chattering classes amused.

**Saffron Integralists et al**

The Integralists, also called the _Whole Heliodor Party_, say the only way forward is to unite the Yellow Land under one central authority. Preferably that of their local cell.

The _Heliodor is Saffron_ offshoot has a simpler plan— this yellowist vanguard wants to set up a temporary revolutionary multicellular regime based in Safranj.

♟ _Aldo per'Tenc:_ inspired by the example of the Red Land District seizure of the local phylakes, Aldo runs a publishing house dedicated to the idea of a saffron ribbon revolution. A frothing authentic working humans' movement is growing around Aldo. ♟ _Iscaffo an'Pusc:_ an upstart of no pedigree who returned alive and with a fabulous fortune from the portal-riddled west is making waves with his populist plans to offer full Safranj voting citizenship to the mass of adopted, generated, and half-born. If successful, it would make his party the most numerous in the Yellow Land.

♟ _Usello HMG-32912:_ a senior manager-president in the

Heliodor Mercantile Guild, Usello has consolidated the guild office guards division (incorporated) into a paramilitary force. How was this done under the ever-staring eyes of the phylakes? No matter. The Yellow Land's dominant mercantile oversight and trading organization forming its own army will certainly have no terrible consequences.

**Decapolypolist Autarkics**

The Polypolists, also called the _Hundred Flowers Caucus_, value local autonomy and economic zones of influence, often at the expense of neighboring settlements. Most local groups are structured as country clubs liasing between citizens and their town's admisymbs.

More extreme autarkics style themselves the _Original_ _Program Alliance_ . They want to restore the elder founding protocols and cut ties with other settlements. They use the mythic Black City as a proof of concept.

♟ _Ercle de Tigré:_ with a pedigree as long as a very long ancestral poem, Ercle is keen to prove that the novel extrastellar servant summoning routines discovered in the Machine Dread can bring glory to their town and local flower caucus. The routines have a non-zero chance of summoning a **greater** **incongruity** (L17, enormous) with each use. ♟ _HS11{tea} "Petticôte":_ the dominant admisymb of "Cycad" settlement has developed an unforseen ambition subroutine and is quietly rallying a federalliance against Safranj and the Emerald City. ♟ _Saö Ar Catro:_ restored to life after decades melded into an admisymb, they want to overthrow the symbiote structures and restore the benevolent despotism of the town's once sentient autofactory.


<a name="page_0187"></a>

**Periwinklers, Bypoliticals**

The Yellow Land autochthones might be satisfied with their two-faction system, but the majority of humans in these regions do not fall neatly into the approved superior local-sprung caste. While nativists might scoff at the idea that these peripheral groups matter, perhaps they should not be so hasty.

1. The _dieselers_ (diesel dwarves) are several corporatist colonies loosely affiliated with the Red Land District and other dewerker anti-theists. They have a close relationship with the Unlord Vulkana and control most of the regional fuel fountains. The biggest name in hydracarbons is the bombastic **Puël Pumptzar** (L5, pickled) of Naphtaline.
2. The _nomranchs_ (nomad ranchers) account for the majority of the mobile agriculturalists beyond the reach of most urban idea-speakers. Clannish and usually divided, nevertheless anyone who would control the hinterland must deal with them. **Tenforé of UpliftedFowl** (L7, flesh trader) is the most famous of the nomranch clan heads, once selling 10,000 heads at a single session of the Pardon Market.
3. The _sufferseals_ (suffershield anthroposeals) have come to control the anemone-like proteinspewer géants that favor the coastal waters of the Chaos. The floating shanties of these aquatic posthumans are tolerated, but many traditional humans view them as nearly animals. Perhaps a dangerous folly. The **Groaning Family** controls Loaned Island's protein with a **scoop-brain undine** (L14, fear-filter).
4. The _wirites_ (wire ghouls) are a number of electromagically sustained post-mortal communities dwelling in the Mountains of Light. Keeping them content and quiescent keeps Safranj safe. Turning the survivals under the Charcoal Apotheote into a post-mortal army is the fever dream of one **Gnonc the Wise** (L8, self-named) of the Orange Borderlands.

**Barbarians and Barbarophiles**

Local political disunity and disorganization means that non-Garden humans can infiltrate local society to a degree impossible nearly anywhere else. Not just that, many soil-born locals bored and disappointed with ossified native traditions enjoy the novelty suggested by all things barbarian, from playing with autonomous motor vehicles to wearing forbidden colors such as ultra purple and solar jade.

1. The _dusterlings_ (canyon humans) of the narrow places beyond the Garden are a branch of iron humans who have reinvented pre-dream traditions. Whether they are crazed fundamentalists or dangerous survivalist zealots is, uh, up to you. The Clan of the Little Sun under **Brothermother Sarc Aspic** (L5, wizardress of old vidy-tech) has gone to Greetsuns, hoping to redirect the little sun and move the Glass-Like-Water Sea.
2. The _glaziers_ (glass humans) control a number of aerolith islands in orbit around the Mountains of Light and further east. They seem to communicate mostly through light emmissions and occasionally trade rare oldtech for worthless scavenged goods. They say their leader, **Crystal Torso** (L4, fractured), is a god. Why? Who knows. It does not speak.
3. The _infrarotted_ (infrared posthumans) are a category of trader zombies who survive the terrible radiations of the Doublesun Reach, beyond the Mountains of Light. Their auras cause pain to normal humans, but there are few better guides for the far east. The most affordable infrarotted guides are the **Owe-Us® clones** (L2, hardy) survivors of a failed solar farming franchise in the deep Doublesun Hazard.
4. The _steppers_ (steppe-landers) is a broad term for the herding clans who live free of city and wijk in the posturban desolation of the Little Steppe and beyond. Many view them as dangerous, but their ability to bypass phylake violence restrictions with their unarmed combat styles makes them popular as guards and mercenaries. The most noble, good, and generous of the stepper lords is **Att Golc the Bonetaker** (L9, hero). No other lord is wiser in justice or kinder to their underlings. None have won so many lawsuits against evil, chaotic fools who would slander their name and reputation.


<a name="page_0188"></a>

**ABACO'S TEMPLE MOBILE**

_"No mere géant, no mere temple. This great crawler, this_ _megamorph has accreted and grown around a divine spike,_ _a heart of builder, and a seed of milkweed."_ —Local folklore.

The ever-growing temple-beast-mountain of the lord of numbers harvests excess knowledge and sets it in stone. Numerarians, maintainers, and other savants of the Long Long Ago, who feel the pull of the older world and wish to ascend to a nobler state of academic pursuit climb the ivory shell of the great Temple Mobile. There, they are welcome to carve out an ivory shack and live their exalted lives in the contemplation of perfect axioms.

_**Temple Stay.**_ For €10 per night you too can experience the cosmos in a grain of temple-beast-mountain sand.

_**Abaco's Ivory Village.**_ To live in a shack made of Abaco's temple beast's evergrowing bones is to become closer to the universal reason. Spend a year in a shack to remove one trait or burden of your choice, lose one random motivation or passion, and gain +1 aura.

_**Void Brain.**_ The beast has no brain, it is run by the void at its heart where the **nihil priests** (L5, dispassionate) sing.

**Yellow God, also Mathic Lord Abaco**

By dream calculus their stone is the heliodor, their loved bird the hawk, their blood-marked tree the drago.

"The eternal scribe who tallies and accounts. They that accumulates and invests, rations and divides. The bringer of profits and poet of growth. But also, the devouring machine, the taskmaster, the grinder of dreams."

**Prayers to Mathic Lord Abaco**

Once per session or so; should you seek accumulation, eternal increase and momentary surcease, whisper:

> "Ascend our line, ascend our moon, ascend our star;
> eat my toil, eat my soul, give me now my elevation..."

**Roll d20 + Thought - Aura**

| Result | Effect |
|:---|:---|
| 1 or less | Numbers flee your mind, everything is one, everything is zero. Confusion reigns. |
| 2–19 | Hold your rolled number hot in your head. Add it or subtract it once. |
| 20 or more | A clocktruth presence. A machine promises law. Regularity. Hold a blessing in within, sacrifice it to save without rolling. |


<a name="page_0189"></a>

**GARDENER GÉANTS**

The Decapolitan Chaos is an unstable landscape, still alive with the great megamorphs, the biomechanical soilformers surviving from the Builder Era.

The local cities claim to control them—at least they manage to keep them from destroying too much of their lands. At the same time, these divine creatures keep the divided land safe from the imposition of mere human will, free of the Cogflower worshippers of the Green Land and the deadly reasonable overtures of the

Orange Land.

**Number:** One.

**Level:** 17 / Life: 289

**Defense:** 15 (as living bone). **Move:** Very very slow. **Morale:** 11 (divine biomachine)

**Attack:** +11 builder ray 100 damage and 1d6 x +5 limbs or pseudopods 3d20 trampling damage. **Special:** An aura of corrupting, fiery radiation surrounds each géant. If their innards are exposed, the aura strengthens. A slain géant revives after a year of sunrises and sunsets, unless its soul is crushed and mined. **Treasure:** Their blood, droppings, bile, ichor, and other leavings run with: (1) powerful fuels, (2) rich nutrients, (3) precious minerals, (4) refined metals, (5) desirable pigments, (6) crushed soul stuff worth €500 per sack.

**This Géant**

| d6 | Function | Form | Error |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | skymaker | slithering hill of ... rubbery ... flesh and ... stone | It believes it is creating a new world. |
| 2 | soilmaker | creeping mat of ... thorny ... ooze and ... bone | It is subverted by an anarchist nemesis. |
| 3 | watermaker | crawling cube of ... scaly ... veins and ... glass | It is deluded by an outgarden brain worm. |
| 4 | firemaker | squirming tube of ... sinewy ... plates and ... metal | It is undead and needs souls to survive. |
| 5 | nutrifactor | floating mass of ... fuzzy ... limbs and ... wood | It is spreading corruption with its touch. |
| 6 | ruinbreaker | writhing clumps of ... grisly ... fronds and ... radiation | It is a dead biomachine run by ill-lings. |

**Its Passage**

| d6 | Omen | Vicinity | Aftermath |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | venomous lightning storm | the gift of speech is taken away | soils are more fertile for a season |
| 2 | howling acidic gales | eyes can see no colors | waters spawn new species for a month |
| 3 | rumbling rattling tremors | hair rises as electric sparks fly | creatures need not eat for a week |
| 4 | fleeing beasts and birds | machines lose all motion | machines work more smoothly |
| 5 | darkening of all lights | mineral and metal become malleable | roads and rails live once more |
| 6 | clouds of firefly wisps | plants grow at terrifying speeds | ghosts wear flesh and walk for a while |


<a name="page_0190"></a>

**A DECAPOLIS — A DECAYPOLIS?**

_"There are ten cities. There are always ten cities. Whether your fingers count negative seven or seven hundred settlements, there are ten cities."_ —Semmelvis the Numerian, Count of Towns

_"I have counted the independent polities who acclaim each other cities and make Congress together, and they are today eighteen. Tomorrow they may be more or less, but eighteen is the number of true named free cities in the H.M.G."_ —Collera den Xudt Xudt, Corsair Banker Advocate

As the land shifts, so shift the cities. Yet, both cities and land remain. Some officially accredited, others criminally rooted in the holy yellow clay. Yet, they are one of the ten cities uncountable.

**This City ...**

| d10 | Form | Architecture | Origin | Center | Periphery | Demographics |

<a name="page_0191"></a>

**Onomastic Secrecy**

Each Yellow Land town has a public name displayed on map and map, spoken in public. But this name is a mask-name, an invocation to avert the daemons of strife, corruption, envy and decay. Each town also has a true name, which captures its essential sacred history.

This name is inscribed in the source code of its citizens, bonding them and affirming their autochthony. They share this name by secret gesture and sign, glyph and symbol, but never utter or write it, lest it be stolen by outsiders, whether human, daemon, or machine.

**Ominous Omens ...**

_"This shining city will shine forever!"_ —anonymous inscription, Glass Crater Stele 21

Every admisymb, every merchant priest, every town praise-singer is taught to divine the Lords' will in sky and sand, wind and weird. These omens are feared:

1. Lines cross the sky, as when the lightbringers brought low the Other Garden and ushered in a season of winter.
2. Pools of light open in the mountains, as when the great Death Stork laid low the town we do not speak of.
3. Birds aggregate and speak the cacophony of bees, as when the peckers of flesh blinded the city of Au Venn Venn.
4. Triangles of shipstuff, powered aeroliths, descend as when the Ill Chosen were disappeared, resetting the Land of HS 12.
5. Red clouds blot the sky over the mountain goddess, as when the seven myriad wire ghouls were disgorged.
6. A new moon looms over the valley of town, as when the Bloom of Hungry Green overtook the settlement that was HS 256.

**When the City Falls ...**

_"Lord! Your faithful gather at your Screen, but it is dark! Your faithful gather at the fountain of flesh and alcohol, but it is still. Lord! The rotborn, the outsiders mock us and threaten us, but we do not waver! Lord! Come to us now!"_ —last vidy record, Chamber of the Hand of God, HS 39

Was it revolution? Was it a fool archaeologist activating an ancient Lord? Was it a divine beast gone mad?

1. Desperate citizens queue into the Harvester, to store their minds and give their souls to be remade.
2. Phylakes cart away the bodies and pave over the ruin with shipstone, entombing all evidence.
3. The ruins turn to glass, the doomed preserved in merriment and joy, specters in their tomb mirrors.
4. Golems build a cenotaph to the departed, engraving face and source and statement in the plastic stones.
5. Steppers pasture their hexachels, grickles come out of the feral parks, fields spread where towers stood.
6. Water drowns the ruin, fish and whale and undine now rule where another human experiment failed.
7. Vine and thorn thrive in the ash and bone, the verdant Green of Aspera reclaims the ruin.
8. Preserved in time-like-amber, the horror and the misery remain, a warning to future humans who would raise their hands against their Lords.

**A Town's True Name (Roll Thrice)**

| d8 | 1st | 2nd | 3rd |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | [null] |  |  |
| 2 | [holy title] | [profane title] | [error title] |
| 3 | [input] | [output] | [byproduct] |

| 5 | [article] | [expletive] | [possessive] |

<a name="page_0192"></a>

**SAFRANJ — SAFFRON CITY**

_"This Public Thing, this city in yellow, this glory of the common weal, this product of personal ambition, this triumph of positive externality..."_ —The Private's Paean, Jelado yd ll Lesje (Soil Dandelion II)

**Background**

A cube of loomstone rose from the fertile Field of Gold (Oracrí), over the confluence of the Yellow (Jayhal) and Black Gold (Naftalrí) rivers. Was it the remnant of some plateau the builders shaved away? Or a loomstone spun by the Maker to show its infinite favor for the posteconomic fervor of the merchant humans who would one day build the hub of a drug empire upon this cube?

Whatever the true history currently approved by the Heliodor Mercantile Guild, the tunnel-threaded polychrome urban mass rises over the lush-gleaming fields and protein-rich waters. A rainbow jewel in any other land, it seems nothing more than a fitting pediment for the cloudscraping saffron-tiled towers and gilded rooves of Safranj (Freedom of Saffron).

First among the free cities of the Yellow Land and master city of State HS01Y "Saffield Brick Roads", Safranj is built on control of trade with the lands of distortion beyond the twice-insolated realms of the Infrared Desert. That, and a monopoly on the production and distribution of the mind-exploding, human-improving spice saffron.

Contemporary tourists also claim to visit Safranj for the vibrant binaural opera scene, the gilded impressionist dance companies, the fleshmelding parades, the reciprocal autosummoning circles, and the refacing performing art zombie troupes.

But really, that's just rationalization, isn't it?

_If you could turn your mind into a utopia, why would you_ _need struggle further against this ever-falling world?_

**Districts**

_**The Rooves.**_ Airy cloudscrapers of aerolith struts, saffron tiles, cedarwood pillars, and wallskin membranes. The locals wear aerolith belts and harnesses in case of falls.

_**The Landing.**_ One great mall covers the entire surface of the cube, with retractable chitin wings to shield against rain or ash. If you can't buy it here, it's out of style.

_**The Bowels Theatrical.**_ Great spherical halls, arenas, theaters, and declamatoria hollow out the cube. Tunnels, monastic cells and sleeping pods flesh out the rest.

_**The Bycubes.**_ Sprawling garden-houses cater to wealthy othersoil non-residents, ringing the cube of Safranj like seaweed deposited on the fringe of a popular beach.

_**Bricked Saffranches.**_ Dead ranches, their house-ghosts subdued, designed to offer visitors an approximation of the symbiotic Yellow Land farming experience. As well as discounted saffron experiences.

_Star Chicken Five Station._ Possibly predating Safranj itself, this major right road station is an autonomous vagabund enclave with its own “laws”. Or lack thereof.


<a name="page_0193"></a>

**Ambient**

The surface weather is normal: morning and evening storms, sun-drenched days, cold nights, and periodic pollen blooms that turn the atmosphere into a yellow soup teeming with filter-feeding air plankton shoals. The weather inside the welcoming builtmass of the Safranj cube is still somewhat regulated by the tethered **envirogéants** (L11, mostly harmless no reason to worry really it's fine).

| d6 | 1–2 Day | 3–4 Night | 5 Bloom | 6 Regulated |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1–3 | sun-drenched, whistly winds, dry moods | cool, still, fuzzy stars, stuttering signals | ecru fog, running noses, echoing sneezes, itchy eyes | clear air, dry throats, regular thumps, soothing voices |
| 4–5 | scattered clouds, damp zephyr cold, still breeze | zephyr cold, crystalline, jonquil clouds, plankton | wispy air, flaking skin, ominous glows | wispy air, flaking skin, mind-numbing whine |
| 6 | humid, still, bated, soft, waiting, sweating | howling winds, lashing dust, flying plankton slime | gamboge air beasts, howls, ectoplasmic pseudopoda | thick, cloying airs, dead silence, damp emotions |

**Events**

| d6 | 1–3 Expected | 4–5 Surprising | 6 Error |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | Ruderalist **explorers** (L2, skilled) hawking devices: portal switchers, weather editors, time-warpers, etc. | Ruinland **scavengers** (L4, expert) offering replicators, synthetic minds, and doomsday machine poetry. | Remote-controlled **human drones** (L6, master) of the **Electric Dread** (L15, corrupter) looking for a way in. |
| 2 | Distraught relatives demand news about their ancestors' stolen bodies. | **Wirefolk** (L2, skulking) stealing neural tissue and unattended hardware. | **Stumblecorpses** (L1, icky) with infectious implants fleeing the dewerkers. |
| 3 | Decapolitan representatives here to negotiate trade rights, water routes, géant controls, or client executions. | Overload **agents** (L3, humanish) selling dangerous, corrupting insights. 1-in-6 chance of a random power. | Postmortal **prophet** (L3, liberated) preaching about the seed of an undying god in the desert. |
| 4 | Stepper meat **merchants** (L2, six-limbed) on a spiritual trading journey. | Nomranch saffron **dealers** (L3, polite) peddling legalish mind-altering spices. | The **defaced vagabund** (L6, deathless) offers €5,000, a bomb, and a letter. |
| 5 | Traveling zoo-circus with everything from **infrarotted lizards** (L3, hot) to **radiation wights** (L2, hotter). | Dubiously traditional dusterling public feast. [spend 1d6 days then save to gain +1 aura] | **Loomstone Relic** (L12, fossil) offers secrets of the Good Engine. [decipher to gain +1 thought and 1 power] |
| 6 | Public hallucination opera with free saffron samplers. [may lose 1d100 x level xp to gain a random trait] | **Archetypes made flesh** (L2, numinious) visiting from the Infrapsychic Palace offer ponderous omens. | Find cursed die: (1–3) lose mind, body or soul, (4–5) wipe your sins, (6) gain +1 charisma, aura, and thought. |

**S.A.F.F. Approved Stays** **€/week**

| d6 | Stay | Description | €/week |
|---:|:---|:---|---:|
| 1 | Podboat Penthouses | Floating aquaplant accommodations on the lakes, rivers, and bays. Not actually penthouses. 5-in-6 chance the in-pod nutrient spigot is completely safe. | €7 |
| 2 | Dewerker Motor Courts | Hydrocarbon storage landwhale bladders turned into “cozy” rooms. Complimentary refined breakfast included. Local mechanic discount. | €15 |

<a name="page_0194"></a>

**THE VOIDWAY LANE**

_"Hwoosh! Just like that, everything was so white it felt purple-green. Like I could see through myself and the others. Then I looked back. Fico, Tanry, and the Bellweather were ... smeared out over a mile of regolith. Hard day."_ —Avoid the Voidway: Oral Histories of a Danger Zone.

Beyond the debris of builders and gods, older than those times are the aberrant artifacts—the aberracts. Perhaps they are the Maker's work? Perhaps an unlord's corruption, such as Ill-Nano? Or something else, a cosmic flaw, a portent of a future, a fragment of another past? Few aberracts are as dangerous as the Voidway Lane, that shifting highway out of time, the slippery roadside of the gods. It carves a vicious gash, a line of error through the gently rolling Little Steppe, the Rancheria Mosaic between the lands Yellow and Green.

Along the Lane something else moves through our space and time. Its colors are not our colors. Its numbers not our numbers. Its advent is not our advent. Flags inscribed with prayers flutter and tatter in the ill breeze, a smear of color, shattered bone, snapped wood, and lying new-growth marking the voidway lane.

At chaotic intervals, the 'Advent' visits. Or perhaps our space moves through the 'Advent'. Whatever happens, living matter in the voidway lane is suddenly and completely rearranged along its entire length.

Usually, the new arrangement seems half message, half mockery. Rarely, pearls of shipmetal, whorls of shaved spacetime, a manna of edible soul-stuff, and other stranger cargo is left scattered along the Lane. Never enough to sustain an industry, but attractive to desperate scavengers and hopeful gamblers. Enough for another fool to end up scattered across the voidway. Yet, this curse-formed barrier is also blessing, separating the Yellowland's local-patriot heresiarchs and the Greenland's love-demanding inquisition.

**The travelers stand at the first flags**, those least touched by the strange aberract. They mutter prayers, toss stones, and look to their ticker clocks and guidebooks. May the Advent be like it has been these recent days: predictable.

| Today ... | When ... | The Advent Comes ... | It Manifests ... | ... Better Run |
|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | thrice | it is here<br>uses minds as beacons | luminous faces curling true | grim, gasping, zig-zag |
| 2–3 | twice | soon<br>a strange, complex design | misfortune of blameless hue | swift, hopping, curving |
| 4–6 | once | later<br>yesterday's path is today's | electric fire from the blue | blind, determined, straight |

You cross into the danger zone, **to ford the voidway lane**. Your manual swears by the saving grace of ...

| d20+ | Charisma (Desire) | Aura (Substance) | Thought (Upbringing) |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 3 or less | The fire! The wind! The green! Your body is strewn along the way. | The colors! The movement! The not! Your mind is lifted away. | The blood! The rushing! The depths! Your soul is taken. |
| 4–6 | You decide, turn towards the voidway, and with ... the Advent is here. Safe passage is blocked for 1d6* hours. |  |  |
| 7 | Blown across. Groaning. A painful memory is erased. Something precious is piercing your flesh. | Thrown through. Prostrate. Bleeding. Something precious is missing. You feel a new memory (trait) within you. | Strange lights, distant whistles. Bang! A limb is missing. A new power resides within that phantom space. |
| 8–12 | You step, the voidway vibrates; then you are through, no memory of your passage. |  |  |
| 13 | Odd breeze. Air pressure distortion. You pass out. An eternity passes. One of your motivations shifts. | Gravity wrenches. Your clothes and gear and burdens lift. Choose one, it is gone. One of your colors shifts. | Voices. Laughter. You are fed, welded, melded, bled. Stop. Repeat. Rinsed. Restored. One of your traits shifts. |
| 15–17 | The flags and bones flutter, but you see and feel nothing. You are through. |  |  |
| 18–23 | You step through, safe ... then the world oscillates and the Advent remakes the voidway, blocking the path behind you for 1d6* hours. A shower of debris narrowly misses you. |  |  |
| 24 or more | The roaring Advent steals 1d6 days. Then you save. Success: gain +1 strength. Fail: gain a sense of self-confidence and humility. | The gabbling Advent steals 1d6 offerings or gifts. Then you save. Success: gain +1 endurance. Fail: gain a sense of deep time unbound. | The snuffling Advent steals 1d6 substitutes. Then you save. Success: gain +1 agility. Fail: gain a sense of contentment and true adequacy. |

Distrustful of your guides, you spend 1d6 days navigating around the prayer flags to avoid the danger of the Advent. No force, no lying Cat will trap you in this aberract. Not for you the broken time and space of Long Long Ago.



<a name="page_0195"></a>

**This Valuable Debris, This Stranger Stuff**

Many would say there is no Advent. They'd say it is but a legend. But what of the scattered bones and battered jewels?
