All these gifts of the aberract decay in a year, faster if used. But while they last, they celebrate the ineffable Maker.


<a name="page_0196"></a>

**REMARKABLE HELIODOR**

_"The guide used colored flags to speak with the okel orm and secure our passage onto the Refining Plain!"_ —My Journey, Arduous Villain (anon.)

**The Diesel Mountain—Vulkana**

_builderspawned aclhemititan_ Beyond the Fields of Jet, across the Hills of Slagga, above the Mountains of Light, rises Chem Caoutchouc, the all-chemical mother that transforms crude reality.

They that took the raw and made it cooked. The hacker of the builder’s raw perfection. But also, the refiner, the mistress of fuel, the bringer of fire.

_**Propitiate.**_ This unlord, this ungod, this divinity made flesh brings forth both woe and wealth in equal measure. Gaze into obsidian, make offerings to the olm, smoke the fireweed to avert Vulkana's wiles.

_**Ascend.**_ Climb the fuming mountain, brave its guardians, its **feral phylakes** (L7, demi-angelic) and **flambents** (L5, treeish), burn away part of yourself and fast for a week. Then, ascend again in a vision to improve a trait.

The Automatic Tourist Entity (A.T.E.) has compiled a list of must-see places in the Yellow Land for centuries. Recently, many warn it keeps suggesting destinations with a terrifying preponderance of surprisingly cannibalistic local practices.

**The Refining Plain** _dieseler holy region_


Autorefineries of livingstone linked by arteries of basalt and tentacles of shipmetal, sinews of standardstone and great mushroom vent-mounds stud the plain below the void-touching mountain Vulkana. Here the chosen oil-drinkers of the dieselers propitiate **okel orms** (L3, watching) and **antilich orms** (L7, destroying), to gain access to the corpsefuel, the hot gold that makes modern engines run and golems happy.

_**Worry:**_ within those passages, hidden from the sun, strange things happen to unattended humans. Many grow greyscale and machine-like. Are they becoming better servents of the autorefineries, or are they becoming agents of Error?


<a name="page_0197"></a>

**The Food Factory** _oldtech nutrifab, protein assembler_


After the great unification event of Mal Pop-poc III the labor citizens of Food Factory split between those who became one with the great Protein Mind and those who remained Dividuals. The unified humans live, breathe, and die for the great engine of food, converting organic fuel from trade and ground into food beasts carefully synthesized to stimulate the post-human palate.

The dividuals survive on the nutrients they filter from the rich effluveins of the factory, turning them into an array of foods fit for human palates.

Most visitors will be satisfied with a gastronomic tour of the great fortress of nutrition. The most adventurous may book an illegal tour of the flesh catacombs, the labyrinthine leavings of the immortal self-replicating factory.

_**Inside:**_ the **food beasts** (L5, tasty) have opinions, have thoughts, have dreams and souls. That is what the Great Howl of the dogheads says. If this is true, then is not the food factory farming people?

_"Hosts be praised! The archaeindustrial deposits are rich! Feed stock for our matter makers!"_ —Pit Survey 775-343, Walveduc Dieseler Archives

**The Pits of History** _archaeindustrial mining zones_


Gifts of the Builders and the Géants, the Yellow Land is pockmarked with places where the top soil hides rich deposits of prehistoric industrial wealth. Compacted aluminium corpses, layers of fine glass, grand boluses of adamant and biomatter, whole ground crystal cities, veins of bronze and copper still filled with permaplasm.

_**Wonder:**_ the striated layers, a prehistory of the Long Long Ago written in divine gifts left for the comfort of this later age. A day's careful prospecting may deliver jewels of the past worth €1d10 [3].

_**Worry:**_ steer clear of **mechanical ghosts** (L1, gremlins) and **petrochemical oozes** (L3, flammable), of course, but more than that—beware the **petrolier heretics** (L2, cursing), anti-dwarves espousing the false blood.


<a name="page_0198"></a>

**WARBARIANS**

_No human was born free that was not born in blood._ —Ill Nano, Against the Flesh Remade, 5:13

Do not think that just because you venture to lands where the phylakes' stern visage still holds dominion and enforces the ancestral peace, you may avoid all danger. Once, the grand phylakes were not alone. Lesser guardians dwelled within them and among the humans, making of the land a pacific paradise.

Now, those lesser guardians are gone, and the grand phylakes that remain cannot account for every machete and missile in the many lands. Humans, treacherous apes, find ways and means to subvert the gentle conditioning of the old gods and restore conflict and history to the Circle Sea.

Here, in the fringes of this disunited land, where dusterling and stepper and other semi-humans dwell, you may well meet sentient creatures bred to violence.

**Whose This War Band**

1. Industrialist harvesters, canker-dwarves breaking free of the restrictive sustainability dogma.
2. Bodysnatcher entrepreneurs, keen to supply the great plantations of the Orange Lands.
3. Cogflower radicals, permanent reformulators.
4. Marginals, half-humans driven mad by the need for survival and the demands of civilization.
5. Betters and hammers pushed into coalition by their predatory lephines.
6. Feral scavengers from beyond the Garden, hunting for parts of flesh and metal for their neopolities.
7. Cloned aristocrats, mentally-conditioned lephines operating as an extension of a single estate's will.
8. Brutal fundamentalists who deny the machine and celebrate the glory of the original made form.

| d20 | Title | Lvl | Life | Mor | Def | Bon | Dmg | Special (Roll Separately) |
|---:|:---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|:---|:---|
| 1–5 | Crier | 1 | 8 | 6 | 13 | +4 | 1d6* | Tricameral mind. Immune to mental attacks. |
| 6–10 | Corporal | 2 | 12 | 7 | 15 | +5 | 2d4* | Bugkiller or killer bug? Long range biotoxin attack. |
| 11–14 | Chevalier | 3 | 16 | 8 | 17 | +6 | 2d6* | Bioborg. Living equine exosuit for mobility. |
| 15–17 | Captain | 4 | 24 | 9 | 16 | +8 | 2d8* | Second head. Split attention. Attack twice. |
| 18–19 | Champion | 5 | 36 | 11 | 19 | +10 | 3d6* | Relife parasite. Return to life stronger if killed. |
| 20 | Colonel | 6 | 60 | 7 | 15 | +12 | 3d8* | Holy blood. Invisible to phylakes. Immune to poison. |


<a name="page_0199"></a>

**How They Avoid the Gun-Breakers**

1. They gather in small, loose bands only. As the folk hero saying goes, “a hundred will rarely call the angel death, a thousand always must.”
2. They blot their minds with spirits, drugs, possession, mantras or cloudy helms to be less sentient.
3. They disassemble their weapons.
4. They wield multipurpose items not covered by the phylake's current weapon recognition algorithms.
5. They offer sacrifices to the phylake's gods to receive user permissions to enter their domains.
6. They don't, but by some glitch (1-in-12), the grand phylake does not react. Still, few generals would risk an army to such a roll of the dice.
7. Their bodies are their weapons, their minds still as water even as they kill.
8. They march through tunnels and dull-ways, shielded by the weight of rock and world-metal from the eyes of the grand phylakes.

**Left Unopposed, What Havoc Will They Wreak?**

1. Settlements burn, pillage is taken, refugees stream into cities; new labor to delight the hungry masters.
2. An ancient autofabricator is gutted, never to work again. Its parts are sold for a fraction of its value.
3. The old order is upturned, the betters and lephines are eaten, a new popular tyranny is established.
4. Defenders destroy bridges, break dams. The war band retreats, the settlements decline.
5. An ancient guardian awakes, a cruel godling from an older time. The warriors are destroyed, the locals subjugated to a new immortal lord.
6. A great oldtech monolith is reactivated. The war band is enslaved. The settlement militarizes.
7. The abbey of memory is despoiled, the golden pages of record are melted, the megas are freed, the wealth vitalizes a merchant scavenger revolution.
8. A vault from Long Long Ago is opened, but no treasures they find, only death and pestilence and mere chaos to loose upon this latter world.

**The Chronickler of Lost Times**

_mobile buildergolem archivist_ There, beyond the realms controlled by humans, out where even warbarians grow sparse, wanders **Chrolt the Chronickler** (L15, sentient monastery) with his coterie of **whispering ghosts** (L1, ermine) and **gibbering maintainers** (L2, canine).

He observes. He documents. His recounts are always perfect. Alas, his archive is full so every new record purges an old one, leaving history lost in an eraser fog, drowned in the paper recycler vats.

All are welcome who donate paper and ink, lenses and films, porcelain tablets and micromodulators. Alas, food and drink are not allowed in the chronickler.

_**Atop.**_ Sad decay has crumbled the human settlement atop the grand golem, much like history has humbled the great dreams humanity once had.

_**Within.**_ Corridors and conveyors, televators and eleporters riddle the archivist, full of trips and traps and murder holes to catch thieves of knowledge.

_**Stele of the Heart.**_ A lustrous midnight slab of captured carbon hidden from the Chronickler's own memory records the dread of the bi-aerate coal. This elemental union of two genies of air and one of coal nourished jungles and trapped heat. Eventually, it suffocated animals and drowned a tribe of sinful humans with their own wastes to teach the other tribes their place.


<a name="page_0200"></a>

**L'OST 'SPITAL APOTHEOTIC**

_"Once, the Masters of Dream and Bone saw fit to give humans life everlasting in the gemstone matrix of the Second Maker. Since the Undreamt Rebellion, no hereditary minister would suffer such waste of human potential."_ —Education for Labor and Purpose, 5.75 Edition, Safranj Alltechnical Mercantile College (W(s)MXX-sh)

Beyond the grasp of any one city state, past the hulking bulk of the ungoddess-mountain Vulkana swells the soils and stones of the Given World beyond the membranes of air and its nourishing acid forming constituent, stand the apotheotes. The ever-living independent facilities, the builder-given palaces to the betterment of humanity.

One infamous such apotheote is the Prison of Ghosts, the Eastern Apotheotic Hospital, _L'Ost 'Spital_ in the older local dialect. Once, it was a simple spiritual eden, a place to garden the minds of the corporeally embarrassed until such time as their bodies could be recreated.

Alas, it is the nature of humans to corrupt all good things given by the wisdom of the builders.

When the 72nd Improving Jubilee was announced the anti-prophet who shall not be named led the Salvaged in a disgusting raid upon this facility, to take the Makermade gemstone matrix and use it to set their mind-souls free of the Garden of Humanity.

Of course they failed, but they also corrupted the gemstone matrix and left the surrounding terrain a foul wasteland of wandering half-minded ghosts, a warning to all who would leave the appropriate and proper path.

**Conspiracy Salvaged**

Trust not the lies of the ministry's smallminded heirs. The _Daughter of Mercies_ sought to set humans free of the unholy trap, the accursed path of the Canopy. Yes, she failed, but her key she projected forward through time and an order of the salvaged remained in the wasteland, on the periphery of humanity, to await its return!

**'Ware the Apotheotic Wasteland!**

1. A **half-eaten phylake** (L13, angel), cursed to burn the humans it once saved.
2. **Radiant wights** (L3, medicant), lying that they wish to heal and improve the world.
3. **Half-minded ghosts** (L1, possessive) who would drag you into a useless past.
4. Groaning **boulder flora** (L3, rolling) gathering moss and dreams.
5. **Zombie cactus** (L2, cross-infested) hungry for cerebral fluids.
6. Nomadic **post-lapin colony herd** (L3, radiovorous).
7. Definitely **not salvaged monks** (L3, plastic humans).
8. Yellowland **fabrispectors** (L4, conspiracy merchants).

♟ _Saña an'Cuoio:_ the leathery, mummified Chief Liberator of the Not-Salvaged Order, dedicated to “preventing” the return of the Salvaged Heresy; awaits the arrival of the _Key of Mercies_ to again unlock the human mind.

♟ _Lom Umolom:_ an ambitious junior pirate banker of the Bank Movil of the Sailing Isles has simpler plans for the gemstone matrix. According to reputable estimates, mined and sold, it would net €1,500,000,000.


<a name="page_0201"></a>

**The 74th Bled Army**

A time capsule preserved this seed corps of mummified warriors, waiting for the human mind to be unlocked. The return of the Key of Mercies is the sign the army has waited for. Leached of all color, pale as bone, they approach the L'Ost Spital apotheote to turn it into the home base of their body superpolitic.

The **Bled Army** is a slime mold-human mummy symbiote with no singular mind, rather it is a super-cellular collection of distributed processes and complexes animated by a coherent subconscious drive to unity. Their ancient dialectical cause may be swamped in layers of dogma and propaganda, yet: they remain ready to:

1. Share the gift of perfect and eternal postmortal equality.
2. Raid humans for new mummies to grow its polite body.
3. Grow new sunlight and radiation harvesting sproutfields.
4. Transmit propaganda messages, swamping all frequencies.
5. Send runners to seed colonies-in-waiting for future spread.
6. Craft encampments that look like occult symbols from above.
7. Self-organize into collective industrial manufacturing teams.
8. Sing in perfect, tireless union.

Individual **Bled soldiers** (L1d4, moldy) may:

1. Be incredibly damage resistant, continuing to move even if dismembered or decapitated.
2. Reassemble or combine multiple parts and bodies, using symbiotic cellular stalks to knit tissues together.
3. Suspend their metabolism completely, using dust or sand cover to become nearly invisible. A whole corps might leave a few lookouts, while resting merged into its environment.
4. Exhibit a personality when alone, but subsuming into the greater whole when reconnected.
5. Wear a purposeful, beatific smile, as though the mummification process was euphoric and uplifting.
6. Develop gas-filled fruiting bodies to rise on the wind, like mummified, militarised dandelion seeds.
7. Express weapon and equipment blueprints encoded in their symbiotes' source codes.
8. Spontaneously combust with a smell of charred pork after centuries in their dry seed barracks.

**Aftermaths of the L'Ost**

☗ _Psychosocial Revolution._ The Not-Salvaged Order reveals they are Salvaged followers of the Daughter. With the infectious Key of Mercies they liberate populations from their dreamings, unleashing a cycle of regional social wars.

☗ _Gemstone Matrix Salvage._ The pirate bankers flood the markets with billions in new, hard gemstone currency. Inflation sweeps the Circle Sea, doubling all prices. Socioeconomic crises and violence follow.

☗ _Bled Home Base Established._ The Bled Army hive mind blooms into a new major faction, its gifts of purpose, euphoria, and immortality (of a sort) finding ready recruits among the masses of less-uplifted humanity.


<a name="page_0202"></a>

**SUNRISE IN THE WEST**

_"The Little Sun is no true sun, no generative void-orb, instead it is a coiled Angel trapped within the shell of a Dragon, a divine 3rror stolen from the Unlords and chained to the Given World to drip gold and other metal treasures upon the Twice-Sunned Land."_ —New Dewerker Revolutionary Manifesto (Rewritten), Naphta Locks Diesel Archives (Novel Era 15)

Out past the flanks of [praise/flatter/scrape/bow] Divine Vulkana, goddess-not-demoness Mountain, where sand dragons whirl like clouds and solar wisps hurl themselves upon the old tether-fields of the Near Companions, there is that place called in the tongues of the Yellow traders the Golden Desert, but also the Twice-Sunned Land.

As in other lands, the Green Sun that now gives life and feeds the phytoles, rises beyond the edge of the Given World and swings about in the Far Void, but here also the Little Sun, the Gold Dripper, emerges from bubbling, fuming Soil, a sphere of Heat and Light, to cycle through the Upper Airs, shedding stone and aerolith, metal and gold, sending hot winds flailing North and South while it passes countersolar from the Glass-Like-Water Sea.

Its ascent and tides wash the shores in waves of molten metals and send up clouds of superheated gasses, treasures to be harvested by the canopic shadows, the golems or ghosts of thin stuff able to dwell in the open air while the Little Sun sets brings gifts up out of our common underworld.

**The House of Revival**

_Buildertech solar birth-marked monument_

The hospitable ziggurat, extruded of shipstone to glory a peace between Mathic Abaco, the Chaos Dwarf, and the Invisible Hand. Here, they divided the bowels of the Chemical Mother among themselves and bound this Land's géants forevermore to their solar gyres.

That is what the antentropic plastic plaque in the automated lobby proclaims, anyway.

Today, the House of Revival serves as hospice and midwife both to golems who would repattern their souls and forge themselves anew in the glow of the Little Sun.

♟ _Library of Matto:_ the umbral golem, woven of thin stuff, stores retired golems' patterns in the dark of the house.

♟ _Jaw of Lantern:_ the hard light golem of luminous matter like glass, weaves new souls and minds for golems. But what is the fuel?


<a name="page_0203"></a>

**Wandering These Daily-Seared Shores**

1. The **great dark body** (L14, daemon-woven shadow), absorbing heat and life, radiating confusion.
2. Posse of **canopic shadows** (L5, operatic) hunting for ceramic aeroliths.
3. Wing of **golem wasps** (L3, metal hive) who mold fresh aerolith into their ceramic hives.
4. Herd of glitter-scale **boulderbeasts** (L2, photovores).
5. **Thin-stuff ghosts** (L1, timebound) in solar suits.
6. Dreaming **crater heather** (L2, thinkweed).
7. Travelers from afar, self-styled **khans and magi**, bearing poison gifts (L4, posthuman).
8. **Solar géants** dragging their great aerolith bodies as they harvest the drippings of the Little Sun (L12, magitechnical megafauna).

**Sunrise Extractor**

_megafaunal pleasure facility_ An ageless autorefinery, staffed by hundreds of **thin-stuff laborers** (L2, placebound) bound to the Wheel of Renewal in the geometric gardapartments, each death followed by a blissful interval of synthetic heaven. The autorefinery invades the minds of géants, giving pleasure in exchange for harvested heavy metals.

The autotruckers who took this treasure to the spinfactories atop the Ladder of Heaven are gone, so laborers dump it back into the Glass-Like-Water Sea.

♟ _Theofré the Ill-Renewed:_ dreams he is an autotrucker.

<!-- Begin: Our_Golden_Age_09_Green_Land_204-223 -->

<a name="page_0204"></a>

**GREEN LAND**

_"The Maker gave the Cosmos to the Builders,_ _the Builders gave the World to the Lords,_ _the Lords gave the Garden to the Humans,_ _the Humans gave the Helm to the Ministry,_ _the Ministry takes the Lead down the Garden Path."_ —traditional Green Land postulate


<a name="page_0205"></a>

The Green Land is the first of all lands, the cradle of humans, the light of progress and forward motion, the engine of growth, the machine of sustenance, the measure of civilization. It is eutopia, the good place.

All is as good as it could ever get here.

If any land can claim to flower as the Garden was meant to flower, it is the Green Land. All is growth here, all is renewal here; death is recycled into new life, humans live in perfect harmony with the total technoecosphere of the Mother Machine, who upholds better than any other extant Mind the will and spirit of the Lords and Builders.

The eternal civilization on the banks of the Green River, from the feeder tells of the lesser towns to the space-time expanding wonder of the Emerald City, manifests the perfection of the temporarily-absent divine Lord Aspera.

**Climate**

Balmy, subtropical, with frequent rains and gentle radiations. Cooler and harsher in the highlands. The valley air is cleansed of impurities by floating filter mats and the ceaseless labors of aerolithic golems. The Emerald City makes its own weather for the good of its humans and the Mother Machine.

**Population**

Land and outer city: ~17 million, portal city: 72,334,912

**Groups**

Greenlanders citizen 34%, Greenlanders corporate 17%, false humans 15%, barbarians resident 13%, rainbowlanders resident 10%, golems 6%, others 2%

**Languages**

Canopic (official), Betterspeak (ministry), Emerald (commerce), Greenspeak (lower), Feralshi Cabal (barbarian), Bilder (generated humans)

**Capital**

Official: Mothercity Practical: Evergarden, the model city in the biolithic canopy of the emerald livingstone platform.

**Government**

Interpretative oneirocracy. The Ministry Inquisitive interprets the dreams of Aspera's avatar, the all consuming Mother Machine slumbering at the equidistant heart of the Metropolis. The Rites Banked and Corporate implement the interpretations for the Greater GoodTM of the land and the invisible hand.

**Ideologies**

Cogflower: growth (official), Invisible Hand: panhedonic (tolerated), Blue God: anomic liberation (suppressed).

**Economy**

By divine law, the richest land and the measure of developed human contentment. All manner of semisentient oldtech fabricators operate themselves in accord with the interpretations of the Ministry.

**Resources**

Omnibatteries, autofabricators, nutrient processors, anthropogenerators, plant- and beastmakers.

**Means of Production**

The Butcher Bankers preserve the holy growth of the circular economy and maintain the incorruptible C.A.S.H. The Cogflower Corporations ensure golem gears and human hands work together for common prosperity. Individual human ownership of the means of production is illegal. Share systems provide aristocrats vital revenues to support their esteemed social roles.

**Material Conditions**

Official: each citizen is provided a customized livingwood sarcopod plus 7 cash per week. Effective: publishing socioeconomic census results is illegal as of Stasis Tulip VII to prevent ill humors.

_Source: Millemotto Facet, Aggregated Academics, Hive University [unofficial], Flux Edelweiss IX_

_The human spawner was (is?) a phytohominid experiment._


<a name="page_0206"></a>

[![Green Land map (page 206)](images/page_0206_green_land_map.png)](images/hires/page_0206_green_land_map.png)

The human body, fresh decanted from the synthetic matrix where it had grown to the flush of young maturity, blinked its eyes. It was still too fresh to be a full human. The artificial experiences of its three-year gestation from zygote to orimonate (ripe-born) still sat.

“Pray tell, good progenitor <INSERT NAME>, where do I find myself?” it asked, in the archaic Bilder of most orimonates.

“I am Timpanes VJ-gamma-final-fi, madire of the independent incorporated settlement of Second Coel Estis, local-framed New Green. You may call me Tim.”

The body nodded, eager to please. “Indeed, good progenitor <TIM>, I thank you for this knowledge of Second Coel Estis, local-framed New Green.”

It gazed curiously at the simple brick walls, the polished concrete floors, the exposed ductwork under the roof ceiling. Tim knew what was coming.

“Good progenitor <TIM>, I am taking in a very ... simple environment, unlike the dream of polished surfaces and flying cities I knew as I grew to this maturity. What happened?”

“Nothing happened. There is no story. This is the best possible world. This is heaven. That was a dream.”

“Why is this place called Second Coel Estis, local-framed New Green, good progenitor <TIM>?” it persisted, relentless like any toddling flesh-born of four years.

“That is not a valid question, humorno. Now, get up and let's get you working. After all, work hand enough you might become human!”

The soft-skin body bowed to the glowing glass face in the middle of the elephantine rubber-and-steel frame of the good progenitor and intoned in the sing-song of joy-good teaching programme, “Service makes us human!”

A rusted door opened and chartreuse light limned a figure far shorter than the ripe-born, dressed in a shabby uniform piped with long-cared-for plastic and copper.

“A post-human dwarf regressive!” escaped the surprised cry from the soft-skin.

The shabby little creature, face covered in whiskers, scalp sprouting multicolored fur, did not understand the slur and spoke to the good progenitor as though the new body was not even there, “Yave, bow’n’scrin’, Tim-tim, what scraw. Tis a new-bird agenting?”

“Tis te new-bird mackoy stipend. Agentling yaw-naw, choose Miton Star, shruck, naw-me chewing” replied Tim in the local ‘Merald neo-common.

<a name="page_0208"></a>

**JOY GOOD DISPENSARY**

_"Pleasure, treasure, big surprise! Monkey, donkey, dead inside! Fritter, titter, blessed watching eyes. Wriggly bread, have no pride!"_ —Pleasure Eyes 2bis, Procedural Classics Vol. 172

All consumption is directed and controlled for the Greater GoodTM and private mercantile activity is strictly forbidden. All licensed dispensaries are provided by retail hives supervised by the Three Rites and tailored to the class-needs of the citizen.

According to the _Guidebook on Human Cultivation (37th ed.)_ citizens are free to access dispensaries for the goods to live “free from the hedonic treadmill and in keeping with the collective best interest.” Practically, whether out of hunger, desperation, or boredom, most humans seek out non-dispensary vendors for food, goods, and memetics to supplement their allotted quotas.

Despite regular “pruning actions”, illegal gray and green markets abound. Non-citizens cater to the upper strata who prefer the human touch that vegetal retail drones cannot manage. The falschers and lower classes self-organize bazaars in the hollows and roadlots of the towns and cities. Secret maps and code words can lead to some spectacular shopping discoveries.

<a name="page_0210"></a>

**FACTIONS VIRIDIAN**

_"There are no factions in the Green Land. Everyone works together in peace and harmony for the common weal."_ —Grand High Intern Sesti od Mamon, Ministry One

**The Three Rites**

In truth, the Three Rites—finance, industry, and administration—dominate the upper echelons of Green society. Managers, burghers, scions, and aristocrats climb interwoven ladders of meritocratic success through a system of poetry trials and athletic exams.

The Rites share control of the _Wonderful Pneumatic Refinery_, a soul mill that annihilates the spirits of select sentients, powering the Green Land’s oldtech. It also serves as a meeting point for the Rites' Pie Division—their most august and sacred coordination committee.

An _error is brewing_. More and more of the humans produced by the Mother Machine are flawed, some without souls at all. A controlist splinter argues that interpreting the avatar’s dreams is no longer enough to promote the Garden Path—and maintain control.

♟ _Senes iy'Luó:_ rogue junior lord of industries. Leads efforts to reverse-engineer the Machine’s sarcopods and disrupt the human generator market.

♟ _Sad Me Difort:_ elfin vice-minion of finance and forestries. Populist head of the mass regeneration movement, feeding pure human stock to revitalize the Mother's pangenerative virtues.

**The Soiltwined**

Born on and of Soil—the laborers of the land and the golems of the garden find common cause despite their disparate, unnatural, and unmachined origins. “Are we not all red in tooth and claw, born to struggle, to strive? This is our nature—toil of the fittest manifest,” babble their luddite priests and waldenite landlords.

The Soiltwined induct one another through the _Living Clay of the Old Visions_, connecting with the Soil to absorb crushed memories of Long Ago roots and shoots, robots and ships, portals and voids from the dirt.

The Mothercity demands _increased organic taxes_, but the bioreactors, soilgivers, and rainmakers are failing. In the countryside, this is clearly unsustainable. In the great Portal City, the masses merely shrug.

♟ _Bense Defaces:_ half-barbarian, half-lord, all-peasant. Songs are sung of the great harvester. Rumor has it that this honorary golem will soon return.

♟ _Iamedos Atribut:_ awakened hauler autogolem. Ruthlessly ambitious, they want to secure a seat at the Rites for the autogolem unions. They'll strangle the city and break legs and minds to do it.

<a name="page_0211"></a>

**The Feralfolk, the Aperu**

Sentient almost-humans unrecognized by the authorities. Unregistered anthropobeasts dwelling outside the Dream, rats skulking among the cities, scavengers unseen by the Authority. Deniers of the Ministry's gentle ministrations.

The _Forest of Weights and Measures_ is the preserve of the **System Guardian** (L12, gray-flesh)—a perfect human banker-priest rewired into a biomachine. This walled garden sprawls between the remote inner domains of the Mothercity and the Permitted Areas of the Daughtercity. Here, the feralfolk are hung and dried, weighed and measured, formatted for their designated roles.

Yet fewer are harvested, and _more escape every year_. Why do the fecundic divisions of the Mothercity generate so many of these untagged human-analogues? How is one to interpret the Mother Machine's intent?

♟ _Acadaemon Moroü:_ free lord and activist academic, collecting willing shiprats and ferals for their humanification projects. There have been no failures—so they claim.

♟ _Tunca IV:_ high chief of the Second Skylight feral clan. Her false-soul scouts have told her there is a large, empty world beyond the Daughtercity. She plans to lead her feral confederation there.

♟ _Canta VVI:_ a songbird human who lived for years as an amuseant in the Evergarden. He fears the ferals don’t understand the weapons and industry possessed by the old humans of the Rites. Can he convince the ferals to abandon rebellion and escape through the Portal instead?

**The Mossdwellers**

“Suck air! Drink sun! Let mossfriend feed you. Leach nutrients from pipetree. Harvest joy from noötree,” warble the moss-skinned, leaf-bearded, elf-gone mossdwellers. They have drunk too deep of the verdigris mold juices and supped on too much airplankton.

The reviled mossdwellers use the grand phylakes to remain uncaught. They hunt humans instinctively, without malice or hate, taking their victims to the _Giving Crater_, high in the Shucked Hills, where they crack them open and give their cores to the **Angels from the Upper World** (L7, much-delighted). They fill the husks with verdigris mold, growing them into the **stuffed people** (L4, vegetable ogres) who roam those highlands.

Excitement sparkles in the air, passing through the chemical dance of the mossdwellers. They whisper that an **epitome** (L14, superior) is being born—a perfect mosshuman, a nature giant to help them carpet the world!

♟ _Elder Phernu:_ so long in the moss, their brain is green. Yet, a love still stirs for the red humans. Will they bring warning or infection?

♟ _Cass Descender:_ groombat specialist third grade. A servant nobody. Yet, their bats have warned them of the coming mosspocalypse.

Will no one listen? Can they find an ally, or must they take action alone?

<a name="page_0212"></a>

**COGFLOWER EXCHEQUER**

_"The great old baobab bank, the immense living machine tree, an island all its own! There the accountant monks keep the Hunger Away. There the fiscal inquisitors keep the Invisible Hand manicured and moisturized. There cash is made from crushed dreams and repurposed souls."_ —Island of Bank, Econotourist Guide Book (207YF)

Aspera's great living tree, the cogflower avatar, once reached to the Void. Then, cargo flowed from on high and beyond, and all had plenty and all was happy. But humans were an evil lot. Monkeys with the hearts of rats. They gnawed at this Root of prosperity, they offended the Chosen Lords, and the Economy punished them by truncating Aspera's tree, leaving them divided by class and wealth. This is their punishment for doubting the Garden Path. But, if they repent, if they sacrifice to the accountant monks often enough, if they whisper their secrets to the inquisition regularly enough, the thorns will be swept from their path and the money tree will reach to heaven once again!

Crowds of newmade humans throng the marshy base of the grand exchequer, supplicating for employment, for purpose, for assignment. All are given what they deserve, from holy corporate postings to sacred menial duties, from bodily recycling to soul milling. Yes, harsh—but fair! Thus is the stock of humanity refreshed and renewed! Praise the Mother Machine, the Maker's Giver, the bringer of multitudes into this wonderful world.

Visitors can also buy newmade humans for their estates.

**Garden Lord Aspera, also Green Aspera**

In the living stone, emerald is as the root stone, the eel as the way stone, the baobab as the sky tether.

"The great builder who nourishes the growing things. The giver of living stone and undying flesh. The maker of homes and hearths. But also, the wrathful one, the dictator of needs, the judge of right thought."

**Prayers to Green Aspera**

Once per session or so, to accept failure and creative destruction, to reconcile to the path:

"Rage is done, end is over. Dust! Stand! Grow anon!"

**Roll d20 + Strength - Thought**

| Result | Effect |
|:---|:---|
| 1 or less | Dust is dust. Failure compounds. Face doom again. |
| 2–19 | Hold the rolled number. Once, spend it for a sacrifice or to fuel a power. |
| 20 or more | Aspera gnaws in your flesh. The motivation burns within you. Release it to double a hero die roll. |

<a name="page_0213"></a>

**MINISTERIAL ESTATES**

_"Acceptance into ministry is the highest of honors, the perfect proof of high baseline functionality, the essence of merit, the ultimate of deserved leisure."_ —Servitors Handbook, Revised Rev. 3.5 Ed. (237WE)

The best were chosen by the ministry. The chosen are the best. The proof of aristocratic ministerium is a perfect circle. Thus, it is just that they have the ears of the Lords of the Dream Canopy.

And yet! Unjustly despised. Falsely worshiped.

The life of a minicrat is harsh and their humble gift estates bare compensation for their sufferings.

Also, may each serving minicrat earn €100 per week in convertible cards to properly maintain the dignity of their better status.

**Prodigies of Merit**

Thus Aspera and the Lords favor this place:

1 The sun shines green with growing force.
2 The weight of ground is less, each human is lighter.
3 All extremes of climate are moderated.
4 Sung trees and living stones sculpt themselves.
5 No eyes in the fast stars may see within.
6 The soil is alive with controlled generative fungi.
7 No daemon or unlicensed corpse may enter.
8 A house phylake hushes violent impulses.

**This Estate**

<a name="page_0214"></a>

**VERDANT PLACES**

_"We passed rich fields, crossed fine bridges, travelled through lovely dorps. Everywhere golems and falschers, living trees and singing birds. But people?"_ —Daly Setemani, A Barbarian in Eden (V/s/R-6, Sky Goat)

**Giver of Wisdom and Gifts**

_builder remnant, refuge guardian_

Humans become bound daemons. Long life in a body of posty-material synthetic stone. Awesome and pitiable; servants of distant, capricious Minds.

_**Without:**_ a humming altar. A significant sacrifice? The Giver may bestow (d6): (1) meaningless number string, (2) soothing platitude, (3) magical blessing, (4) healing meal, (5) radiant body scan, or (6) oldtech gift.

_**Within:**_ the meaningless string unlocks an in-dimensional refuge-village. A generously preserved time-vault of pods, survival gear, and treasures (d6):

1 Uncorrupted **dragon daemon** (L7, prescient). Gain a level if it possesses you.
2 Corrupted **dragon daemon** (L6, revolutionary). Gain strength and thought if it possesses you.
3 Pure-strain rendered human source-sludge!
4 Cache of oldtech weapons invisible to the phylakes.
5 Frozen timelost **access-prince/ss** (L3, daunting) who remembers the times before the Builders' left.
6 Bubble **travel orb sentience** (L4, pilot) embedded in a wired-shut clay pot. Why is it here?

**Gate of Green Waters**

_nutrient spigot, oldtech in-portal_

Some scholars imagine the Builders made the oceans by throwing down the icy stars. The spigot gates shew they siphoned the celestial waters more directly. This one still brings nutrient-rich fluids to invigorate the ancient fields.

_**Approach:**_ the lands grow richer, the soil spongier, the plants meatier, the colors more ornate. Plump fluid-birds cloud the skies, leaking nutrients when agitated.

_**These Waters:**_ they glow with a healthy virtue (d6):

1 Swim in the absinthe glow to heal a terrible injury. _Then:_ save or gain an unusual mutation.
2 Drink the prasine fluid to gain resistance to disease. _But:_ also bestows a pungent, medicinal odor.
3 Sprinkle the chrysoprase water on a golem. It now recharges in the sun. _But:_ its armor softens.
4 Paint the virescent foam on your skin. Now you grow green and mossy. _Then:_ save or become slower.
5 Ignite the feldgrau oils. See the air become opaque with air plankton. _But:_ hold your breath, toxic.
6 Touch the larimar scum on the waters and be thrilled. It whispers with sentiences. They offer to answer questions three. _After the third question:_ behold! The **cerulean gatekeeper** (L10, three-headed, three-minded) now comes! The connection: your questioning mind. Oh, bringer of the hydra!

<a name="page_0215"></a>

**Carbonivorous Dendripores**

_coalmaker tree-sponge colony forests_

An eerie forest-sized symbiote, somewhere between landcoral and coaltree, it harvests carbon from the air and converts it into a sooty mass. False historians suggest these symbiotes were designed to scrub the atmosphere and reduce the green-sun effect. The truth is clearly that these energy-rich deposits were created by the Builders to bless modern coalem-kind.

_**Rivers:**_ **union coalems** (L7, bristling) belch along, grinding the banks and raking the spoils. Their friendly transport is greatly appreciated by modern humanity.

_**Concrescence:**_ within the false forest harsh silence reigns, certainly helped by the **adamechs** (L4, soot golems). These refractory synthetics seek to become more organic than organic, converting themselves into post-machine biocreatures. They offer good prices for bodies, compounds, fluids and tissues.

**Oldgrowth Noötree Grove**

_ageless noösphere access forest_

Once, humans could swim free in the hollow comforts of the noösphere. Now it is a distant realm of fragmented gods and minor daemons. Yet, in this grove, the local noösphere still gives simple forecasts, synthetic tunes, and eternal hedonic treadmill experiences.

Some say this entire noëxperience is generated by a single ten-millennial meta-tree, the server organism **Pingu X** (L13, electrorgone generator).

_**Within:**_ **liars** (L1, grifting) and **parasites** (L2, soul-eating) prey on the unready, but the real threat are beyond the tree-plug: the Blue God's **malign babavores** (L5, succubi) jostle for your dreams and identities. Beware the antipsychic crumpets!

<a name="page_0216"></a>

**EMERALD CITY**

_"Mother City, Ten-Thousander Portal, Metropolis Temple One, City Proper, Living Wall, The Model City..."_ —The Name for City is Green, Adaü bene Aün (Soil Tulip III)

**Background**

The legendary Triple Skull cycle holds that the distorted space around the great green portal corresponds perfectly to the eight hundred thousand square miles of the legendary Human City One.

Perhaps the popular name "Emerald" comes from the way the old portal bends light. It casts a viridian pall over the great living bulk of the city. Perhaps it is due to the biomechanical forest cradling its visible districts. Perhaps the malachite faces of the All-Seeing City, the Mother of Humans, also play a part.

In any case, the Emerald City is the all-consuming motor of the Circle Sea economy and its Mother Machine is the giver of nations to maintain the human population.

_Cargo goes in, humans come out. A perfect circle._

**Districts**

_**Manor Islands and Buttress Boroughs.**_ Relaxed, lightly networked areas for the higher managerial castes of the Rites Banked, Corporate, and Ministerial.

_**Apartarbres (the Understoreys).**_ Lusciously surveilled livingstone and crawlingwood hives for the lowest ranks.

_**Evergarden.**_ Corporate, union, and scion headquarters. Public-civic facilities such as academic gladiatoria.

_**Emeraldcity (the Living Wall).**_ Life in the embrace of the perfect living city for good boys and girls who have pleased the Mother Machine (and her Interpreters).

_**Mothercity and Daughtercity.**_ ERROR. The zeno division of the portalspace is not complete. Citizens are not permitted outside of permitted areas. The domain of the Mother Machine is restricted to approved agents.

<a name="page_0217"></a>

**Ambient**

Sympathetically tethered **angel-moons** (L13, weathered) swim within the portalspace of the Mothercity, eating waste gasses, sprinkling pleasant waters, emitting sweet airs. Aerolithic **shepherd golems** (L4, pitied) herd flocks of engineered air plankton to cool, cloud, water, or heat the outportal districts.

| d6 | Day | Night | Understoreys | Portal |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|:---|
| 1–3 | bright and pleasant | cool and refreshing | green, viridian, mossy | chilly, windy, whistling |
| 4–5 | hot, humid, smelly | cold, clammy, rancid | spore-choked, dripping, clammy, crawling | whipping liquids, odd hues, perfumed |
| 6 | astringent, electric, ozone odor, flashing ghost lights | ammonia, char, glitter of see-beams, oldtime ghosts | burbling, swallowing, chewing, burping, glowing | thick, oversweet, rattling, heaving, psychic lights |

<a name="page_0218"></a>

**THE LEAVES OF FORMER TIMES**

_"Fragments of an older world tree reveal themselves in the thorns and pains of our modern times."_ —Against Aspiration, Anti-Ministerial Ananas (Green Marigold XX)

**Airmaker Bergs**

_mountain-void worm symbiote_

Lo, before the world was young, before the Long Long Ago, the Builders made the mountains and the valleys. This is probably true; or some magistral mountain-worms say so.

One such worm is the airmaker lusëpei' 7-Wandé (L16, lesser urge), who gives us the sweet, perfumed airs that make our lungs to sing and our golems to listen so well. It certainly has no ill-intent with its whisper of post-corporeal liberation, with the suggestion that the ultras of the Moon Mountains have humanity's best interests at heart.

♟ _Gongathor:_ a foul-mouthed barbarian of impressive stature and noble mien. They are clearly lying and only interested in personal power as they spread panic about the mountain-worm.

**Chantler Ceonobia**

_synthetic mantric monasteries_

In their wisdom, the Good Ones, who some falselings call Vile, built the wonderful self-fulfilling monasteries, fed by the flux and shifting of the void-worms. There, the ritual synthetics, our kind **chantlers** (L1, monkbots) repeat the technomagical mantras that placate the subterrene monsters who might undo our world and maintain humanity's User privileges under the Builders' guidance.

♟ _Erasthenes Pinchbutton:_ the ex-halfling hobnoble cog-lord of salts and vapors has come up with a profitable scheme to turn the chantlers into profit-maximizers.

♟ _Psalm 200rpm Maximus:_ the reincarnated liberation chantler has clearly been infected by the adamechs universal biotic heresies. Why else would it be planning to organize meat-tourist meditation retreat sessions at this ceonobium?

<a name="page_0219"></a>

**The Time Ponds of the Pseudologians**

_the bone vultures' water gardens_

A carnival of pale and crimson among the verdant sungwood and livingstone, the ponds epitomize the open culture of the Three Rites. Marvel at pseudologists preserved in the reflective waters, living out authentic routines in their Uz labyrinths, crystal libraries, or cosmic coffee houses. Each habitat resets at midnight, ensuring the heretics' contentment and the tourists' amusement.

_**Secret:**_ the caretakers are agents of the Invisible Hand, the false Poppy Vulture Era deity of possibility and plurality. Their goal: to reincarnate **Mohlack** (L13, oikotheote), bringer of delights and treasures.

♟ _Rocket Bull Semaphore_ (L5, ardent): the lead pseudologist of the Invisible Hand, seduced by the cancer of knowledge, convinced humanity can bear the power and desire of the Burning One.

☗ _New Soul Oven:_ this sacrificial furnace converts souls into divine flesh. The Invisible Hand is cultivating secret cultures in an accelerated time pond to produce souls for the oven.

**Post-Archaic Cerebrasarium**

_reactivated traditional re-existentialist sanatorium_

Long Ago not all humans were happy and some required mental recalibration to see the meaning and purpose in their service to the [redacted]. Fortunately, every modern citizen in the Green Land is happy; however recent regrettable events in the Blue Land have created a need for intensive human re-education and re-purposing.

The cerebrasarium uses crude but effective classical era medimagics to help patients become compliant, satisfied citizens, fond of freeform electro-stimulant music and not prone to existential despair, stress, or status anxiety.

Barbarian anti-scholars claim the facility is being used by some noble corpocrats to create a biologically subservient underclass incapable of comprehending their own lack of freedom.

♟ _Gliss Chervel_ (L6, radiating): lich-administrator of the cerebrasarium, brought out of cold storage to speed up the Blue Lander Rehappiness Project. Certainly not plotting to brain shave any local nobles.

♟ _Visitor Mary_ (L1, virtuous): true believer in civic virtue and corrected corporate patterns. Convinced faithful reason and not brain shaving should be used to convert the fallen to the Cogflower.

<a name="page_0220"></a>

**PORTALSPACE**

_"Dullway travel is completely safe. There are no recorded cases of catastrophic disassembly, bodily alteration, gross material mutation, or psychic decay. All reports to the contrary are illegal misinformation coded blue-blue."_ —Great Tablet of Travel, found during excavations of the third anomalous layer, Metropolis.

Each portal is a hard-coded passage between two locations. Portal temples serve as transit hubs.

Since the dawn of prehistory, dullway portals have fascinated humans. Folk memory holds that the Lords of the Dream Canopy, in their kindness, gave the portals to humanity, offering travel between approved locations of interest in the hylosphere. Feral outlanders believe portals are nothing more than primitive magic. Civilized people know they are just a fundamental cosmic structure. Heretical archaeologists claim they have found evidence that the portals are actually the work of early Proto-Gods or Builder subalterns named "Engineers".

The dullway protocol dismantles the traveler at the starting portal and reassembles them sometime later at the end portal. Depending on the information density of the portal, and the number of travelers, the journey can vary in duration. The busiest portals, for example between the Ministry and the Anti-War Dome, take mere hours and can handle up to a hundred travelers at a time. Smaller village portals linked to local polis temple hubs may take a month or two and only handle a single traveler at a time.

Urban legends say that when the great portal of Metropolis was open to the public, it could transport up to ten thousand travelers at a time. They would reach the mythical realm of Babylon Beach in mere minutes.

<a name="page_0221"></a>

**Portalspace Islands**

_"All portals are yellow coded. Good, salt-of-the-earth humans do not need portals. Emergency portal use requests are always granted before catastrophic loss of life occurs. No settlements have ever been lost due to delays in unlocking portal access because. Such ideas are slander and heresy."_ —Final Printout, Central Temple of Communications, buried city of Pompelmo.

In portal engineering, the _island_ refers to the distorted spacetime around the portal. Portals puncture through reality, from one cosmic to another. Thanks to the Luò-Iğne incantequations, this requires less energy than pre-cosmic scholars thought. However, the bigger the portal, the larger the distortion island. The portal’s engineer can choose to:

1 **Dilate Space.** A room with a portal is bigger on the inside than on the outside.
2 **Dilate Time.** Time flows faster near the portal.

After many experiments with journey-pigs, the grand punta Serim Anhalib figured out a crude equation for portal effects (capacity × 1/(time) = island diameter). Only a desperate incanter would fully trust Anhalib's equation.

**Example P-Islands**

| Portal | Capacity | Travel | Island R |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 Factory | 100 | minutes | 5 metric miles |
| 2 Town | 50 | hours | 250 meters |
| 3 Village | 10 | weeks | 1 meter |
| 4 Mansion | 1 | weeks | 5 centimeters |
| 5 Pig Test | 1 | hour | 5 meters |
| 6 SUPPRESSED | **[something]** (L10+1d6, demented horror) | 1d6 -2 to 36 hours | 1 to 200 meters |

| Notes | Details |
|:---|:---|
| 1 Factory | Extra space for facilities. Distortion delays shipping. Rail and cargo portals recommended. |
| 2 Town | Covers the central mall of most standard issue sanctuary towns. Comes with soothing drugfume dispensers. |
| 3 Village | Excellent for a governor-chief's discretionary getaway. Can be concealed in a wardrobe, safe, or privé. |
| 4 Mansion | Emergency escape solutions to fit in a puzzle box! Today, such portals are treasured heirlooms. |
| 5 Pig Test | The basis of Anharib's seminal experiments. The original is on display in the Mausoleum of the Pointer. |
| 6 SUPPRESSED | Warning. Do not open. It keeps [something] from returning. |

**Experiencing Portalspace**

From the perspective of a four-dimensional human, portalspace distorts light and sound. Large portals can completely block light and information from the outer world. Higherdimensional beings, such as Builders, may see and move through the distortion, like a stone skipping over water. Portalspace can also have other effects on baseline humans:

| d20+End Symptom | Effect |
|---:|:---|
| 1–2 Soul Leakage | Local color interferes with your aura, depleting it. [-1d4] |
| 3–4 Blanking | Local noösphere-personality mismatch. Memories are cut rather than copied. Who was Spot the Go-Hound anyway? |
| 5–6 Headaches | Take an aspirin. It'll be fine. Please use a handkerchief as a courtesy to others when your nose gushes blood. |
| 7–8 Nausea | Please use an antiemetic next time. [lose 1d4 meals] |
| 9–10 Existential Dread | Have you considered alcohol? [burden if sober] |
| 11–12 Mild Unease | Tamp down those useless emotions. [lose one for a day] |
| 13–14 Gastrointestinal | Gasses expand at different rates. [loud, lasts 1d4 hours] |
| 15–16 False Symptoms | Expecting the worst, you suffer the nocebo effect. |
| 17–18 Invigoration | There's a vim in the air. [+1d6 life] |
| 19–20 Euphoria | You feel amazing. On top of the world. [remove a burden] |
| 21+ Soul Skim | The gods siphon off a bit of your charisma and aura. You didn't need it anyway. [lose 1d3 of each, gain 1 HD] |

<a name="page_0222"></a>

[![Portal One map (page 222)](images/page_0222_portal_one_map.png)](images/hires/page_0222_portal_one_map.png)

**PORTAL ONE — MOTHERCITY**

_"Inside the city is another country."_ —Archives of Fallen Sentiment, Chronicler Gentle Seed (Stasis Dandelion XIII)

Past the aerolithic orbital burghs, wijks, and comptoirs of the Daughtercity, within the portal horizon of the Mothercity, space folds and curls like a fractal posteuclidean dream. This is the greatest of portal spaces, the greater part of the Green Land, the true garden country of zeno divisions and languid channel rivers.

**Portal One Travel**

| Travel | Notes | Price |
|:---|:---|---:|

<a name="page_0223"></a>

**Major Stations and Towns**

_**Abattoir Apartment V.**_ Everything has always happened. Feed the **meaters** (L1, translucent). So it goes.

_**Against Woe.**_ Shut until the **guiltless** (L3, cannibal not-zombies) fade away and disappear. Should be soon.

_**Anteportal Station.**_ Last town in this cosmos until the ten-thousander portal reopens. Have you considered submitting to the Ultimate Uplift? The **motherniks** (L3, not a cult) offer versions for all personality types.

_**Bravery and Worldliness.**_ Bypassed to allow the **orcans** (L2, war-test) to regress in murderous isolation.

_**Cold House.**_ Want to pass a few aeons? Store yourself here and let your money grow for you! T&C apply.

_**Door of Many Sides.**_ Plenty of residential space after the execution of the **Portalmaker** (L11, luminous). Safe-ish.

_**Final Eden.**_ This will be the last eden ever created. Daily tours available with the **Angle of Deaf** (L11, error).

_**Firetree.**_ Not confirmed. **Metagolem** (L17, query?).

_**Flowering Eyes.**_ The dire cherries have **eyes** (L2, biting).

_**Giver of Grooms.**_ Get your **groombat** (L0, helper) here!

Pet butler courses. No cats allowed.

_**Good Restrictor.**_ This **brainfac** (L11) removes bad abilities.

_**Greet the Worm.**_ Pay the Mother's wyrm-tax here. Always reasonable for the insights received. Do not talk to the Worm (L12, seventeen-folded).

_**Hospicoppice.**_ Replacement bodies, limbs, and implants grow on these trees. Funeral services free.

_**Impudent Grass.**_ The gall-grass **colony organism** (L7, unstuck in time) is not a threat. Please ignore it.

_**Integration Town.**_ Inculturation and learning center.

Re-education facilities available.

_**Lotus Hall.**_ Attain permanent inner peace for the low-price of half a soul and four years. IOUs accepted.

_**Humanity Station.**_ Processing hub for the Mother Machine's newmade humans (the mud-born). Also a monument to the majesty of the Builders' oldtech.

_**Lethe Town.**_ Memory enhancement center. Bad thoughts and ideas removed, personalities improved.

_**Maze of Humus.**_ Here the unworthy feed the worthy.

_**Mother's Mind.**_ Worship it when you see it.

_**Mrest.**_ Do not talk to **Mister East** (L10, electric divine).

_**Nomad Moderation Station.**_ Private property. No entry.

_**Port Deliverance.**_ Strip away false humanity, return to nature. Peel back the bark, reveal Aspera's red teeth. Indoctrination-ready **orimos** (L0, almost-folk) available.

_**Railfather.**_ This autofactory spits out the best rail golems in the world. Accepts payment in souls and minds.

_**Skywatcher Beach.**_ A popular resort. No zombies here.

_**Soul Fisher.**_ Feel ground down? The **Fisher** (L12, animated) brings forth fresh soulstuff from limbo's roar.

_**Sub Burrough.**_ A living town for living pod humans!

_**Unistadium.**_ Regrowing after the Soil Tulip incident.

<!-- Begin: Our_Golden_Age_10_Omega_Jubilee_224-254 -->

<a name="page_0224"></a>

**OMEGA JUBILEE**

**Synthetica**

We all live in a golden age.
Everyone tells us so.
This is the best of all possible worlds.
Everyone tells us so.

“I believe in overkill,” whispers the silver ship.

—Catechism of the New Eden Bunker Aspirational (Redacted Heresies)

<a name="page_0225"></a>

This final story section is about generating, inventing, and discovering the conflict between the two metafactions, the Ministry and the Nemesis, order and upheaval, survival and foray. It uses:

1. The **I.N.T.R.** — an interruption generator that throws up events in the background to slowly but surely toss the world off its axis.
2. The **Nexus Grid** — a diagram for the referee to fill out with factions and characters, and their relationships: public, secret, and false.
3. Competing **Narratives** — mutually contradictory explanations and predictions that generate conflict between factions and characters.

Three final narrative tracks, Jubilee, Palace, and Mother, form a final arc that can play out in the background of your adventures—or that could inspire a cycle of short trips and adventures the PCs could meddle with to tilt the future of their Circle Sea into an odd and unusual direction.

4. The black hole towards which sessions, and the story, swirl is the **Omega** [Jubilee], a feared, possibly prophesied, likely misunderstood event involving the Gods (or what they might be) and the End of All Things. It suggests possible end credit scenes for the end of a season of sessions, an interlude, or perhaps a new beginning.

**Confessions of Play**

“Reader. Reader, hark. Your ear. Here, you dropped it. Sorry. Reader, yes. Player of games? Referee of games? Master of games? Yes? I am the narrator. Yes, the most reliable of narrators. Everything I write here, all of it, everything is true and factual and reliable. I make no mistakes. I conceal nothing. I distort nothing. You see, my memory is perfect and factual, and every part of this Golden Age I present to you, this Golden Age of ours, I have it on the best and finest of authority. These lords of the future spoke to me, yea, through quantum whispers fed through the echoing vibration of my auditory ossicle. See, their voices proved to me that I am not mad, and so, since I am not mad, you can trust the words I convey to you of our Golden Age.”

The voice leapt and jumpt, manic 'pon its crackle-tape, quivering through the ages, saved and resaved, the Fool Prophet who, in full ignorance, described the Great Lie of the Ministry, the permastasis of the Stone Garden, where living humans, creatures of dream and hope and soul, are pruned and ossified and redacted into the clay that shields the dried machine hearts of the Unlords and the Lords, the Liars all, the Ghosts who stole the World, the Daemons in the Machine.

The old man-mind in the young fresh shell glared at Tomias with burning eyes, willing the little dog-loving reprobate to see, to see through the wall, to see the scurrying rats that guided his life, to see the dumb spirits, the idiot daemons, the soulless machines that had ground him so fine ...

"I don't get it. Is this ... some kind of old joyfeel vidy?"

**A Host for Your Ghost**

Here, puppet, dance, dance. Do you wonder, puppet, at the things you do? Feel a spirit pull your strings? A master beyond the veil? No, slumber good puppet.

Slumber and enjoy enjoy the gift of the Given World. The Green Lands where all things go, the Yellow Lands where beware, the Red Lands yet unready for the peace, and the Grey Lands without hue, forsaken by the Spectrum Canopy.

Thrill, puppet, in these dangers above all.

_Click_

The dream ended and the human’s eyes flicked open.

Another prophecy nightmare. It shook, then hugged itself. Its thin arms wrapped around its bony frame made it look like an exotic pupa surrounded by the layers of metamorphic machinery.

“01000111 01101111 01100100 00100000 01110111 01100001
01110011 00100000 01101110 01100101 01110110 01100101
01110010 00100000 01101111 01101110 00100000 01111001
01101111 01110101 01110010 00100000 01110011 01101001
01100100 01100101 00101110,” it beeped in a quavering voice.

The blue golem swung round on its slipforce field to face the human, “Hmm. Too deep. Reboot it and let’s try again. What class was this one anyway?”

The red golem rotated a secondary head and gave the skinny human a hard scan, “An eleven, I think.”

The blue golem nodded, “Ah, that explains it. Those have soft personalities.”

“Don’t be so essentialist,” clucked the red golem, while flickering a humor staccato of lights.

<a name="page_0226"></a>

**SCENE, SESSION, STORY**

_"We followed the Garden Path and here we started again, mannequins in a plastic desert!"_ —Antintern Sofanny Blintz, _Firing Squad Letters_

The adventure skeletons are past, the flesh that is the Circle of Lands is concluded, where should players and referee now turn? How to knit disparate sessions—trips, explorations, return, homes, investments—together into something resembling a story? How to stuff a weirdland of characters and concepts, places and problems, into a coherent roleplaying experience?

The setting is presented in an impressionist manner, with unreliable narrators, distorted facts, and blurry vistas that would flesh out your sketched-out sessions and scenes, creating a unique Golden Age of the Circle Sea at each table. This is a conscious task for the referee and a subconscious contribution of the players' imaginations.

How does a referee perform their task? They need not build a world entire, complete as clockwork, rather they provide the foundation and the building blocks with which the players' activities create a vivid world.

**Scene**

It all starts with the scene. A moment of meaning for the PCs and their players. It could be mere seconds or hours. Investigation, fight, conversation, or exploration. The referee presents challenges and dilemmas, adjudicates time and space, rounds and actions. When outcomes weigh uncertain, dice roll to give answers.

Scenes come in all shapes:

- rooms or regions of a timelocked vault,
- random encounters in a wilderness or wijk,
- trifling conversations on a train or by a campfire,
- visits to cajole bureaucrats or charm bandits,
- tearful farewells or jovial homecomings,
- a minute of quiet contemplation at the scenery.

Scenes can be strongly or weakly interactive for the PCs. In some, the referee may offer the PCs an opportunity for swashbuckling action and violence, in others the PCs may simply have a chance to talk over something memorable they see, in yet others it is a mood painting to fire their imaginations. Using scenes of high and low intensity, the referee conducts play, building tension, mounting challenges, offering release.

The crucial thing to remember is that scenes are never fully scripted by nature of the players' choices—even if the choice is only how their PC reacts emotionally to a moving advertividy they have not seen for years.

**Session**

The session unfolds from the moment the players sit at their table—real or metaphorical—to the moment they clean it of dice and dreams. In-character and out-of-character, they discover how the story unfolded for them through the scenes experienced during that session.

The referee organizes elements to fit the session:

- scenes prepared beforehand (see above),
- characters, events, encounters, obstacles, traps and other tools prepared for improvising scenes,
- notes, lore, items, places, and more sketched out to build links to other sessions and ideas.

Session timing and rhythm also play a role:

- pre-session messages recap previous sessions and events, while coloring expectations going forward,
- the opening of a session shifts from banter between players to play-as-characters, lighter scenes serve as a low-stakes re-entry into the game world, or the referee may opt for a more striking approach,
- the deep session moves the game forward, with players choosing between the referee's scenes,
- breaks during longer sessions benefit from framing with cliff-hangers or tense pauses,
- the session endgame usually calls for a high-impact scene: a crucial conflict, moment of high uncertainty, or resolving finalé. Getting the endgame right takes practice and skill: reading the table and clock, adjusting remaining scenes, dropping low-impact scenes or reducing low-stakes conflicts to a single roll, so that the players hunger for the next session or are satisfied at the conclusion of a story,
- finally, after-session notes reframe a session's events, bring together player drawings, notes, and ideas, and fuel future scenes and sessions.

At the end of a session the referee can ask the players for feedback: what didn't work, what stuck in their memory, what was particularly boring, what was annoying or fiddly. Especially asking questions about what went wrong is a fast way to figure out the pain point and adapt one's style of refereeing to the table at hand.

<a name="page_0227"></a>

**Story**

As several sessions string together they reveal a story. The story is not some pre-imagined thing, rather it is emergent from the players' action and reaction upon the scenes built by the referee and played out at the table. No one person can know how play will unfold, whether the PCs will snatch defeat from the jaws of victory or not. This shared exploration of the unknown, collaborative writing of the sessions' story, is the wonder of roleplay.

The scenes and sessions built out of this book's first adventure skeleton begin, as in many traditional tales, with the PCs at home. There they receive a call to adventure. They examine the call, gather their resources, and leave to face it. Along the way, they face challenges and dilemmas, finally they succeed in their quest or fail, having learned and grown—or not.

The second skeleton begins with a journey, a discovery of a new place, and the (re)claiming of a new home. The two form a diptych, one a journey outwards into the strange, the other a returning or making a home. The referee could, quite easily, link the two skeletons into a circle, with the town and inherited home expanding the sketched out setting of the first session.

But that's just two arcs, two possibilities. How to weave more sessions together, leaning towards a comprehensible overarching story (or campaign, if you will) without actively building rails on which the players and their PCs must skate?

The referee plays two roles, or solo games, between sessions, that of creator and editor.

The **referee as editor** watches the players' actions, listens to their talk, and asks questions about their PCs goals, fears, desires, hates, burdens, families, mistakes, friends, follies, and skills. The referee doesn't grill the player, like in an interview, rather they may ask them:

- how their PC feels at a betrayal, after a narrow defeat or a bittersweet victory,
- what their PC thinks about a place, faction, or event,
- who their PC visits or spends downtime with,
- what tales and worries their PC shares in the wee hours of the night as they party waits for the automechanic to repair their lobogolem,
- why their PC stands firm or flees,
- when will their PC feel like they have succeeded if they stand morosely at a celebration.

The referee notes down answers and ideas that pique their interest. Some players will be more forthright, suggesting clear goals and motivations—even there, the referee should use their judgement to get discreetly behind the surface level. The referee doesn't simply give the player what they say they want for their character, rather they edit their notes, picking building blocks that the _referee_ also finds interesting and fun to build with.

The **referee as creator** plays the solo game of sketching out scenes and elements for future sessions:

- NPCs and factions that pique their interest based on what they have gleaned from the PCs' activities, the setting content in this book, and any other source that seems interesting that day,
- places—dungeons, vaults, facilities, towns, trains, ships, tombs, plantations, factories, forests, mountains, beaches, glades, géants and more—that they feel could be enjoyable, some of which connect to the PCs, others that don't,
- published modules that could be slotted in as written, or adapted to match the goals of the PCs and major recurring NPCs or factions,
- photos, paintings, drawings, and other art that could serve as interesting scenes or mood backgrounds for future sessions,
- problems, challenges, dilemmas, and conflicts that appear, mount, or resolve from session to session,

Crucially, the referee as creator does not make a finished work of art, rather it is something like a rough bricolage, a collage or assemblage of elements they will (or will not!) use in future sessions. It may all arc towards some greater resolution—for example, the Omega Jubilee detailed later—but this arc is beyond the scope of the PCs' own adventures for now and can remain entirely outside the scope of the PCs' adventures, unfolding and resolving as some great background to their human-scale adventures in the foreground. The PCs do not have to be the little quarterlings taking the nuclear finger of the Machine Beast into the maw of the Vulkana's great maw; they might remain simple mercenaries of the Bled Army, marching from the south to storm the battlements of the Mother City or die trying.

The referee sketches a map of ideas and concepts in pencil, eraser at the ready to adapt it session by session as the players and their PCs wreak their havoc upon the world, tilting at the windmills of a disquieted world.

Over the next few pages the Meta-Factions framework, the I.N.T.R. Generator, and the Nexus Grid provide three tools the referee can use to structure their scenes and sessions and, just possibly, bend gameplay towards a connected story over several sessions.

<a name="page_0228"></a>

**I.N.T.R. GENERATOR**

When exploring a location, PCs can count on regular encounters sapping their resources. When traveling, regular events break up their voyages. Between sessions and when chilling at home, **interruptions** demand the attention and time PCs are trying to devote to private pursuits, whether those are rest, recreation, or reanimation. These interruptions follow the standardized severi-frequent scale of player impedimentation: **I.N.T.R.**

1. **Incident** (common): routine annoyance, petty dispute, vermin infestation, suspicious letter.
2. **Nuisance** (uncommon): big upset in Little Golem Empire district, tax trouble, guild feud.
3. **Trouble** (rare): serious disruption, political assassination, trade embargo.
4. **Rupture** (legendary): eschatonic jubilee, regional war, angelic retribution, corruptech awakening.

**Roll on the incident table once per week (or so)** of game time for the whole party (or household). The I.N.T.R. tables are linked, allowing for occasions of "when it rains, it pours hellfire from the sundered sky-vault."

**Incident**

The trivial but time-consuming vexation occurs at (d6): (1) the least convenient time, (2) the beginning of the week, (3–4) the middle, (5) the end, (6) the best time.

**d00 — A Trifling Bother, Really**

| d00 | Result |
|---:|:---|
| 01 | Groundhog Reality Error. A week is lost to (d6): (1) petrification, awaken stiff and lose 1 agi, (2) stasis, awaken starving, (3) noöspheric transfer, awaken with missing memories and 0 tho, (4) divine inspection, awaken with one affliction removed and a random mutation added, (5) zero-point gate formation, awaken to a new slow portal next to your estate and a terrible headache, (6) backup transcription, awaken with a jewel copy of your current state of mind and spirit (free body not provided) and lose 2 str and end. Since it's the next week, _immediately_ roll 1d80+10 for **another incident**. |

They tell you tales and drink your wine. Over a long night you lose 1d6 x level life and gain level x d100 xp and 1 step towards learning or improving a trait. |

The referee may swap out incidents, or escalate them further, to avoid things getting boring.

<a name="page_0229"></a>

**Nuisance**

The frustration coincides with (d6): (1) an unlucky day, (2) a market day, (3) a sacred message day, (4) a cultural reeducation day, (5) a full moon, (6) a celestially bothersome alignment.

**d00 — Just a Socioeconomic Flesh Wound**

| d00 | Result |
|---:|:---|
| 1–3 | A quiet week. Everybody is talking about the (d6): (1) nutball finals upset, (2) disappointing parasocial letdown of the new vidy season, (3) unseasonable warmth, (4) new improved chocaine rations, (5) upgraded anti-bedbug deodorants, (6) latest barbarian game-war. However, holy fools and other odd ducks were already noticing the omens of the coming rupture. Roll _immediately_ for a **trouble**. |
| 4–8 | Daemonic infestation manifests as (d6): (1) psychic possession of elites, (2) mass psycho-somatic disturbance, (3) local machine rebellion, (4) aggressive animal or plant mutation, (5) community-wide lassitude, (6) a waking sleep as the daemons use spare mental energies for their own odd ends. |
| 9–12 | Paladins of the (d6): (1) Ministry, (2) Butcher Bank, (3) Local Postorganic Corporation, (4) Board of Ancestors, (5) Vampire Cooperative, (6) Cat House come through, reading hands, detecting the Lie, and upsetting the Apple Cart of Progress. They say they are stalking an error dragon (L15, post-imperial). |
| 13 | It's quiet. Too quiet. Business is down. The birds are silent. Next week _also_ roll a **trouble** and a **rupture**. |
| 14–15 | Erratic disgarden phylakes on an angelic mission to enforce legal compliance with outdated diktats on (d6): (1) human facial hair, (2) accented lilting speech, (3) empirical observations, (4) capital accumulation, (5) physical fitness, (6) building dress codes. |
| 16–20 | There is an ominous (d6): (1) ash storm, (2) rain of hail, (3) sky fire, (4) land tremors, (5) water re-coloration, (6) monochromatic field error. Panic claws at your throat like a dying cat. Lose 1d4 aura. Next week _also_ roll a **nuisance** and a **trouble**. |
| 21–25 | Permanent revolutionary agitators incite (d6): (1) student agents, (2) barbarians, (3) dogheads, (4) second-tier residents, (5) orimonates, (6) tenants. |

| 31–40 | Tension coils like oil snakes, fights break out between (d6): (1) foreign infiltrators, (2) sleeper agents, (3) illegal students, (4) local iron humans, (5) timelost liches, (6) freshly delivered orimonates and another group (roll 1d10+20). Lose 1d20 life. Next week _also_ roll d20 for a **nuisance**. |

| 00 | The arrival of a (d6): (1) cosmic stork, (2) deathbat flock, (3) vome swarm, (4) luminous faerie storm, (5) undine upsurge, (6) ERR0R incursion devastates 1d8 x 10% of the town ... but not your estate, which rises in value due to the scarcity! Lucky you! Next week _also_ roll 2d20 for a **nuisance**. |

<a name="page_0230"></a>

**Trouble**

This temporary setback in the inevitable and perfect arc of humanity's divine history takes place (d6): (1) on a profane day, (2) on a day of remembrance, (3) during a festival, (4) between two bouts of electoral combat, (5) on an ill-starred night, (6) one quiet morning. Once a trouble starts (the keg column), it evolves under its internal logic unless stopped or redirected. Each week after it starts roll d6: (1) it erupts, (2–3) it moves right one column, (4–5) it simmers, (6) it moves left one column. Trouble doesn't die down unless a major faction benefits from successfully stamping it out. The PCs could be(come) such a faction.

**d00 — Keg → Spark → Eruption**

| d00 | Keg | Spark | Eruption |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 01 | Knowledge corruption. Ink crawls out of books, memory crystals crumble into toxic dust. Intellectuals panic. | Ritual failure. Nobody knows how to activate the Temple of Humanity. Some citizens start to devolve. | Feralized citizens, regressing to beast or even mossfolk, start consuming the town like a voracious ecosphere. |
| 02–03 | Portal collapse. Static crawls out of screens. Ministry visitations are cut. Silence on the ether waves. | Group of tourists arrives through the collapsed portal. Dismembered. Uplifted groups try to flee on foot. | Skies close over the town. A bubble portal is eating it from without. Fossils and body parts rain from on high. |

The thief's angry guild-clan sets fire to the Agency of Stable Peace. | Gangs rush to seize strongpoints. The abandoned nether cellars of the angel begin to vomit forth hostile errors. |
| 07–10 | Rattling cough proliferates. The grand ospedal runs out of medication. The autodoctor starts reciting poetry. | Scarlet flux. Cough morphs, melting many patients. Recriminations! | Cyan sporelings hatch from dead buildings and citizens. Chemical warrior suits recommended. |

Vidys degenerate into slop. | Failed attempt to fix the vidy generator infects golems with a strange disease—the tower protocols. | Golems and machines begin dismantling the settlement and its citizens to build a tower to heaven. |
| 95–97 | Memetic addiction loop. An error in the vidy programming ensnares citizens in catatonic soap-slumber. | The captured dance like dream zombies of the night, their choreography attracting a strange star. | A black obelisk lands. Objects begin to whisper, dreams to compel. The ensnared prepare to depart. |
| 98–99 | Mirrors go blank. All reflections in town cease. Outraged guild of beauticians organizes a general strike. | Academic detects movement behind the mirrors. Accused of causing the blankout, they are scapegoated. | Mirror clones of the citizens emerge from the mirror portals to replace them and reset the town. |
| 00 | Signal from the void floods all the channels. Bees sing in terminal flight. Fires whisper in the night. | Daemons wiped. Babel amulets fail. Languages are confused. Doors go silent. House minds die. | The dragon assembles from wiped machines and begins collecting volunteers against the Mother Machine. |

<a name="page_0231"></a>

**Rupture [of the Era]**

[ERROR] Horizon eventuation during (d6): (1) the next solar eclipse, (2) the death of a hereditary president, (3) the birth of a star child, (4) the next economic crash, (5) the next technomagical involution, (6) the celebrations of a new and glorious beginning. Warning. Border failure. Please return to your sarcoph... sarcopod, bones will be clothed, flesh will walk again, have no fear. Fear. Fear.

Once a rupture omen appears, the anguish follows in 2d6 weeks. The true rupture occurs 1d30 weeks after that. With the help of a powerful faction the PCs can ameliorate or direct the rupture, but a permanent change is inevitable.

**d00 — Omen → Anguish → Rupture**

| d00 | Omen | Anguish | Rupture |
|---:|:---|:---|:---|
| 1 | The sun rises white. No colors appear. Everything is monochrome. Electric phantoms frolic in the shade. | Inky other-selves emerge from many creatures' shadows. They gather and build a diaphanous altar of equations. | The dead sun, the orb nocturne, hatches and a larval MKR emerges to help eat your way into a new cosmos. |
| 2–3 | Rainbows fall from the sky, tendrils of light climb to the clouds, lighting anchors the Altar Stars to the Soil. | The sky winches closer to the soil day by day. Mountains then hills begin to gasp and suffocate, bereft of air. | The Ladder of Heaven is chopped down by the Ill Nano and three lines of destruction fall across the world. |

| 76–85 | The air plankton changes, thickens, clogs vents, and gathers in great clump-clouds that block the light. | Many phylakes abandon the human settlements and ascend to hover in the middle airs, far above the soils. | The mountains rise into the sky to announce the age of the sky whales. Waters and fires flood the gaps. |
