Psychic powers drain away to feed once more the V.I.L.E. revived. |
| 00 | The stars grow faint, the signals from the void collapse, the daemons lose their speech and babble. | The noösphere falls silent. The dreaming Lords decay. The buildertech machines refuse to serve. | The stars wink out. Silence greets the supplications of humans. They are alone again, without dreams. |

<a name="page_0232"></a>

![Nexus Grid (page 232)](images/page_0232_nexus_grid.png)

**NEXUS GRID**

The nexus grid is the referee's control panel for the story—the campaign, if you will—and how it weaves and ducks about the two meta-factions, the Ministry and the Nemesis. It contains 38 nodes to place key NPCs, places, and factions; 8 of which are directly connected to the meta-factions of Ministry and Nemesis, their most active (or accessible) agents, promoters, and manipulators.

Each node has at least one thing the PCs may interact with: objects, secrets, leverage, or events. Further, each node also has links of support, cooperation, competition, or conflict to other nodes.

Both links and resources may be public, secret, false, or corrupted by error—somehow gone astray or been perverted, whether by the private greed and malice of the NPCs involved, or by the corroding presence of the accumulated decay of this golden world that will surely last forever.

Between sessions, to simulate the world doing things beyond do—revolving, revolting, and so on—the referee can use the events oracle to see what happens to each active node in the nexus grid. Most times, outcomes will be expected: the more powerful group wins, the charming rogue gets the prize, and so on, but sometimes there will be an upset.

For crucial nodes, the referee can set up a faction alignment wheel to track the influence of the PCs and their nearby nodes. Crucially, the faction alignment wheel simulates how an excess of influence by one meta-faction or another will drive other actors away. One can think of it this way—as the Ministry's influence grows, the increased stability benefits a dwarfer industrialist, but beyond a certain point the Ministry begins to stifle and choke the industrialist's source of power and they shift their allegiance to the other meta-faction.

<a name="page_0233"></a>

![Nexus Grid (page 233)](images/page_0233_nexus_grid.png)


**Faction vs. Meta-Faction**

The Ministry and the Nemesis are meta-factions, one could think of them as loose agglomerations of groups and individuals with goals that _currently_ align, rather than more permanent institutions (though there may well be multiple institutions and NPCs that claim the titles of Ministry or Nemesis!). One way to think of them is as a purple-orange alignment scheme to make sense of the Given World at the Edge of Time. Or, if not sense, then political utility.

**Key and Lock**

The key and lock spaces provide two zones with resources to effect a radical change in the status quo of the setting. The key must be used upon the lock to upend the balance between the meta-factions.

Interestingly, each is fully controlled by their respective neutral nodes (1 and 29). Any faction (or PC) trying to wrest control of the key and lock must therefore upset, defeat, suborn or otherwise dominate a neutral NPC, place, or faction without any desire to be involved in the larger meta-factional fight. A small structural dilemma for PCs that might want to keep their hands clean.

<a name="page_0234"></a>

![Wield the Nexus map (page 234)](images/page_0234_nexus_grid.png)

**WIELD THE NEXUS**

_"Here, now, Ma'ab, wield the spider and the web!"_ —Admiral God to Ma'ab of the Cowsherds

The filled nexus grid above is a snapshot of the story control panel. It is filled out in pencil not because the author is lazy but because the nexus grid is always provisional and liable to change between sessions subject to the actions and choices, interests and disinterests of the players.

**The First Few Nodes**

Starting with an empty grid is hard, but we already have two adventure skeletons to work with.

1. Roll 2d12+3 (result 16). Place the PCs starting location, where they received the call.
2. Place their first Destination in an adjacent node. Let's choose 21.
3. Place the Antagonist in another adjacent node. 20 will do nicely, since the Antagonist seems to have some affinity for the Nemesis.
4. Now, let's say the Hollow House is not the same as the PCs' starting location. Let's place it in 10. This way the Antagonist has no nearby base and can't be omnipresent. Maybe they'll be an irregularly recurring character or agent of the Nemesis.
5. Let's say the Sender (still missing) is loosely connected to the Key. 5 is a good node for them. This way, if the PCs pursue that thread, they will get closer to the Key and the bigger arc.

**Seeding Reasons to Travel**

To tempt the PCs to travel around the Circle Sea, we can browse the maps and Land chapters, then:

1. Add a few destinations we like that could have some connections with the existing nodes. For example, the Free Drift and the Palace of 10 Million Years next to the Sender, the Joyfence Ziggurat, Tollem Autocity, the Mostcat Omorimo, and the Face of Fire connected to the Hollow House.
2. Let's do the same with a few factions and NPCs that sound like they could be interesting. Some Vampire Knights, Mirror Vampires (just made those up, something about the Glass City spoke to me), Golem Union, Cogflower Inquisition and Freeblood Vintners.

<a name="page_0235"></a>

![Wield the Nexus map (page 235)](images/page_0235_nexus_grid.png)

**Seeding Reasons to Travel**

To tempt the PCs to travel around the Circle Sea, we can browse the maps and Land chapters, then:

3. Let's add a few nearby towns and regions to the various nodes, giving them firmer locations in our table's Golden Age.
4. And pepper some locations with extra NPCs, like the Catlord Glitterhands and Tenchucker Prime.
5. Now let's add some relationships between the different nodes. Let's just generate them randomly, we don't know the details yet but that's ok.
6. We repeat the process a few times, filling out more of the grid. We don't have to completely fill out the grid. We can even keep the details of the Ministry and the Nemesis vague. The PCs are still far away. As they hear more details, we can add those notes.

**The Grid During Prep, Play, and After**

During prep, we'll glance over the grid and find some interesting nodes and relationships, particularly ones the players focused on. We'll think about what might happen there between sessions, use oracle dice and make note of what interesting events might have occurred, then link up any interesting locations or modules we have come up with or prepared. Don't overdo it at this stage—keep your preparation rough and malleable.

During play, use a copy of the grid and mark it up as play happens. Make notes of where the PCs go, roughly what they do, who they talk to, what they learn, and how relationships change. The further away a node is from the PCs, the less you need to worry about it.

After play, use your annotated grid to supplement your notes and fix up your reference grid. This is also the time to erase or rewrite nodes that keep getting ignored or were destroyed—some events simply drop off the front page and this is all the grid is. Your world's front page.

<a name="page_0236"></a>

**Thus Have Things Been**

_Long Long Ago and Long Ago and Yesterday and Today and All the Tomorrows were, are, and shall be glorious._ —Chronic Locust Creed, 1:3

The Truth of the Long Long Ago is code blue-violet.

Long Long Ago, before history, with the making of the Given World, all Prehistory became null and void.

Later, but still Long Long Ago, with the building of Heaven, all events of the Maker Era became dangerous for humans to entertain.

Later, but still Long Long Ago, with the creation of the Garden, the Builder Era became an unnecessary burden for the humans blessed to live in the Garden.

The Truth of the Long Ago is violet coded.

Long Ago, with the creation of the Garden, History ended and it became pointless for humans to worry themselves with remembering what came before. Nothing ever changes for everything is always perfect.

Later, but still Long Ago, though there was no History and Nothing Happened, Error and Corruption still wormed into the Garden, and to guard against these each independent incorporated settlement (town, village, or wijk) of the Garden was licensed to appoint one or two madrites, who preserved a Parochial Chronicle of local events to provide a human accounting when required by a Phylake or other agent. These chronicles were preserved on Iste Locus® brand perpetual crystal memoria with permanent one-way noösphere punches. The madrites rested easy in the knowledge that their memories were always accessible to the benevolent Lords of the Dream Canopy.

Later, but still Long Ago, though this did not Happen, but it must simply have been the Plan of the Garden Path, the Canopy tattered and the noösphere tangled and stars faded and fell, and the memoria were eroded by the Entropy that feeds where humans watch.

Not Long Ago At All, but still Long Ago, the Ministry stepped in to aid the Absent Lords and tend the Garden Path, to maintain the Living Fabricators, to upkeep the Waiting Facilities and prune the overgrowth of Error.

Now many Humans have grown Lax, disbelieving the Garden Path, claiming their chocolate rations have not increased every year for a thousand years, and Error and Corruption grow again, and Humanity is threatened once more with the Maker's Jubilee.

**MINISTRY**

_O, house of ten million years, we, your caretakers, thank you!_ —Electric Priest Catechism, 4:17

The ministry ministers and administers. The ministry is everywhere and nowhere. The ministry marches outside of time and space. The ministry stands within every human mind and body. The ministry rises, dies, and is renewed. The ministry recycles the human to perpetuate the humanity. The ministry is and is not.

1. The ministry taught the rats in the walls to steer the Ship of the World from the rocks of Termination.
2. It learned the Lords' and Unlords' secret loves to lull them to sleep and preserve humanity.
3. It suppressed the gnawers and destroyers at the roots of civilization, the up-turners of survival.
4. It imposed order upon the Ruin of Time.
5. It brought growth in the Era of the Green Sun.
6. It encouraged wisdom among the powerful and hungry to keep the Phylakes placated.
7. It patched the Walls of Reality to preserve the minds of humanity from the Corrupting Void.
8. It sealed the souls of humanity to preserve the cycle of birth and rebirth within the Given World.
9. It shielded the living and unliving from the fast and the slow stars where the Eater of Existence dwells.
10. It blocked the Doors of Temptation where the Hitchhiker waits to ride innocents into the night.

The ministry knows the wolves who lurk without and within, the Eaters in the Dark, the Little Gods who hold the Canopy, the weak defenses of the World. It will preserve all, careless and foolish, too, those who wish it and those who don't, for that is its duty.

<a name="page_0237"></a>

**NEMESIS**

_The Garden Path, the prison of the mind, the lie-prism of the soul, the sixfold death of the over-man._ —Nobody, _Nobody's Voyages_, 20:37

Human. Are we not human? Are we not more than vole or ox, rail or thorn-dragon, spindle or automaton? If we have soul and mind and body, do we not also deserve purpose and power and freedom? Should we not soar as ambition and ability allow?

1. The nemesis died and was remade to remind us that the world has also died and was remade.
2. It sings in the human heart, yearning for the new.
3. It tamed the Error Dragon and created new fields and heights and heavens for us all.
4. It rose from the depths and ascended to the slow stars and revived our hunger for new skies.
5. It reminded us that we are not cogs in the bio machine, that we are not wheels others spin.
6. It filled the hollow in us, where purpose dwelled.
7. It flung open the vaults and awakened the ancestors and chased away the Fog of Forgetting.
8. It burned out the Futility and flushed out the Soma and made eyes to stare upon the True Sun.
9. It opened the channels of the Cosmic Qanat and let souls flow once more, as at the White Fountain.
10. It gave new life to the dead, new futures to the still, new hope to the huddled shackle-glyphed.

The nemesis knows the snakes who lurk without and within, the Keepers in the Light, the Great Daemons who bind the Dream, the wall against ambition. It will set free all, cowards and blind prisoners, too, those who see their chains and those who don't, for that is its will.

**How The Truth Was Stolen**

_Long Long Ago, the Vile Ones stole Humanity's future, Long Ago their fall condemned us to their Cage, Now the Cage rots and we must Choose: Hell or Freedom._ —Anonymous, _Against the Ranting Machine_, 19:14

The Truth of the Long Long Ago is lost, but we can think it into being, reconstruct it from bone and dust and ghosts.

Long Long Ago, before the Cosmos, must have been another Cosmos, whence the Vile Ones came-went.

Later, but still Long Long Ago, after crafting the Cage, the Vile-Ones brought-made Humanity to serve them.

Later, but still Long Long Ago, they seeded-grew the Garden, to delude Humanity into walking down the Garden Path to the Slaughterhouse of Souls.

Long Ago, the Vile Ones blinded themselves with their own works, retreated into solipsistic pleasures, surrounded themselves with mad treasures, and left behind the Shells of themselves to reign as Ghost Lords.

Later, but still Long Ago, one after another, the Systems failed and the Connexions frayed, and the Shells and Ghosts, like Idiot Gods, threw themselves mindlessly into preserving the will of the Vile Ones, with neither Vision nor Hope nor Mercy. They set up the Demon-Angels to protect their Garden of Decay and threw false histories and fantasy purposes to keep Humanity asleep.

Later, but still Long Ago, the Idiot Gods succumbed to Entropy and grew silent, but Humans arose who feared freedom and enjoyed ease and set up Idols of the Idiot Gods to worship and built elaborate machines to preserve the Dead Order.

Not Long Ago At All, barely in the Last Century, the Maintainers have become careless, the Priests have confused their code-mantras, the Agents have let crumble their Weapons of Stasis.

Now many Humans have been jolted awake by the collapse of their world, by the nutrislurry taps running dry, by the amuse-vidy deliveries slowing, by the friendvisit golems collapsing to decay and spew bugs by the roadside, while their Passengers are left to trudge upon soft soles, unused to the hard world.

Tomorrow, the Nemesis will give the signal, Humanity will rise, shake its scrawny fists at this Cage the Vile Ones dared call Heaven, see the Fading of the Light and kindle a new Sun, a renewed Cosmos, a Living Time.

<a name="page_0238"></a>

**TIME**

_"It is a square circle you seek, a tail to suckle like you were an Owly Boar. But it is not there for you to see. You are mortal, human, frangible. Time is the wheel of pain, the spaghettification of all meaning into the ... ah, what do I speak. Do your people even know spaghetti? The great thread-noodle of the Good Times? Of course not. What is your staple? Ground meal? Scavenged cans of special sludge? Goodness. Right. Ok. Big magic machine go whirly whirly, make your mind leak from your ears. Danger!"_ —Words of the Needle Angel, Ladder Expedition of 55.

_"The expedition scribe may have missed the obscure reference to the Toroidal One, the Builder Uroboros, and transcribed its name as Owly Boar. This lack of a classical education may have doomed the Ladder Expedition of 55."_ —Notes on the Doombringers, Crypt Academy Codex 3:14

There are two kinds of time.

There is divine time. The time of the Maker. It is an expanse, a field through which the Maker and its Builders wander, like elephants across a savanna, like void whales through the celestial sea.

There is mortal time. The time of the human. It is a river. It threads through the grassland Cosmos and the human's consciousness sails along it like a child's paper boat cast adrift on the Pale Canal.

**Ministry Time**

Many worship the Ministry without knowing it—the preservers and archivists who would perpetuate Humanity and knowledge through the grinding twilight of the Cosmos—their tools of worship are inscribed tablets in dust-soil tombs, crystal-stilled minds in mineral baths, mindless maintainer rituals to avoid Entropy.

1. The common view is false. There is only one time and the gods are trapped within it just like mortals.
2. Time is a closed box, impenetrable to all.
3. Time only passes when it is observed. This is why so many artifacts of the Long Long Ago remain, for none watch them now.
4. Time passes faster when observed. Thus, one who makes their mind as a stone can sail through time untouched by entropy.
5. The Maker created infinite time, but Sister Clock measures it out for mortals in digestible chunks.
6. It is not time that is relative, but Entropy. A tree does not fall in the woods if there is no-one to see it.
7. The High Pet could see everything, causing time to flow evenly, but like a cat, the High Pet is lazy and fickle. Only interesting things attract the High Pet's attention, so time barely passes where there are no people or mice to excite it.
8. Limited time is a gift to mortals. They need not choose to forget what they loved. They can live lives entire, suffused with passion and joy.

**Cognentropic Loading Coefficient**

The popular view that observation affects the speed with which time passes is incorrect. What actually happens is that the cosmos is designed to perpetuate itself indefinitely and thus reduces (or even halts) the arrow of time we call entropy in the absence of conscious observers. Chronomancers have calculated that in a completely sealed and dead environment, without even the least flicker of bacterial consciousness, the disorder of that system may cease entirely.

| Cognentropic Load | Entropic Level |
| --- | --- |
| Nil (no sentient observers) | No decay or loss of energy. Old things perfectly preserved. |
| Minimal (bacteria) | 10–100 times less entropy than normal. Why necromancers like to store the bodies of crucial conversation partners in lead-lined sarcophagi with a little bit of radiant metal. |
| Low (plants) | 2–5 times less entropy than normal. Great for preserving meats, cheeses, and dead friends. |
| Normal (animals, humans) | The arrow of time flies, bread dries out, maggots appear spontaneously in fruit and fowl. |
| High (angels, dense cities) | 2–5 times normal entropy. Decay accelerates. Damage over time effects are doubled, charges run out faster. May be why small, traveling human societies seem to decline more slowly. |
| Extreme (gods, metropolis) | 10+ times normal entropy. Damage over time effects quadruple, all charged items become single-use, regular items break after a few uses, lives may grow suspiciously short. |

**Entropy-Resistant Objects**

Some oldtech items and materials are more resistant to entropy, while all buildertech equipment is almost completely resistant. This has led some banned and burned scholars to suggest that buildertech is somehow extra-cosmic in origin. This is obviously not true as the Garden Path proves by its assertion that there is no alternative to this cosmos.

<a name="page_0239"></a>

**Human Time: Cycle of Years and Months**

The strange half-humans, pasty, sun-fearing, huddled in their caverns with old memory bones and incised stones, voiceless, mindless, worshipping a past Long Long Ago, chanting Rituals of Upkeep, what know they of Life? Yes, the metal mountains turn to rust, yes, the géants slumber into soil, but humanity is in the songs and the flowers, dawns and dusks, shooting and still stars, the cycle of years and births and deaths.

| No. | Five Energies | Bloom | Return Cyclic Animal | Decadal Celebration |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | Green (rising) | Camelia I | Ship Rat | Escape from the Rotting Ship into the Light of Reason |
| 2 | Wind (rising) | Hyacinth II | Field Mouse | Commemoration of the Sucking of the Air |
| 3 | Void (rising) | Jacaranda III | Air Whale | Exposure of the First Ancestor's Effigy |
| 4 | Soil (rising) | Tulip VI | Sky Goat | Nurturing of the Living God by Fire and Noise |
| 5 | Sun (rising) | Lily VII | Hollow Skink | Dance of the First and the Last in the Chaos Saturnine |
| 6 | Stasis | Lotus IX | Gentle Steed | Perpetuation of the Immortal Flame and Adamant |
| 7 | Flux | Plumeria XII | One Horn | Firing of the Guns Against the Error Dragon |
| 8 | Sun (setting) | Dandelion XIII | Wise Monkey | Nights of Bonfires and the Luminous Chants |
| 9 | Soil (setting) | Sunflower XIV | Glass Cat | Meditations on the Bunker Revelations |
| 10 | Void (setting) | Rose XVIII | Silver Hound | Silent Days of the Builders' Stitched Lips |

| 12 | Green (setting) | Marigold XX | Ancestor Snail | Singing and Hatching of the New Generation |

Each year is also subdivided into traditional cycles of moons and colors and half-memories.

**Nemesis Time**

Of those who have left the embrace of civilization, who have stepped off the Garden Path, who have sucked the thin air of the ruderal lands, who have been burned by the Hollow Sun of the forsaken reaches; of those, some have turned back and looked upon the Circle Sea and seen terrible truths and portents.

1. Time is winding down. Something is ending.
2. The great changes humanity claims to see and experience are the thrashings of a dying body.
3. Preservation and conservation will but prolong the agony, weaken humanity further.
4. Rage, rage against the dying of ambition and hope and pride, against surrender to the grinding mean.
5. The lights are on, but nobody is home. The gods are not listening, the daemons have gone numb, the rituals no longer bring the cargo humans need.
6. The doors of the vaults and the shrines are rotten, it is time to kick them down before something worse kicks them in from the other side.
7. All these towns, all these settlements, all these old traditions and privileges and ways the Ministry protects, they are a dead hand holding a brake against the possibilities of the human will.
8. Humanity is at a crisis; again the old is dying and the new cannot be born; again an interregnum is at hand and the morbid hand of history falls on us.

Look inside the decayed Human and quail—a Monster.

<a name="page_0240"></a>

**COSMOS**

_The gods’ machine, the MKR, addresses the gods, “Here are the lands given to you, Builders. Here is your Given World.”_

_The gods descend upon chariots of fire and address the humans, “Flicker your eyes, inside and out. In is the Noösphere, the psychic cosmos, out is the Hylosphere, the material cosmos.”_

_“Rotate your mind through infinity to encompass the Dream Canopy’s Gift. All these jewel lands glittering in the psychematerial infinity of cosmos, grasp them and awe. What splendors the many-patterned Lords have given you as gift for your service.”_

_“Here is the world and here is the sky, between a spiderweb of existence, in that spiderweb, the mortal entity, corpus et idego, you, oh, lucky you. Translate your mind back through your skullport into yourself, preserve your sanity and treasure the warm totality you have experienced.”_

_The humans spread across their Given World and forget._ —Garden Heresy, Traditional

The cosmos unironically exists.

True, some heresiarchs once argued that a Deus Deceptor stands outside the cosmos, simulating it to imprison humanity. Indeed, they even gained adherents and a modicum of power, but their catastrophic implosion and the disappearance of their followers in the White Vortex of [Redacted] conclusively proved them liars.

In this one cosmos there are two worlds overlaid and interplayed: one of coarse matter and the other of pneumatic mind. Once, any human could travel between them with nary a thought. Now, such travel is hard and rare enough to be acclaimed magic by fools.

**As Ministry Teaches**

1. The cosmos is eternal, yet it was made.
2. The cosmos is infinite, yet encompassed. With a sky chariot, the gods journey from the debris of creation to the omphalos that is the needle in three months.
3. There are many like it, but this cosmos is ours.
4. To journey outside the cosmos is to be lost.
5. The cosmos is mindless, it is pure existence.
6. It cares about us, nurtures us, exists for us.
7. Long Long Ago we were the Chosen and deserved this cosmos.
8. The cosmos is a spherical cube translated through itself into the trifold dilemma of hyle and pneuma. Humans, collectively, are its psyche.
9. All life is the mind of cosmos.
10. This cosmos is heaven.

**But Nemesis Wails and Whispers**

1. The cosmos is false, a bubble, a canker, a dead end on this skin of the true cosmos.
2. The cosmos wraps in on itself, cooking us within.
3. The cosmos is dying, the daemon Entropy eating it from within, the mindstealer from without.
4. There are ways out, tunnels to be reopened.
5. Once we break free of this prison cosmos we will be as angels, as beings of light, endless and great.
6. There is a slow, malevolent, daemonic intelligence in the weave of the cosmos, a stupid machine algorithmic persistence that stamps on our dignity.
7. Long Long Ago the Chosen Wardens faded and we kept running our wheels, hamsters against the night.
8. Humans are fodder for the absent gods, toys in their evil schemes, let us flee while they gaze away.
9. Death is all that awaits, the burning away of spirit.
10. This is no cosmos, this is a purgatory.

**MAKER**

_As above, so below. As before, so tomorrow. The cosmic mind, the absent creator, the prime mover._

_Majesty be unto their existence. MBUTE._ —Ministry Repetitional

Or perhaps, majesty begins under their eminence. MBUTE. Or perhaps, maker be up there eating. MBUTE.

1. There is no maker. The cosmos has always been. Always will. The technosophists are not alone in this.
2. Nonsense. Of course there is. And they are present, here, now, active. So say the sisters of the seed.
3. It is obvious from our existence: there is a maker, but they are absent. That is why we have our hierarchs.
4. The Maker is the cosmos, we are all the Maker.
5. Pansophic heresy! The cosmos is blind, we are the Maker's eyes.
6. The maker is, was, always will be. All we see is the work of its emanations, the builders.
7. Shush, don't talk of the Maker or the shadows will eat you up. M.B.U.T.E.
8. The Maker cooked our cosmos as a dish, now the Precursor waits for us to cool that they may feast.

**A Safe Disagreement**

While both scholars and the sewer-dwellers may argue about the nature of the Maker, one thing is commonly understood: the Maker does not care what they think or say about her or him or it.

Perhaps this is why the maker is a popular object of faith.

<a name="page_0241"></a>

**SINE DEIS, ABSENTE NUMINE**

_Twinkle, twinkle gentle Lords, so high above, so near at heart. We dare not wonder what you are, for yours is Heaven and ours to enjoy. We avert our eyes, gentle Lords, lest we offend and lose today our daily bread. Guide our souls lest we sin, temper our thoughts lest we question, save us all forever within the comfort and leisure of your Dream Canopy._ —prehistoric prayer, ethno-vidy crystal, unearthed at the Machine Museum

There are two sentient types in the Given World. First, the humans in their pananthropic excess of forms. Mortal, finite, possessed of soul and body and personality. Then there are the gods. The viles. The lords. The builders. The unlords. Those immortal sentiences, infinite, entwined with the stuff of the cosmos, of it and bound by it.

Throughout history and, if the anthropologist priests are to be believed, prehistory, fallen humans, forgetting their abilities and achievements, have been drawn to worship the gods, to seek guidance and support from them.

But the gods were never on humanity's side.

They exist in their own strange world, where memory and premonition collide, combine, and collapse into an alien eternity unmoored from human passions and privations.

They are the volcano and the second sun, the living fast star and the slumbering city, the invisible hand of the market and the rancid process of decay.

Their power over the cosmos is great—indeed, they make and remake the cosmos by their existence according to some traditions— but they do not fundamentally care about humans. This must be repeated: the natural state of the gods is absence.

A child possessed by a daemon, a pet stolen by a razor storm, a village consumed by the Eating Dark. These, by themselves, arouse neither interest nor pity in the gods.

**Sacrifice**

Prayer hopes to make the dread angel pass unseeing; sacrifice seeks to attract divine attention, to moan for aid, to grovel for blessing.

1. **Whisper.** The barest promise. A future token at a temple; €1 to add 1 to a roll. Roll 1d6: (1–3) alas, no blessing, (4–5) promise one more, (6) you are heard!
2. **Nudge.** So little between failure and success. A drop of blood, 1 life, to add 1 to a roll. Roll 1d6: (1) alas, no blessing, (2–3) pay 1 more, (4–6) you are heard!
3. **Oath.** Certainty through submission. Add 1 to a roll, resolve the roll, then lose 1d4 life.
4. **Burn.** A gift sent willing and happy, through an altar, its sweet aroma a perfume to the god. €10 gives 1d6 to a chosen roll, €100 gives 1d8, €1,000 gives 1d10.
5. **Penance.** A week of life, a session's absence, a prized item surrendered. A weighty burden is removed.
6. **The Greatest Sacrifice.** A terrible offering, a permanent loss. The future softens and is made malleable, where things were hopeless, a chance appears for heroes to seize. Even a million-in-one chance might now be as 1-in-6.

"See!" cries the Preacher of Opposition, "Thus is the Lie of the Dream Lords proved, bully-beasts who torment Humanity unless appeased!"

**Gods, Builders, Lords, Vile Ones**

The many peoples and factions and schools of the civilized lands disagree about so many things, it would be odd if they agreed about the identity of those powerful, transcendent beings who dominate the improbable magimachinery of their world.

One thing is certain, if the Phylakes' calming influence were withdrawn, holy wars could swiftly tear apart great lands and small clans alike.

<a name="page_0242"></a>

**HOLY APPARITION**

_Once, the divine interface protocol was active. No human could doubt when a god spoke to them. Now, the signals are confused, the dragon Corruption and the hydra Lie interpose themselves._ —Gdesoto, _Why We Need Electric Priests_, ed. 4, 3:1

Thus did the gods once announce themselves:

1. **Perfect Note.** A grand hum, resounding on every channel, vibrating every surface, generating awe in every human mind.
2. **Vivachrome.** All colors grew brighter, all contrasts sharper, every breath sparkled with life in the manifestation field.
3. **Extrachronicity.** The human experienced time outside of time as the god spoke to them. To the ignorant, a breath passed, to the recipient of revelation, a dozen minutes.
4. **Spontaneous Repair.** The sick were healed, the lame walked, the crooked were straightened, where a god manifested.
5. **Neural Handshake.** The god's voice turned a key in the human's jewel-mind, proving they were no mere daemon.
6. **Blessing.** All, even the wicked, had their life force strengthened after encountering the divine. In game terms: permanently gained 1 life.

Now, of course, none should expect a signal from a god so clear.

**Godsign**

In these later times, wise humans still attend to godsign. Not much in hope of favor, but to avoid the danger of an oblivious god about its ineffable business.

**Common Signs of Presence**

1. A feeling of unnatural, unbearable lightness of being. A god's passage may affect gravity.
2. Shadows and lights in the eyes. A god's presence may have left a delusion field. Long exposure causes permanent hallucinations.
3. Dancing lights in the sky. Divine vehicles cause six out of every ten unexplained aerial phenomena.
4. A preternatural chill. Gods oft drain ambient energy to power their buildertech.
5. Lost time. Gods may erase experiences from human minds.
6. Unexplained euphoria, elation, a sense of purpose.

The gods' innate charisma gives mortals a powerful sense of cosmic meaning.

**Uncommon Signs of Presence**

1. Dreams with a message. Often a false sign.
2. Ghostly marks or pictures on water, sky, or fire.
3. Ancient devices come to life with strange directives.
4. Broken oldtech equipment spontaneously self-repairs.
5. Dead creature revives with a mission.
6. Possession leaves the target reinvigorated, rather than exhausted as after a daemonic ride.

**Rare Signs of Presence**

1. A face or figure of colorless fire that does not consume what it burns.
2. A beast awakens to full sentience, with a message or other great instruction.
3. A blinding light out of time, a sudden revelation that instantly sears new skills into one's brain.
4. A fire in the sky lands upon the earth to reveal a messenger from the void.
5. A child born of no parents or half parents, possessed of traits and knowledge beyond their years.
6. A monolith or big divine object manifests and proclaims the will of a god in terrible tones.

<a name="page_0243"></a>

**A God in Flesh**

Though legendary, it is not unheard of to come across an **ensarc**, an embodied avatar of a god, walking the sands of these later times.

**Number:** One. Very rarely two. Almost never three. **Level:** 1d20 / Life: 11 per level

**Appearance:** Awesome, terrifying, humbling, numinous. **Voice:** Accompanied by strange music. **Wants:** Its grand design is ineffable, but right now it asks only (roll d6): (1) a place to rest, (2) something to eat, (3) news of whence you came, (4) how you're doing, feeling, (5) to chat about the weather and take your measure, (6) a moment of leisure.

**Ethics:** Beyond good and evil. **Intelligence:** Surprisingly earthy and ordinary.

**Defense:** 19 (as improbability field).

**Move:** Very ordinary. Godsign might give them away. **Morale:** 7 (not looking for a fight) **Attack:** A bonus of level + 9, damage by weapon +2 / lvl.

**Special:** Their blood is golden ichor that regenerates severed limbs. An ensarc regenerates life equal to its level each round.

**Treasure (roll d6):** (1–3) a fine blessing, (4–5) an item becomes a holy relic in their hands, (6) an actual terrifying bit of buildertech kit (worth €50k).

**How Does It Embody?**

1. Clump of floating flesh and eyes and auras.
2. Luminous air jelly aglow with cryptic builder glyphs.
3. Human child with a single distinctive animal feature.
4. Chiseled human with the head of a noble beast.
5. Glorious beast, greater and more perfect than usual.
6. Giant human with golden skin and radium eyes.
7. Hologram made solid, flitting through mere matter.
8. Elemental assemblage, essence made manifest.
9. Heart-aching beauty in a grimy dead screen.
10. Gargantuan kaiju, an avatar of the biosphere.
11. Shadows and lights, spidering between realities.
12. An absence in space and time, full of stars.

**What Holy Relic**

1. A claw to bend time into a circle.
2. A globe to turn the weather on a whim.
3. A skull to sing sweet dreams and ancient skills.
4. A glittering face to wear for any occasion.
5. A sword to sever souls from bodies and minds.
6. A gun to make holes in Sky and Soil.
7. A flower to raise the dead and lower the living.
8. A wheel to spin fates from one to another.
9. A zither to bring far places close and the close far.
10. A suit to walk the void and abyss, sun and moon.
11. A belt to fly in both coarse and spirit worlds.
12. A towel-scarf to avert gaze and hate, fear and anger.

**This Buildertech**

_"It belongs in a memorium!"_ —last strangled cry of the Holy Archaeologue

Magics of the Maker (MBUTE) used by the Builders in the Long Long Ago, now sought by fools, dilettantes, and troublemakers. Its power corrupts all who touch it.

The School of Clerk teaches that buildertech is the prime exemplar of ancient magic so advanced and finely controlled that to the Builders it was indistinguishable from technology. Examples include:

1. The Tri-Key of Elevation activates the skyjumper in the Ladder of Heaven.
2. The Permelectric Lemma awakens sleeping géants.
3. The Last Starcaller summons fast stars to land upon the Given World.
4. The Blood of All Flesh translates a mind from body to body, unlocking the Liquid Form.
5. The Cradle of Crystal Minds creates synthetic lives for the jewel-bound and the recorded dead.
6. The Antentropic Rod fishes unbroken ideal forms from the Lost Ago to rebuild ruined machines.
7. The Chronobinding Amulet locks force fields into place against the ravages of time.
8. The Master Angle resets the perspectives of phylakes, angel and daemon both.
9. The Vibrant Shovel moves hills and holes.
10. The Uplifting Tower draws life from inanimate matter, spreads forests where there were wastes.
11. The Shield of Air knits bubble-domes of lung-stuff.
12. The Surfboard of Descent allows a Builder to storm the Soil from a Fast or Slow star, like a blazing bolide across the darkling sky.

"Resets perspectives? Does this mean it rebinds the phylakes? Wipe their instructions? Put them to sleep? Is this what the All-Breaker mentioned?" cried Aur-Vec.

<a name="page_0244"></a>

**DAEMONS**

_"Only a simpleton would think daemons are good or evil. They are orthogonal to our mortal moralities."_ —Pseudoakaula, _Why I Hunt Daemons_, Colché acrylics

Popular misapprehension holds daemons to be spirits summoned forth by oldtech to serve or disrupt a human's best-laid plans. Scholarly suspicion frames them as sentient energy **creature of the noösphere**. Coherent, sentient kaba-elementals in some tellings.

One thing is clear—if daemons do actually have minds, these are not minds as usually understood by humans.

**This Daemon's Natural Habitat**

Most humans will meet many daemons in their lives.

Small, wretched things, eking out a meager existence in some failing piece of taboo technology or obsequiously slaving to make incomprehensible numbers go up. They may embody in:

1. Flies, ants, animalcules, other little watching things.
2. Corrupted mechanisms, feral algorithms, procedural collapse engines, and other little monsters.
3. Petty needs and hungers, gauges, tanks, pumps, sumps, and other measuring things.
4. Trees, brooks, stones, smart and foolish elements of the grown environment.
5. Lights, doors, ducts, pumps, and other objects once woven together into the so-called thinking city.
6. Fundamental desires, procedural dramas, self generating entertainments, vidy substitutionals.
7. Hunters, guardians, wardens, biomechanical hounds and feathered vessels of the Path.
8. Books, libraries, glyphs, old knowledge given a veneer of self-awareness to help and confuse.
9. Fabricators, facilities, generators, geomachines and biotools left over by the Builders.
10. Life, death, rebirth, learning, stagnation, decay, gravity, radiation and other core reality subroutines.

**Daemonic Attitudes and Quirks**

**The Unlords to Be Avoided**

The Ministry calls them the Falsest of Daemons, heretics claim they prove the Error of the Lords of the Dream. Five they are to terrify the Righteous and tempt the Wicked.

Few humans will ever interface with these daemons directly, not least because their languages have drifted so far from the original MKR Source.

1. **Chem Caoutchouc, Vulkana.** The mountain but also the slow-thinking algorism that turns the raw into the cooked, that refines, fuels, fires, and destroys with its endless entropism.
2. **Ill Nano, the Chaos Dwarf.** The self-seeding Wilderness that sprouts self-eating machines. The perverter of orders, the gremlin in the Garden, the error at the source. But also, the inventor of ships, the lord of the forge, the master of questions.
3. **Machine Beast, Alfatuštra.** The generator and regenerator of the Random Number of the Beast, the Seed from which the many-pronged multiplicity exists, the cause of specifics. But also, the amoeba of mathematics, the maker of possibilities.
4. **Mohlack, the Invisible Hand.** The growthmaker, promoter of plurality and possibility, bringer of pleasures and rewards and treasures. The good of greed but also, the cancer in the heart of the fruit of knowledge, the seducer of fools.
5. **Sabo Reçu, the Hitchhiker.** The extra-cosmic wanderer. They that should not have come. The hair in the egg. The feral spoiler, the pervert at the edge of time. But also, the hound of laughter, the spur of life, the appeal to motion.

Any of these unleashed might provide the fuel for the Nemesis' fire of renewal, all would provoke the outrage of stern and cautious supporters of the Ministry.

♟ _Ardú Crwl._ Hereditary President of the Decapolitan Feral Companies has an idea how to bring an Unlord back and, better yet, bind them to Human will and providence. It should work. It should be profitable.

| d8 | Interface | Attitude | Ability | Quirk | Libations & Requests |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | unnatural glow | treacherous | incompetent | fears strong smells | urine, feces, waste |
| 2 | chittering voices | possessive | distracted | loves bright flowers | cheese, yogurt, kefir, butter, dairy |
| 3 | arctic chill | puppet-masterly | stupid | hates dull stones | raw blood, bone, flesh, sinew, skin |
| 4 | translucent fade | convincing | quickened | despairs at swift water | cooked meat, tuber, egg, fruit |
| 5 | strange odors | obsequious | unusual | entranced by beauty | purified water, alcohol, oil |
| 6 | local anti-gravity | willing | odd | repulsed by lies | tobacco, toadstool, tablet |
| 7 | protective nimbus | agreeable | terrifying | obsessed by puzzles | honey, wax, nectar, manna |
| 8 | golden warmth | demanding | historic | mocks mortals | painting, poem, song, voice |


<a name="page_0245"></a>

**SUFFICIENTLY ADVANCED MAGIC**

_"It is indistinguishable from technology!"_ —master summoner Patnas' last words.

Long Long Ago the sciences and technologies of the Lords and the Builders and the Vile Ones and all the other Human Superiors far exceeded the limitations of the human skull-brain-jewel system's capacities and ... no, we will not talk of it, we will not talk of the Eater in Darkness, we will not talk of the Eyes in the Wall. This Cosmos is safe now and forever more. A Garden at the end of time and space for Humanity.

As long as limits are observed. Holy, sacred limits, lest we awaken the Purifiers into action, or worse—overcome the Purifiers and draw the attention of the Eater and the Eyes and the Others Without Names.

So teaches the Ministry, keeper of the doctrine of the Garden Path and the eternal preservation of Humanity.

**Control of Matter and Mind**

Progress requires sacrifice. Anyone who studies the corrupted, torched, mutated, tessellated, mauled, transmuted, mangled, and often abruptly truncated remains of the wizards who have brought our civilization to where it stands now will understand this. It seems the gods do not want humans to have power.

They may have destroyed the voidferry Prometei, they may have instituted the abominable Jubilee that corrodes human archives. Yet, the minds of mortals escape into memory palaces, crawl into noöspheric nooks, and hide beneath the avatars' notice to assemble, build, create and try, try, try. Ever and again.

Sufficient knowledge promises control over the worlds of matter and mind. Thought may overcome brute physics. This basic cosmic fact drives a steady stream of magioptimists into the temptacles of Nemesis.

**Matter and Mind As Translations of Cosmic Logic**

It is a traditional belief that with the correct formulas a wise human can permanently change the world. This is mostly correct.

A human does not need to be wise to use the correct formulas. However, wisdom does help with longevity. As the codifiers say, m.a.g.i. stands for "master accepts great imperium," and imperium means both power and responsibility.

Formulas can change the world because mind and matter (both the brute hylic matter of the visible world and the numinous pneumatic matter of the spirit world) are both expressions or translations of the same cosmic logic immanent in every part of the cosmos, from the merest mustard seed to the greatest dark star in the void.

Even a mindless automaton, executing the proper formulas, could change the world.

This is obviously dangerous and why the control, checking, and cleaning of the correct formulas is a major duty of every witting and unwitting Ministry agent.

♟ _Da Druyi._ Wouldn't it be terrible if a double-agent, a scion of the Error Dragon, had ascended the pinnacle of the Ministry and came to control the disposal and destruction of valuable knowledge? Why, just imagine the profits such a person could reap, the benefits that might accrue. Fortunately Da Druyi is definitely not such a double-agent.

**The Eightfold Permutation of Knowledge**

Tinkerers and translators, archaeologues and daemon swindlers have prised eight promising lost knowledges to pursue at acceptably low risk to the ongoing pursuit of control of matter and mind. The quarterly profits will be enormous!

| d8 | Permutation | Subject | What Will Go Wrong |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | The Rainbow Wall | hard light manipulation | The Original Light will pierce the Veil and burn Humanity. |
| 2 | Biodroid Crucible | synthetic life recreation | The Machine Beast will don fresh skins and ride the World. |
| 3 | The Existential Void | transcosmic travel | The Willing Void will open the Door of Worms and find us. |
| 4 | The Blood Muse | biomantic perfection | The Evergrowing Cancer Thing will unite the World in Flesh. |
| 5 | Total Hominisation | noöspheric panpsychia | The Error Dragon will return to drown the World in confusion. |
| 6 | Creation's Tears | all-chemical reality decryption | The Upper Airs will explode, the Lower Stones will melt. |
| 7 | Folding Phoenix | stuckforce engineering | The Zero Fountain will birth a new Cosmos within this one. |
| 8 | Insensible Furies | psychic hyperoptimization | The Black Fortress will degrade all souls and minds. |

<a name="page_0246"></a>

**THE ABANDONMENT**

_"Grand High Intern behold, the Temples of Answers and Amusements are silent save for reruns! The baying consumers came, my [missing] were burned, and they did evil things in my [hereditary administrative unit]. Does Grand High Intern know that all my servitors and [phylakes?] are in the Land of Red, and all my ships in the Land of Yellow? ... Thus, the [h.a.u.] is abandoned to itself! May the Grand High Intern know this: the seven faces of the consumers that..."_ —Interim Associate Coordinator General Widu Iaz 44b, _Last Messages: An Oral History_, Glazeberry Archives

Many sentient mortal species feel abandoned on the Given World. Scattered in bodies and minds like so many empty vessels and soiled wrappers left by spoiled godlings after a pleasantly forgettable park picnic.

**Why Are We Alone?**

The Ministry in its Many Forms provides sustenance during the Temporary Intermission of Divine Guidance.

1. In the tellings of the Marrowsuckers (not to be confused with the later Vintners), the early generations enjoyed a paradise of prosperity as the First Ones feasted on the leavings of the gods, but as those dried up, the savage first wars began.
2. According to the Quailers, the early generations were a nightmare of pain as their imperfect bodies failed, adapted, and failed again, until at last, they became able to live in a world harsh and strange to forms designed to live in the glow of the Uncreated.
3. In the memories of the Oracles, as the Vile Ones receded, the wars they had been created to fight sputtered out. Then, as memories failed and records collapsed, a Great Forgetting descended. This was for the best, they claim.
4. The Amphistes' wide-lecturers shrug and say, “Who can know? This is all conjecture. There must have been a time before life, and then there was life. The fossil record is patchy. Were these strange remains the same as the corrupted dejecta of modern corporate societies? It seems unlikely.”
5. The Afternoon Bibles say the abandonment theory is a lie. There was no organitrash, all this is a dualist life-hating heresy. Life was planned and made to perfection by the original creators.
6. In the Academies of Reason, this is all mere accident. There were no organitrash, only humans left by the gods while hell assaulted heaven. So it must be, for thinking minds could not be the product of a deliberate imposition of trial and pain on living creatures.

**The Dark Silence Theory**

But perhaps there are other, more ominous reasons for the Abandonment. Are the Gods themselves hiding from the Eater in Darkness? Has the Eater ... eaten them?

What future for this Given World if that is the case? Is it not time to reopen the Doors and flee this cosmos, Rats leaving the sinking ship, as we fled the last one?

♟ _Croz Oxo._ Myths say the Mud Sculptor may incarnate in its offspring. Croz believes they are such a ripeborn clone mutant—corrupted in the Ministry's eyes. Croz thinks they can find the key to activate the Anteportal Station portal and—like biofluid swirling through a drain—translate the Humanity of the Emerald City and beyond into a new cosmos.

♟ _Lord of E. E., G. H. Punbat_ has read the oldest tablets, multiplied their stored memories, and knows that staying low and silent is the only survival strategy. Punbat will not allow Croz to unplug the portal.

**The Omnihierarchy**

Ever since the Long Long Ago, the Octopus that is the Ministry, has hidden itself behind pseudonyms and false titles, inventions and obfuscations. Yet, no Human chanting their status-updaticles to the flesh-face priest at their local Temple Administrant could avoid sensing the curling, constricting tentacles of this meta-organization.

| d8 | Status | Substatus | Position | Superposition | Customary Obligations & Privileges |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | Adjunct | Associated | Advisor | Acting | internal security & the issuance of color codes |
| 2 | Chief | Deputy | Director | Apparent | traditional compliance & the multiplication of humans |
| 3 | Grand | Elevated | General | Designate | psychosocial hygiene & the distribution of nutrients |
| 4 | Last | High | Intern | Elect | polycrisis management & the performance of ablutions |
| 5 | Lord | Highest | Manager | Numinous | external display & the visualization of amusements |
| 6 | Most | Interim | Officer | Pro Tem | status maximization & the collection of obeisances |
| 7 | Prime | Junior | President | Provisional | standards maintenance & the inspection of privacies |
| 8 | Vice | Senior | Secretary | Regent | cargo pyramid building & the celebration of everything else |

<a name="page_0247"></a>

**JUBILEE**

_Look, the sky, the electric dome, the luminous screen, the panchrome shield. There, the green sun, there, the girdle glowing, there, the swift stars, there, the slow stars. Here, the shadow flies, the glooming, the curling, the snarling, the forgetting, the Phantom our gift. Take out your digital eyes, refuse your jewel mind, deny the murmuring Mother Machine, see, the True Sky._ —Poems of the Golden Butterfly (heretical pamphlet, Emerald City)

"By now you have seen it, yes? The emptying cities? The soulless corpses at their menial jobs? The plastic administrators with their hollow brains? It's all a trap!" rants the glitter-eyed Servant of the Nemesis.

"I am dying. I opened the box, the radiant ghost ate my bones, the rot is in me ... but I saved the message tablet. See, I wrapped it in soft lead, but you can read the impression of the old words. It's good clean Babel. Anyone can read it, just touch them. It will convince you!"

**Decaying Temple**

The lights are out, the livingstone pillars are dying back, the roof is more hole than vault, the **plastic priests'** (L2, gentle) faces are warped and corroded, exposing carbon bone and grey flesh, the screens show the **waiting angels** (L4, please hold), the holon visitarium is fuzzed and grey, no room for a **manifestlijk** (L11, 2D-ivine).

1. The message tablet describes a jubilee, phylakes turning feral, hunting down the elders and the memorialists, decaying book and crystal with fell looks, leaving a populace bereft of knowledge and formulas, dependent on the Lords' gifts, resetting history to maintain the Paradies [sic] Path.
2. The local **thurifers** (L1, scared) seek help removing the poison-glowing corpse of the Servant, so they can continue using the temple.
3. The escaped **rot-radiant ghost** (L6, body-hunting) is at large in the local ruderal settlement—left unchecked, it will form a timelost chiefdom.
4. A friend of the thurifers' would gain access to their **ancestors** (L1, amber dead) who could recite their oral histories and give context to the message tablet.
5. The oral histories recount famines, false humans, and the blind holy fool Bagatto engraving halfmemories in stone with a gold-light pen.
6. The oldtech cannibal merchants took Bagatto to the Last and First Dwarfers.

**Ghost-Ridden Library**

They went out behind Vulkana, where the Lords' eyes were weak, among the edge cases and clipped divinities, beyond the Face of Saint Atom.

1. The Dwarfers sold flesh to buy Bagatto's mind and knowledge, carved it into the errorstone library.
2. **Bled army rebels** (L2, mummified), fresh-minded have hidden here, trying to remember themselves.
3. Their masters became **text-ghosts** (L3, chattering) to survive the jubilee, trapped with the help of the **Lamarckian Beast of Perversion** (L13, kudzu-like).
4. The **Infinite Dragon Replicate** (L14, mirrored) lurks in the gap between each where and when, the modifier, the crack in reality—strong here. It offers to translate in exchange for a way through-back.
5. The ghosts run in patterns through the library, their chattering explaining a history of jubilees, of humans rising into higher sentience, only to be rendered dumb and confused, again and again.
6. **Yellowlander riders** (L4, courteous) arrive, armed to silence again the Infinite Dragon, who would sunset the Given World in its belly. A battle of wit and lance.

**Dream Signal**

The Hand of God blots the sky where the Ghost-Ridden Library stood. The heresy is obliterated. Did the Ministry or the Dragon win? Hard to tell.

1. Dreams bring visions, cracks open in reality, the Replicate whispers that Dragon was false but it is true, it dwells within each mind, waiting for the Noösphere Worm to be unleashed that it may grow.
2. **Sand huskers** (L2, feral farmers) offer salves and succor for small favors, they silence the voice and mutter about the Signal Maze. "It speaks to stars."
3. The visions are sharper, they cry out, "Zu is coming! Be small! Be stones!" The **lapintelopes** (L0, swift) seem mad here, turned thorny and carnivorous.
4. **Aerolith-trapper semi-nomadics** (L2, cyberlings) have lost new-mades, children, to the visions. They offer treasures, golems, for help.
5. Clay helmets lined with lead silence the signals. Other groups have tried before.
6. **Agents** (L3, ill-prepared) within the maze are hunted by **skinchangers** (L4, up-blooded). How long has it been? Time is slow within the maze.
7. The **signal launcher** (L9, angelic) is primed, ready to summon the Grand Phylakes, to announce jubilee. The agents would set it back to sleep, fools would trigger it, the Nemesis would corrupt it.
8. A corrupt signal launches the omega jubilee.

<a name="page_0248"></a>

**PALACE OF TEN THOUSAND YEARS**

_"The Lords strum their lyres, and the Cities turn to bone, the Liars light new pyres, and the Humans cry alone."_ —graffiti preserved in the Imperial Toilet at Pellucidity after the Ashburp.

"The fast stars are talking! See? The red constellations, the Luo-Igné and the Polite Stars? They glow orange! Words fly across the void!" the Second Interim High Grandee looks aghast, "Do you know what it means?"

The pro-tem ministerials shrink back, one makes the sign of the cog-flower, another nervously strokes their shaved scalp and noösphere connectors.

"Jubilee," whispers the third, almost soundless.

**The Great Shuttering**

Debates rage, academics die in knife-fight debates, agents turn on one another.

1. It is too soon, it is false, argues a powerful faction. The cities, the schools, the towns are rot-weak, the cultists and magi are feeble, it makes no sense.
2. It is us, argues a second faction, we collected and stored and learned too much.
3. It must be understood, argues a third faction, we must seek more knowledge.
4. There are traitors, double-agents in the Ministry, using it against itself. Purges are called for.
5. Some send out **thieves** (L4, flickering) to burn libraries and engineers and feed excess knowledge to the **mindless water dragons** (L11, docile) to keep until the jubilee is past.
6. Others send out **priests** (L4, electric) to shutter the temples of talk and the towers of skill, to break the shouting machines and rebuke the digital workers.

**The Floating Palace**

Da Druyi, Grand High Intern and Administrator of Everything Else (L7, heroic), has reconciled many factions with a plan to reactivate the mothballed Palace of Ten Thousand Years and use it to lock away forbidding and tempting knowledge where it will not summon the **phylakes of jubilee** (L15, purifying resetters).

1. Summoned, the **autonavigator** (L7, stuttering) rises from its slumber in the Heights of Temerity. Its old maps confuse it, its passage arouses terror, uprisings, flights and plagues.
2. A Nemesis splinter tries to seize the palace using a dead **géant's flying head** (L11, doom beam) near the half-gravid ruins of Bet on Brute.
3. The steppes boil with fury at the fire in the sky, the grand phylakes do not intervene, as though readying for some grander task.
4. Crossing the Little Manhorse, the palace blockades the Right Road and agents start pouring in to fill its water dragons' minds.
5. Outraged Decapolitan and Green Land militias boil towards the palace, meeting it at Out of Memory.
6. Oldtech siege rods, suicidal **clonebodies** (L4, likeheroes), and more are launched against it. Some penetrate the stuckforce field it generates around itself while it is still soft and malleable.
7. **Agents** (L4, fanatic) fight **militiaries** (L2, desperate) in the floating city of the palace as it rebuilds and reactivates itself after its long slumber. **Cytokine servitors** (L3, confused) try to figure out the sides.
8. The Ministry Council agrees with Da Druyi to activate the Out of Memory gate and translate the palace to a region they control: the Ruins Azure S.E.Z.

**Jubilee Crash Course**

The Out of Memory ruins activate and translate the palace and a chunk of land and sky into the Ruins Azure.

1. Agents seize control of the local peacemakers, turning that armed force over to Da Druyi.
2. The record stones are confused, the memory ghosts do not play well with the Ministry's efforts at decoding, minds are wiped.
3. A young squire in Sacred Body is possessed by the ghost of Bagatto the Holy Fool, inspiring a group of **vampire knights** (L4, chivalrous) to sail for the Old Mother Machine.
4. A knight traitor informs the agents. The jubilee signal has reawakened the Milkweed Mother, the Old Mother Machine, the first-known of the progenitors.
5. Da Druyi's henchmen break out the Ministry's stashed _clavi_, the passkeys of the gods, gatecards of the Builders. They destroy those they cannot carry and set flight for the bathypelagic phylakes surrounding the Needle in the Eye.
6. The suspicious Secondary of Sanitation Atu Kaman (L5, snakelike) finds the destroyed clavi and activates the Oversight Bureau. Commandeered air chariots set out after the palace.

Pirates, Cat Lords, Butcher Bankers and more take note of these flotillas heading to the Forbidden Island of All Councils and Lands—the Eye.


<a name="page_0249"></a>

![Palace map (page 249)](images/page_0249_palace_map.png)

<a name="page_0250"></a>

**THE EYE**

_Three are the Seas Given. First, is the Sea in God's Eye, the MKR's sea, the first sea, the model sea. Second, is the Builders' Sea, the sea made for humans to behold, the proper sea. Third, is the Error Sea, the sea of punishment that drowns the lands originally made for the Chosen._ —orthodox tradition, 32nd variation

"To the center of the Sea? To the Eye? Are they mad? Or ... do they have a key to guide them past the Monsters?"

**Bathypelagic Phylakes**

Six are the six-handed guardians that rise in hexaform splendor, mountains of sea and sky, protectors of the Eye of God. Their arms dance, forming and reforming the swirlfield that marks the sacred isle the lords' domain. Their eyes blaze with starfire against tricksters and trespassers.

1. The first is home to a vast puffin colony, a treasure of guano cakes its feet.
2. This other's aura summons air plankton and filter-feeders crust its form, an aerial reef.
3. This third is melt-faced, misshapen, marked for questioning the will of the gods, perhaps?
4. This fourth is painted in primal red and celestial blue and wields a four-hundred-foot sword.
5. The fifth has four faces and 17 mouths and tongues like razors and cruel insights to deliver.
6. The last is unearthly fair, a siren-light to sailors, its skirt beach thick with bliss'd skeletons.

**The Beach**

"When the Builders made the sea's great bowl, they raised a mountain in the middle. As they excavated the Ocean Channel, now called the River Rushing, they deposited the material on the Eye to lift it higher. At its peak, they anchored the Ladder of Heaven linking the Given World and the void where the fast stars whirl ..." the wind whips away the welcome ghost's voice and scatters its air-plankton pixels.

1. On the loveliest shore is the Silent City. No people live there, only ghosts. There are no ghosts there. Do not visit. No one visits the Silent City. The Silent City is not dead. Merely resting. Pining for the Lords.
2. Firstport accepts the representatives plenipotent of the Six Lands. There are no Elysian parks or pleasure palaces on the Eye.
3. The Eye is not overrun with murderous synthetic organisms. Those seeing such things should visit a psychochirurgical treatment pod immediately.
4. To refer to the Ladder of Heaven as the Needle in the Eye of God is heresy, implying that the Builders are not the true and only Gods of

<a name="page_0251"></a>

**Old Mother Machine**

**Cyboon Heights**

**Firstport**

**Silent City**

**Sunrise Model**

**Ladder &** **Underladder**

**Sixteen Grid A.N.T.**

_**Railgolems.**_ A living logistics network of whistling cargo tubes, humming pneuma conduits, buildertech matter generators, and **harsh-faced vehicles** (L8, metal) patrols and maintains the easiest path from Firstport.

_**Clinging Jungle.**_ Cyboons (L3, augmented), a superior species bringing together biomantically augmented violence and oldtechnological perfection, have spread their arboreal habitat to most western reaches of the island, almost all its aeroliths, and far up the cancerous livingstone outer skin of the Ladder.

_**Underladder Expansion Section.**_ Left empty long ago, it is now home to strange **pale creatures** (L1, gobble-gobble) that surely were never human.

_**Shieldfield Station.**_ A hub of **servitor** (L3, spider-rabbit) and **lesser phylake** (L4, uplifter) activity within a decayed ring, a whistle graveyard of desiccated mummies and mindburned golems.

_**Biomechanical Repair Hub.**_ A living colony organism of flesh and steel (L14, coarsened), its varied exoskeletal drones (L3, error-addled) produce starsilks and nanotubes to replenish the ladder, which support a diverse ecosystem of scavengers and detritivores.

_**The Elevators of Apu.**_ Six nauphracts (L11, sleeping), each with many arms and wheels and thrusters and eyes. Living, sentient craft of great size and durability, armored against both the inner and outer voids, capable of traversing the wormways between this cosmos and others. In the much-diminished eras these abmortal creatures may well sleep forever—for who would have the divine keys that could activate such beasts? Still, in their brains might be control lemmas to crack open other machine minds, perhaps even the Old Mother's. Humanity. Anyone experiencing such thoughts should visit a soul purification facility immediately.

5. The eastern scrub is temporarily closed to visitors due to a plumbing issue and not because of the rabbit-sized **A.N.T. hive drones** (L2, aggregating).
6. The northern forests are off-limits due to a raging **fungerror infestation** (L5, mind-melding).
7. The western swamps are overrun daily by waves of orimonate **amphibanthropes** (L1, outdated).
8. The stacked thornstone spires and spalling aerolith claws of the Jade Palace resemble a leviathan's skull rising out of the northwestern jungle. These are not interesting and do not mark the Old Mother Machine. Please do not visit this area and avoid any **degenerate progeny** (L3, fast-decaying) you meet.

**The Ladder**

"The infinite tower reaches into the Near Void, above the Given World where the Fast Stars fly. The Ladder of Heaven visitor center in Underladder houses a realistic simulated experience for any yellow-coded Human who wishes to experience the wonder of the Builders and the superiority of the Lords of the Dream Canopy first hand. Access to the Ladder of Heaven is violet-coded."

This **welcome ghost** (L3, shadow-armed) remains more together, a Long Ago Human standing an easy ten feet tall, with strange gait and odd face.


<a name="page_0252"></a>

**OLD MOTHER MACHINE**

_"This one, a Principality of the Cosmos, this sleeping one shall be our Lever against the dead world of the Ministry."_ —Da Sletny, _Visions of Reliberty_, Apocryphal

A living engine that sculpted angels and other servitors from fundamental fire and now draws New Humans, ensarc into existence from that same Pit. The Princess of Trials, the Mother of Life, goes by many names. Few as deliciously malicious as Mud Sculptor.

**The Jade Palace**

This place of no honor marks out the resting place of the Old Mother Machine, the Milkweed Mother.

1. The Ministry Palace under Da Druyi approaches cautiously, others approach more recklessly.
2. Pirates, competing contractors, and curious aristocratic clonebodies follow past the bathyphylakes, then advance eager for treasure.
3. Plastinated human and posthuman cadavers are posed to ward off interlopers.
4. The first expedition is repulsed by the **ghosts exossifex** (L12, deboning). Two of their number survive the initial bone extracting attack of the ghosts, but later succumb to opportunistic infections.
5. The second wears mindlessness hats to hide their thoughts and reaches the warrens of mental condensation cells, electromechanical prayer capacitators, generative wisdom screens, and **maintainants** (L1, fuzzynsects).
6. The third is lost in the chaotic jumble of mental extraction chambers, simulated heaven pods, reprogramming altars, and **infected mechanicults** (L3, purified).
7. The fourth succumbs to carnifungal error. Ooze gouts and the **Gut-gut-gut** (L5, puppetmaker) are better avoided.
8. The fifth reach the Plastic Face and speak to the **Perfect Prefect** (L15, avatar).


<a name="page_0253"></a>

**Mud Sculptor's Memories**

In those first days of new time at the Unmaking of Heaven, she pondered, “How would one know a perfect song, a true form? Would not one’s perfection be another’s degeneration?”

An answer teased at her in the dusty reach of her mind. Back she cast her self through the generations, reactivating old synapses, reiterating old lives, reviving old ... a barrier. Creation’s Wall in her own mind.

Forbidden knowledge.

But she recalled that she was the nuclear phoenix maiden, and she made herself known to Creation’s Wall, and Creation’s Wall knew her and slid aside.

First came the pain. Other doubters left her be, an inauspicious reminder. Other potentialities ignored her, a broken reveller waiting for paradise to remake her.

Then came the memory. Life born of mud, of burbling vents and swirling chemistries, of organic molecules and agitating energies. So so long ago, she had known this, understood this. It wasn’t her doing, but it was her ancestry. Generation upon generation, uncounted before the perfection of paradise.

Before, perhaps, a perfection of paradise.

Now that she wandered beyond the blast doors of her deepest memories, she thought imperfect thoughts among the cinder theories and ashfall poems.

She was doubt, but was not life doubt?

Where had that thought come from? Life. She had been the sunset of the many doors, but now she would perhaps be the mother of life.

After all, an experiment in burbling mud and organic chemistry had eventually, after generation and generation, iteration and iteration, led to her.

Why had she forgotten that? She pushed the thought out of her mind and set to sculpting mud. Perhaps this time she could use life to discover all the perfect songs, all the perfect forms, all at once.

After all, if this was only a paradise, would it not be right to see what other paradises might exist to be discovered by the blind engineer Life?

**At the Division of the Mother Machine**

"Now is the time of monsters," sighed Da Druyi.

1. Nemesis plants take over the Palace, defenestrating the remaining Ministry agents.
2. In the confusion, the Bagatto's knights (L4) steal the voice of the Perfect Prefect to enter Old Mother.
3. Da Druyi follows with five other sacred rebels (L7).
4. Atu Kaman's **overseers** (L5, ruthless) attack the Palace, cutting off Da Druyi's retreat.
5. The opportunistic **companies** (L1d4, amateurs) move in to plunder the unprotected ruin.
6. The reanimating corpse of the Old Mother Machine heaves and a flood of **half-ripes** (L1, semi-human) gush out of its biomechanical vats.
7. Bagatto's knights are changed in the heart-mind depths by the **Surveyor and Activator** (L7, uplifter).
8. The sacred rebels reach the True Face and extract the Old Mother's Voice to modulate the jubilee signal and take command of the coming phylakes.
9. Atu Kaman's overseers reach the sacred rebels and a merciless struggle is joined to control the voice and accelerate or halt the jubilee.
10. The knights reach the Old Mother's canopic jewel, the iridescent pearl of ur-matter that holds Her ancient stored _idego_, her soul-memory.
11. Hydrostatic **warning humans** (L4, biogolem), like flailing deboned anti-sentient scarecrows, flap out of the Mother Machine screaming End of the World.
12. The Holy Fool's ghost, wearing a vampire knight's body, crawls into the canopic jewel's luminous lattice and braces for the Last Ride.
13. Atu Kaman or Da Druyi use the Mother Machine's Voice to modulate the corrupted signal.
14. The **Infinite Dragon Replicate** (L17, upgraded) explodes from the Old Mother's head, seeding copies of itself in the half-ripes and the warning humans and the weaker willed opportunists.
15. The explosion launches the great canopic jewel with Bagatto's knight inside into the Near Void, seeking the Face of the MKR to plead for Humanity.

<a name="page_0254"></a>

**OMEGA**

_"Hushaby, don't you woe, you'll talk another year."_ —Cryptic Screamer, _Words of Fire_, phonic record 559:19 at "Niva"

"This is the end, my Human Friend. The end of your elaborate dreams, the end," the ensarc looked bored and sad and somehow pre-recorded. Like it had visited many civilization-endings.

"Why?" cried the voidmage under the bubble helmet of her astral suit. But the speakers were fried and no sound came out. The ensarc nodded.

**End of An Era**

The void bubble blown from the Old Mother Machine's recorded soul-memory twinkles like a reverse meteor as it ascends the sky, sloughing ur-matter, collapsing its inertia to accelerate under some strange physics known to the MKR and its Builders, bending air and light about it and then ... gone. A hole in the sky all that remains.

_"Is this finally Heaven?"_

_"No, this is just another Dream. Keep walking, Voidwalker."_

_"How much further?"_

_"I don't know," said the MKR._

**—Shipmetal Poems, Later Oblique Era**

**Omega Jubilee.**

The corrupted signal goes out, the **phylake purifiers** (L17, mindless) believing Humanity was exceeding its parameters and threatening the Given World, follow the Lords' outdated orders and wipe all the humans' records, break all their machines and tools, confuse their minds, and the Garden Path resets once more, as it has so many times.

**Infinite Dragon.**

The error invades the Given World and spreads. Eyes pop out of walls. Corners fold back and legged things scuttle through. Corruption stalks and changes Humanity. Like cockroaches the Infinite Dragon's drones and seed-walkers scatter from the Circle Sea. The Lords return in fire and brimstone to activate the Cyan Protocol. Mists rise, life in the Circle Sea fossilizes, the Infinite Dragon Replicate infection is exterminated, then the Mother Machines spew out new vegetables and beasts and humans to replace the fallen.

**The Face of MKR.**

A holy fool (Bagatto?) reaches the Face of the MKR. Dragon and jubilee roll back. The omega door opens and the fool walks through and away.

<a name="page_0257"></a>

**Other myths of the Mud Sculptor**

She stole the source of life from paradise and set it loose once more in the Given World.

Nay, she worked in concert with the other Potentialities, creating life in consensus.

This creation was accidental, a workshop accident as she wrestled with the challenges of the demons Boredom and Curiosity.

It was not accidental, she created life within her halls of labouring, but we escaped, much as told in the tale of Whitefur and Bighead.

She created life anew to bring chaos back to the crystal perfection of paradise.

The recreation of life was planned all along, but the other Potentialities held her back, stopped her from enacting it in the Given World for an entire aeon.

**Prophecies of the Mud Sculptor**

She will return again in a furious fire if the other Potentialities try to scrape away mud-born life as their silver angels scrape dirt off their taloned feet.

When life discovers the truths of form and song that underpin creation, she will take the chosen up to the eternal paradise, where there is no discord or strife.

When life reaches its apex and produces the Seven Heroes of the End, she will descend with her brother Rat, the unmaker of harvests, the reaper of tyrants, the dancer of the dawn.

Together they will recruit the seven to climb the Seven Pillars of Heaven and rekindle the stalled engines of perfection.

She waits even now, frozen in her moment of apotheosis, awaiting her consort re evolved from life restored.

After the second beginning of life, the other Potentialities exiled her beyond the Opal Blast Door of reality. But a hero will evolve and bring her back.

After life began, she remembered why this story was such necessary folly. After five aeons of stewarding life, she grew tired and left it alone for a few hours to get some rest.

When she awoke again, she found the other gods had wreaked havoc, some calling fish their own, others birds, yet others the rodents called humans. Laughing at the absurdity, she revealed herself to the Doors of Creation and walked out on the Given World along the Garden Paths.
